## THE BOOK OF GENESIS: How To Regain Your Artistic Brain


### The Best Way To Use The Mystery School

Achieving excellence is fun.

Three things to do before we start the journey (do them as you read this so you don't forget):

As for the correct order to do these modules...

There is no "correct order".

Jump around if you want. Totally cool.

Get a "lay of the land" if that's what will inspire you.

Btw, the ones with a 🔑 are modules you should keep coming back to. They will mean different things to you at different points in your journey. Third of fourth time around is when people really "get it".

The Mystery School is based on timeless principles, so it will take on a layer of depth every time you go through the modules. Don’t just read through it. Don't just watch videos. Study it.

My job is to keep giving you keys to try as you go through different doors.

Some keys that maybe didn’t work the first time around may work the second or third.

Or, you can go through it from top to bottom, like a book. That's cool too. (Which is fun since it does follow a logical order).

But remember THIS at all costs:

I know this may seem like a weird statement coming from me-- especially inside an "online course", right?

But The Mystery School is NOT about giving you a bunch of information.

That’s not what we do here.

The Mystery School was designed to help you gain knowledge.

And knowledge comes from DOING.

You know you’re on the right track when you read or watch something inside the school and you get so excited that you go apply it right away.

Stop in the middle if you have to— the videos and essays aren’t going anywhere.

You have to strike while the iron is hot. Because motivation is fragile. It could easily disappear.

Absorbing this information without action won't get you closer to your goals.

But DOING, and ITERATING... That’s what will get you closer.

After ACTION in the real world-- come back to The Mystery School again and you will see things you read before take on new meaning. You'll get new a-ha moments that could have only come from DOING

Re-read old modules and you will see a layer of depth you didn't catch the first time.

Or watch how the module I upload that week turns out to be the "perfect module" that answers the questions that have been nagging you all week. That's not coincidence. It's synchronicity.

When you and I talk over email or through Skype, we will have more powerful conversations because your challenges will come from your recent EXPERIENCE... Not from you WONDERING "what will happen if something doesn't work"... That's just you overthinking.

Study. Go do. And then study some more... But now with just a little bit more experience under your belt.

This cyclical feedback is what will lead to transformation in record time.

Reflection.

More action.

And remember this too:

While yes, it's true that The Mystery School is based on timeless principles and strategies (and NOT "hacks" and "tactics" that are valid for only a few weeks like what you see on YouTube)...

The way to use everything here is as a strong foundational STARTING POINT. There is no such thing as the final word.

Think of each module as IF / THEN statements that could unlock your potential.

IF your art isn't connecting with people...THEN maybe it's becauseyou don't have a message.

IF you're sick of Instagram and don't feel like it's working for you...THEN maybe you shouldtry using something radically different like EMAILto connect to your fans.

IF you're not making progress in the multiple avenues you're going down...THENtry focusing on only ONE thing for 90 daysand see if that gives you a breakthrough.

Everybody’s path is unique. And so is yours. These short films, essays and weekly emails should feel like they're giving you an unfair advantage... Not stressing you out.Take the parts that serve you... And ignore the rest.Find the nuggets of inspiration that help you get to YOUR destiny faster.

Fall in love with this journey... The process... And you'll already feel successful. And the financial and social rewards will come right behind.

Don't just read. Study.

The best information is it’s own sequel. Each time you experience it, it’s like you’re learning something new.

Whatever you READ in the mystery school is only an idea, or concept, until you discover it’s truth for yourself.

And that can only come with relentless obsessive action.

It’s action that brought me to these conclusion.

Thousands of hours of action.

Learning from my own actions and other successful people I've worked with have paved the way to make it way easier for you to go further, faster.

But you still need to reverse engineer these concepts with action.

That’s the only way to make them your own.

Use The Mystery School toaccompany you while you focus and achieve your goals (until the rest of the world finally catches up to what you're scheming).

With that in mind... Let's dive in!

• THE ART OF DISCIPLINE"The Book Of Transformation"-- Discover my road-tested approach to personal transformation -- Powerful enough for entrepreneurs and athletes... But Made For Creatives™. Start applying these intense techniques to turn your limp habit of procrastination into the rarefied air ofGod Momentum!

• OVERTHINKERS ANONYMOUS"The Book Of Mental Health"-- The opposite of overthinking is FLOW. This section is here to keep you remind of that fact. Oh, you'll fall off. It's law. But use this section to make sure those moments are just a blip in the journey not big chunks of your precious youth.

• MAKING YOUR LIFE A WORK OF ART"The Book Of Dares"-- When you repeatedly come out of your comfort zone and share it with your community, it inspires them. You’ve already been doing it. Here in there... Randomly. But the moments are few and far in between. This section will show you how to do it deliberately. Until it’s a way of life.

• FINDING YOUR MESSAGE"The Book Of Purpose"-- If you've been searching for a guide to help you unearth your purpose... Here it is: The exclusive 7-day 'Drill Down Method'. (With downloadable resources so you can do it with a friend - highly recommended.)

• BRAND VOODOO"The Book Of Influence”-- Learn all the "extreme productivity" ninja methods that I've been using for the last 10 years to create staggering amounts of culture-defining artistic content for brands and artists likeThe Weeknd, Redbull, Converse, 2 Super Bowls, and The Hakkassan Group.

• BUSINESS ART"The Book Of Money”-- How to make a living from your craft without having to "sell out". Learn the exact, copyable, process that I used to build lastnightsparty™ from nothing... Into a world-renowned brand.

Before embarking on the journey towards excellence, here are three important tasks to complete:

When engaging with the modules, remember that there is no specific order to follow. Feel free to jump around or explore as you please, taking note of the 🔑 modules for revisiting. The Mystery School is built on timeless principles, requiring active engagement rather than passive consumption.

Key points to remember:

Throughout the journey, study, apply, and reflect on the materials provided. The optional order of viewing the modules can bring new insights and a-ha moments with each repetition. Remember that everyone's path is unique, and you should tailor the lessons to your own journey.

As you progress, make sure to utilize the tools effectively to gain an unfair advantage in reaching your goals. The focus should be on personal growth and action, not solely on reading or watching content.

Lastly, embrace the process and fall in love with the journey, allowing the financial and social rewards to naturally follow your dedication and commitment. Let the information guide you towards transformation through consistent action and reflection.

In summary, The Mystery School offers a framework for personal development, productivity, and financial success, emphasizing action, reflection, and individualized approaches to growth and achievement.

## THE BOOK OF TRANSFORMATION: The Art Of Discipline


### 🔑 1. The Secret Of Daily Practice

Art by@sarahscribblescomics

0:40 "The Daily Practice" Principle

1:40 Why you feel like shit about your art

2:15 How to find energy to do your art even when you get home from your day job

2:55 How long should a DAILY PRACTICE be?

3:10 Why a DAILY PRACTICE improves your self-esteem.

4:00 The Zeigarnik Effect

5:00 How to stop feeling like a fraud

6:10 "How do I choose a daily pattern?"

7:20 The indirect version of the DAILY PRACTICE

8:30 The one non-negotiable

Recently I posted this on IG:

"If you're too tired when you come home from work to do the thing you love... It isn't love."

Some agreed.

Some were triggered.

This module will show you the best way to combat the "I don't have any energy" syndrome that you feel after "a long one".

Right now...

You're always exhausted...

It takes tons of effort to rev up your motivation to do the thing you love!

Dear Creative... Don't beat yourself up. It's not your fault.

It's because you don't have A DAILY PRACTICE.

You really think it's your job making you tired?

Nope. It's the fact that you aren't doing your art every day that's making you tired.

Having a DAILY PRACTICE...

Will give you inspiration.

Your powerful subconscious is formed by what you do every day. Put it to work for you on the DL.

And all you need is anywhere between 10 minutes - 1 hour IN THE MORNING depending on what activity you choose.

(Hear me out here. What follows isn't some BS "theoretical ideas" you'll read about on Medium. Or some influencer "YouTube hack" improvised by someone selling you a lifestyle not accumulated expertise. -- Everything I'm about to share with you comes from years of being in the same situation you're in right now... And then figuring out how to conquer it. I will show you by the end -- in a major TA-DAH moment -- how everything I'm explaining will translate into MORE ENERGY IN THE EVENING... AFTER WORK. But bear with me. Let me explain the basics first. It will be worth it in a sec!)

The idea is simple.

First, pick one thing related to your craft that you can do every morning without fail.

It should be:

Something you can do every morning WITHOUT FAIL.

Something you can do between 15 minutes and 1 hour.

Something where you can measure progress.

Something that will elevate your creative game.

You can choose to practice your craft.

Or learning a new technique and practice applying it for 30 minutes.

Or experimenting with creative ideas for 45 minutes. (You'll develop them later in larger blocks of time.)

Or copy the style of an artist you love to see what you can learn from their technique.

A classic daily practice is "freeform writing". In certain circles, they call it "doing your Morning Pages". This one is amazing for writers. Or even non-writers want to get better at writing captions.

If you're a photographer, it can be "going for a walk and taking pictures for 45 minutes".

If you're a musician, it can be coming up with a collection of riffs or "song starters".

If you've wanted to start a podcast, it can be taking the next few steps necessary to get that going.

If you're an artist who's weak at promoting themselves, it can be 1. researching people to send your art to and 2. writing the cold emails to one of those people every day.

Or it can be doing stretches if you're a dancer. So you get closer and closer to performing those splits.

Or it can be adding a few more strokes to the painting you've been working on.

Or continue editing a video.

Or writing a few more pages of your book.

Or creating one piece of "quality content" for Instagram.

Spend an hour making art.

Or an hour editing art.

Or an hour promoting your art.

Or "get your mind right" to "approach your art" with meditation.

Or keep yourself healthy so you are vital for your art by working out.

It's up to you. You're the creative. Be creative. Choose a daily practice.

Pick a task that is meaningful enough to make a difference, but simple enough that you can always get it done.

The reason why people procrastinate is not that they don't want to do something.

Otherwise, why would they procrastinate even the things they love?

No, people keep delaying some activities because of the tremendous psychic energy it takes to START them.

It takes so much mental energy to start.

Think about it.

Running every morning isn't hard.

It's getting into the mood for running that's hard.

Artists are lazy. We would rather keep doing whatever we're already doing then start something new. We hate "context switching". Every time we "context switch" it takes tons of energy.

But ever notice how, once you're in the groove.. "It's not so bad." Or how you always tell yourself: "I love doing this. Why did it take me so long to start?"

The funny thing about "exhaustion" is how it disappears after 10 minutes of working on something you're passionate about.

THAT'S why you need to do it every day.

When you do something every day you eventually forget the reasons you were afraid.

When you wake up and do the same thing every day, it gets easier because now it's a habit.

But please! Don't call it a habit. That's not fun.

Call it your... Ritual.

When you have a ritual, it takes no psychic energy to do.

You look forward to it.

It becomes "what you do". It becomes your quirk. And by doing it every day, you create momentum. Your body anticipates doing the activity.

It teaches you how to become as consistent as an I.V. drip.

But there's one little trick you can use to make it almost impossible NOT to do your daily practice:

This simple gesture prepares you psychologically.

For example. If you're editing film... Write out the shot list of what scenes you will edit the night before and leave it next to the computer.

If you're "freeform writing", decide on the topic you will write about the night before. Also, prepare the pouch of tea and saucer for the snack you'll be having while writing.

This step prepares your mind for your ritual.

It becomes hard NOT to do it at that point.

So this is what we have so far:

The formula for doing a daily practice...

Preparation the night before

Doing something every morning where you can measure improvement (practice)

A daily ritual that will change your life for the better

Yes, that's right. Change your LIFE for the BETTER.

A big claim?

Let me prove it.

Imagine how you will feel for the rest of the day-- Knowing that you already did something for YOURSELF and YOUR FUTURE... Before you started doing something for the man.

You don't think that will have a profound psychological effect on you?

You don't think that will put a "pep in your step" for the rest of the day?

Dude, no matter what happens later, no one can ruin your day now. You gave yourself this gift in the morning.

But that's not it.

Your daily practice will start to transform your inner voice.

Right now, your inner voice needs to be fact-checked as much as our politicians do.

Your inner voice is what convinces you to check your phone every 10 mintues.

Your inner voice is what gets you to invite your friend over for wine and gossip even though you said you were too exhausted to start working on the craft that you swear will make you famous someday.

Your inner voice is what prevents you from blocking out the next 2 hours without interruptions.

Your inner voice is what scares you into thinking that you may miss something, so you scroll Instagram instead of writing your next hit song.

I hate to say it, but...

Your inner voice is a traitor.

But thankfully, all is not lost:

When you have a daily practice, your inner voice quietens, and your higher self emerges.

Your daily practice raises your self-esteem.

You don't feel like a fraud anymore.

You only feel like a fraud when you say you're a writer-- But you know you haven't written for three months.

Or when you call yourself a photographer, but you haven't picked up a camera for a friggin' year. Hell, you don't even remember where your camera is-- Or if you have film in it!

You feel like a fraud when you know your guitar is gathering dust.

But... Do ANY activity every day, and you will feel "at one" with that thing.

You feel like Rocky cracking eggs into a blender at 4 am.

Your muscle memory of your art will always be connected to where it left off yesterday. It will stop being a distant memory. And all it takes is 15 minutes grow that cognitive plasma. Tomorrow you will fall right into the groove from where you left off yesterday.

And best of all:

You will be keeping "flow" on the horizon for when you have longer blocks of time later.

Instead of what you feel right now...

Like making art is some impossibly tall mountain that you have to climb every time you go to approach it.

Daily practice even has the by product of being able to control your moods better.

That’s a pretty wild by product.

People pay thousands of dollars to therapists for help with this.

And you can have it for free as a by-product of making art.

But you know what's better than everything we've talked about so far?

Back in high school, I use to start my days by waking up an hour early to write a song before school.

(I know, I know. Not your typical teenage activity. But I wasn't a typical teenager.)

The reason I was so religious about doing it BEFORE I went to school is because I noticed something crazy:

Whenever I did that, my brain would think about it all day.

All these ideas would pop into my head throughout the day that I would write down for later.

And then, by the time I got home, I was so pumped with all these ideas that I COULDN'T WAIT TO CONTINUE. I had been thinking about this moment all day.

I used the same "trick" when I worked a 9 to 5 at H&M in Times Square.

I remember having the morning shift on one Black Friday at H&M. Now, if you know retail (especially discount stores like H&M)... You understand how this could be the most draining soul-sucking experience known to man.

But I came back with energy to burn to take pictures (my newfound daily practice)

True, my body was physically tired.

But my brain could easily over-ride my body because I was EXCITED.

And why was I excited?

Because my daily practice gave me the kind of momentum that no amount of discipline could ever beat.

So... When some crazy woman at H&M gossiped about her husband while I was selling her a pair of "divided black" jeans... A moment like that could trigger a lyrical idea. Or the snare EQ I needed to use would suddenly become apparent.

I started expecting these moments to happen.

So when I finally got home, even though I was exhausted... I was inspired and excited to work.

Today, I'll even put obstacles in my way to engineer that feeling.

Only later did I find out there was science behind all of this...

Whenever there is an interruption of a task... Especially if it happens before there's a resolution... That task will linger in your subconscious.

It will fester in your mind.

Your brain keeps "thinking about it". "Working on it."

It's called "The Zeigarnik Effect". A Russian psychologist discovered it.

It's the reason why so many creative people get "a-ha" moments at random moments when they're NOT working on the art anymore.

Your subconscious is continues the work from where you left off even though you physically stopped hours ago.

Especially when there's unfinished business.

So when you do only 15 minutes to 1 hour of your daily practice and then you "suddenly have to stop -- just when you were getting into it "...

Don't worry. That's good!

This will keep your subconscious "in the zone" while you're doing the job you hate. You will get incredible creative ideas even as your eyes glaze over while your boss is yelling at you (this happened to me many times).

If you're a photographer who took pictures in the morning as your daily practice...

It will put your brain in "photography mode".

You will "see" things "different" all day.

When you go for your lunch break, you might find yourself experimenting with new angles using your camera phone.

This daily "seeing the world as a photographer" primes you for the long hours you'll get later to be creative.

You won't feel like you're starting from scratch every time.

You'll ease immediately into taking magical photos when it's creativity time.

So that's why you should wake up an hour earlier.

30 minutes! Is that too early for your art? Come on. That's like 2% of your day.

If you can scroll Instagram for 2 hours before you get out of bed, surely you can do THIS.

And think of it:

Your new daily morning practice will make it impossible for "the man" to steal your soul.

It will keep you connected to your art, your eye, your success.

ALWAYS do your MORNING PRACTICE.

Make your "daily practice", the non-negotiable thing you do every day.

Advance your art no matter what's going on in the world.

Even at Christmas.

Even on your birthday.

Even when your parents come to visit for a weekend.

Even when you get a fever.

Even when you get in a fight with your girlfriend.

Even on election day.

Make it the "minimum viable activity" of your day.

Make it short enough so there's never an excuse not to do it.

Don't wait for tragedy to strike to make you realize that you haven't been living the life you want this whole time.

Be your own wake-up call.

Let me leave you with this:

Creatives love to romanticize the idea of major 4-5 hour blocks of working on their craft...

And because of that...

They underestimate what they can get accomplished by doing 20 minutes a day.

You'd rather do NOTHING for a month waiting for that "big open block of free time "... than build your artistic journey brick by brick.

The truth is: Those big open blocks are rare.

They're rare BEFORE you're "successful". Obvs.

But they're also rare WHEN you're "successful".

Real-life is an interrupter.

Accept that, and you will find other ways to create "flow" no matter your reality.

15 minutes is the basic unit of measurement of the TMS Daily Practice.

I discovered, through trial and error (while on tour with The Weeknd), that 15 minutes was the minimum time required to activate all the positive effects of "showing up" for yourself (no imposter syndrome, Zeigarnik effect, energy building etc.).

If your time allows, you can go up to 1 hour. Never more. Use 15-minute increments to figure out your perfect time block (15, 30, 45 or 1 hour). Anything longer than 1 hour won't be sustainable when real life wants to kick your ass. It's not to say you can't "unofficially" go over that time on good days. That's on you. Turn the timer off and keep going. But your prime motivation should be keeping your daily appointment time allocation first. Don't do two hours today so that you can take tomorrow off. Even if you do 8 hours today, make sure you come in and do your minimum the next day. And every day after that... For the rest of your life.

It's CONSISTENCY that makes daily practice change your DNA. Not big bursts of output.

SIDENOTE: It's funny. Whenever I suggest limiting phone usage to one hour a day... Students freak out. "How can I survive on so little phone time?" But when I tell them to commit to making art for 15 minutes a day without fail, they give me 100+ excuses why that's a problem. This is when you know you have your priorities wrong. Here's some perspective... I have never had a day without making art since I was 16. Not one. It's possible if making art is like breathing to you.

If you want to make daily practice your default state, remember:

Daily Practice isn't about getting in some quick work on your "main art". Daily Practice is the "brushing your teeth every day" part of your creative schedule. It's the "you planted a seed, and now you're watering it every day" part of your day. Nothing major. What you choose should be short and easy enough so that you never have to miss a day. For example: a painter might sketch for 15 minutes, or fool around with a quick painting on canvas. All "daily practice" does is get your motor running. Then you have the rest of your day to continue your real pieces, or promotion stuff etc...

People are always trying to "change things up" so "it doesn't get boring". But that's also how you end up not moving the needle on anything. You're practicing discipline and consistency. You'll need to master this mindset for what's to come in The Mystery School. It's the cornerstone habit of being amazing at what you do. Same thing. Every day.

Crucial. Your Daily Practice is the first step to regaining control of your mind. You do this by breaking the cycle of mere "survival". This is the time you get to see yourself get better at something or make inroads in an activity even if the rest of your life isn't what you want it to be. Seeing yourself improve, or get results boosts your self-esteem. And then guess, what? You have more energy.

Keep a calendar, whiteboard, notepad etc... nearby. Every day you do your daily practice mark it down. Notate it where you can see the accumulation at a glance. You need to see the mountain of days building. It'll energize you.

But if you're already good at your craft, don't make that your daily practice. Choose something that will help your art, but that you suck at right now instead.

Since you are in TMS, even these actions of creating media is still you making art. It's all about intent. If you write an email as an extension of creating art... It will feel that way to the receiver.

So remember... Pick something you need practice on that's OUT OF YOUR COMFORT ZONE and within weeks you won't even recognize yourself.

Anything done in the morning is most likely to get done.

That's how you get the maximum benefit of the "Zeigarnik Effect" described above. And that's not a small thing at all.

Morning is the time when you have the most energy, so you might as well give that time to the thing you love the most. This is your "ME" time. You bring yourself to the highest energy so that you can share that energy with others for the rest of the day.

Even if you have to wake up an hour before work to do it, DO THAT. This is the cost. Pay the cost. Give YOURSELF the best hours of your day. Don't let your art settle for the tired, burnt-out hours after work.

Here's a trick to help you: Lay out everything you'll need for your daily practice the night before. That way, it's waiting for you when you wake up. This prep will make it so much easier to ease into your daily practice even if you're running slow.

Your self-sabotaging artistic ego will make you forget why you're doing the daily practice. You'll still be doing it, but only going through the motions. That's not sustainable spiritually, so you'll eventually quit.

Come back to this page every 21 days to remind yourself.

Just scroll to the bottom of this page and re-read THE 5 KEY REASONS YOU DO YOUR DAILY PRACTICE.

"Tomorrow I'm going to try to write about..."

"Tomorrow I'm gonna try this new technique..."

"Tomorrow I'm gonna see how fast I can..."

It makes it impossible to "go through the motions" when you're constantly testing your limits and diving into fun new "unknown territory".​

Great artists who are constantly asking "what if" statements. And then showing us the best results of that work.

For example

Banksy: "What if we created a work that would self-destruct 5 minutes after if was sold at an auction?"

Kanye West: "What if I made an album of autotune singing and combined it with hiphop?"

Quentin Tarantino: "What if I made a movie about slavery where the slave wins?"

Lady Gaga: "What if I ditched my whole glam persona and released a folk album?"

Daily Practice is a powerful, low pressure way to nurture this constant discovery.

Don't be surprised if you find unexpected gems that change your art forever during these low-key mornings.

That's the point.

So never let it get to the point where you're going through the motions.

Keep it fun by usingThe Mystery Formulainstead:

1. Start with an idea you wanna try

2. Try it 15 mins (30 mins, 45 mins or 1 hour)

3. Analyze how it went, and see what you can improve tomorrow

- Sending cold emails or DMs to gatekeepers who can help you every day.

- Working on short promo TikTok’s or Reels of your work... A little every day.

- Daily steps for starting your email newsletter to communicate with your fans.

### 🔑 1. The Secret Of Daily Practice

### "Most creatives over-estimate what they can accomplish in a day and under-estimate what they can accomplish in 20 minutes." - Father Bronques

## CHOOSING YOUR DAILY PRACTICE

## OK, WHY EVERY DAY?

## PREPARE EVERYTHING YOU WILL NEED TO DO YOUR DAILY PRACTICE THE NIGHT BEFORE SO EVERYTHING IS WAITING FOR YOU IN THE MORNING... READY FOR YOU TO START

## The TA-DAH moment of how your daily practice will increase your energy AT NIGHT

## The Zeigarnik Effect.

## But Make It Non-Negotiable

## CHOOSING A 'DAILY PRACTICE' CHECKLIST

### 1. A 'Daily Practice' is between 15 minutes to 1 hour. Never longer.

### 2. A 'Daily Practice' is THE SAME THING every day

### 3. A 'Daily Practice' is something where you can measure progress.

### 4. A 'Daily Practice' is best done in the morning

## GOING THROUGH THE MOTIONS

## THE 5 KEY REASONS YOU DO YOUR DAILY PRACTICE.

#### 🔑 Key Reason #1:So you never feel imposter syndrome.Imposter syndrome is a result of calling yourself an artist when you're not actually BEING anartist. Once you start making art every day again... You will FEEL like you're the real thing even on your low days.

#### 🔑 Key Reason #2:So you stay in the zone with your art at all cost. This enables you to get into "flow states" more quickly on the days you can fully dedicate to art. Daily Practice subdues your habit of overthinking.

#### 🔑 Key Reason #3:So you can get better and faster at making high quality art. Making art, even just for 15 minutes a day, improves your muscle memory for your technique and improves your relationship with your creative tools.

#### 🔑 Key Reason #4:For self-discovery and growth. When you set an intention the night before for your daily practice, you gift yourself the possibility for an artistic breakthrough. You joyfully bump against your current limitations.

#### 🔑 Key Reason #5:For your mental health.An artist who doesn't create doesn't feel whole. Any time you feel depressed, or unmotivated, look and you'll see... You're not making art. The moment you do, everything lights up again.

### 🔑2. The Most Attractive Quality That You Can Possess

What's the most attractive quality that you can possess?

People will say:

Intelligence!

A sense of humor!

A hot body!

A great personality!

Well, they're ALL wrong.

I've learned that when you're looking for the truth never ASK the masses for it.

Instead... Observe.

Observe different types of people.

That's why photographers are so lucky. That's all we do all day.

Sometimes we observe people with their permission... Like when we're on a photo shoot.

Or we do it on the DL... Like when people are talking and we're reading between the lines.

But to answer the question... "What the most attractive quality that you can possess?"

First, tell me... What's your best guess?

Come on. Try. Dig inside your soul.

I'll give you a clue. It's something that's never mentioned.

It's the most powerful trigger for our reptilian brains.

I always look for it in all my models.

I look for it in my friendships too. And even in my business partnerships.

And what's crazy is that every single person is born with it... but only a few people ever activate it.

But when they do! Look out!

It's a quality that'll make even the dumbest guy beautiful.

And make even the shyest girl hot.

It will make a "pimpled-- fatty-- loser--" yes, even them... Get a second look.

It's a quality that's mostly hidden on your Instagram feed, but impossible to miss in person.

What is it?

Dude, it's ridiculously simple:

The most attractive quality that you can possesses is...

THE AURA THAT YOU GET WHEN YOU'RE WORKING TOWARDS BECOMING THE PERSON THAT YOU'RE DESTINED BE.

Think about it.

People that are in the process of "becoming" are irrationally more attractive to us than those who aren't.

We FEEL it when this powerful energy is swirling around someone-- and we feel it wayyyyyyy before they actually "get to where they're going" too.

Creatives always see it first. We have x-ray vision for that shyt. We've done the math. We know to choose the seed over the fruit.

Like The Weeknd says on "Echoes Of Silence": "They only want you when you're next."

Like Drake says on "Lose You": "People like you more when you workin' towards somethin'".

Are these examples just a coincidence? Nope.They know.

This is the secret to how someone can end up being mega desirable EVEN in their "awkward" phase.

Even haters see it. What IS a hater, in fact? A hater is a person who sees that you have “the most attractive quality you could possess” and tries to do anything they can to knock you out of that mode.

Of course, most people won't see it at first. And that's ok.

They're like kids who overdose on candy: They've become immune to the taste of great food.

The rest of us. Those that haven't MURDERED our senses with the drug of "instant gratification"... We see it. Way early.

And boy, when you see untapped potential manifesting in someone-- It's VERY infectious!

There's a scent to it.

Women especially... They are geniuses at spotting it... They always know the magic seeds that can become a beanstalk.

Guys... Well, we mature slower.

That's why I'm telling you now. When you see that "ugly dude with a super hot chick"-- Don't just assume that she's in it for the cash. The guy may actually be dead broke. Instead, ask yourself... "Who is this guy becoming?"

Or when you see some "homely girl" with a rockstar who could be with anyone in the world... Don't just assume that she's "the childhood sweetheart" who got in there early. Ask yourself instead... "What is the future that HE sees in her that I'm totally blind to?"

And as for yourself...

Don't worry about looking the part yet.

You've come to The Mystery School to nurture "who you're becoming".

We're about to make that person shine through in all your actions.

And soon enough...

You will attract your "ride or die" family of fans.

Let's begin.

### 🔑2. The Most Attractive Quality That You Can Possess

### 🔑3. How To Become A Creativity Machine (Part I)

“I don’t think that I’m necessarily like a super-talented songwriter. I think I’m just really productive. One out of 10 songs is a hit. So where a lot of people will spend three weeks on one song, I will write 10 in three weeks.”— Sia

I learned that from Raymond Laliberte, my art theory teacher back in the day.

And I took it to heart.

Most people have trouble finishing stuff. They always want to make it perfect.

But he'd always tell me to practice my speed: Practice doing things at the same quality but finishing it faster. He'd encourage me to develop systems. And he'd show me how to improve my discipline.

And I ate it all up. I didn't know any better. My Haitian dad had already instilled a work ethic in me, so it was easy. And my hero was Prince, the ultimate creativity machine. So back then (I was a musician),I would create a new "song" every day and at the end of the week, I'd share "the hits" with my friends.

But even with the accolades... There was one person I was insanely jealous of. Sylvio. Sylvio made such beautiful art. (And his mom made the best chicken pizza, but I digress...)

His music was so layered and symphonic. The kind of music that you could never make in a day.

He labored on his art until it was perfect. Sometimes it would take weeks before he finished one song. But when he did... It would always be masterful.

Even though the other kids thought I was cool for coming out with songs so fast... Here I was jealous of the person who made songs SLOWER.

One day, Sylvio played his latest opus for us. It killed. All the girls swooned. That's when I started doubting my way of doing things.

So I went to see Raymond Laliberte in his office. I asked him if maybe I was on the wrong path. He was the one that was always pushing me to go even faster. So I had to confront him about it.

"You have a gift," he told me with a graveness I still remember. "The gift of the speed. Don't ever lose that. This world we live in is not getting any slower. This ability you have will be an important asset to have later. You should cherish your audacity to finish things quickly. Don't fall for the curse and start becoming paralyzed by the search for perfection. Keep pushing yourself to create completed art in a few hours... At a level that would take others days to do."

Nice words. But all I had in my mind was those girls swooning.

"But what about Sylvio? I could never..."

"Sylvio is talented. But he will never survive in the commercial world. Not unless he learns how to get out of his head. There are brutal schedules and deadlines to keep up with in the real world. Yes, it's true... The music he creates can't be made overnight. But it doesn't need to take a month either. You're on the better path."

Those girls were swooning, though.

Raymond Laliberte could see that I wasn't convinced. "Okay. If you're looking to create art that requires more of a "slow burn" like his does... Do this: Work on those kind of pieces IN PARALLEL. Work on them bit by bit-- a little more every day, while STILL USING YOUR GIFT AND FINISHING OTHER THINGS DAILY. Work on more complex music on the side... But never stop practicing your speed. Speed is a muscle that if you stop using it, you will lose it."

And that became my formula.

And all these years later... I can tell you that Raymond Laliberte was right.

I've had the privilege of being in the best studios, watching the biggest artists in the world work. And everyone works FAST. They turn things around. I'd like to give you examples, but I can't for confidentiality. But take my word for it... People are FINISHING their art in record times. THAT'S what make you a professional.

Sylvio took over the family pizzeria.

And in August 2020, The Spotify CEO Daniel Ek, made some controversial but truthful statements that "triggered" and pissed off millions of musicians around the world... He said:

"... These days you can't release music every three to four years and think that's going to be enough. The artists today that are making it realize that it's all about putting the work in, and creating a continuous engagement with their fans."

But of course some of you will say, yeah, "That's only happening in the music business. I don't need "speed" for my art form."

If you are in an industry where you have to "create content"... This applies to you too.

Like, let's say you're a hairdresser. And you're trying to maintain an Instagram that will attract more clients. You'll need to learn how to become a content creation machine too. Or hire someone who is if you can afford to.

It's a minimal requirement in this crazy digital age.

Anyone who wants to use Instagram, Tiktok, podcasting, or email marketing the right way needs to become a content creation machine.

Because I followed Raymond Laliberte's advice, before I ever took my first picture at a party I had already recorded 1,500 songs.

(That's why it only takes me a few hours to create the fully formed soundtracks you hear on my podcasts now.)

And when I transitioned to photography I continued to use the Raymond Laliberte ideology:

Take a thousand pictures a day and share photo galleries on my website every single morning before 8am. And for my "slow burn" art: do photoshoots with girls on the side that I take time to conceptualize and edit.

I overwhelmed the New York party scene with the sheer amount of quality photos I was releasing every day. The irony is... I was only sharing 2% of what I was creating. And it was easy for me. Not because I was talented (I sucked at photography at the beginning!). But because I had sheer momentum on my side.

And eventually, that momentum helped me become a better photographer in the process.

Here's a truth I discovered that makes people very uncomfortable:

Take a less talented person... who can develop a high output of good quality art ... And they will surpass the "hugely talented artist" who creates their "masterpieces", "once in a while".

How do I know this?

Because I was that "less talented person".

But with insane focus and discipline... I eventually became among the more talented people in the room.

And I watched many talented people abandon their creative journey.

I hate to burst the myths our society has created around "special people" but...

Let's be real. There's only one type of "special person" that deserves the title of legend:

People who create at the highest quality AND do it with spellbinding frequency. Like Steve Jobs. Like Basquiat. Like Drake.

Like that graphic designerreleasing a new 3D artwork on his Instagram EVERY SINGLE DAYfor the last 13 years.

That is what it takes to become the G.O.A.T.

Becoming a high-output creative doesn't guarantee that you will be recognized as a legend.

But you can't become a legend without it.

Let me paint the picture of the work ethic that was involved in building my brand over the years:

You gotta be a little crazy if you want crazy results.

So if you didn't have your own Raymond Laliberte to set you straight when you were younger...

Now you do.

Let's turn your life into a work of art.

By working up to that level.

Right now, whatever you think you're only capable of...

I'm gonna show you that your ceiling is a lot higher than you think it is.

You just haven't tested yourself yet.

But when you finally do... You will surprise yourself.

Yes, it will take discipline.

And it will require momentum.

But it's a special kind of momentum that is tailor-made for creatives.

God Momentum.

Now, wanna know the steps to actually increasing your speed? Click this last sentence...

### 4. How To Become A Creativity Machine (Part II)

This module is the most underrated of all The Mystery School modules. Ironically it’s also the one most likely to lead to impressive show-off results that yourself AND the outside world will immediately see. But while most of the other modules will give you an inspirational push or aha moment simply by reading them (unfortunately that’s as far as the information junkies will get)… The words below will only be understood in your bones when you apply it. None of it's value will translate just by reading it. No matter how much you try to “imagine” the benefits. Actually, it’ll all sound so much like blah blah common sense you you might be tempted to gloss it over. But that would be a mistake. Do the steps and you’ll see the magnitude of the impact they will immediately have on your workflow.

ILLUSTRATION BY AMADO GARZA AKA@MOMENTO_MORI

AKA How To Produce ART With The Speed & Consistency Of A "Content Creator"

AKA How To Be Prolific

AKA How To Improve Your Speed While Still Producing Quality

There are tons of articles and videos on the internet about making videos, blogs, taking pictures etc...

But what they all gloss over: how to start THINKING about your work so that you can create more of it faster.

Stress-free too.

Just because you spend weeks on something doesn't make it ART.

Just because you spend weeks on something doesn't make it BETTER.

Quantity isn't what's affecting your quality.

Some people are just faster than others at making amazing things.

But wherever you see repeated success, it's not happening by accident.

It's time for you to create what looks like luck to other people too…

Understand that if you can make something of quality once... Then with some practice and the right thinking, you can eventually make something of equal quality even FASTER next time.

How do you get there?

Let get into it.

THE DIFFERENCE BETWEEN ART AND CONTENT IS... INTENT

Content is created:

to put something out there

because you have to

for your boss

because you're bored

to get attention

Art is created:

for self-expression

to make people think

to say what can't be said in other forms of communication

to move our culture forward

So make sure you know WHY you're creating.

Content is created FOR:

"everybody"

the mainstream

the lowest common denominator

whoever will pay attention

Art is created FOR:

"your people"

those who have "gone through the same thing."

a community

The moment you know WHY you're creating this work and WHO you're creating it for... YOU HAVE ALREADY HELPED YOUR SPEED.

Now you'll be able to toss out ideas that don't work. And you'll be able to see all the promising concepts that might have been otherwise lost.

You have a filter to put everything through.

This step is easy.

Create what you want to create a few times with a notepad at your side. Create at your regular speed. But take note of how long it takes for you to do each step.

Figure out your current average speed for every step it takes to bring your work to completion..

Steps like...

Whether you're creating a podcast, writing a blog post, making a video, writing a song... Break the process down into the smallest possible components. Micro-steps if you can. (This will be important for later)

Don't do this from memory.

Figure out the real times it takes you to do things. Including where you need breaks etc.

Go through your whole process a few times until you're confident with the steps and the times allocated for each.

Society will have you believe that you have to be unorganized, flaky, and "all over the place" to be an artist.

And that only out of chaos can inspiration come.

If you hate structure, make sure you master this step before moving on. Step into your shadow self on this one.

Write out your linear schedule with EVERY SINGLE STEP it takes to bring your art to completion. (You think you have it all in your head? Write it down anyway.)

And next to every step, add the amount of time it takes on your worst day.

Create your next work by looking at this schedule. Respect the times you set wrote out. You're not trying to get faster yet. You're just getting used to thinking of your process like a film producer who's looking at her watch, keeping things "rolling" and "on time".

Your only goal is to become a finisher now. Your "perfectionism" is only allowed WITHIN THE ALLOCATED TIMEFRAME. Once time is up, you have to move on. Keep the clock visible so it keeps you focused.

So if you wrote down that it usually takes 5 hours to come up with lyrics. You only get 5 hours. If they're not perfect after 5 hours. Tough. Keep going.

Learn to get comfortable within these reasonable hours that you set for yourself.

Remember, these times are based on analyzing your performance! So it shouldn't be THAT hard. The only thing that's making it "hard" is that you're on a schedule now. And maybe that's freaking you out. Get over it.

Up until this point, we haven't created SPEED yet.

All we have is the foundation and structure for you to build on.

If you skip creating this foundation because you think you're "better than that" or because you're "experienced enough, "... You're setting yourself up for failure.

Failure = non-sustainable creativity.

No structure is why you always burn out after a few weeks.

To recap those crucial steps, you might arrogantly or stubbornly want to ignore...

1. Figure out why you're creating and who you're creating for.

2. Figure out how long it takes you to do every micro-step of your process from beginning to end (by actually doing it - don't guess, don't "imagine", DO it) and WRITE IT ALL DOWN.

3. Practice creating while following the map/times you've written out to get you used to "factory mode".

Once you've done all of this, you're ready to reap the rewards of the next phase.

Here are the 8 techniques that will make you faster...

Don't brush this off. This is accurate AF.

Approach every day like what you're going to do is easy. Because if you've broken down the steps enough, it should be easy.

Once I've set up my schedule, it never occurs to me that I may "fail".

I may forget to shower... But "fail"? As if.

Writing lyrics, starting a painting, writing 1,000 words, taking pictures... They all become as easy as salting fries in the shape of an 'M'.

Some day's results are better than others, but it's never HARD.

Create a list that tells you what to do next so you literally don’t have to think. It should be right next to you. It acts as your hardcore production manager taking you from task to tasks and making you complete each one on time.

MAKE THIS LIST THE NIGHT BEFORE so you hit the ground running in the morning!

It's okay to do tasks out of order. Just because there's a linear process, doesn’t mean that you have to stick to it. It's like when they shoot big Hollywood movies out of sequence. Create your list so that the BEST thing comes next. Best according to energy/resource levels. For example: I'd suggest doing the hardest things first in the day... And fun things after lunch etc.

Remember... There are two big energy leaks you have to beware of in creativity:

1. Overstaying your welcome with a step. (Keep it moving!)

2. Fiddling about in-between steps because you're wondering what to do next.

Those days are over now.

Isolate the parts of your process that are taking too long.

Use daily practice to work on that one part. (If editing pictures is taking too long. Use daily practice to practice editing until it's like breathing to you.)

Use daily practice to create volume (if coming up with ideas is what takes long, then use daily practice to come up with ideas. That way, when it's time for that part of the process next time, you have tons to draw from.)

Consider handing off this task to someone else who can do it faster than you.

Make Day 1 of your process as organic as possible.

Write things out long-form. Diagram and sketch things out by hand.

For just this first day... (Or the first few hours if your process is shorter)... Stay away from your computer and phone.

You're making art. This keeps your ideas connected to your soul for as long as possible.

Even Peter McKinnon, who says he hated the idea of paper and pen, now SWEARS by it. He put aside his comfort zone and stubborn beliefs and was gifted a whole new way of doing things.

Artists get thrown off their productivity game because they're usually all or nothing. (It's really just a disguised procrastination method.)

The moment they don't have 4 hours to paint... They don't paint at all. Or if they don't have a whole day to create music... They don't make music at all.

But if you only have 30 minutes, why not use this time to test mixing colors? Or to make new sketches?

That's where the magic of knowing your STEPS intimately pays off.

Move the steps around to accommodate a hectic "real life" schedule.

Dentist appoint?

Why not use the waiting room time to do writing research?

Already have your research for this week done?

Research the NEXT piece. That way, you have a head start.

Using this technique will make you a fcking creativity machine in no time. And it's especially good for days when you feel "slow".

Schedule one day only for "regrouping". A whole day where as soon as you wake up you know it's all about throwing things against the wall.

This is essential for "sustainable creativity".

Have a "fun day" that's only for generating new ideas, learning new equipment, or mastering new techniques.

It's incredible how everything that you will do on this "wasted" day will turn up as the saving grace on the next project you're working on. Thank me later. It happens every time.

If you're creating art that takes multiple days to make, you should take sleep very seriously.

Getting 8 Hours of sleep will make you faster.

Sleep = Better memory

Sleep = Focus

Sleep = Seeing more connections between ideas.

All those things make you faster and more creative.

Sleep is a performance enhancer.

Our culture has brainwashed us into thinking that there’s a trade off between sleep and productivity. It's the opposite. Sleep is a powerful tool to help productivity-- Especially creative productivity.

BONUS: It's been proven that the 7th hour of an 8-hour sleep cycle is the one that helps creativity the most by remixing subconscious thought and handing the results to conscious thought.

Soon you'll be waking up with new ideas.

Have a system for gathering ideas no matter where you are. At dinner, at the airport, driving... Make sure you have a way of collecting those ideas immediately.

Make yourself available to inspiration 100% of the time.

That way, when you go to create your new piece... Or continue on to the next step of your process... You never have to force things. Your moves are always coming from an inspired source.

I still can't believe that people don't keep a folder or notebook of ideas.

You're not trying to get everything to be a masterpiece.

That wouldn't be possible even if you only created one thing a year.

What you're trying to do is get it so that everything you create is at least at your bar of quality.

Some pieces will be better than others.

But every one of them will be memorable.

None of them will be trash.

And once in a while... One will be GENIUS!

That's the case with Emma Chamberlain, Drake, Christopher Nolan, Virgil, Rupi Kaur, and everyone else that releases work on a regular schedule.

We all have our favorites from what they've released.

Some are better than others. That's the name of the game.

But everything they release is always of a certain quality because they've mastered their process.

And now it's time for you to master yours too.

Your role as an artist is to drop bombs. Your role is to release work that affects people. Work that gets people thinking. Or that makes them reassess how they live their daily lives. Or that challenges what they believe is "possible". Keep dropping bombs until you create bigger and bigger explosions. The more bombs you drop, the more chances you have of one of them being "atomic".

But wait. I said there were 8 techniques to help you improve your speed, didn't I...

Well, the last one is so important I gave it it's own module:

NEXT:The Mystery Formula

### 6. The Make Art Not Content Podcast = 'The Mystery Formula' In Practice

This was my first attempt at creating a new style of podcast which eventually became 'The Make Art Not Content' podcast. This episode was never released outside of The Mystery School. But I wanted to leave it here so you can see this iteration on my way to finding the vibe of the podcast.

I didn't have a "dream" to make a podcast.

I had a goal.

I heard my friend Carmela's podcast and I asked her how to do it.

And then I iterated with every release.

I'm still iterating.

The only time I "overthink" the podcast is when I'm looking at the listener data and wondering how I can make the next one even better next week.

"What can I talk about that will stop creatives from stop procrastinating and start taking steps to accomplishing their goals?"

Listen To My First Attempt At Podcasting:

There's a great passage in'The Alchemist'where the boy is leaving the glass shop to continue his journey, and he asks the old man why he never pursued his dreams. And the old man says:

"Because I wanted them to remain my dreams."

Everyone has dreams.

But the aspiring artist, has to decide at some point, which of those dreams is worth pursuing.

And at that point, you stop calling them dreams.

You call them GOALS so that the universe understands your intention.

You see, dreams don't ever have to be attained. They exist as a sort of spiritual entertainment. They keep you warm on long drives. They're something to talk about over beers.

But goals... Those are the fulfillment of your potential.

Goals require a commitment.

But best of all, they give your life meaning.

Once you identify them... They become worth fighting for.

"Goals are Dreams with a deadline." Napoleon Hill

If you don't figure out which of your dreams that you want to turn into your goal... Then you will keep dreaming while you work your life away -- fulfilling someone else's goals.

Goals are the things that your working on in your life that you're making sure come to fruition.

You have to be in relentless pursuit of your goal.

You have to wake up with your goal at the forefront of your mind.

And never wanna sleep because you're too excited.

Your goals should be the only thing that no one can ever fuck with. When they'll say you're "going too far", you'll smile and tell them you're just committed.

Eventually even complete strangers will know what your goal is. It'll be like it's tattooed your forehead.

You'll organize your leisure time around it.

You'll chose eating habits that help you attain them.

Everyone that who knows you, will know what you're trying to achieve. And they'll try to help you achieve it -- Especially when they don’t have goals of their own.

### 7. The Five Stages Of Commitment (Babe, Passion Is Only #3)

There are five stages of commitment.

'Interested' is stage #1

'Desire' is the second stage.

'Passion' is the third stage of commitment.

Ah, passion.

Culture has us brainwashed that passion is everything.

But you can't sustain passion.

It wasn't designed for that.

One moment you're passionate about something... The next moment you're passionate about something else. And on and on it goes.

The world is full of people who started out with passion.

Some kept the passion up for long enough to develop some skills. They turned those skills into a job. They did good. Then they died.

But no one remembers people who had passion.

They don't make statues of people who had passion.

The ones that end up standing out from the crowd? They've transcended that level.

They evolve to the FOURTH stage of commitment:

When you're obsessed, your goal is the first thing you think about when you wake up and the last thing you think about when you go to sleep.

The object of your obsession even appears in your dreams.

It's annoying sometimes, I admit.

This lifestyle is not for everybody.

That's why before you consider taking this road, ask yourself:

Yes, I know... All your heroes were obsessed.

They were willing to sacrifice their personal lives, their health, balanced meals, Game Of Thrones season finales and "cute relationships"... all in the pursuit of their goals. So that's why I have to ask you once again...

You know you've found your "calling" when people think you've gone crazy.

To them, you are unpredictable. Unrecognizable.

They call you a genius but stop inviting you to the movies anymore because you'll probably derail the night into another one of your adventures.

That's why I urge you to think this through.

Leading a life of "passion" is so much easier!

It's more socially acceptable too.

You can be passionate and still go on ski trips with the family.

You can be passionate and still clock out 'cause it's "date night".

But obsession is uncomfortable.

The sort of "uncomfortable" that has led to otherwise normal human beings do incredible things like finding cures to horrible diseases...

Or revolutionizing the state of music.

Or overthrowing whole governments.

Or leave behind 64,000 works of art.

But people don't like the word "obsession".

It triggers them.

They prefer middle-of-the-road words like "moderation".

And then they quote articles from other semi-passionate people about work/life balance.

They say obsession is unhealthy behavior.

But the way I see it.. Creatives out there are ALREADY obsessed.

They're just obsessed with all the wrong things.

Things that are destroying their lives.

Things that don't matter.

They've practically made it a religion.

I mean... Am I wrong?

That's why you reach for your phone every two minutes.

That's why you have anxiety.

And you think these obsessions are perfectly ok. And why? Because we live in a world where "everyone else is doing it".

Even if the reality is:

It's slowly killing you on the inside.

But the kind of obsession that I'm talking about, and want for you... Is way healthier than the bullshit they subscribe to.

I want you to direct your obsession towards "expressing your unique voice".

I want you to get so focused on your unique journey that you can no longer hear the negative influences that are crowding your headspace.

I want you to start being the total embodiment of your values and your beliefs.

Yes, I want you to have the kind of obsession that can SELF-GENERATE ENERGY for you to go on for hours…

aka God Momentum

The kind of energy you exude when you know that what you're doing matters.

Obsession where every fiber of your being is dedicated to your mission.

Obsession where you see creativity in everything. And you act on it right away.

You've been operating at the passion level for your whole life.

Now it's time for you to evolve to a new level.

Directing all your thoughts towards one thing.

Systematically and consciously.

When you focus on taking daily steps on a singular path... All the atoms of life start congregating in that direction to assist you.

But you'll have to put energy out there consistently before you'll begin to see any results.

Don't be like a child who keeps unearthing the garden to see if the seeds are growing.

Be patient.

Have faith in the process, and in the laws of the universe.

They haven't failed anyone else who follows them.

So why would they fail you?

The reason people don't achieve their "goals"? Because they don't do what they "love" with obsession.

They do it with passion.

But they eventually find the repetition boring.

And then eventually find "being consistent" tiring.

So they do what they "love" with passion once a month and then wonder why nothing is changing.

While you can be passionate about many things in life...

You can only be obsessed with one.

Passion affords you the luxury of time.

Obsession does not.

Passion is influenced by what "you're feeling that day".

Obsession knows it's got a job to do either way.

Passion is that thing you talk about while you're doing something else.

Obsession is that thing you do and sorry you "don't have time to talk".

Passion is a temporary state of mind.

Obsession is a lifestyle.

When you find that every conversation you have and book you read relates back to your mission...

You're obsessed.

When you're ready to work on your goal even on weekends, on birthdays, anniversaries and even Christmas...

You're obsessed.

The only people who will understand you?

Other obsessed people.

So tell me...

Where do you fit in?

Those "goals" that you've been talking about for the past few months...

The one's that you keep putting off, and putting off, and putting off again...

Are they your passion?

Or are they your obsession?

Oh, and yeah...

I almost forgot:

The FIFTH stage of commitment.

Yes, there is a stage more intense than obsession.

A rare altitude that's granted to only a few.

I include it here for the sake of completeness...

But it's probably not for you, no offense.

It's the closest seat to God.

The 5th stage of commitment is...

It's when you're completely possessed by your purpose just like that girl in The Exorcist was by the devil.

You barf green lava on all your haters.

Family, friends try and fail to calm you down.

Institutions try to rid you of your demons because your attitude threatens the status quo.

But nothing can stop you.

Even mortality isn't an obstacle.

You know that you have a gift to return to humankind.

It's when your goal has captured YOU.

You have no choice in the matter anymore.

Your purpose is in your DNA.

G.O.A.T.s are the only one's who operate at that level.

It's not a lifestyle you choose.

It chooses you.

### 8. God Momentum (Part I): What Is It?

In the previous module you learned about Daily Practice.

The Daily Practice is 15 minutes to 1 hour a day of something you get better at. Then you go on with your life etc.. until the next day same time, same thing, every day.

Daily Practice is the minimum.

But God Momentum...

God Momentum takes over most of your day and requires energy.

God Momentum is when you're ready to make art your life.

People have it wrong. They think "motivation" can kick them into gear.

The problem is... Motivation and willpower require a tremendous amount of energy. And because of this most people can't rely on those energies to get things done "day in, day out".

Increasing your momentum is the better way towards success.

Momentum uses EXISTING energy to manufacture MORE of it.

How do you get on that kind of roll?

There are two ways to gain momentum.

One is by increasing your energy.

Everyone goes down that route.

They'll even try diets and take pills to bio-hack their way to success.

But there's another other way that's much less popular.

And ironically, it's the easiest to do.

If you can put yourself through 30 days of violent daily action. If you can commit to that, you can completely change your future.

Focused relentless daily action gets you to a point where your energy start to feed itself.

The more you act, the more you wanna act. The action is will be it's own reward.

Energy begets energy.

You won't need "discipline" or "willpower". Objects in motion stay in motion.

The second way of gaining momentum is by reducing friction

Until you get that “hockey stick”-like momentum.

Once you have speed that has no friction, you have achieved God Momentum.

God Momentum is the snowball effect where working hard becomes easy.

God Momentum is when you've been explosive for so many days in a row that NOT being explosive feels weird. It’s when you no longer question waking up early, or saying "no" to some party this weekend etc... And even natural low energy days when you just don't feel "motivated" don't matter. This powerful force magically guides you to do it anyway.

You start dreaming about doing things that other people (and your former self) shy away from.

Synchronicity starts to happen... You find yourself being at the right place at the right time, and getting emails where people want to help you out of the blue... Why? Your energy is infectious.

Confirmation bias starts to happen... Because you've only been engaging in success-driven activities, now the world throws you all sorts of opportunities...

Energy begets energy.

A thing called "The Power Law" goes into effect and you start seeing exponential gains for even the smallest actions.

All that effort you made at the beginning... Now the same effort has compound interest results.

Your process of transformation becomes so beautiful to you that...

You HATE the idea of conflation.

Conflation is when you take something that happens over a long period of time and condense it so that it happens quicker.

Storytellers do it in movies and novels all the time so that the story is less boring.

It's like when they show a couple falling in love in a 20 second montage in a movie

Conflation is good in storytelling... but bad in the real life journey of achieving success.

In real life, progress happens slowly over time and when you start to feel its effects you're going to want to lean into it.

Even though when you tell the story later you’ll probably make it shorter. But when you experience it you'll want to feel every moment.

God Momentum is as exhilarating as sex.

The longer things take, the deeper and more meaningful they become.

But that doesn’t mean everything will take super long... It just means that everything has its process and you will come to enjoy and respect it.

Remember. That painting may have taken 30 minutes to create, but it’s the 3 days of hitting a wall before it "came pouring out" that made it possible.

Remember the British guys that won the rowing competition at the 2000 Sydney Olympics?

Do you know the story of how they managed to do it even though they were the least likely to win?

Their coach always asked the same question before every decision they had to make:

"Will it make the boat go faster?"

If a training regiment or a a diet regiment wasn't making the boat go faster it was abandoned.

They put everything through that filter

Everything was centered on increasing energy.

Is that burger bringing you closer to what you're trying to achieve? Or would you achieve more with a salad that keeps you metabolism running high for a few more hours of cognitive genius.

But the secret to God Momentum is reducing friction.

Is Instagram bringing you closer to what you're trying to achieve? Or did you just lose 3 hours and now feel like shit? Get rid of it

Stop hanging out with negative people. If they're going to be at the dinner, don't go.

Some people (including your own internal bad cop) will tell you that eliminating fun activities isn't really "living life". And that "You have to enjoy yourself sometimes too.

You've been "enjoying" yourself for years. Are you ready to WORK now?

Don't worry. This isn't forever.

You'll be in this mode few (memorable) years so you can live an extraordinary life that only 1% of the world gets to see

If you want that life... Then you have to pay the price that others have paid. And make the sacrifices that others have made.

But what those people saying "You have to live life sometimes" don't know is:

When you join this club... Of disciplined athletes, of prolific creators, of black excellence, and of women who run with wolves... You get to experience a side of life that is more rewarding than the humdrum life the majority is leading.

You'll be happy to leave all those ordinary things behind

But a word of warning to you. No matter how many Mystery School modules you read...

And no matter how many inspiring emails you absorb...

You'll never get God Momentum without those first 21 days of violently focused action. There's no way around it.

That's when everything I've been saying will take on new meaning.

You're standing at the door today.

And it looks like you've been standing on the porch pacing... Wondering if you should ring the bell?

You should.

This is my invitation for you to come in.

LISTEN TO THIS:

(Ant Chamberlain, a 21 year old musician explains how if you don't reach your goals it's because you're not ready to adopt the 'military mindset' that's needed)

### 8. God Momentum (Part I): What Is It?
