### 9. God Momentum (Part II): How To Achieve It

EVERY TIME YOU FEEL LIKE YOU'RE LOSING ENERGY... COME BACK TO THIS PAGE! ...Remind yourself of what you should be doing to get it back.

When you wake up, you start with 100 points of energy.

As the day goes on there are things that will steal your energy and there are things that will increase your energy.

These are the 7 ENERGY STEALERS working against people trying to build a career or become G.O.A.T.s.

1. NEGATIVE RELATIONSHIPS (PEOPLE YOU LIVE WITH / WORK WITH)

2. WEAK BODY / WEAK MIND

3. JUNK FOOD & ALCOHOL

4. YOUR PHONE (SOCIAL MEDIA / TEXTS / TIKTOK)

5. PORN / MASTURBATION

6. NETFLIX / VIDEO GAMES

7. PARTYING

All of these things have their place in regular pedestrian life.

But if any of these things are distracting you from doing important things that will help you achieve your goals, then they're called: energy stealers.

Any activities you do that keep you away from the life you really want is really just an addiction. Deal with these addictions head on before you wake up one day with massive regrets, low self-esteem and no time or resources left to do anything about it.

As we learned in high school chemistry, nature hates a vacuum. So you can't just eliminate the bad things. That will create an uncomfortable void that is unsustainable in the long run. You have to fill the space with new, creative, and attractive activities that bring you towards your goals.

There are certain activities available to you that will do more than "fill the void". They INCREASE your energy.

For every energy stealer there's an energy multiplier that you can fight against it with.

And the more you engage with these energy multipliers, the closer you get to God Momentum. Your goal is to reduce friction until the energy stealers become a non-issue.

30 days of violent daily action will get you that “hockey stick” momentum... God Momentum.

This is how you fight NEGATIVE RELATIONSHIPS (PEOPLE THAT YOU LIVE WITH / WORK WITH)

It's impossible to get momentum if you can't control your environment. And sometimes that's impossible to do because you're surrounded by people who seem make it their job to infect you with their negative energy, negative ideas or negative outlook on life. Sometimes maybe they don't even mean it. But it's just the way they are.

You have to protect yourself against these negative people.

Fighting temptation is too hard.

And the best way to do it is to stay "locked-in".

In the Social Network movie there are several depictions of what it looks like when coders do it. They have headphones on and they're in front of their computer focusing in on the task at hand.

If you want to get momentum, you're going to need to get locked-in especially when you're NOT working on your goals.

It's all those times in between being creative that's stealing your energy. People talking shit around you, and making you focus on other dumb things makes it nearly impossible for you to ramp into the zone when you finally want to get to work.

So control that in-between time. Get headphones so you can get locked-in.

Tune negative people out by putting headphones on CONSTANTLY and listening to audio books related to your goals (books are better than podcasts because they keep you in the same environment for longer. And because you can't finish a book in one sitting, the ideas linger in your subconscious when you stop for breaks. Or if you're more tactile, you can keep a pocket size book with you at all times, or on your phone or IPAD or whatever.

The best books to use are biographies and autobiographies: books about people who did great things! Self-help books are fine too. Anything that re-aligns your focus on what matters.

Have other people's energy building thoughts ringing in your head at all times.

You have to stay “locked in” for as long as possible. Every errand you run, put those headphones on. Use it as a shield. Most people won't interrupt you because you'll look busy. But of course, the people you know will try to get you out of it. It's funny how desperate they will be at first. They'll say anything to curve your attention. They just hate that your discipline reminds them that THEY'RE slacking. So they say things like: "You're being anti-social!" "You always have your headphones on!"

But as tempting as it will be... Don't tell them what you're doing. Just tell them you're "locked-in". Tell them you're "studying". Society views anyone that keeps others away from studying as assholes, so that should be all you need to say. Keep your 'negativity shield' up. If you tell people what you're doing, you won't gain the massive energy you could have from having your "secret".

The world looks different when you have headphones on.

Negative people seem more and more ridiculous.

But don't stop there.

Now it's time to surround yourself with people who are the opposite. Make friends with people who are motivated, disciplined, and on the same kind of God Momentum journey as you're on. People who will scheme with you on ways you can go harder. Someone that can be an "accountability partner".

You will slip back into old habits if you don’t isolate yourself from the world that's not on the same path as you.

Don’t talk about your goal (except to your confidantes).

Telling everyone what you're doing will dissipate it’s energy.

Grow the energy by keeping it to yourself.

THING AFTER THING LIST

Create a “head down” list of “thing after thing” that needs to be violently executed every night in preparation for tomorrow with headphones.

MAKE A MOODBOARD

Make a mood board of images representing what you’re trying to achieve.

Put these images wherever you spend most of your time.

Pick a new wallpaper for your phone.

This will help center your vision.

STACKING THE ODDS IN YOUR FAVOR: THE ULYSSES STORY

I love the story of Ulysses.

His ship was about to go by The Island Of Beautiful Sirens. Sirens are hot women with voices so enchanting that if you hear them sing, you will plunge to your death trying to reach them.

So Ulysses gets the idea of having his crew tie him to the mast so he can still hear the singing, but not be able to leave the boat. He orders them that no matter what he says, do not untie him until they've made it safely past the Siren Island.

So they tie him up. The crew puts their earplugs. And then the music starts. And he sees their stunning beauty. Ulysses is so enchanted by the music and by their charm that he gets rope burn trying to get himself loose.

But he can't.

Luckily for him, he hears the singing, he sees their beauty, but doesn't die.

That's what YOU gotta do. Tie yourself to your boat. No matter how sweet the distractions are around you, stay locked in to your goals.

Mindset is everything, true.

But if you don't take care of your body, your mind won't have the resources to help you like it could.

The mind / body relationship is the most crucial denominator of success. The better you feel, the more ideas you get, the more energy you have, the more you do.

In science, it's called "the psychosomatic relationship".

And the best remedy for mental health is physical activity.

But don't fool yourself into thinking you can put later in the day. The best time to do it is first thing in the morning. That needs to be the first fight that you win. Or else you won't do it.

Remember, you start out with 100 points of energy when you wake up. But, there are certain activities (we'll see more later) that increase those points. Think of them as "extra lives" in a video game.

When you work out in the morning you increase your energy by an extra 20 points that you'll be able to use to do even more later.

Physical excercise.

You can run.

You can go to the gym. Weights, cardio...

You can do yoga.

TRY INTERVAL TRAINING FOR CREATIVES (33 MINUTES)

This one is for the really intense creatives out there.

What you do is you set a timer for 33 minutes. You work non-stop for those 33 minutes. And during that time you're not allowed to touch your phone. You have to be LOCKED-IN. You can only work on the task at hand. When the timer goes off you get to take a break for 10 mintues. But, you HAVE to stop right away. You do 10 push ups or 30 sit-ups. Drink water. Check your phone. Do this interval training all morning and see if you don't feel amazing at the end of it!

DEEP BREATHING FIRST THING IN THE MORNING

"Deep breathing" means from your diaphragm.

When you breath in, make your stomach expand like a balloon. This is how you know you're doing it right.

Use a 2-2-4 sequence. Inhale for a count of 2.

Hold it for a count of 2.

And exhale for a count of 4.

Every time you go around the cycle you'll feel like you're getting access to a little more lung, bit by bit.

This type of breathing activates the lymphatic system.

You know what the lymphatic system does?

It carries your white blood cells.

Do you know what white blood cells are for?

You guessed it.

Fighting disease.

And you can't afford to get sick because that will break your momentum. So use prevention. Deep breathing is part of your prevention routine.

SHORT NAILS

So is grooming your nails. Make sure they're short so you're not carrying bacteria.

WASH YOUR HANDS

So is washing your hands. Haven't you learned anything from COVID-19?

In "the west" we don’t reward prevention. Instead we reward band aids solutions for when people fuck up. Step outside that thinking.

You don't have time to get sick. Make the right moves.

Treat achieving your goals like you're an athlete.

GET A GOOD CHAIR

Having the right chair will make you be able to work for longer days, and for months at a time while keeping your body aligned. We're in this for the marathon. Have the right tools.

It's time for you to stop treating food as entertainment.

In this period of your life, you need to treat food as what it actually is:

Your source of energy and nutrition.

Carbohydrates, for example, will kill you. They definitely don't "make the boat go faster"? They make you sluggish especially in the afternoon.

When you look at what you're planning for breakfast, avoid sugar.

Don't just eat to "not be hungry". Food is your fuel. Choose foods that will give you fuel.

And notice I used the word "planning"?

If you don't plan your food, you'll eat poorly.

Some things are just too basic.

Drink water. Ok?

I know. It's boring. But all you have to do is put water in your environment. It’s funny. When it’s on your work desk, you just tend to drink it. It just happens.

How much water should you be drinking? Until your pee is clear every time you go to the bathroom.

I recommend Rooibus tea, because it's high in anti-oxidents and has zero caffeine.

GINGER / GARLIC CLEANSES

Add garlic and ginger to your diet.

All it takes is to slice it up and add it as a side with whatever you're eating. Garlic with protein is so good. Ginger with fish or fruits is tasty.

Don't just eat it. Plan it in advance, and treat the consumption of garlic and ginger like it's a cleanse!

You know I love tequila. I do. But during a period of self-discipline... Alcohol a momentum killer.

That's just too high a price to pay when you're in 'Mamba Mode'.

INTERMITTENT FASTING

Do a one day fast with nothing but tea while you work. It'll make you sharp. It'll also start to change your relationship with food because you'll learn not to give your body instant gratification.

All these new rituals will make discipline seem like fun instead of hard work,

This is easily where everyone loses the most energy.

This is not a battle you can win. These apps are constructed to addict you. Your only hope is to keep them away from you for as long as possible in a day. You shouldn't check email, Instagram, tiktok, or text on your phone until noon. If you're especially strong... Don't check until 6pm. AFTER you've done all your work of the day. It's too risky. Your phone can change your mood too easily. And three hours later... Nothings done.

Don't allow the outer world's "control dramas" to take over your mind.

Put the phone very far away from your environment. Remember, the first rule is to protect your environment. Put that grenade far away from it. Somwhere where you have to make an effort to get it.

Even better: Give it to someone to keep for you until later in the day.

"BUT WHAT IF I NEED TO GET SOME INFORMATION ON INSTAGRAM OR SOMETHING? CAN I HOP ON FOR 2 SECONDS?"

Don't break your social media "fasting" for anything.

Make a note to get the information or communicate with whoever later.

Let yourself suffer so that the next time you don't "forget" to accomplish everything you need to do in your social media freedom hours.

Sexual energy is so powerful that if you don't use it to your advantage, you're really missing out.

There's a reason boxers abstain from sex when they're training for a fight. The last thing you want to do is diminish your drive.

No, instead use "sex transmutation" to put that energy to work for your achieving your goals.

Let it build inside you, but let it cum out of your most powerful work ever. People will feel that there's an intensity to what you do.

Don't tell them your secret.

'Moments Of Zero' are seemingly simple boring activities that give you incalculable energy.

WORKING OUT (Mentioned above)

READING (Mentioned above):8 BOOKS TO BUILD ENERGY

As convenient as it is to read on a mobile device-- The best way to read for re-connecting to yourself is by reading the physical book. If you prefer to read audiobooks... Don't do anything else while you're listening for maximal benefit.

20 minutes of meditation every day has a cumulative effect of increased energy. It sucks because you will only start to feel it's effect after you've been doing it for more than 10 days straight, but when you do...!!

"It's not for me..." If you say that, it's probably because you have some idea in your head of the "correct" way to meditate, and you're not into doing it that way.

Let me tell you all that meditation really is...

You don't need to read a 250 page book to understand meditation.

It's simple.

It's when you stop.

All you have to do is stop and smell the roses-- Until you're not thinking of the past or the future. Smell the roses where you are right now. If you're doing that... You're meditating. Don't let people fool you into thinking it's more complicated than that.

Stop for 20 minutes a day.

Learn to be with yourself for those 20 minutes.

And do nothing.

If thoughts appear, just watch them passively. Let yourself not give a fuck.

After you get good sitting with yourself for 20 minutes, you start to see the benefits.

Meditation expands your energy so that your vibrations extend beyond your aura. It's powerful. But it's silently powerful. It will give you charisma. When people say "I like that person's energy..." Chances are the person being appreciated has some sort of meditative process in their life. Meditation is the fastest track to the kind of powerful temperament that others feel. Meditation will heal your addiction to noise. And eventually, your mere presence will do it for others around you too.

WARNING: This "stupidly easy" activity is, for some reason, the hardest thing in the world for people to do.

It hurts at first, because your ego will think "This is boring."

But, I'm telling you... If you're brave enough to get past your ego's chatter...

Ahhhhh.... THE BENEFITS!

So meditate... Then work out.

Or work out... Then meditate.

You will have energy to burn and laser focus that may burn a hole through your computer or your canvas.

GO HERE FOR A WHOLE MODULE ON GETTING THE MOST OUT OF MEDITATION (MADE FOR CREATIVES IN MIND)

LISTENING TO MUSIC

LEARNING SOMETHING NEW

Whatever your profession is... You have to keep giving yourself new ideas. Your 'inputs' are important.

TAKE A WALK OUTSIDE

How many writers, entrepreneurs, and artists have credited their genius ideas to that one time they took a walk and it "popped into their head"...

Gathering your thoughts clears the way for newer more constructive thoughts.

Most people go around in a loop in their head thinking the same thing over and over again.

But that's not likely to happen on paper.

That's why journaling is so powerful.

When you put down all your thoughts, it'll feel like you're "taking out the trash".

Write on paper instead of into your computers. There's energy in handwriting. On a computer all you have is the words.

TAKING A MOMENT TO FEEL GRATITUDE

Taking a moment (especially at the end of the day) to reflect on everything that's positive in your life is essential to re-aligning your perspective. Think of all the things around you that "give you life". Who are you grateful to have in your life right now. What things are going in the right direction in your career? What advantages do you have that others don't?

Try to think deeply on those questions until you get lost in them. Feel all your blessings deeply.

Daily switching to a perspective of gratitude will postpone burnout... forever.

What eventually emerges when you engage in as many 'Moments Of Zero' as possible is something quite beautiful...

Something you maybe haven't encountered in a long while...

Your real thoughts.

Your real genius.

Your real creativity.

But you need to give it the space and the time to appear.

You haven't been living life to the fullest. You've been living life on automatic.

But when you can quiet yourself inside... Even when you go to a party, or a concert or a protest, you will be bring a quiet strength and energy to it that will impact the whole outside environment.

In 'God Momentum' mode, SLEEP is the antidote to PARTYING.

It is non-negotiable.

You go to bed at the same time every night. You wake up 7-9 hours later.

If you live with people, the earlier your sleeping block the better. That way you're active before other people around you are. It's easier to focus when everyone else is still sleeping.

There are two ways to achieve momentum. One is by going faster. But there's another way that requires way less energy...

Removing friction.

Waking up early falls under the "removing friction" category. No one can bother you if they're sleeping. So use this to your advantage.

Your morning starts the night before.

Plan the next day, the night before, so you hit the ground running.

You don’t want to waste any of that precious morning energy on “planning”. Are you crazy? That’s like driving a sports car in traffic.

Create a “head down” list. A list of “thing after thing” that needs to be violently executed the next day before you ever take a second to look up.

Sleep enough (between 7-9 hours of sleep). But also make sure that you don't oversleep (that weakens your body and kills your energy).

Getting sleep = more creativty.

You create more connections between things in that magic process that happens overnight.

Sleep is a performance enhancer.

Our culture has brainwashed us into thinking that there’s a trade off between sleep and productivity. It's the opposite. Sleep is a powerful tool to help productivity-- Especially creative productivity.

Become part of The Mystery School Sleep Elite: the ones who use sleep as their secret weapon for endless creativity.

You can take my word for it, or you can fail and then you'll know for the next time you try to master your discipline.

Wake up at the same time every day.

Go to bed at the same time every night.

Sound boring?

So is the unproductive routine you're in now where you're pissing your life away.

Give yourself the gift of God Momentum.

And make the next few months a journey to mastering the art of discipline once and for all.

But maybe you should make sure you can handle it by peeking at how intense it will be first?

### 10. God Momentum (Part III): The 21-Day Challenge

If you've never done anything like this before, I'd suggest you start with having aDaily Practicefirst. The God Momentum challenge is about having discipline all day, every day. It's a lot to handle all at once.Daily Practiceis about carving out discipline for one hour a day without ever missing a day. Master that first. Don't let this be an ego thing. Like "I'm cool enough to do God Momentum. I don't need to start with baby steps.". This isn't about being cool. And what you're calling "baby steps" is a game changer for everyone that does it. TBH, if you're here to make creativity you life-long mission... You won't be interested in skipping steps. You'll be more concerned with how to raise your self-esteem and use these insurance policies so that you stop falling into your old patterns of failure.Daily Practiceis how you guard against this.

I get emails and DMs like this one every week (let's avoid it ok?):

The problem with discipline is that the person with the all the big goals at 7pm the night before is not same person you're dealing with at 5am next morning.

So you have to go to war.

And I suggest that you don't bring a knife to a gunfight.

I personally prefer to bring a tank.

Everyone is always like "yeah, yeah, I'll be good. I can do it." But I know that's a lie. I never trust myself.

That's why I stack the odds in favor of my 7pm self.

I make it impossible to choose any other option than the one I decided on when I was my best self.

I create an atmosphere for the 5am version of myself to succeed.

Tell everyone around you (people that want you to win) what you're going to do. Especially people who won't let you live it down. This is using the principle of accountability. You don't Just let them know that your habits are changing, so that you if you go back to your slacker ways you're disappoint them too.

Planning means:

Put your clothes out in preparation. If you're working out then I put out your work clothes, with your heart rate monitor and your deodorant skipping rope.

Planning means:

Put your alarm somewhere in the room where you have to get up to turn it off. This prevents the endless snoozing that could happen (especially if you're hit with self-sabotaging insomnia that will make you extra tired the next day).

Planning means

After you're up... You put your cell phone (ringer off) somewhere you can't see it until you've done all your work of the day.

Ok let's plan for real...

Write down your goal as a simple sentence containing 2 things:

"I will have a ripped body in 3 months."

"I will finish my poetry book and find a publisher by the end of summer."

"I will produce 2 new songs a week"

It's amazing to me how many people think they can get things done by winging it. "I don't need to write things down. It's all in my head." Is exactly what people say who have no discipline. That's what you say when you don't want to be ACCOUNTABLE.

In this section, you will do what every successful person has done before you:

Write down the schedule of what you'll be doing every day so that you can see what you're committing to.

And so that your accountability partner can see what you're committing to also.

You make it real by writing it down.

For the next 21 days you’re going to act like that person every day.

By the end of it you will see true progress towards being that person when you look in the mirror.

Define who you’re trying to become.

Make a list of all the repetitive (and potentially boring) DAILY tasks that this person would do-- that you don’t do right now.

Those repetitive tasts are what will make you become the G.O.A.T.

Repetitive actions change the shape of your brain. It's called Neuroplasticity.

That's why you keep checking your phone. You hard-wired it.

You need to unlearn those old habits that stop you from growing.

And develop new ones that will help you ascend.

If you want to have high output-- You have to thoroughly embrace routine.

Steven King has a great passage in his book "On Writing". He talks about how you have to "meet the devil (creativity) at the same time and place every day. That way it knows where to meet you." Eventually, you'll find him waiting for you there when you arrive.

That's the power of routine.

Find it boring? Some days it will be. Some days it won't be. Welcome to the life of a professional.

Here are the 7 things you need to clarify when you're making a schedule:

Get up earlier than everyone else (if you live with people) so you have alone time

In his book 'The 7 Habits Of Highly Effective People', Stephen Covey introduces the idea of "Important but not urgent".

"Important but not urgent" is the category of things you want to do in life that will make you feel like you have a good life. These things are more long-term.

"Important and urgent" is the category of things that stresses people out. There's often an outside force responsible. This is where you become the world's puppet and prioritize other people’s goals by being a slave to their emails, texts, and calls. Everyone does the "Important and urgent". And then you have no energy left for the non-urgent things that will move the needle for their happiness.

Solve that by STARTING YOUR DAY with "Important but not urgent".

And put the hardest things on your schedule at the beginning of the day.

Wake up earlier if you have to.

That way no matter what happens for the rest of the day... You will have invested time into your future.

If you don't have the luxury to put everything in the morning... Do this:

Figure out which activity has the most profound impact on achieving your goals.

Make that first every day.

Make sure your daily schedule has as little "context switching" as possible.

"Context switching" is every time you change to a new activity.

For example: Writing... And then cleaning your room... And then eating... That's two context switches.

Every time you change activities, you'll have to ramp up your energy to get you in the new zone. And every new activity you add in the day takes twice as much energy to ramp into as the last.

So, for profound results... Schedule your day with as little context switching as possible.

If you want to write a song, send some demos out to people, and work on your website. It's better to do large blocks of these on different days than to do small blocks of each for 3 days. Finish the song in one day. Organize the addresses, mail-out letters and package contents and go to UPS all the same day. Start and finish draft one of your website in one day.

What it ends up looking like is these very big blocks of doing ONE thing. That enables you to stay in the zone as long as possible, and will give you results that will surprise even you.

For things that require daily exposure, like practicing an instrument or going to the gym... Schedule these before or after your big block of achievement. And connect them to things you already do. Like after I shower, I will practice for an hour. Make it part of your daily routine.

IN THE BIG BLOCKS OF TIME YOU'VE DECIDED ON, YOU SHOULDN'T BE DOING ANYTHING ELSE BUT THE THING YOU'VE COMMITTED TO DO. NO EATING. NO PHONE. NO SOCIAL MEDIA. NO EMAILS. NO CONVERSATIONS. NOTHING ELSE. YOU HAVE TO STAY INSIDE THE ONE THING YOU'VE COMMITTED TO DOING FOR THE FULL BLOCK OF TIME NO MATTER WHAT. IF YOU'RE NOT INSPIRED, YOU STAY THERE ANYWAY-- UNTIL THE TIME RUNS OUT. THIS IS THE ART OF DISCIPLINE.

What is your daily reward for winning the day?

Pick something you love.

Mine is listening to music.

You take violent action, followed by purposeful rest.

Every relentless day has to have a daily reward for your accomplishment.

Leave yourself an hour of brainless activity. It's no secret that recuperation is just as important as the workout. It's part of the art of discipline. It will keep your momentum streak going.

Get in the habit of making a HEAD-DOWN LIST for yourself every day.What's that?It's a TODO list you execute IN ORDER without thought. A list to perform in "robot mode". A list where you do what must be done without hemming and hawing or wondering if you "feel like it" or not. Just STFU and execute the tasks one after another. Don't think this list is only about boring tasks like cleaning or laundry, though. I write HEAD-DOWN lists that include creative tasks all the time. The idea is to behave like a creativity machine. You will surprise yourself. Remove the ridiculous friction of overthinking everything.Key:I always have my HEAD DOWN LIST written out the night before. Even if I'm going to a party (cheat day) or I have a family dinner. I write my HEADS DOWN list early. Before I've even hopped into the shower to get ready, that way, when I wake up the following day, it's already there… Waiting for me. I'm ready to hit the ground running without wasting energy thinking of what to do first or next.Bonus:Having my plan written out before I go out makes me even more present when I'm out there being social. Because nothing's hanging over my head. I can let go and have fun.One warning:On regular days... Don't try to make your HEAD DOWN LIST right before you go to bed. You'll have low energy and try to rush it. Besides, right before bed is your "wind-down, clear your head" time. Write your list right after dinner instead. And don't forget to include 'making your list' in tomorrow's list, of course!

Cheat days are low impact days that happen at the end of your cycle. And they're crucial. Seeing that finish line as you work helps you work HARDER.

Cheat days are the days (decided in advance) where you break your discipline. YOU STILL WORK, but the rigid time schedules don't matter.

It's important to have this day when you burst the bubble of discipline. Just so you can WILLFULLY and quickly impose it again the next day.

That's how you show your mind who's boss.

You choose this day far in advance. Typically, by the time your cheat day arrives, you're so addicted to your new routine that you don't even wanna do it.

Do it anyways.

And then the next day...

Whip yourself back into action for the next 10-day journey (or whatever your personal 'extended circadian timeframe' is).

The only thing you can't cheat on a cheat day is your bedtime and planning the next day.

This needs to stay religious so that the next day is FIRE.

Cheat days are to wake up late, have a chocolate bar, and watch some youTube. NOT to go "full civilian".

Use 10 day planning cycles (or longer) to help you achieve your goal.

Break out of the "7 days in a week" societal pattern.

Your mind has a memory for your patterns beyond just daily sleep habits. I call it the "extended circadian rhythm". Your body knows what day of the week it is and secretes chemicals in you, to prepare for what it thinks is going to happen.

When you're building discipline and momentum you have to disrupt the "normal people" rhythm that you've been following all your life.

Impose a new rhythm to regain your mental power over these old physical processes.

Show your mind who's boss. While everyone slows down on Sunday, you'll still be hitting it hard. This will tell your body that something new is going on now. There's a new rhythm in town.

And when you finally get your "cheat day" on the 10th day (for example)... Everyone else will be going about their business as usual.

Another reminder to yourself that you're "on some other sh-t".

If you can... Do the real baller move and start the 21 days on a Friday morning.

People like to start challenges on Mondays and that's just some "set yourself up for failure" bullshit.

Start on the weekend and Monday will be day 4...!

Pushing your new discipline through the weekend will make you face all those slacker tendencies head-on.

Find a friend who has accomplished big goals before.

Show them the daily schedule you've set up for yourself.

Ask them if you're lowballing your potential.

Or if they think that you're setting yourself up for failure by reaching too high.

Once you have that...

Right now your schedule is only a hypothesis.

You don't KNOW if it's realistic yet.

That's why you need to practice your schedule for AT LEAST A WEEK before you start your journey. This will give you time to fine-tune it what you'll be doing for those up-coming 21 days.

I can't stress this preliminary practice enough.Not doing this is why 90% of artists will fail. Stay on this step until you have something sustainable.

Yes, I know... Your ego wants you to jump in right away. Your ego wants you to feel like you're "doing something". That way, you have something to brag about. But if you don't have the discipline to practice your workload, you won't have the discipline to keep going. You will run out of gas. You will fail. Just like every other time. If you want things to be different this time, DO THINGS DIFFERENTLY THIS TIME. Don't try toguesswhat your workload should be. TEST IT FIRST. Practice your schedule until it feels right. Then, and only then, start the countdown to the new you.

With every single day of intense productivity, you will learn something new about yourself.

It's the nature of pushing your limits.

So document this beautiful era of your life in graphic detail.

And the side benefit is... You will see your progress right there in front of you.

And guess what?

It will give you even more momentum (ENERGY MULTIPLIER).

So answer this question before reading on:

Where will you be keeping your journal? Online? A note pad?

Your mind is going to fight with you to the death in the first 3 days.

The first couple of days and a half should go fine, but somewhere between Day 2 and Day 3, when your mind realizes that this is for real it will create diversions.

"Why you doing this shit?"

And yes I'm speaking of your mind in the 3rd person because until you achieve discipline, the mind is a WHOLE OTHER PERSON to us. Trying to make it's own decisions. For so long it has been your master, so you didn't even notice. So when you try to make it your slave, believe me... It won't like that.

The easiest place to sabotage you at the beginning? Especially if you've committed to earlier mornings?

By keeping you awake at night it will give you reasons to rationalize sleeping in... So that all your hard work for the first few days can unravel.

That's why most people never make it past a week. They succumb to this rookie mistake.

Go to be at the same time every night.

Everyone dies right here: Because they had a "good day", they think they get to go to bed late.

They figure, if they're doing everything else right then sleep doesn't matter.

Sleep is 🔑.

Creativity is an alternation between the conscious and subconscious realms.

Nurture BOTH realms. Pride yourself on being disciplined with sleep.

LIGHTS OUT MEANS, LIGHTS OUT.

If you "can't sleep", lie there. As tempting as it is, don't get on your phone. Pay the consequences.

Focus on the thing you’ll be doing tomorrow as you fall asleep.

Insomnia is funny. You'll usually fall asleep one or two hours before you're supposed to wake up.

Wake up at the same time every morning.

This is the part that sucks. Because even if you've only had 30 minutes of sleep... Wake up anyways.

Even though it hurts.

Even though you feel groggy.

Even though you're about to have the worst day of your life.

Pay the consequences.

And tonight... Go to bed at your appointed time. NOT BEFORE, EVEN THOUGH YOU WILL WANT TO.

Pay the consequences.

Keep doing this routine until your mind obeys. (It usually only takes one night. Maximum three.)

With this kind of discipline, it'll be a while before the mind tries that trick on you again. (It'll come back between Day 12-15)

But you know why your insomnia will persist?

Because you haven't accepted the idea of PAYING THE CONSEQUENCES.

You'll get on your phone anyways.

Or you'll "sleep in" anyways. Instead of putting your alarm far away from you and super loud.

Or on your 2 hours of sleep day, you'll crash early instead of waiting for your official bedtime to arrive so that it reset your circadian rhythm.

Yes, you'll try to get away with doing less than what is required because you haven't accepted the idea of PAYING THE CONSEQUENCES.

Well until you do, your results will always be average.

Not just in this. But in your art as well.

Willpower as you will learn soon, is bullshit. When you achieve God Momentum, you don't need any willpower to do anything.

But right now?

It's all you can rely on.

That's why the first 10 days are so critical. Because you still have to "convince" your mind not to fall into your old habits. So make sure you'regoing crazy with the ENERGY MULTIPLIERS and avoiding the ENERGY STEALERS. 'Cause your willpower will be in short supply.

On day 11 when you shake your body and mind into submission by cracking the whip again after a cheat day... You will already feel the wisps of God Momentum setting upon you. A new coating of neurons will have been created on your brain. Where you start loving to do the thing that you used to procrastinate.

When you do things daily, you develop a muscle memory for them.

When you get back to your "thing" the next day, it'll be like you never left.

The body can miraculously remember-- and build on-- even a 10 minute activity that happened 24 hours ago.

So imagine what happens when you do an intense 6-hour block of sheer creativity every single day.

The only thing you have to conquer is "starting".

Starting is hard.

Continuing is never a problem. 'Cause you're like, "Might as well continue... Might as well do this 'goal' thing... Might as well get my gold star..."

The real muscle you're training is "starting".

You have to decide now:

Are you ok doing this even when it gets boring?

Because it’s gonna get boring.

There are these severe "down periods" that you’ll have to go through. That’s what discipline is. Getting through those repetitive times that are boring while everyone else is having fun.

You will go through these down periodsa few timesbefore you reach full God Momentum.

Are you anticipating this low? You better be.

No matter how good you feel today... You need to prepare yourself mentally and spiritually for this day.

Otherwise you'll get blind-sighted.

And you'll get shiny new object syndrome.

But, here's the secret that the people who quit will never know:

You feel amazing after you push through it.

You get a feeling of satisfaction that runs through you body knowing that you won the war against your weak mind and did what was required today.

And that's what makes the initial fire eventually come back.

Be ready for this.

They say it takes 21 days to create a new habit.

But what "they" DON'T tell you:

Is how hard it will be when you finally get to "Week 3".

The funny thing is it won't look hard.

Quite the opposite if you've done the first 14 days right.

It will FEEL easy breezy. You will have started achieving something thatlooks like momentum.

Yet this is exactly when people start planting their seeds of failure.

Before I tell you how to reverse engineer the powerful magnet that will try to pull you back into lameness this week... Let me explain why this tendency isn't even your fault.

Do you know about the law of 7?

It's a useful concept in numerology that anyone can use to their benefit. Don't worry, you don't have to believe in any of this touchy-feely stuff to use it.

It states that in any cycle divided into 7-- That on the 3rd and 7th spots there will be some kind of hurdle. Just like the spaces between the keys on a piano. The ones without the black keys (yes, they designed musical instruments that way because of these mathematical concepts).

For example that's why "hump day" sucks so much.

And why Sunday is such an energy transition point for, like, everybody.

So when you're undertaking any long project, you have to watch out for "Week Three".

This is the pivotal week where you can track the first seeds of failure even though in the moment you will feel like you're winning.

Here's how it usually plays out:

It's fun. You're finally doing it! Your only struggles are energy and fighting your old habits and "urges". But if you've designed your environment to succeed, it's actually a blast.

You've started getting regular. The new "project" you've started is starting to feel commonplace and familiar. People start to notice you're acting "different". They compliment you on your discipline. You get your first whisps of momentum.

But then Week 3 happens...

You get "cocky".

Remember how you had to beat that chattering mind down into submission during the first 3 days? Remember how it was trying to sabotage you with "insomnia". And how you fought back and won. Afterwards, it's mostly been quiet. If it showed up, you beat it down again like Wack-a-mole.

But what did you think? That it was gonna submit without coming back with new disguises?

In Week 3 your mind will come back at you harder than ever. It will arrive dressed up as your most irresistible weakness:

It will make you think you're "more disciplined than all those other losers".

It will make you forget the days where you sucked.

It will make you feel strong so that it may slowly wreak havok.

Your mind dressed up as ego will start convincing your that you’ve been going hard enough.

And the permissiveness will only get worse.

A downward spiral that anyone looking-in can easily see. But YOU will be oblivious to. If you have an accountability partner, tell them to look out for WEEK THREE.

Meahwhile... Those around you (that are invested in your failure) will smell blood. Your so called "friends" will encourage you to “take it easy”, “have a little fun”, “spend some time with us”...

All the forces of evil will start working against you.

And not long after that... You'll realize that you're not "into it" any more and you'll slip back to your old ways.

And you'll wonder what happened.

It was going so well.

"Week Three" is what happened.

If you did Week One and Week Two properly... "Week Three" is the bitch you gotta watch out for.

Understand that the good feeling you feel once you've reached Week Three is not God Momentum.

It's just a "good moment".

All momentum is made up of many smaller moments.

God Momentum is made up of hundreds.

And each one is to be celebrated, yes!

Including the feeling you feel right now.

But you should celebrate this powerful moment that comes over you during Week Three by doing a simple "trick" that will stop the forces of inertia from sabotaging you dead in your tracks.

ADD something.

That's right. When Week 3 starts, you raise the bar.

You use your own sabotaging mind against itself.

Now that it has made it's re-appearance as 'ego' you can use the occasion to put more kindle in the fire.

It's the only language that a pleasure-seeking monkey brain will be helpless against.

You have to challenge your inclinations by waging WAR AGAINST YOUR WEAK MIND.

Get more serious.

Kick sand in your ego's eyes.

Believe me... Everyone else... All over the world... Doing the "habit in 21 days" thing... When they get to Week Three... They will go in relaxing into their newfound routine... And that is precisely why they will fail.

It's right about this time where they will settle in bad new habits that will lead to their PLATEAU.

Habits that will have them convinced that they're going hard even when they're actually getting soft.

Until that dreaded day they wake up depressed 'cause "it's not working anymore".

They will be like when DJ Khaled was on the treadmill every day on Snapchat... But somehow never losing weight.

You know the secret now.

You will double down.

You will use the satisfaction you feel for having achieved the first 14 days... To propel you to upwards momentum.

Here's a lock-screen image to put on your phone to remind you every single time you wanna cheat and waste your time on Instagram (you might have to wait for it to load):

godmomentumLOCKSCREEN.png

John (mystery student) created it to help him stay "locked-in".

If you end up using it too...Send him a DM and thank him yourself.

But getting to GOD MOMENTUM takes more than 3 weeks, my friend.

God Momentum is when artistic FLOW becomes a way of life.

Prepare to change the course of your life with the next milestone...

### 10. God Momentum (Part III): The 21-Day Challenge

## Why You Need A Plan / The Multiple 'I's

## BUT SERIOUSLY... IF YOU CAN'T COMMIT TO SOMETHING FOR 21 DAYS, WHAT MAKES YOU THINK YOU'RE READY TO MAKE IT YOUR LIFE?

## WRITE DOWN YOUR GOAL (THE 'WHAT')

### 1. The ONE goal.

### 2. The timeframe it will take you to achieve it.

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: THE BASICS

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: REPETITION = SUCCESS

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: THE NITTY-GRITTY

### 1. What time will you wake up?

### 2. What time you will start each activity.

### 3. Where is it happening? (Try to make it "same place / same time" for each activity)

### 4. How long you will doing this activity. (You need to commit to a block of time to be able to measure progress.)

### 5. Write EXACTLY what you will be doing and how much of it you will expect to get accomplished? What KPIs (Key Performance Indicators) will you use to measure it? As creatives, we love to keep this loose. "Keeping it loose" is our built-in failure switch. Don't fall for it.Write down EXACTLY what you will be doing tomorrow and how much of it you expect to get accomplished. Put it in writing WHAT WOULD MAKE TOMORROW A PERFECT DAY.

### 6. What time will you go to sleep? This is just as important as what time you will wake up. All those trendy success magazines and YouTube videos always talk about the "wake up" times of successful people. But what's just as important (if not more) is bed-time. Most people can wake up early if they're passionate enough. It only takes a few days to re-adjust your basic circadian rhythm. But what's hard is forcing yourself to go to bed when you're still amped. Yet, this is the exact discipline which will allow you to do what you lovelonger than anybody else that's alive. If you don't set, and respect, your "LIGHTS OUT" just as if you were in the army... Well, in the long run... You will run out of steam, just like everyone else that 'tried discipline for a couple of weeks and failed'... Don't be one of these people. Respect this legend behavior and make sleep a non-negotiable.

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: 'IMPORTANT BUT NOT URGENT' MORNINGS

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: REDUCE CONTEXT SWITCHING

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE (ADD THIS): DAILY REWARD

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE (ADD THIS): WRITING TOMORROW'S 'HEADS DOWN' LIST EVERY DAY AFTER DINNER

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: DECIDE ON YOUR 'CHEAT DAYS'

## MAKE YOUR SCHEDULE: WEEKENDS DON'T EXIST... THE EXTENDED CIRCADIAN RHYTHM

## REFINE YOUR SCHEDULE: TEST IT WITH A FRIEND

## ***REFINE YOUR SCHEDULE: PRACTICE IT FIRST!

## KEEP A JOURNAL

## PREVIEW... THE FIRST 3 DAYS: INSOMNIA

## PREVIEW... THE CURE FOR INSOMNIA / PAYING THE CONSEQUENCES

#### Not having "sleep discipline" is just planting the seeds for your failure later.

## PREVIEW... THE FIRST TEN DAYS / WILLPOWER

## PREVIEW... MUSCLE MEMORY

### So you will rationalize longer breaks... and later mornings... and you tell yourself "Hey, what's a little scrolling on Instagram gonna hurt? I deserve it..." And worst of all you'll start to think you don't need as much sleep. Rookie mistake.

### And today I'm here like the Ghost Of Christmas Future to point out the direction you want to avoid.

### 11. God Momentum (Part IV): "40 Days And 40 Nights" Of Creativity

If you decided to continue beyond the first 21 days...

Congratulations.

Between Day 22 - Day 40 is where you will seek to turn your new habits into a way of life.

This is where you will begin your true transformation.

The first 3 weeks (21 days) was the rite of passage you had to make it through.

You needed those 3 weeks to prove to yourself that "you can do it".

It's where you experience all the fundamental patterns and challenges of acquiring discipline.

But it's also about as far as most people with "passion" get.

That's why I don’t trust people with “passion”.

I trust people who are “on a mission”.

You know how many people I see who start with “all guns blazing” ready to take over the world? It only lasts a few weeks before they’re back to their old habits again. I see those types of people coming from a mile away.

But the people who are on a mission? They're a lot quieter about things. They don’t trust themselves. Their human frailty worries them. That’s how important it is for them to succeed. They don’t want their own weaknesses to fuck them up.

That’s why you’ll see them surround themselves with the insurance policies and energy builders we discussed in the last chapter.

They do those things just to make sure they get things done.

They understand that their bouts with insomnia will come back again and again.

But weaker every time if they stay on course.

And their ego will come back again to make them believe they're strong enough to slack.

But that voice will get less loud if they stay aware and focused.

Yes, the devil will come back over and again to tempt you. But you'll get stronger every time.

You will go through this cycles over and over until this new momentum is a lifestyle.

The journey is exhausting, but exhilarating.

The first 21 perfect days was an accomplishment... But from now on life will taste different.

You're writing your artist story in real-time now.

A story that will become YOUR legend.

The 40 days bible story is the perfect allegory to describe every artist's journey on their road to greatness:

*After being baptized by John the Baptist, Jesus goes out to the desert to fast. He is tempted by the devil for 40 days and 40 nights. Jesus refuses each temptation. One torment after another. Until the devil finally gives up. That's when Jesus the prophet is born. He then returns to Galilee to begin his ministry.

All worthwhile journeys follow this same pattern.

1. Removal of yourself from society.

2. Getting your sh-t together with the utmost discipline.

3. Refusing all the destructive temptations you couldn't in the past. (Until you're swatting them like Neo's slow-motion bullets in the Matrix.)

4. You become "the new you". Beautiful, powerful and unrecognizable to those who knew you before.

Is God Momentum.

P.S. The beautiful thing about doing these "40 Days And 40 Nights of discipline" is:

Even if you go back to sucking afterwards… Whatever you did for that month and a half will keeps on paying dividends way into your future.

Not a bad ROI.

But please... Whatever you do... Don't fall intothis tragic God Momentum trap...

### 12. God Momentum (Part V): Beware Of False Language

A student sent this to me after his lackluster Week 3:

"...But anyway... God Momentum isn't about keeping you on the horse. It's about ensuring that you get back on the horse quicker every time you fall off."

False language.

False language is "when you use words to rationalize your failings or to delay real action".

Yes, it's useful for making you feel good. But it's awful for helping you affect meaningful change that will make you proud.

God Momentum is about STAYING ON THE HORSE cause you know what's at stake if you fall off.

God Momentum feels like AA does for an alcoholic: Where every day counts.

So before you start your journey to God Momentum, set proper expectations.

Let's make two things clear, so you don't think you're moving ahead... When you're actually falling behind.

Throw out the false language.

Don't weaken a framework designed to help you with... a bunch of rationalizations.

Just this week someone said to me:

"I took a cheat day."

False language.

Cheat days aren't something you "take". They are days that you "earn".

And they're always planned in advance.

After 9 perfect days of relentless discipline, of course you deserve a cheat day to keep your sanity.

Not so you can go fully AWOL. That's not the point. It's the day you can do a little less to give your mind some rest.

But when you go to bed late, or sleep in, or can't resist checking your phone before you're done working etc... Sorry, you're back at Day 1 again.

Unless you do DOUBLE the next day. That could mean... Waking up 3 hours earlier and doing twice the work.

Be honest with yourself, though.

Penance has to be severe enough to make you never want to slack ever again.

Without a penance for failing to continue your discipline... It's a momentum leak.

Pay the consequences. Or guess what? The next day is... Day 1.

Only that kind of commitment will give you actual momentum.

Momentum is the point.

It's not "21 days of seeing what happens when I try this cool idea I heard on a podcast"...

That's like saying you've been to Thailand when it was only a layover and you never even left the plane.

Treat the missteps you may get like a practice run. That's totally fine. I encourage that actually! Practicing first is like insurance for your 21 or 40-day journey.

It'll give you a sense of what toll all this discipline is going to take on you.

It'll also help you make sure your schedule is challenging enough. Because if you don't feel any pressure, then no transformation can occur.

But after you officially start, understand that there's no breaking stride.

Momentum is a cumulative thing.

If you should falter, you won't get to keep counting the days like nothing ever happened.

You guessed it... Back to Day 1.

"I'm seeing my family this week. It might upset the momentum. But I'll continue after."

False language.

Even with a natural disaster, unforeseen circumstances, or a note from the doctor...

If you miss a day, it's back to Day 1 again.

Don't lie to yourself.

Don't worry...

This is all going somewhere...

After months of momentum you'll get the ultimate reward:

No single day will be able to throw you off your game anymore. You'll be strong enough to go in and out at will.

You'll be in flow.

But for now, you don't have those gears yet.

"I've been going for 74 days," said a student I had been watching from afar.

False language.

What he had been doing is sputtering down the street like an old car that needs gas. Starting and stopping...

1st succumbing to "drinking with friends".

Then starting again... But succumbing to "going to bed late because he "was watching YouTube videos on his phone in bed".

Starting again... Then succumbing to "hanging out with my next-door neighbor all afternoon".

The truth was, he wasn't really on Day 74. He was actually on Day 5 (since his last existential crisis).

Don't get me wrong. It's not that he didn't gain anything in those 74 days. He did. And all the "practice" was critical for him understanding his journey.

But he didn't have God Momentum, yet.

I wish that for him. 'Cause with his talent, he'll be unstoppable.

But no one gets there with 'False Language'.

That's why I won't sugar-coat it.

God Momentum isn't this year's "feel good" challenge for people to latch on to.

It's not another self-help hack to add to your collection of shiny new "motivational concepts".

God Momentum is a decision you make to change your behavior patterns, once and for all.

God Momentum is "do or die".

So, only begin when there is no question of failure.

Only attempt it when you have achieved that kind of singular state of mind.

Everything you do before that?

It's just practice.

### 12. God Momentum (Part V): Beware Of False Language

### When you make "achieving excellence" your mission, you can't afford to have your eye off the prize. Not even for a second. What? And risk of losing everything you've built?

### Your goal is to get to 21 days of uninterrupted discipline.

### You're either building momentum or you're building a habit of inconsistency.

### Only begin when you're ready to mark the X's on your calendar for the next season.

### 13. God Momentum (Part VI): Why We Keep Going When Times Are Hard

I remember when I was in high school... There was a Parisian girl that got transferred to our school one year.

Everyone was in awe with her. Perfect face. Cute clothes. And...

She was a musical prodigy.

Sophie played violin better than anyone I had ever seen.

She could even play Paganini caprice #24... AKA The Devil’s Song.

Seems her dad had put her through a vigorous Serena and Venus Williams disciplined type of musical upbringing.

It was weird to see someone with that much talent.

She always had her violin with her too. She called it “her wife” (or “ma femme”, as she would say in her cute little French accent).

Everytime the rest of us were hanging out... she went somewhere quiet to go practice.

Without fail.

I was taking piano lessons at the time. Man, the only time I practiced was an hour before I had to go. I hated that shit.

But for her... That had been her lifestyle since she was four years old or something.

Well, one day after a long weekend, she came in with her arm in a cast.

She had gone skiing with her family and took a dive.

It wouldn't have been that big a deal for anyone else. I mean she WAS gonna be fine. Her cast would be off in as little as 2 months or something.

But she was MORTIFIED.

She couldn’t play the instrument she loved.

Despite that... After a couple of days, she started getting integrated into our circles.

She let the artists among us draw funny and rude stuff on her cast.

Her and I bonded one day at lunch on our love of Oreo cookies. Yeah, she splits them apart before she eats them too.

And on the weekends... We started seeing more of her now.

Even at the “illegal” beer drinking nights near the river.

But the craziest moment for me was seeing her walk to school one morning hand in hand with a new boyfriend. I had never seen this guy anywhere. He wasn't in our school.

I even felt a pang of jealousy.

Shit, I had never even considered asking her out myself. She had always seemed unattainable.

But it made sense... now that she didn’t have her "wife" anymore, there was a vacuum that could be filled.

When she finally got the cast off finally (in what seemed like overnight TBH) I knew that the honeymoon was over now.

I felt bad for the guy she had started dating.

Sophie was going to go back to practicing and that dude was about to get the shaft.

No more beer clinks and laughs with Sophie at our river parties.

No, It would be back to seeing her passionate head bobbing through the window of chemistry class as she practiced her scales at lunch.

But guess what?

That never happened.

She quit the violin instead.

She became like everyone else.

Years later I found out that she had married some guy who worked in the government and was raising kids.

I've never lost that moment of "awakening" that I received as a teenager.

I had seen firsthand that all it takes is for you to start sucking is to stop for just little while.

You can lose everything you gained over all those years of hard work... Overnight.

The vacuum will always get filled with something.

So if you’re trying to achieve greatness but you’re feeling down... Or diminished energy lately... Or feeling like you need some “self-care”...

Here’s the secret:

Don’t dare stop! Just go slower.

Do the absolute minimum you can handle every day, if you have to.

But keep going.

Take baby steps if you have to.

That's what will keep your excellence at top of mind.

It's still God Momentum when it's narrow.

It's still God Momentum when it's small.

You know when people accept their awards? What you're going through right now is the hard times they're talking about -- that they made it through. You will too.

Lean into this moment and it will get easier... Right there on the spot. Just watch!

Try it now.

### 14. The "Life Happens" Protocol

I'm guessing these next 3-4 months will be crucial for you?

You've made promises to yourself. You're going to be more disciplined. You're going to take things more seriously. But I ask you…

How do you know that this isn't just your seasonal optimism?Here's one way to find out... Answer this question:"What will you do when you get derailed?"Notice I didn't ask "if". I asked WHEN.Artists who are truly READY have something the others don't:They have a 'Life Happens' Protocol.Bank on it… Something unexpected will happen at some point in the future that will derail your art-making. Things will get in the way of your discipline. It is law.But artists who have prepared for when 'Life Happens'… They don't crumble. They don't scramble. They don't succumb. They are ready.They have a protocol.

The 'Life Happens' Protocol

What is a protocol?

It's "a system of rules that explain the correct conduct and procedures to follow in certain situations".

When "life happens"-- For example... You get sick. Or a family crisis comes up. Or, you get hit by a wave of numbing depression...

You need to have your protocol ready to execute.

Here is an example of what it might say…

Life happens.

But I want to remind you that you are still a superstar artist in the making.

Everything you do in this intense period will be part of your story. It will be where you will draw anecdotes for future interviews. It will be fodder for acceptance speeches.So, no need to panic. No need to despair.Just follow the protocol:1. This is what you should eat to stay healthy in this challenging time: (examples of: your comfort foods, your favorite fruits)2. This is how you should take care of yourbody to keep your physical and mental strength up. Simple rituals: (examples: stretches in the morning, walk at night, meditation)3. This is how you should reduce your art-making work-load for this crazy time so you still feel like you're making progress: (example: daily practice reduced to 15 minutes, research and organizing that you never had time to do before)4. Stay in the community: (examples: reach out to collaborators, read artist biographies)Use this time wisely.Use it fully.===

Print it out.Date it.Sign it.Place it in a sealed envelope.Address it to: TO MY FUTURE SELF: The 'Life Happens' ProtocolAnd then place it in the bottom of a drawer for the day you'll need it.

Today, you will have taken a step you have never taken before. You will have prepared yourself for the unknown. You will have created an insurance policy for your art.

NOW I believe you.

NOW you can believe yourself.

Here is an example of a "Life Happens" protocol that a student sent me. It had me in tears.

Dear Parker,

Life happens.

But I want to remind you that you are already an influential, showstopping artist, and you cannot stop now.

Everything you do in this break out period is part of your story. Every moment is a prized gem of future talk show interviews. It will be fodder for acceptance speeches.

No need to panic or withdraw.

Follow the plan:

I. This is what you should eat to stay healthy in this challenging time: Water with electrolytes, grapefruit, tofu, collards, slaw, hopping john salads

II. Simple rituals, meditation and exercise will make you feel better than sleeping-in or drugs. Stretch in the morning. Breath in to allow. Breathe out to nurture.

III. Reduce your load.Use crochet, reading or skating to return to flow.

IV. Stay in the community by being honest about life's struggles.

I love you endlessly. It's just for fun.

Be accountable. Send me a picture of your sealed 'Life Happens Protocol' envelope!
