### 15. "This Is What EVERY. DAY. Looks Like": The 40-Day Challenge

"Getting started" is the hardest part.

Everyone waits for external motivation. But even when you get it-- it only lasts a few hours until the movie, or the article, or the podcast that inspired you wears off. Then you go right back to looking for a new "drug" to motivate you.

That's not a way to live!

You could be motivated every day.

By replacing motivation... With momentum.

Becoming the best at your craft doesn't happen waiting for inspiration.

Getting faster at making your art doesn't happen waiting for motivation.

You need momentum.

And the only way to get it?

You do "the thing you love "… every, single, day.

Any artist that's not creative every day will eventually start feeling incomplete. And at worst? God forbid...They'll feel like a fraud.

Are you ready to improve your speed, increase your output and make 'making your art' a 'rest of your life' thing?

The 40 day challenge is designed to help you do exactly that.

Whether you're starting aDAILY PRACTICE...

DAILY PRACTICE:15 minutes to 1 hour every day. This is for for students who don't have a whole day to dedicate to art. Like, maybe you have a day job, or you're in school or you have a family to take care of? Use the secret of daily practice to keep you in the zone. And to build up the habit of consistency. From now on you will make art (or do something for your art) every single day WITHOUT FAIL. With this alone, your artistic life will completely transform. And your mind will be more at ease.

Or doing the full onGOD MOMENTUM...

GOD MOMENTUM:6- 12 hour days of full creative immersion. This is for students who have large chunks of time in the day. Usually they waste time trying to "figure out what to do". Or they spend their days procrastinating. Or they rely on sporadic inspiration. These students are ready to adopt the intense 'God Momentum' rituals to gain that momentum and fully dedicate their days to art like an athlete does with their sport. It's so intense it will require a sleep schedule, meal plans, Social media bans and cheat days so you never burn out.

Either one of these approaches will require daily consistency:

Knowing an instrument intimately... Making instinctive choices with brushes or colors... How to craft words to deliver emotion... Using premier pro to tell stories... Manipulating sound in Ableton... Or learning how to connect with your body to make it an expressive tool...

Consistency is the fastest way to reach mastery.

And consistency has probably been your problem for the last few years.

'Going daily' puts you in competition with the only person you should be competing with:

Yesterday's version of yourself.

If you've never made this kind of commitment before... Go slow.

Start with ADAILY PRACTICE(watch that module first).

Do it for 15 mins - an hour a day.

See if you can go for 3 weeks straight.

Doing it this way is like when you decide to move in with your boyfriend before you get married-- You're finding out if your passion / obsession level is compatible with the goals you've been bragging about achieving for so many years.

Prove it. To yourself.

But if you already know that art is a "for rest of your life" thing...

Then it's time to reschedule your life in a way that serves your goals.

Go for the full 40 days to achieveGOD MOMENTUM(read Part I-VI first).

Just like the "Jesus in the desert for 40 days and 40 nights" story, when he found his true calling was to die on the cross.

Or when David Blain was suspended in a glass box in London for 40 days.

40 days is the amount of time that it takes to achieve that feeling when NOT doing what needs to be done is HARDER than doing it.

This incredible phenomenon is what I call God Momentum.

"Passion" won't get you to 40 days. Sorry.

To do 40 days the way I describe it in the 6 modules in 'The Book Of Transformation' requires an OBSESSION level of commitment.

I'm talking...

John Wick determination... Like someone killed your dog and stole your car.

Uma Thurman in Kill Bill conviction. Like when her body is paralyzed and she focuses on "wiggling her big toe" until she's a full-fledge warrior woman again.

THAT'S what this will feel like.

If you want revenge against all the forces that have been against you for so long...

And you want to say goodbye to laziness, procrastination, and lack of self-belief...

This next period of your life will be worth every bit of effort.

It'll be all-out war.

But the best part of this challenge?

Is that even if you stop cold after 40 days... You will continue to feel the rewards of having gone "daily" for months after the challenge is done.

Not a bad side-effect, right?

Society has been pushing a romantic myth of artists "waiting and suffering for inspiration" since the year 1770, when that movement began.

And tabloid media continues to spread a lucrative fantasy of drug abuse as a conduit to great art.

I've dedicated my life to exposing how false this is.

The truth? The artists who keep releasing amazing work year after year are disciplined warriors.

Boring to realize, I know.

But it's a truth you'll need to swallow if you want to get into the big leagues:

"I'm gonna tell you what he does with his crew... They get up every morning and have breakfast together, and they talk about what they did yesterday and how to make it even better today. Then they go exercise together. They lift weights and focus on raising their 'chi energy' up. Then they get to the studio at 4pm. And they stay there until 4am. 12 hours! They go to bed... They wake up... And do it all over again the next day. It's this focused energy. I've never seen anything like that before. I can honestly say, it's not his talent that took him to the top. It's his focus." (RZA describing what he witnessed while he was in Hawaii for two weeks watching Kanye West work on 'My Beautiful Dark Twisted Fantasy)

How do you become high-output?

You adopt 'VAULT MENTALITY'.

You become such a creative machine that it's necessary to start logging your output on a spreadsheet, labelling multiple hard drives and keeping a filing system for it all.

After a few weeks, you will have more songs, sketches, photos, paintings, videotapes of rehearsals etc... Then you could ever share with an audience.

Welcome to being a professional creative.

You're SUPPOSED to make more art than you could ever use.

How do you think Tupac, or Juice WRLD are still releasing new albums after they're dead?

The healthy creative's problem isn't CREATING.

It's CHOOSING what to share that's hard.

The healthy creative "struggles" with abundance.

I want you to have that "problem".

'VAULT MENTALITY' is what Prince had. He left behind a vault of hundreds of albums to release into the next century!

That how ALL the greats create.

All of them.

With abundance.

The culture AND the fans cherish artists who create a BODY of work.

This could be YOU... But you're 'overthinking.

No more. Not on my watch.

Let's get you started on a journey that will gradually leave you no room for overthinking. That's the old you.

The worst part of daily practice is how lonely it is.

That's why I document my daily online. So you know at least ONE other person is waking up at 4 a.m. on Christmas day along with you to "do 1 hour of freeform writing"...

You know how they say, "Those who can't DO— teach."

When the 'Make art not content' turned 1 at the end of the end of April 2021, I celebrated it by bringing 'Episode 14 ("Why Do The Same People Always Win?")' to life with the students.

I started recording and edit a one-minute podcast every morning.

That way you also get to hear clips from upcoming podcasts before they get released to the public; and probably some questionable stuff that will never get released too. 😂

You are part of that family of renegades now.

Aspiring high-output creatives unite!

If you've been thinking of starting a daily practice... This is your time.

If you've been thinking of improving your speed, or increasing your output... This is your time.

If you've always felt like you needed some form of accountability... This is your time.

If you've been thinking of immersing yourself in your art with obsessive discipline... This is your time.

I'd love to see you raise the bar in whatever you've been trying to achieve.

Start with 21 Days Of 'Underthinking' to conquer consistency.

Or go full-on 40 days of God Momentum-- if you're ready to for full immersion towards your Polaris Star.

Whatever you think you can handle.

5 Things...

MAKE IT SPECIFIC. MAKE IT MEASURABLE."I will work on design stuff," is not specific. INSTEAD SAY: "I will master every parameter in After Affects by isolating one a day and make something out of it for 1 hour."

"I will write every morning," is not specific. INSTEAD SAY: "I will write 1,000 words every morning." OR "I will set my alarm and write for 30 minutes straight."

"I will get better at programing my synth," is not specific. INSTEAD SAY: "I will master every knob on my synth by choosing a different one every day and trying to make three presets I love by using only that knob. By the end of the challenge, I will have 120 new sounds."

Pick your ideas, or themes, or parameters for each next day's daily practice THE NIGHT BEFORE so that you hit the ground running. Don't give your brain excuses to be lazy because you're trying to "figure out what to do" for 10 minutes before you start.

Pick an activity that you know would make a severe positive dent in your creativity or your career—something you've been procrastinating or feel you don't do enough of.

For example, ask yourself:

"What creative activity do I want it to "be like breathing" by the end of this challenge?

Is it writing a song a day? Painting daily?

Or take practicing new camera techniques so you stay fresh?

Or maybe it's mastering the software you use to make art?

Or maybe it's the non-creative artistic boosters like:

PSYCHOSOMATIC DAILY PRACTICE... Some creatives benefit the most when they get their minds and their bodies aligned. That's when all their creativity falls into place. I can relate 100%. If you're that type, then you may benefit from a daily practice of meditation, yoga, working out, and journaling.

Or maybe you've always wanted to improve your chops at making ARTISTIC, MEANINGFUL "content" for social media, but you're too slow?

Pick ONE social media to get good at for the challenge. I suggest Instagram. Pick someone out there who has a great IG that you love. And every day practice by recreating a piece of content they did. If you do that for 40 days straight for this challenge, you'll become a wizard. And the great thing is, you'll be able to use your new skills on ANY other platform you choose.

Or this one that I love that Marya did:

CHALLENGE: "Wake up early and don't touch social media for 3 hours." Uh... First of all... That shit is HARD. Especially if your phone is the first thing you reach for in the morning. Secondly... That shit will change your life. You will be so focused. And once you start "using" again, you'll notice immediately how quickly your focus deteriorates.

Or maybe you REALLY suck at promoting yourself?

Imagine you spent 30 minutes to an hour every day reaching out to people (gatekeepers, bloggers, influencers, brands, agents, and yeah even fans.). What do you think your life would look like after a month of doing that? If you recently released music, or a book, this might be the perfect daily practice. (THE ROLODEX GAMEPLAN: You spend 10 minutes racking your brain, looking through your address book, or through Instagram, and asking friends who to add to your 'reach out' list-- and then for 20 minutes, you feverishly write DMs and cold emails to those people.)

A LESS OBVIOUS EXAMPLE FOR DANCERS, ACTORS AND OTHER PERFORMERS WHO USE THEIR BODY...

Why don't you decide to choreograph something new every single morning. Give yourself 30 minutes. In the last 5 minutes, film it. Do it every day. But instead of increasing the time every day… Increase your SPEED. Work up to choreographing 2 things in that 30 minutes. Or work up to longer and more elaborate routines... But still within the 30 minutes. That way, 2 months later when someone's like "Hey can you come up with a choreography for my music video…" It'll be the easiest flex. You'll think back on your spreadsheet of 65 videos you already have collected in YOUR VAULT, and you'll be like 'Yeah, no problem'. Your self-esteem and confidence will be sky high because you've BEEN doing this! You'll be so fast now that you can come up with ideas on the spot instead of panicking and saying "give me a couple of days" and never getting back to them. You are now a creative machine. Professional creatives do hours, and days, and months of daily practice so that when we need to come up with something in 5 minutes... It's easy. No humming and hawing. No procrastination. It's now in our blood. I went from "knowing nothing about photography" -- to having "unethical marketing agencies trying to copy my style". It took less than a year, using this exact method. It's time for you to deliver on YOUR potential. Add to your vault of ideas every, single, day.

The point is to pick something you'd like to see yourself improve.

Something that you can realistically do every day.

Something that stretches your abilities beyond your comfort zone.

Something that you can commit to for at least 21-days... then eventually for 40.

Ask yourself: "What would I like to add to my "vault" every single day? What new skill would make me feel like I developed a new superpower at the end of this challenge?

It should feel hard enough that at the beginning you get a pang of "Oh shit, what did I sign up for?" But by week 2, you're laughing that you thought this would be a problem... That's how you'll know how far you've come (And then we'll raise the bar again, just like I talk about in God Momentum part III)

People like to start challenges on a Monday.

Rookie mistake.

Start on Friday BECAUSE the weekend is when most people have the most distractions... BUT it's also when your 'will to succeed' is at it's highest-- That way, by Monday, it'll already be DAY FOUR.

Look, you may miss a meal (not recommended). Or you may get insomnia (it'll happen, but you can't hit snooze the next day... you'll have to suffer). Or you may even end up breaking plans you made with others (priorities, baby)...

But failing? That's not an option.

You need to make this pact with yourself now.

Understand that this isn't a challenge to "see IF you can do it".

Just like a marathon, you WILL get to the finish line.

What you wanna learn is what shape you'll be in by the end of it, compared to what you've been doing until now.

Test out your daily ritual to make sure it's manageable.

Are you giving yourself enough time to do it? Are you waking up at the right time? What time do you need to go to bed to make this work? What do you need to prepare so you're ready to hit the ground running?

Make a schedule / plan AND TEST IT OUT.

If you're going for God Momentum... Get your VAULT hard-drives ready (main drive and backup). Label the folders you need.

Just make sure you have a system in place where you can watch the abundance that you create accumulate. THAT alone will self-motivate you.

But PRACTICE BEFORE DAY ONE to iron out the kinks.

People like to "jump into it" without practicing.

Another rookie mistake.

That's your ego fucking with you.

Somtimes it's because you have something to prove to yourself.

Sometimes it's because you have something to prove to the people who always doubt you.

Let all of that go.

Take your time to get it right BEFORE you start.

This is a LIFE commitment. Let's approach it with care.

A methodical approach that will reward you later.

It'll give you time to "mentally prepare".

You'll read more about this in:HOW TO SUCCEED AT CONSISTENCY: A 40-DAY DIARY

Make sure I have your Instagram @ so you can see MY private daily stories as you do yours.

Feel free to tag me EVERY. DAY.

When you feel like giving up (and you will), I'll be there to keep you in the zone.

When you try to slack... I will call you out and raise your intensity back to your own standards.

I wanna see what you're doing. And how you're improving.

I wanna hear about what you're learning during these 21-40 days.

I may repost your messages at times to inspire others on the journey.

You will see me highlight moments and tips from everyone participating that we can all learn from.

Are you ready?

Sometimes all you need is a start date.

Give yourself one.

Send it to me.

Tell me what your "daily practice" will be.

Make sure I have your IG @.

### 16. How To "Plan The Next Day The Night Before" (Detailed)

You wanna mesmerize people with your ability for achievement?

Master the principles in this module.

YOUR "problem" is THE WHOLE MODERN WORLD'S PROBLEM:

Distraction.

To get in "flow", you need a no distraction zone.

I repeat: There is no "flow" if you keep distractions around you.

A "block" is a UNINTERRUPTED PERIOD OF TIME.

And you will need those blocks to succeed at anything in life.

You've had no problem giving "blocks" to school or jobs your whole life, right? Well, now it's time to give them to yourself.

No phone. No internet. No "research on YouTube". No chats with your roommate. No "getting snacks" (prepare those beforehand)

Stephen Coveyhas this business concept called The Four Quadrants.

We're going to steal two of these quadrants today in the name of creativity.

Quadrant I: Important and Urgent.

Quadrant II: Important But Not Urgent.

What does everyone do first?

Important and Urgent, of course.

Sounds logical, right?

But life is constructed in such a way that our most important goals are IMPORTANT but they're never URGENT.

There's never any drama if we don't do our "goal related things" in today.

There's no "do or die".

No one's gonna break up with you... Evict you... Or fire you... If you don't do "goal related activities" in your life.

The urgent things carry such a heavy social burden if they're not done that society trains everyone to put those first in line.

Our lives become a life of putting out fires.

But then what happens?

Everyone else's priorities get pushed to the front. And by the time we get to our shit... We're drained.

And the needle never moves towards our dreams.

Well, if you keep doing this...

Your life degrades.

You'll be living for everyone else but yourself.

And you end up with regret and resentment.

Not a pretty ending, I've heard.

That's why we're going to stop this pattern for you today.

From now on, the first block of your day will go to "IMPORTANT BUT NOT URGENT".

AKA "YOUR DREAMS".

No more making them #2.

This block will become known to you and everyone around you as "your sacred time".

Wake up earlier to give yourself "your sacred time" if you have to.

(Like when I was on tour with The Weeknd. I had a whole life of creativity for 3 hours before I ever touched anything related to touring. That's why every day I felt refreshed and full of ideas when I had to do my killer job.)

You become a nicer human being when you honor "your sacred time".

Oh, and look at that... Wow. You have less anxiety!

Ask yourself: "What's essential for my goals that I hate doing."

Guess what you're going to be tackling FIRST in that block?

Or ask yourself this: "What's something I need to do, but I'm intimidated by its 'grandeur'."

Well THAT'S another option of what you're going to start your day with.

Start your day with things that move the needle.

Plan your day so that the longest / most challenging blocks happen at the beginning of the day.

(Don't schedule a call with AT&T to change your plan when you're at your highest energy point! Come on!)

As you lose energy during the day... Your blocks will get shorter, and the tasks should become more and more brainless.

Everything else gets the 75% you. Just like it deserves. It's all stuff that one day will be replaced with computers anyways.

When you look back on today, you'll be satisfied knowing you're moving towards your dreams.

But what if you...

Get "such a great idea for another project" or if "You remember something crucial that you forgot to do?"

Can you take a 10-minute break to take care of it?

Yes, sure. IF your goal is NEVER to reach flow. 😬

Instead, do this:

Keep a "Distraction Notepad" next to you when you work.

This notepad is where you will file away these 'distractions' posing as 'inspirations'.

Distractions like "DM 'so-and-so' on Instagram", and "research "blah blah" on youtube". All BS distractions, believe me.

Don't fall for the mind games that your own mind is playing on you.

Transcribe them to your "distraction notepad". And when your block is finally done... You can joyfully (or tearfully) deal with those "big issues" afterwards. (But notice how they suddenly don't feel as urgent anymore? Classic.)

Don't just write "8 am: paint".

That's too risky.

You need to fill in the details.

For example:

"8 am: Paint Elise's face. Start with a sketch. Experiment with new colors.

Eliminate the need for thought going into each block by writing down what needs to be done.

DESCRIBE IN DETAIL HOW YOU'RE GOING TO BEGINNING THE ACTIVITY.

Flow will take care of the rest.

Okay, so you wrote down how you'll be starting each block. In detail. And you have your distraction notepad next to you. But why is it that when you wake up, you STILL feel unmotivated to tear into your work?

It's because you ruined it right after you wrote your "next day plan" down.

Instead of keeping your mind locked into those exciting morning thoughts for the rest of the evening... You went on Instagram or Netflix to "wind-down".

And what did this do? It unwinded your focus on your goals.

It planted the wrong seeds into your subconscious.

It robbed you of tremendous psychic energy.

Not bad for a little photo sharing app, right?

But that's why you're drained.

You let the blue light of the digital screen distract you right before you fell asleep.

It may seem innocent... It's not.

Do this instead:

When you're winding down in the evening, start doing life-affirming, energy multiplying activities.

You'll see. AFTER a few days... After your brain has suffered withdrawals from the former "nightly vices" (3 days typically)...

You'll start experiencing the kind of mornings the old you was envious of.

Sometimes you have no more energy.

You're like DONE.

You know what's a productivity weapon I love?

Keep a special todo list of things that take less than 5 minutes to do.

That way when you're feeling low energy... Go to that list and do them one by one while you eat cake and watch yourself feel lighter and satisfied with yourself.

### 17. Extraordinary Action, Extraordinary Results

(This is the first draft of this module -- But I had to share it with you now because THIS IS AN EMERGENCY.)

I'm gonna ask you to do something none of your friends are doing.

And why should you be ok with that?

Because none of them are trying to reach the heights that you are.

Yeah, you're gonna be the weird one of the bunch for a while. The black sheep.

But “being different” shouldn't only be about how you make art. It should be your whole lifestyle. Total immersion is the only version of authenticity that an audience believes anymore. I agree with them.

But before I tell you how the “lifers” do it, let me remind you of WHY you can't wait for another second to adopt these changes…

Simply put... Every time you start scrolling on your phone, you're saying no to reaching flow.

Instead, you’ve decided to feed your mind with other people's ideas, other people's dramas and other people's lifestyles and dreams.

I know that when you're at your best you want to double down on YOURSELF. But as soon as your self-doubt and lack of motivation creep in you fall back on the same destructive patterns.

One step forward. Two steps back.

And why stop now, when everyone else is doing it.

I'll tell you.

Because you’re not trying to be like everyone else.

You’re trying to make a difference in the world.

You want to bring art to a new level. And show people things they've never seen.

And accomplishing that isn't even that hard.

What if I told you that most of the challenges you've been facing are because you never give yourself long windows of creativity without distractions?

You haven't designed an environment for your genius to thrive.

Remember the "initiation email #2" I sent you when you joined? Remember what your creative goals were?

And do you remember what your answer was for "What's stopping you from getting there?"

Whatever you wrote down was just "the effect". But "the cause"? It all boils down to you not carving out a period of time dedicated to your art.

Because if you did... There would be nothing stopping you. Nothing.

Time isn't your problem. "How you're using your time" is your problem.

"Not having connections" isn't your problem. "Not reaching out to people who can help you" every day is your problem.

Instead... Whenever the going gets tough, you grab your phone.

And scroll, and scroll, and scroll...

I'd love to see you fix that. Starting TODAY. Once and for all.

Don't worry, I'm not going to tell you to give up Instagram for a few months. That's not realistic anyway. And besides, you need it to stay connected to your audience.

No, I'm gonna ask you to join me in what I've been doing since April when we did the 40-day challenge together. (F-ck, that was intense.)

Here’s the prescription:

I stole this idea from the world of "intermittent fasting". But you and I are gonna use it for your "social media addiction” instead of food.

Here's how it works:

For 16 hours every day, any 16 hours, you're not allowed to touch your phone or go online at all. Not once.

And then for 8 hours, you can scroll to your heart’s content.

You don’t need more Tiktok/Instagram time than THAT do you?

And besides, for 8 of those 16 "no-phone hours" you're sleeping anyway, right?

So what are we really talking about here? Nothing crazy. Only half of your day dedicated to being productive. Creating. Promoting.Engaging in Energy Builders.

(But yes you can PREP your social media posts and newsletters for when you get back online.)

Once the 16 hours is up? You have 8 hours to to piss away on Instagram and Tiktok all you want. Or go lurk on your ex. Or go re-post someone's meme. Or go watch what celebrities are doing.

But once the eight hours is up... You stop again. Cold turkey. Back to the bubble of creative flow activities again. (Let's be real, this shouldn't sound like torture. This is the window where your ART will happen!)

Here's an example of what a typical day could look like for you:

You wake up at 8 and do things that will build you. Until noon. Then you have phone access until 8pm. You don’t touch it again until noon the next day.

Or another way... You could break your “phone diet” as late as 4 pm end resume the ban at midnight.

Or (this one is the hardest to do) wake up reaching for your phone but after 8 hours it's over for the whole day. (It's hard because once you start consuming social media, the hard part is STOPPING. It becomes a reflex.)

But really, it's up to you. Put the 8 hours wherever you want.

Will it be hard? In theory, it shouldn't be. But I'm not gonna lie... It ain't easy. You don't realize how addicted you are until you start doing something like this. But the beautiful thing? It gets way easier after the 3rd or 4th day. Just like when you're “food fasting”. Remember… You have to go through the bad part to get to the good part.

Email me for accountability if you want.

Or if you have any questions.

Honestly, I'll do anything to help your artist side experience what being "locked-into flow" feels like over and over again.

### 18. The Biggest Enemy Of Creative Flow

Within minutes of each other, I got these messages from two students who live five time-zones apart:

And then another student sent a message...

Do you see a trend?

I already talked about it in God Momentum (Part III). But I know that if I don't emphasize this idea with it's own module, it won't stick in your mind.

So here it is.

It's own module.

And I'll even give you "scientific proof" (further below) that I hope internalizes all of this for you once and for all so you can go on a much anticipated, long awaited, creative streak.

Context switching = doing "two or more unrelated things a day" versus...

"Doing one thing at a time until you finish."

It's hard enough to ramp up the energy to do even ONE thing. And you wanna stop just when you're getting in the groove? To go do something else?

It's just like context switching's cousin: Multitasking.

Multitasking is that thing you do when you have a 9 to 5 job that you hate and you wanna give the "appearance of working" to your shitty boss.

But when you're being creative...

Multitasking and context switching is THE BEST WAY TO NEVER ACHIEVE FLOW.

Read that last sentence again, please. And let it sink in once and for all.

Not only am I suggesting (if your goal is to be a high-output creative) that you never multitask (doing two or more unrelated things at a time)...

I'm also advising that you to stop context switching (doing two or more unrelated things in a day!). Immediately.

If you want to be a creative "machine" like Drake, Basquiat, Rupi Kaur, or Beyonce...

Do ONE thing... And THINK OF ONLY THAT ONE THING... until you finish.

It's better to work on ONE thing for two weeks... And then work on ANOTHER thing for two weeks...

Then to work on two things that you STILL WON'T FINISH at the end of a month.

You wanna see the math behind it? Will that help cure you? Go here:

How Context Switching Is Killing You

What does the beautiful alternative look like?

Well, first of all, because you're focusing on only one thing at a time, you'll finish each thing faster. That's already good enough reason for me. But there's more...

The newfound focus gives you more epiphanies, and just like that... Your work is of higher quality.

Second of all... The most significant side-effect, I think... Is that because you're finishing things, you feel good.

Feeling good about yourself is a creativity booster.

See how the two students in the examples above didn't "feel good"? And what happened? The work got slower.

Here's a little secret you may not even realize about creatives likes us... We can hate our life and all the world around us and we STILL won't stop creating. But the moment we stop feeling good about our own abilities... That's when we're in trouble.

And the best way we have of keeping that feeling away?

Finishing things.

Even if you don't love everything you finish, you can't help but grow and learn. And within hours, you already have new ideas for the next thing.

You create these building blocks that help you finish the next thing faster.

Instead of going back and forth between two or more things at a snail's pace and feeling bad about yourself.

Creatives hunger for forward movement.

So stop starving yourself with endless context-switching.

Finish things. One at a time.

It'll look slow only at the beginning.

But within a year, you'll have made a movie, released a book, learned how to make a website, and then actually made it, and you'll be out on your "Social Distance Saloon DJ Tour" with your boyfriend...

While you watch people with a million balls in the air (like you used to) with nothing to show for it in the end.

### 19. Inputs And Outputs

When people are trying to achieve their goals, most people have the right idea: make a list of things they need to "do". And then go out and do them.

You look at your todo list every day. And if at the end of the day, most of them are checked off... You know that you did good.

But sometimes after a few weeks... For some reason... You don't feel like the needle is moving. And so you may be tempted to give up.

It happens every day. All around the world.

And the sad part is... It isn't even your fault.

You were probably never taught the principle of INPUTS and OUTPUTS.

I've used it for my photography, on tour, for writing and even as I built this school.

To have a successful day, you need to see your activities in terms of INPUTS and OUTPUTS.

Some 'doing' is all about taking in information, processing that information, and making the machine stronger.

Those are the INPUTS.

Then there's the doing that's about creating things, opportunities, or connections with people that weren't there before.

Those are the OUTPUTS.

OUTPUTS create an energy in the outside world that keeps on creating momentum and magic even when you sleep.

People with high-OUTPUT levels always outperform people with high-INPUT levels.

Even though technically, they're both 'doing'.

If you're an aspiring writer, yes, it's important to read.

But it's just as important to contact outlets that could publish your work.

If you're a photographer, it's important to organize your photography and workplace.

But it's more important to reach out to new collaborators like brands and models.

Making sure that your OUTPUTS are way higher than your INPUTS is key.

And only IF... your goal is to make creativity your profession.

If this is only a hobby to you don't worry about INPUTS and OUTPUTS.

But if you want to achieve levels of excellence like Beyonce, Oprah, Kevin Hart, and Drake you're going to have to increase your OUTPUTS.

List of INPUTS (important activities that will fool you into thinking you're moving forward, even when you're not):

List of OUTPUTS (important activities that create careers even if you had no INPUTS at all)

There's no rule to this, but start out with 70% outputs and 30% inputs when you're planning your day (that's an INPUT btw), and from now on and you'll start seeing results.

Don't let the shortness of this module fool you... The impact of this mindset is enormous!

### Creating a new work of art but not sharing it (because it's not ready yet, or because you think it sucks)

### Creating AND Sharing a new work of art

### Emailing your list

### Cold calling people that can help you

### 20. How To Succeed At Consistency: A "Live Journal" of 40 Days

Whether you're starting:

1.A new daily practicefor 15 minutes - 1 hour. (Minimum 40 days)

2.The God Momentum Challengeto completely reshape your creative life and career. (21 - 40 Days)

Your biggest weakness has been: consistency.

This is how you will conquer it.

🌡 FEELING: Excited

For 10 Days before I start a 40 day challenge. I practice (lightly) every day until the challenge starts.

I've done this so many times, I know that the first few days can end up wasted if I don't iron out the kinks first. And wasted days are not real days because they don't build momentum.

When you practice doing your daily ritual BEFORE you start your 40 days, that's when you realize that:

Maybe this challenge you chose is too easy and you're selling yourself short?

Or maybe the challenge you chose is too hard and you're setting yourself up for failure?

Or that all the little things you have to do when you wake up don't actually take "10 minutes" like you thought... They take 35 minutes! Oops.

Don't wait to find out such obvious things on Day 1.

Those are all DAY 0 technicalities that should be figure out beforehand.

What tools do you need handy as you begin?

A coaster for your coffee?

A notepad on the side to document other ideas that come up so you don't have to stop or move.

A do not disturb sign on your door?

Will you need a timer?

Extra batteries?

2 towels instead of 1?

Video camera battery charged in advance?

Oh man... And practice your sleeping schedule!

Otherwise be ready for heavy duty insomnia. And once the challenge starts "hitting snooze" won't be allowed.

You'll have to pay the consequences and work with only 2 hours sleep in ya.

Have you warned your boyfriend that you're going all "Rocky" on them?

Have that argument now, if it's gonna be an argument.

Or let them know what they can do to help you succeed if they're the supportive type.

Have you made note of all the important dates on your calendar that could throw you off your game? Is Mother's Day coming soon? Or a friend's birthday? Or a government holiday that may mean your favorite coffee shop is closed?

Figure these days out in advance so you'll know to wake up earlier that day. Or how to successfully prep some extra things the night before etc...

How will you organize your work as it accumulates?

Hard drives?

How will you measure your progress?

A spreadsheet? (When you're creating abundance, you have to plan for how to manage it so you don't get lost or confused. That will rob your momentum.)

How will you effectively eliminate Instagram, Tiktok, Twitter, Email, Text from your life for the time you're working?

Where will you put your phone so you can't even see it until you're done work?

And yes "no phone" includes when you take breaks (if you're doing 'God Momentum').

🌡 FEELING: Like David Goggins

I have all my systems in place now.

Procrastination always happens at all the points where you're unsure what the next step is.

I've identified all those weak points ahead of time. And I'll continue fine tuning until day one.

I'm treating my schedule just like an athlete would.

I have my food menus.

I know my break times. (Got a little timer. Don't give yourself excuses to use your phone.)

I've factored in times for stretches and for working out. (Literally the most important part of my day. It's the only way to have a HEALTHY 15-hour day. This is my anti-burnout insurance.)

I have my non-negotiable wake-up time. 4 a.m. I chose this time because I will have total silence during my creative block for 2 hours before the world wakes up.

I don't wear a watch usually, but I'll be wearing the heart monitor/watch that I use for the gym 24/7 now-- Another reminder of how serious I'm taking this.

I find that it's those little things you do... The new behaviors... The new rituals... They all set you up for success against a world that will be trying to pull you back into lameness every single day.

🌡 FEELING: Not gonna lie. I'm scared. Good scared.

Not because I'm afraid of not making it...

But because I know that nothing will stop me unless I'm dead or unconscious.

Got a physical book to read during wind-down every night. (If you're gonna do the same, I suggest a biography. It's good for getting you out of your own world into someone else's.)

I used to read on my IPad but... I've been totally eliminating screen time before I go to bed for the last 3 days. And, you know what? Total game changer.

Insomnia doesn't stand a chance now.

And finally...

I've told my close friends and family what I'm doing so they don't take it personally when I'm focused as hell for the next two months.

SO IMPORTANT!

Make the people around you your co-conspirators.

🌡 FEELING: Overwhelmed.

Today was the longest day of my life. I'm going straight to bed.

🌡 FEELING: Woke up before my alarm. Pumped.

I remembered something I do that always helps me when I'm in discipline mode:

KEEP A NOTE PAD AROUND AT ALL TIMES

I always plan my days, the night before of course. But this give me a place to prepare ideas for days further down the line. That simple action will keep you in the zone. It keeps you thinking about adding stuff to "the vault".

🌡 FEELING: Uninspired.

The only rule is... Even if you're not inspired, you have to stay there, no phone, no internet until the timer goes off. Learn to face the wall instead of running from it.

🌡 FEELING: Hungy.

I fasted today on top of everything else. I'm crazy.

Thankfully, I did all the hard stuff before I started fasting.

I remembered something major about hunger:

You get to that point where you're sure you're gonna die. That's when you wanna cave in and go eat something. You REALLY want to cheat. But if you don't... After a while, you just forget. And you start doing other shit.

I got to that point today.

I waited the hard part out.

And when the fast was over, I didn't even notice until 15 minutes late.

The mind is crazy how it works.

You just gotta wait to hard parts out.

🌡 FEELING: Getting good at this.

I have a new killer ritual. As the water boils for my tea. I prep everything (that's ready for me since last night) into "go" mode.

Open the guitar case and plug it to an input in Ableton so you're not lazy to grab it if you need it for a track.

Open your notebook to the page you'll be adding to.

Laziness has no chance to win when you're locked and loaded. It would be too much work to NOT do it at this point.

When I asked students doing the challenge how they felt on the 8th day... This is what they said:

"I can make things work even when they seem impractical." Oliver

The beginning of every career is about doing things that you can't possibly "scale". But that's how you develop a devoted fanbase. At every level, you overdeliver. You take things to the maximum. I remember my first tour with The Weeknd. After every single show, he did a record signing with anyone who bought merch that night. We're talking a line-up of thousands of kids. The signings were often longer than the actual concert was. Would he be able to do that now? Of course not. But he did it in the period of his career where it was possible. Will you be able to greet every new follower with a personal DM voice memo when you're a superstar? No. But you CAN now.

"I learned that I have limits. And to fit within those limits, some things have to be sacrificed." Ines

That's the difference between a professional and an amateur. The amateur things they can "have it all" and ends up having nothing to show. But professionals make the sacrifices early and everyone oohs and ahhs at the results. They will say, "You're so lucky..." Little do they know what you had to sacrifice.

"I learned that I'm capable of way more than I thought was even possible." Victor

The most common thing I hear when people are attempting a new Mystery School concept is "This is hard." or "I'm not good at that." Uh... Of course, you're no good. You've never done it before! It's like if you've never gone to the gym... Just grab a copy of David Foster Wallace's 'Infinite Jest' and do bicep curls with them... You'll probably feel a "burn" in your arms afterward. But after only a week of doing something new, you'll already start feeling like a new human with brand new skin. Most people never know that feeling because they never go past three days.

"I learned to trust the body. The body knows." Viv

"Psychosomatic" is one of my favorite words. The impact of mind and body on creative work is mind-boggling. That's one of the reasons I put exercise and sleep at the top of my discipline. Treat the body like a temple, and suddenly you "have more ideas" and "are depressed less". And once you establish a good relationship with your body, you know the best time to push it to higher limits. The body will always tell you. But will you listen?

"I have the drive. But now I need the discipline." Arusha

Consider this... Only when you start showing up with discipline can you be sure that you actually have the drive. #truthlotion

"I learned that it's not what I do that influences my mood. It's how I THINK about what I do." David

The beauty of creating every day is that you give yourself new things to think about. No more stale thoughts. It's the consistent influx of new data that changes your relationship with your mind.

"I'm no longer available for relationship drama. I'm all-in for ART." Amar

All the bullshit drops away when you realize that if you don't get to bed immediately, your whole day tomorrow is fucked.

"Consistency takes away some of the stress of creating." Roberto

Seriously. The best side-effect of consistency? Speed. When you get asked to create "on-demand" you can do ON THE SPOT what used to take you three days.

"I learned that I don't need to wait for inspiration to hit me. I can set a timer and come up with an idea in a limited time frame." Karen

That's the first thing you drop on the path to becoming a HEALTHY creative. This mythical notion of "waiting for inspiration". Just because ideas come from out of thin air... Or in dreams... Or from the most magical circumstances... DOES NOT MEAN that you have to wait for them.

"I realize now that negative thought cycles that I believed were defeated can pop back up with little warning." Nick

Oh God yes. This will be a life-long fight. Negative thoughts are looking for any sign of weakness they can find. The best time for them to strike? When you have no momentum. Or when you haven't defined a Polaris Star to keep your actions grounded.

"I learned that my subconscious has the power to give me answers when you need it the most." Christofer

That's exactly what happens when you plant seeds in your subconscious early in the morning (your daily practice). You do something for an hour... And while you go on with life, your creativity is bubbling below the surface. And then in the middle of dinner-- a breakthrough for your art pops into your mind. You start smiling. People think it's because of something they said. You graciously let them continue to believe that.

"I learned that for me to stay dedicated to my art, I have to keep my life together." Katherine

It's a sacrifice. But once you get into the habit, it becomes hella easy. You can't believe it because right now because you're struggling. But once you do get it, you won't believe you ever lived with such low aspirations.

"Less expectations = Easier and better songwriting." Chelsea

If you look at songwriting history, you'll notice that many hit songs were an afterthought. "It was the last song we wrote for the album..." "It was written during soundcheck..." "I got the idea on a plane..." Hit songs don't come from overthinking. ( That struggle is reserved for mixing 😂) )

"I've discovered that when I tell my truth and story honestly, people are moved." Heirloom

People use many tactics to get followers. "30 Hashtags." "Thirsttraps." "Posting at certain times." "Follow for follow." But the best "shortcut" is, and will always be, expressing your truth 1000%. And sorry... Expressing your truth at 50% (which is what most people are doing), isn't truth at all. When you go halfway, it's the biggest injustice you can do to your potential.

### 21. Secondary Effects

The reason our culture is f-cked right now is because most people are afraid of sticking to their guns.

And who can blame them?

We're only rewarded for instant gratification.

People don't double-down on themselves because of the silly fear of being an outcast.

So they stay within the lines.

Making themselves... Invisible.

But the truth is... If you're doing something you know is right... Or that's new... And could moving our society forward... And if you can take the criticism for a while... Then you need to hang in there.

Eventually, you'll be celebrated. Or at least you'll find your tribe of people to connect with.

But you have to keep the smoke going long enough to be rescued.

Yes, every action. Has a reaction.

But every reaction...

Has a secondary effect.

And the totally weird thing about it is that the secondary effect is usually polar opposite to the reaction.

If the reaction was negative. The secondary effect is positive. And vice versa. How crazy is that math?

The most basic example is going to the gym.

If you kill yourself on legs day, well, afterwards you can hardly walk.

Sometimes you're slow for days.

But what happens after a few months?

You start to become an athlete.

See how that works?

But nobody talks about the secondary effects.

They talk about "don't do that, it'll hurt".

And everyone listens. Except a few. The few who know about secondary effects.

Now YOU know about it to.

Once you understand it you can shut out the noise.

But remember. If you're doing something different than the norm, you have to be patient with the crowd.

But they'll understand it eventually.

I've been there. Over and over again. It's almost "yawn" at this point because it's so predictable.

I'll do something crazy. People get mad. And then a year later they hire me for thing they used to get mad at me for.

That's why I encourage you to go out on a limb.

Double down on yourself. Double down on the things that make you different.

Too many artists aren’t sticking around long enough to reap the benefits of secondary effect

The things may be shocking tay...

In a year that's what they'll be hiring YOU for.

If you want to go further down the rabbit hole READ THIS.

### 22. A Guide To Visualization (For Creatives Who Think 'The Secret' Is Bullshit)

The first rule of visualization is this:

Ever throw a rock into a rolling ocean full of waves?

Pretty uneventful.

But have you ever dropped a tiny pebble into a lake that's as still as a sheet of paper? And then watched it, like... Ripple forever?

That's how you should treat visualization.

Make your mind as still as a country lake.

That way, when you drop the faintest thought into it later, it will ripple forever.

In your real life, those "ripples" manifest as: ideas, intuitions, and epiphanies.

So that is the first step.

Make your mind quiet.

Do that however you've learned how to do it.

But make sure you get into this state before you start trying to visualize anything. Otherwise it's useless.

You can't visualize in turmoil.

If you're fresh off one hour on IG... Forget visualization. You're gonna have to work doubly had to get to this first critical state.

Bring your mental activity to a grinding halt.

If you came here for results, don't skimp on this step. You'll sabotage everything else that follows.

But how do you get into that "still as a like" state?

You can do any of these activities:

Listen to your favorite music that calms you.

You can read a biography.

Lie down and let goooooo until you can feel or imagine your body floating.

It doesn't matter what you do to "calm your molecules".

Whatever works for you.

But once you finally get there...

You're ready.

But don't do what everyone has been telling you to do.

You don't "Visualize your goals."

That's useless.

Visualizing your goals is like having insomnia and trying to convince yourself to go to sleep.

It'll never work. The opposite happens. You lie awake like a zombie.

Goals are the same. You can't "convince" them to happen either. They can't be tricked into happening.

No, if you want to use the power of visualization right, you need to put your goals aside for visualization.

Articulate to yourself the deep-rooted reasons WHY this goal is important to you.

Why does this goal HAVE to happen at all costs?

Why, out of all the goals that exist in the world, did you choose THIS ONE?

Like... Is it so that you can finally buy your mom a house?

Or... So you can move out?

Or... So you can quit your job?

Or... So your kids can respect you?

Or... So you can collaborate with the artists you love?

(For some reason the most powerful reasons why always include people besides yourself. Those make your goals come to you faster.)

When you close your eyes, focus on THOSE reasons.

It should put a smile on your face AND fill you with healthy dose of angst at the same time.

The reason WHY you want your goal is always more inspiring than the goal itself.

So stay focused on that WHY. Keep it at the forefront of your mind.

It'll give you all the motivation you need.

Let yourself pile on the emotion.

Let yourself get worked up about it.

That's the level of emotion effective visualization requires.

You have to feel it so hard that for a few minutes, you'll feel like the WHY you're imagining is happening.

That's how you know that you're doing it right.

And when you get to that point, you have to add one last layer to begin the process of manifesting your goals for real.

This layer is the ingredient that self-help books don't teach.

Without this layer, people end up saying, "visualization doesn't work for me".

And others who DO get visualization to work? They're incorporating this layer by accident. Or by sheer instinct.

Visualization works for EVERYBODY if you add this last ingredient to the previous two:

After you've calmed your mind wayyyyy down...

And you're focusing on the reason WHY you want to achieve your goal in the first place...

Once you see it... And then you feel it...

The third step is:

Fill yourself with the feeling of EXPECTING it will happen (while you're still visualizing)...

Not "wanting".

It must be so powerful that it changes the whole energy around you.

People never get to this third step because they've been taught to protect themselves from disappointment. And that's why they settle for crumbs. And why they never tap into the real power of visualization.

In some circles they call this “the law of assumption”. Where you assume it’s already done. Yeah, but you have to act like it too.

Behaving with expectancy gives you clarity. Behaving with expectancy makes you DO things that encourage the inevitable to happen.

Expectancy makes you prepare-- and get your house in order.

Every action and interaction you have on your way to your goal will feel eerily scripted.

Behaving with expectancy redesigns the world around you in accordance with the image in your head.

It gives you fresh ideas to ACT upon.

How would you behave if you TRULY EXPECTED your goal to happen?

What habits would you drop? What conversations would you stop bothering with?

Start acting this way and epiphanies will start popping into your head about how to do what you're doing better.

Things you once questioned will have such "obvious" solutions and resolutions that you'll be like "What was wrong with me?"

Nothing was wrong with you. It's just that your newfound "expectancy" opened a few windows in the greenhouse of your mind.

When you're in true expectancy, you stop questioning the outcome. You have no temptation to do things that goes against the natural progression of things.

You'll see your future laid out before you like a story... And you'll simply follow the steps.

"Motivation" will be unnecessary.

You will make moves that fall in line with the outcomes you expect. Fully excited about the outcome.

This energy of inevitability will begin to influence everyone in your vicinity.

Your moves will attract person and circumstances that will help you achieve the things that you now EXPECT.

And you will finally experience the #1 gift that a state of expectancy gives you: You stop worrying about shit. You can be yourself now. You can concentrate on your evolution.

“The flower doesn’t dream of the bee. It blossoms, and the bee comes.” Mark Nepo

Why worry when you know the outcome?

All you have to do is follow the order of things:

Ideas and epiphanies will start to drop on you right away.

I'm not fucking with you. RIGHT. AWAY.

And within a few days...

People will start to move differently around you.

Try all of this for yourself. You'll see.

Don't tell anyone what you're doing, though.

Always... Mystery.

### 22. A Guide To Visualization (For Creatives Who Think 'The Secret' Is Bullshit)

#### (AKA Three Things About "Goal Visualization" That 'The Secret' Should Have Explained Better So It Could Actually Work For Those Who Put In The Time)

## 1. First, you need to calm the sea.

## 2. Visualize in full Cinemascopic Detail WHY you want your goal.

## 3. Finish your visualization with "Expectancy".

## Don't just visualize your future. Take every action you can think of taking-- in anticipation of the outcomes you desire. You must behave NOW like the person you want to become... Until it catches up with you.Make yourself a magnet for the future you desire.

### Calm your mind.

### Re-align yourself with WHY you want your goal.

### Get worked up about THAT. (Not the goal itself.)

### Visualize all the ACTIONS you would take if you EXPECTED your goals to materialize.

### Go out into the world and take those actions IMMEDIATELY.

### 23. The 12 Commandments Of The Mystery School

If your goal is to achieve flow...

If you desire to stop worrying and overthinking...

Here are the 12 Commandments Of The Mystery School

You may not understand them (or feel them in your bones yet), but you will soon:

Artists, athletes, and spiritual people have one job advantage over all other careers.

We get to tap into peak experience (flow) more than any other humans on the planet.

An artist that's stuck overthinking is wasting that gift.

NOTHING is more important than getting back to your essence.

And to get there, you start removing distractions out of your path like your creative life depended on it.

Having a daily practice keeps your feet planted inside your essence.

No matter what is happening outside.

Never deviating from your rituals gives you back your self-esteem.

IDEA > ACTION > RESULTS (REPEAT)

Worship The Mystery Formula.

(aka the iterative process, aka creative process aka the way even nature works).

It's how everything was ever invented

It's how all great art came into being.

As artists, we know that nothing comes out fully formed. This formula describes the alchemy of creation that's unobstructed by the ego.

Most people stay stuck on step 1, hoping to get to step 3.

Don't be "most people".

Anytime someone tells you about someone else... They will tell you a story to give you a feeling of who that person is.

What do they say about YOU in a world that's so noisy and distracted?

An artist always creates their story before others can.

I've never worked with a successful artist or brand who didn't have this part DOWN.

Understand this:

You matter.

I'd just love to see you tell the world why.

A Polaris Star is not your "goal".

A Polaris Star is the guiding light that will reveal what your goals need to be in order to get there.

A Polaris Star is the ONE thing to set your compass on.

What is this "better world" that you're trying to take us to?

Making art is easy.

People like to make it harder than it needs to be.

Somewhere in the middle of the creation process, they start overthinking... And judging... And engaging in various anti-art habits that they've picked up along the way.

Here's a better strategy.

Create ten things.

Share the best one.

Keep it moving.

Get out of your comfort zone.

Talk to strangers. Talk to your audience. Talk to other artists that you admire. Talk to brands you want to work with.

Don't allow yourself to stay in your little corner for too long.

Let the people that surround you add exponential fuel to your potential.

When you're wrapped up in "what people think," your art ends up looking like it.

The more you try to "make it perfect," the more you will lose the essence.

And that's when no one will care anyway.

And damn... You will have lined up another existential crisis for yourself.

It's a typical story:

People keep adding things and making everything more complicated. Out of ennui. Or because right now, they feel strong and inspired and like they can take the world on.

But the moment life kicks them in the ass (as it always does)-- They'll "stop everything" because too much had accumulated.

What then follows is a wasted year of "trying to get back to the initial spark".

Mystery Students please do this instead:

Take out the weeds every week. Reduce complexity. Ignore the bright shiny object distractions.

Instead of adding more to your plate...

Do your ONE thing more intensely.

Your goal is to create so much that you don't have to worry about quality.

"Quality" is what makes you decide what you're going to share.

Everything else becomes "experiments". And there should be a million experiments.

That's how you stay in flow.

That's how you get your momentum.

When you hit a new wall, it's not the "old you" that's gonna get you past it.

You need to become new.

Start doing everything that is the opposite of what you would normally do and see what happens.

You won't always be happy.

You won't always be sad.

So why not learn how to use both sides of the pendulum to make art?

It's the one gift that artists have over everyone else. Self-expression. So use it.

## THE BOOK OF MENTAL HEALTH: The Cure For Overthinking


### 1. The Cure For Overthinking (Part I & II)

Familiar with these?

Overthinking.

Writer's Block.

Depression.

Why is it that everyone always talks about the negative states our minds suffer from.

Hashtag mental health.

But hardly anyone ever talks about the ultimate POSITIVE state of mind that we should be striving to move towards.

Instead they talk about "happiness". A term that no one can agree on what it means.

Flow is the G.O.A.T. of mental states.

And the beauty of it is... When you experience "flow"... All those other negative states disappear.

That's why it's so important for creatives especially to know about it. And obsess eventually about it.

1. In this module I'm gonna show you exactly what it is.

2. But more importantly, I'm going to show you how you can reliably re-enter that state it on demand in your artistic life.

But to truly understand the universal and historical significance of this unique state of mind let me share this story:

When Pythagoras (one of the forefathers of mathematics-- 500 B.C.) was 20 years old, he tried to get into one of the most prestigious 'Mystery Schools' in Egypt.

But they wouldn't let him in.

Even though everyone knew he was a prodigy. A genius even.

But still, they rejected him cold.

Because he kept failing the special "entrance exam" that students needed to go through in order to get in.

The weird thing about this "entrance exam" is that, it was more like spiritual bootcamp. It had nothing to do with measuring someone's IQ, knowledge, or gifts.

Pythagoras was pissed. He couldn't believe it. This was totally unfair. Why were total losers getting in and not him?

He wrote a letter to the directors that said in a nutshell: "I only want to come to your school for knowledge. I shouldn't have to do all this other stuff. I have the right foundation already. Let me bypass this crazy step. I'll show you I'm worth it."

But they refused to bend the rules for him.

They even wrote him back (which they never do). In a boringly calm letter, they explained that the knowledge he was looking to acquire from them would be useless unless he went through this initial training.

What were they asking him to do?

1. 40 days of fasting,

2. master a special type of circular breathing and,

3. focus on something chose by an instructor for long periods at a time - daily.

And a whole bunch of other crazy woo woo stuff of the day.

So because he had no choice... He caved in.

He did their compulsory "bootcamp".

And got accepted. But what no one was expecting was the speech he would make at the initiation ceremony.

When he approached the directors of the school to accept his membership, he said these words looking directly at his new mentors:

"You aren't letting Pythagoras in. That person is gone now. I am a completely different man. I am reborn. You were right. My whole standpoint was intellectual before this spiritual training. Through this purification, my center has changed. I don't process experiences only through the intellect anymore. Things are not just a concept anymore. They are part me. I have become a new man. Thank you."

That “new person feeling" Pythagoras was experiencing— is a mental state that didn't have a name back then.

But it does now.

Flow is like electricity. No one invented it.

But in 1990 Mihaly Csikszentmihalyi, a psychologist, discovered it, analyzed it, described it and NAMED it.

In his book 'Flow: The Psychology Of Optimal Experience', he describes the 8 characteristics of "flow" in detail.

The more of these traits that you have... The more you know that you achieved it (but only in retrospect since you're not aware of it when it's happening):

In our modern world it plays out like this:

A group of LA girls having brunch at Joan's on 3rd might call it "connectedness".

Back-packing europeans who haven't showered in a week would probably call it "peak experience".

Religious fanatics... might use a fancy word like "enlightenment".

And athletes love to call it "being in the zone".

Runners lovingly describe it as "runner's high".

Computer programmers flex and say they're "locked-in".

But creatives...

Creatives now have their own special word for it too: "flow".

Flow the feeling you get in your core being that makes life feel like it's worth living.

And surprisingly, it doesn't seem to happen when you're chilling or on vaction.

It happens when you push yourself:

“The best moments in our lives are not the passive, receptive, relaxing times . . . The best moments usually occur if a person’s body or mind is stretched to its limits in a voluntary effort to accomplish something difficult and worthwhile” (Csikszentmihalyi, 1990).

You definitely know the feeling. Every artist has experienced it before

But maybe you haven't experienced it in a while...

Or when you do, you having trouble holding onto it.

Which is normal because everything we're surrounded with cause us to flirt more often with our negative states than nurturing our relationship with our positive states.

And when we're low... We band-aid these feelings with drugs, Netflix, scrolling Instagram and bad relationships.

Our whole culture is "waging war with anxiety".

Or "struggling with constant overthinking."

Or "BATTLING depression."

And it always ends badly.

You just can't win.

At least it seems that way.

When you follow the crowd.

But what about the one's who haven't fallen into the trap?

What are they doing?

They've figured out that you can REPLACE those mental habits with something much better.

You can at least lower the frequency of "feeling like sh-t".

Start practicing flow activities (it's coming, it's coming).

It turns out that every human being breathing can create flow on demand.

And it's not even that hard. It's not like you need a special talent or something.

You just have to line up a few conditions... in the right order.

Getting into that state of flow used to be the biggest mystery.

People thought that "either you have it or you don't".

They couldn't really explain how athletes, artists and religious people reached this special state.

But because of science, now you don't have to wait around for "flow to descend upon you" anymore.

You can trigger it. You can make it happen on purpose.

Using many of the things you used to do instinctively when you were younger.

You know. Until your friends started calling you a weirdo because of them.

Or until you had to give up your flow habits so you could fit in at work.

But good luck finding a consensus for the steps to achieve flow anywhere online or off.

The book (I read it when I was younger and cherish my underlined copy) has the best clues. But it's wordy, scientific and general. It's not directed to creatives.

That's what this module is for.

I will break down my 5 infallible steps (Made For Creatives™) so you can achieve flow regularily.

These 5 steps will get your 'inner child' magic back.

These 5 steps will make your abilities improve by up to 400% more than they usually are (that number is from official 'psychology of flow' statistics).

These 5 steps will take everyone else's 10,000 hours rule and make it become 3,000 hours for you (to attain mastery).

Rebuild your life around these 5 ideal "flow state" triggers.

One day soon, you will notice that many of the old negative mental habits have decreased, and some, melted away.

Let's get into it:

TYPE A. An activity you're good at. Find something that you're good at and try to outdo yourself. Pick something challenging but attainable. Preferably something repetitive. You should know all the steps it takes to achieve results even if you haven't achieved it yet. ("I know what I'm doing now. I know what I'm doing next.") Put aside enough time to do this thing every single day. (This is what I like to call having a 'DAILY PRACTICE'.)

TYPE B. An activity you suck at (newbie). Something that's outside of your comfort zone. Take a risk. Commit to trying something new. That's one of the reasons DRIVE-BY photoshoots are so amazing. Even if you're a photographer, they put you in unpredictable situations. Approaching strangers to take their picture gives you the ideal excuse to start a new episode of your little "movie" called life... But that's the only safety net it gives you. After that, you're in the hands of fate. And nothing focuses you more than having to deal with the total unknown. Especially when you're dealing with another human being on the other end... AND everyone else that you think is watching and judging.

TYPE C. An activity where you feel like you're giving back. The energy you radiate doing selfless acts shuts down the pre-frontal cortex. Leading you into flow.

You can even combine all three as I've done so often in the past:

My A: I'm pretty good at taking pictures, but I know where I can improve. When I hold my camera I'm always consciously trying to.

My B: Approaching strangers is always rolling the dice. Each new person presents new challenges. I never pick someone I think will be "easy".

My C: My favorite shoots are the ones where the person feels empowered. It's not even about pictures anymore. It's about helping someone (your muse) reach a new level of personal expression.

Start thinking about the activity you're gonna do waaaay before you do it. Go to bed thinking about your flow activity with a smile on your face. (This is going one level further than "planning your day the night before". Now, you spend every waking moment visualizing. You go through/rehearse it in your mind. Dream about it.) Visualize the process more than you visualize the result. Play it forwards. Play it backward. Make peace with delaying the gratification of the result. Romanticize every step of the process through your daydreams. By the time you get to start it for real, you'll find you slip right into the groove easily. No ramp up. No context switching.

Prepare 90 minutes to 5 hours of uninterrupted concentration. A environment of absolute focus. No screens. No phones. No social media. No music. And if possible... No people.

Sorry but, you'll never reach flow with Instagram sending you notifications.

And if you're always checking your phone in the morning?

Well, you just walked yourself backwards from achieving optimal experience... To backing into the arms of anxiety.

It's also time to reduce choices.

The more choices you have the more inner conflict.

More choices give more uncertainty which steals your energy and resolve.

See how we’re moving further and further from flow in this sentence already.

"Energy multipliers" like:

Diaphragm breathing.

A cold shower.

Meditation.

Gratitude. (Think of ONE reason why you know you're blessed. But don't just think it... FEEL that gratitude deep inside your stomach. Then think of another reason. Let it transport you. Think of 3 reasons why you are blessed. Let the feeling wash over you.)

The more often you do your flow activity, the easier it will be for you to slip back into "flow".

The more time you set aside to be creative, the easier it is for you to enter flow.

You'll have less time to overthink, feel anxiety, or descend into depression. These afflictions keep you focused on yourself.

Flow keeps you focused on "outside of yourself". It keeps your mind on the work.

How does it do that?

When you achieve flow, your pre-frontal cortex shuts down (the part of your brain responsible for ego, your inner critic, making decisions, reasoning, willpower, morality, planning, time calculations etc.)

Remember in the story above when Pythagoras said:

"I don't process experiences only through the intellect anymore."

That's what was happening.

And also... In flow, you produce more dopamine (reward chemical), serotonin (mood stabilizer), and endorphins (pain killers) and oxytocin (love hormone) than in any other natural state. (So, yeah, I guess you can say it's like you're on the best Molly and Aderral at the same time)

As you will soon see:

Each "book" in The Mystery School is designed to get you into your unique version of the flow state.

From what I get you to do in 'The Book Of Dares'... Those "drive-bys" put you in new situations where you're "out of body" and forced to be in the moment.

'The Book Of Purpose'... teaches you to find meaning in what you do. Having purpose creates a state of mind where you're focused on a cause that's bigger than yourself.

'The Book Of Influence'... will make you reframe all the distractions that exist around you so that they become slaves to your goals and focus.

To 'The Book Of Transformation'... Which is all about reaching God Momentum. God Momentum is just a fancy way of saying "a level of 'flow' that doesn't stop after the activity stops.

God Momentum is when you make "flow" a way of life.

Go out there and do it.

### 2. Why You Keep Hitting A Wall

I've heard the creative process described like this:

A student emailed last night to tell me that she hit a wall. And "Did I have any ideas of how to get around it?"

I knew that particular wall so well. So I sent her a solution.

It worked beautifully. As it always does.

Two weeks later, she emailed again to tell me that my "trick" wasn't working anymore.

That's always what happens.

The first time worked because she was trying something different.

But the next time didn't work because she went into a fresh situation with an old tool... Expecting the same result.

Oh, we'd love to think that there's a formula, wouldn't we?

A universal fix-all that would make creativity less painful.

But then art would be more like math.

You wouldn't want that, would you?

Instead of trying to find ways to make "easier", why don't you approach the artistic process more like a video game?

Every time you figure out a level...EXPECT to develop completely NEW tricks to unlock the NEXT level.

Don't look for "cheat codes".

All you can do is develop the tenacity to try new things until you find a solution that no one ever dreamed of.

That's what gave us Skrillex.

That's what gave us Joaquin Phoenix.

That's what gave us Kardi B.

They go past where others have gone before them.

And the unique discoveries they make become part of their arsenal. (And what everyone else tries to copy)

So the next time you hit a wall or start hearing the voices of doubt, that darkness is your cue...

Time to dig deeper.

Just like your heroes did.

That wall you're facing... Is where everyone else stops.

Find new "truths" that no one else has found.

A new turn of phrase. A new sound. A new way of looking at the world.

Until you unlock this new level.

You have new abilities.

You have newfound strength.

You have made discoveries that few know about.

You will share some of your souvenirs with others who have never traveled there.

While other secrets will be yours alone.

Some of these new "truths" will become the "keys" that will open doors in this new world of yours. Doors that will remain closed to anyone else that hasn't gone to your depths yet.

Collect these "truths".

THAT'S the continuous journey of being an artist. Of finding these "truths"

So quickly embrace your lulls. And your "blocks". And your lows.

Leave space for the unknown

Don't be afraid of uncertainty.

Use the laws of nature to your advantage.

Ideas hate a vacuum.

So blow a wide-open hole in your comfort zone to speed up your next magical breakthrough.

Let the doubts linger so you can learn something.

All great art is preceded by perseverance into the unknown.

And when it finally comes... It pops out with almost no effort.

Just like when you're cradling a screaming baby after birth, you will immediately forget all the pain it took to get there.

This wall right now...

It's not in front of you because you suck.

It's art's way of telling you that it doesn't want to be science or math.

It wants to be like a game.

It wants to surprise you.
