### 3. State of Mind: Level 4

Ok so, is everything going as fast as you want it to go?

Or do you still need to get your "state of mind" right?

Here are the levels in ascending order (I'll be going in detail in upcoming modules):

Narrowed goals. I know your ego wants you to be a musician / painter / poet / director. And you WILL be all of those things one day. But for now, become GREAT at one thing. Build a strong audience with it. THEN switch.

Your phone? The enemy. Bingeing shows? The enemy. The current news cycle? The enemy.

Time to focus.

Consistency is queen. Only when you're focused can you be consistent.

Drop bombs more often.

But there is one state of mind that I hardly get to talk about.

Because most people are still trying climb the first 3.

It's my favorite one.

Here it is if you're ready for it.

It's tempting to separate our lives into neat little boxes.

Creative time. Time to hang out with friends. Work. Alone time etc.

But the reality is...

If you're creative, that creativity is always bubbling under and waiting to be expressed.

Creativity is a perpetual motion machine.

That's why you get amazing ideas at the weirdest times.

It's always below the surface. Working away...

But armed with this knowledge, there are two things you can do to maximize more frequent appearances of the muse in your life.

One of them you're already doing.

You learned it in the last module:

But the other way to unleash your creativity's full power is to get rid of the boxes.

It may not feel natural at first. And some moments will be downright awkward.

"Father Bronques... You want me to see even my fights with my boyfriend as part of my creative flow? And even when I'm going for a shit? Like, how far are we taking this here?"

All the way.

If you want to improve your artistic output quality, change your relationship to everything you used to call mundane and undesirable.

Observe your heroes. Read their biographies. Watch their documentaries. How did they behave on their ascent?

Imagine how much energy you'd have if you stopped judging everything.

Imagine how your mind would relax when you stop being at war with your schedule. And started seeing everything as connected instead.

Some of it is "maintenance". Some are activities you can't delegate to an assistant. Like visiting your grandmother... Or eating... Or going to the gym.

Activities you'll say are "stealing time away from your art"?

When the truth is...

What you do when you're NOT being creative has more influence on your art than anything else.

So why not treat it with that kind of respect?

People have it half right when they say stuff like, "I need to 'go live a little' so I have something to say in my art."

But where they have it wrong is that they think they need to travel orsuffer trauma. No, no. Chill out.

You're experiencing things every day.

You just haven't been paying attention to the nuances.

Remember that funny scene in the Ray Charles movie?

The one where he's is fighting with his girl about "keeping the baby"? And she starts crying. And he's yelling. But suddenly, he realizes that this moment contains a bottled essence of great emotion... So he starts singing...

"Hit The Road Jack..."

And he starts playing the piano and writes the song.

Even she starts singing! Mad as hell and crying, she STILL understands:

You can't stop creativity.

So yeah, I DO want you to see your "fights with your boyfriend" as part of your creative flow from now on.

That and everything else.

(I remember a student taking two weeks off because their relationship was on the rocks. What?)

So let's imagine that from now on, activities like going to the gym will no longer be called "going to the gym"...

Rename it. Call it something like "exercising mental fortitude for my next deep dive in my writing".

Give care and attention to activities like flossing your teeth and doing your taxes.

The reward?

More energy in the totality of your existence. More flow. More art.

You will become a perpetual motion machine.

If you've never considered this, it may be uncomfortable to hear the first time around.

Maybe it challenges your whole belief system.

If so... Ignore it for now.

Just make a mental note for later when you're at an important crossroad soul-searching.

Continue here to the next module if you like...

If you've had similar thoughts already...

And all you needed was validation, or "permission", or a sign to dive right in...

<sounds of angels and trumpets>

The old way is over.

"Leading an uninspired day and expecting great art to emerge" is a construct of the past.

That used to work just fine:

You wrestled with your mind-- and eventually art came out.

But I want you to be more than "fine" for you.

"Imagine what it would look like if it were easy."

There's a whole new world waiting to show up at your creative doorstep when you start looking at the entire picture of your life as ONE LONG FLOW ACTIVITY.

Are you ready to adopt this? Start right after you read this. You'll feel the change immediately. So will everyone around you.

It's that powerful.

Inject creativity in every "in-between" moment of your day.

No matter how awkward.

Even if the normals call you "eccentric".

And let your language reflect the changes. Other Level 4 creatives will understand you right away.

(These sentences are all taken from real life. From famous people who's work you consume. From people I know you admire. So shhhhhh.):

"Everything I do, I do it for art. There's no point in the day where I'm not trying to sneak it in there."

"I only sleep so I have more energy and ideas. And the only reason I eat is so I don't crash when all my best ideas start coming."

"I wake up at 4 am. I drink water, but I don't eat. I meditate. I know it doesn't sound creative. But without it, I'm useless."

"If I didn't walk my dogs every morning, I wouldn't have written (hit song)."

You get the idea.

Now, how about you?

What "crazy" things will come out of your mouth when you start living every moment like they're scenes from a movie?

### 4. The Existential Crisis Checklist

And here you are again.

In this familiar place: Your reccuring cycle of doubt.

Who put you in this state this time?

What happened in your life to cause this?

Trick question.

You know it has nothing to do with "them" or the outside world.

How you see the world is up to you.

And you're seeing it in a negative way right now.

Could it be because you...

You feel like you've stopped growing?

An artist that's not growing feels lackluster.

Like somethings off.

Like they're not living to their full potential.

And it's sneaky. It creeps up on you.

You may not notice it at first. Especially if you've been blending in with the "normals" who make a habit out of living like this no problem.

But for an artist... "Phoning it in" kills us.

The reason you feel bad / lost / uncentered isn't because of one bad thing that happened, or because you woke up on the wrong side of bed today...

The feelings you have right now are the result of an accumulation of little things that you stopped doing.

Somewhere along the way, maybe you got cocky.

You started believing the Hallmark Cards.

And you stopped doing the things that brought you to your power in the first place.

Despite the fact that me and everyone else around you knows you're amazing... YOU totally forgot.

Because youu stopped doing the things that reinforce your gifts.

And now you feel "lesser than".

From now on... The moment you feel bad, let it trigger a part of your brain that asks:

"What did I stop doing that allowed this feeling to creep up on me again?"

Here is a checklist of questions for you to come back to every time you feel like it's all going to shit:

If you aren't doing these things (the energy builders), why would you expect to be feeling good right now?

You're an artist. You need to re-align with artist-on-the-rise behaviors.

If you don't feel like immediately correcting the things you're missing above ask yourself:

Do I love the angst?

Do I love the drama?

Do I love the emotional distress?

Does it make me feel "alive"?

If so... Am I using it at least to create something incredible?

The fact that you're reading this is promising.

Live up to that promise with what you decide to do next.

Your audience is waiting for you to get back to the mission.

### 4. The Existential Crisis Checklist

## 1. Are you doing your daily practice? Are you CREATING every day?

## 2. Are you staying off social media and other mind-numbing distractions? Especially in the morning. Especially at night.

## 3.Are you journaling?(This is too basic. It's crazy.) Have you read back the last few weeks to see if your current angst isn't all in your head? Are you falling in any noticeable pattern?

## 4. Are you suffering from"Complication Creep"? Is it time to simplify your goals back to their essence?

## 5. Did you write a note to yourself when you were feeling good -- so that you could re-read it in times like these, to remind yourself what your priorities are?

## 6. Have you created an environment for yourself with multiple cues to remind you of your goals? Have you "refreshed them" so that they don't blend into the background (and the recesses of your mind).

## 7. Are you hanging out with positive, vibrant people?

## 8. Are you stretching, breathing, working out, meditating?

## 9. Are you getting enough sleep?

### 5. Journaling: The Art Of Collecting Your Truth

If you already know WHY journaling is important-- skip to the bottom for:

HOW TO JOURNAL FOR TRANSFORMATION

You've heard it a million times:

You should journal.

And for some reason, you still don't do it.

"I'm not a writer."

"I'll remember. I don't need to write it down."

"I tried. But I fell off..."

You say you want to succeed at any cost? And that you were "made for this"? But then you're too lazy to put all the chances on your side by doing the MOST BASIC thing that speeds up the journey?

Tell me... Especially if you have big goals... Like, G.O.A.T. level goals...

How will you know how you're doing?

Especially on the days when you feel disillusioned?

Are you going to rely on your memory?

What did you do for your career last Thursday? And the Monday before that? How does this July compare with July last year with your sleep habits?

Uh-huh... Your memory ain't so good now is it?

Your diary is your memory.

"I don't need to write it down," is laziness parading as bravado.

Your mind doesn't WANT to remember.

People like to remember their past as worse or better than it was.

When you're feeling down, you think you always sucked.

And when you're on cloud nine... Everything goes through rose-colored glasses.

This is fun if you're writing a script or a novel... But it's not helpful for self-improvement or for your mental health.

That's why you keep a journal. To see your journey without the influence of your current emotions.

Get rid of the "filters". Start building the next version of yourself swiftly. Analyze your journey without the influence of your current emotions.

Face the numbers. Face the data.

Creatives are like athletes:

We need to keep track of our progress when we've put ourselves on a path to change the world.

We're emotional people, but emotions deceive. That's why we keep a journal as an insurance policy against that deception.

People seek help every time they're at the same point of their cycle of doubt.

But they don't even realize it's a cycle. They don't even realize that it's the same point every time because they don't journal.

Without a journal, you keep learning the same lessons over and over again.

Why not build on the wisdom you've accumulated instead?

Know your trends.

As student Mayra says:

"We shouldn't be fighting our biology.My menstrual cycle and natural hormonal changes influences my mental state and creative output. Knowing that it's normal prevents me from entering a downward mental spiral. Instead... I can plan my work around it. I can plan a different kind of TODO list created for exactly those days. And progress can continue..."

And boys? You have a biological cycle too. Use journaling to help you figure it out.

So, you're thinking about getting meds for your anxiety? Maybe that's the right solution for you. But have you TRIED a solution that's worked for millions of people throughout the ages?

It's available without a prescription.

I'll show you how to do it in a fun, addictive way.

Wanna get out of those dark times quicker?

Write it all down.

"There's something magical about writing things down."

The philosopher Wittgenstein stated it first. At least that's what someone told me when I told him that I've been keeping a diary since I was 14.

Wittgenstein discovered that when you put your thoughts down on paper... It's much easier to throw them away.

It's like finishing a jigsaw puzzle.

It's like, over. Done.

That's what writing your thoughts down does.

Seriously. Have you ever notice how many G.O.A.Ts talk about keeping a journal?

But they never tell you why.

They say "softball" things like it's "for gratitude".

Well, if you're the "heated yoga" type of person, then I guess that's a good enough answer.

But for the rest of us, Nah.

This why journaling is powerful:

So that you can see your trends.

It's essential to be able to read about all the times you ridiculously thought "your life was over"... But somehow, you overcame.

A journal is a testament to what you've been through AND survived.

And the way I will teach you to journal in this module, you will be able to finally use that "data" to your benefit.

Before you start journaling, you'll need a frame for this new experience.

Write these two things down:

YOU HAVE TO BE ABLE TO SEE THESE TWO STATEMENTS EVERY SINGLE DAY YOU WAKE UP. OTHERWISE, YOU'LL FORGET THEM. AND BELIEVE ME, 'THEY' WANT YOU TO FORGET THEM. 'THEY' DON'T WANT TO BE SHAMED WITH YOUR INCREDIBLE WORK ETHIC.

Now for the fun part:

Your new journal is about to become be the un-edited novel of how you achieved your goals.

A "tracking journal" is a special type of journaling.

It's "data entry" so that you can discover your "truths" (more on that later).

It's the "creative athlete's" alternative to a diary-style journal.

The basic concept is this:

Imagine you went to the gym three times a week, but you didn't keep track of how many sets, reps, the order and time it took. You would take longer than everyone else to progress.

Creatives are like athletes in that regard.

And the bigger the goals, the more intense the documentation of your progress has to be.

But remember

Journaling isn't writing. We don't care about spelling or punctuation.

You're not trying to win a literary award.

Your journal can be all point form entries if you want.

Or diagrams.

Or lists of ideas.

You can even put it in the form of a spreadsheet if you like (how I do it half the time).

Here are a few ways people do it:

This is the most common type for a reason. It's easy, and it works.

Perfect for you if you don't wanna be touchy-feely about it. (Whenever I'm about to undergo an intense transformation,I move my journaling to a Google docs spreadsheet.This enables me to see all the data every day at one glance.)

Look... It doesn't matter what you choose.

You're creative. Be creative with it.

The only thing that matters is that you make it something that YOU'LL enjoy going to every day.

And don't worry... It'll get sexier the moment you start seeing results.

Here are the things you need to document every day in a tracking journal (you can write more, but these are key):

(Wait 'till you see what you learn just from these 4 data points over a few weeks. It's astounding.)

Other things people like to document based on their personal goals:

What did you eat today? (Dancers and musicians especially. You'd be surprised how much food plays into your moods and productivity.)

What did you buy (like Warhol did in The Andy Warhol Diary at the end of every entry. You'll also be able to keep track of if you suffer "shiny object syndrome" or "too many mentors".)

But the journaling game-changer is this last step:

In the back of your journal, start collecting your TRUTHS.

Start a new page with this title in bold: MY TRUTHS.

The "MY TRUTHS" section is a collection of the indisputable lessons that you will figure out along the way.

They are the "cannot-miss" learnings that will become part of your personal bible. (One day you'll be able to turn them into your own Mystery School).

When you collect enough of these TRUTHS... You stop feeling like a passenger in your own life.

You start navigating new situations as if you've already been down that road before. Your past experiences become metaphors for your unique challenges.

Most people only develop their "truths" through the hard lessons of life or by extreme trauma.

What a horrible and painful way to learn.

And so slow.

And it leaves you bitter.

This Mystery School ' tracking journal' will get you there faster and with grace.

By continually taking inventory of who you are along the way... And who you are becoming... You know that challenges are only plot-twists in your story.

Journaling for others is "writing things down".

For you, it's the documentation of creating A LIFE THAT'S A WORK OF ART.

It's where you put the subtle touches on your "personal culture".

Soon you will "Know thyself."

After months of journal tracking, you will re-read sections and see how much of a legend you are.

You will read about moments where you thought life was over and see how you got out of those messes in vivid detail.

And THAT'S what will reinforce your memory.

Your Mystery School journal will flow like a script for an action-thriller-comedy.

There are two moments in your life when you will "figure it all out":

1. When you have the perfect window to apply it.

2. When it's too late.

Start today.

To be the best version of yourself requires courage.

How do you get that confidence?

By knowing yourself.

How do you get to "know thyself"?

1. By keeping a journal and learning your trends.

2. By converting those trends into your TRUTHS.

Identify your strengths. This will give you confidence.

Understand your weaknesses. This will give you wisdom.

Start tracking your progress right now even if you feel like you aren't doing much.

That's how every movie starts. With the protagonist "not doing much".

Just before their greatest adventure.

Isn't it time to document yours?

Here is a GOOGLE SPREADSHEET you can download to get you started. (It's what I use when I need a military-style focus.)

This is from Benjamin Franklin's journal. Year? 1720.

This is a spreadsheet Benjamin Franklin created when he was 20 years old. Every day he ticked off the virtues that he accomplished.

This is a spreadsheet that Dom (Mystery Student) created to keep track of how many songs he's done so far on his "1,000 songs in a year" goal.

Download my GOOGLE SPREADSHEET example to get you started. Click on FILE > Make A Copy. (This is exactly what I use when I need a military-style focus.)

### 6. TRIFECTA I: Meditation Is An Artform (And 7 Other Truthlotions About Meditation)

Ever notice how many of the people who preach about meditation online are often no better off than you?

If you want to do meditation “right”, ignore the people who have curated a pretty online aesthetic with accompanying trigger words to draw you in. They’re still working out their childhood traumas. Instead, look for people who exemplify the outcome that meditation promises.

You know the ones I mean...

People who may have never meditated one day in their life— But yet are outrageously calm…

People who always centered during moments of drama…

People who always have the best outlook on things.

ust being around them makes YOU calm.

Their attitude is infectious.

Somehow they never seem to lose that "light".

When you come across people like that, ask them their secret.

It'll give you clues to figure out yours.

You brush your teeth. You check your phone. You eat. And sometimes… you meditate:

Meditation, for most people, is an activity:

You put aside 20 minutes... You sit in the lotus position... You close your eyes... You are listening to your "calm app" through ear pods…

Meditation has become just another time slot for capitalism to exploit.

That… Is not meditation.

Meditation, when you're REALLY doing it… Isn't an activity at all.

Meditation is what happens beyond those 20 minutes.

Before the 20 minutes?

All your emotions and reactions get triggered by outside stimuli.

Your annoying roommate barges into your room…Triggered.

You see a pretty girl on Instagram… Triggered.

You see something crazy on the news… Triggered.

You get a hunger pain… Triggered.

LA Traffic… Triggered.

The outside world was throwing you around like a volleyball, and you let it…

But, after the 20 minutes…

You enter a state of mind where the reactionary nonsense STOPS.

You become an observer again.

You stop being identified with every little thing your ego puts in front of you.

Those 20 minutes you spent with your eyes closed… were the warm-up to put you into that state of centeredness.

After those 20 minutes, the meditation BEGINS.

In the real world.

You stay in the state you were in with your eyes closed… WITH EYES OPEN.

The 20 minutes was you warming up the car. Meditation is the long scenic drive that you take afterward.

Life throws distractions at you, but you're not taking the bait… Nah, you're meditating.

The 20 minutes were a warm-up to get to that state of centeredness.

A state which aligns you with "your truth".

Where you see things for what they are again.

Where you regain your free will.

No more living your life mechanically.

You're hungry? "Oh, interesting. I'll take care of that later."

The weather isn't what you wanted? "Good to know. Maybe I'll catch a rainbow."

Someone shades your outfit? "Note to self. They're hurting inside. Send them a get-well card."

The 20 minutes isn't an activity that you do so that you could go back to scrolling Instagram immediately after.

Would you pull up to Dairy Queen right after an awesome workout to go get a large Smarties Blizzard?

Extend whatever energy you get while “sitting”, into everything else that you do for the rest of the day. That is how your new consciousness will emerge.

Most people come to meditation for "relaxation" and "calmness".

Instead, all they get is a boring and uncomfortable experience.

If I had been introduced to meditation that way, it would have turned me off too.

No wonder so many beginners think "it's not for them."

No wonder the word itself has become a barrier to people even trying it.

If you haven't felt a wonderful experience meditating, it's probably because you glossed by the first crucial step.

It's like learning how to swim.

First, you learn how to float, right?

And once you've mastered that… then you get to the swimming part, right?

Step 1. Floating.

Step 2. Swimming.

One builds on the other.

Same thing with meditation.

Before you can hope to do 20 minutes that will relax you, you have to use those 20 minutes to get rid of your demons.

Don't call it meditation.

It isn't yet.

"Learning how to sit with yourself."

Before you can reap the benefits of meditation, you have to learn how to sit with yourself FIRST.

The truth is, you might not get to the meditation part for weeks.

But that's ok…

You're preparing the ground.

You're learning… "how to float".

I was able to go so deep, so fast, the first time I "went there" because I've always been comfortable "sitting with myself". It's a typical artist's DNA trait.

For many creatives, "going inside" is second nature, much like those Native American babies who get thrown in the water at birth. They never have to "learn" how to float.

But if that's not you… If you weren't "thrown in the water" as a newborn, you can still "learn how to swim". You can still learn how to be comfortable sitting with yourself.

Why is this so important?

Your breath keeps you alive, but you have never learned to pay attention to it. And you never pay attention to your heart. Or to the sounds in your surroundings. Or to other people's energy unless they're entering your space. The only thing you pay attention to is what other people have put in front of you. You have given yourself an illusion of choice. While everything that actually makes life meaningful has faded into the background for you. What kind of art do you think you can offer with this kind of limited perspective? Most people only "wake up" when there is a tragedy. Or trauma. Or illness. A major loss. Or Death. Only then do they start to feel everything around you again. Only then they pay attention.

Don't be like those people.

Take your destiny into your own hands.

People usually come to meditation when things are going wrong in their life.

But when you approach something as a fix-all, you will come high with expectations.

And expectations is the #1 "experience killer".

That's why meditation never works for you.

The good news about meditation is that it's easy.

But the bad news is that meditation will be excruciatingly hard for most people BEFORE it gets easy.

Sitting with yourself for 20 minutes every day in this fast-paced world, takes a TREMENDOUS amount of effort and discipline… BEFORE it becomes effortless.

Watching your mind race like crazy will cause you inner turmoil… BEFORE the inner chatter finally disappears, and you're "exuding calm vibes".

So start this journey by embracing that none of this is SUPPOSED to be comfortable at first.

The very fact that it's uncomfortable shows you just how much you need it.

It's like if you went outside and tried to run for a few miles and found yourself out of breath after a few blocks… Then you'd know that you're exactly the person who needs to work out more.

Seriously… Think about it. You can't sit there for more than a few minutes without fidgeting? Or going into "panic mode"? Or "dying of boredom"?

That's a problem, dude.

You have no control over your mind. And that's why you're a prime candidate for anxiety, mood swings, and most of all… the lack of flow in your life.

But I know a deep secret about you that you may have forgotten.

I know that you can endure the "uncomfortable part" to get to the "rewarding part"?

And how do I know that?

Well, because that's the same energy that it takes to make art…

Am I wrong?

How often have you endured the uncomfortable part… to get to the rewarding part, right?

You should be an expert at it by now.

People often come to meditation when things are going wrong in their life. But when you approach something as a fix-all, you will come with expectations. And expectations is the #1 “experience killer”. And that is why meditation never works for you.

People who have gotten results from meditation often try to recreate that initial high. Like a drug addict chasing the dragon. But expectations is the #1 “experience killer”. And that is why meditation NO LONGER works for you.

Instead allowed it to be a new experience. (Just like you should do with parties. Or Coachella. Or traveling to familiar destinations. Always let it be its own new experience.)

Let it be a new experience. Or a variation of an old experience. Allow the teacher you need to appear.

It's time for you to think of meditation as the art form that it is.

Meditation is the art form that improves all the other art forms.

You are 60% water. Meditation is the art of… Making that water as still as a pond. Now even the slightest intention will ripple into the new ideas, new opportunities, new cheat codes, and new synchronicities that make life worth living.

Meditation is the art of… Seeing everything around you for what it is— Without losing who YOU are in the process.

Meditation is the art of… Living in the eye of a cyclone. The world is raging around you, but you are still undisturbed and calm.

Meditation is the art of… appreciating life without needing a wake-up call of tragedy or trauma.

Meditation is the art of… feeling all the world's subtle frequencies-- and then using those frequencies as brushstrokes in your art.

While the normals are trying to "preserve their energy"... You won't need to do any of that.

A centered artist CREATES energy—more than they could ever use.

Once you master sitting with yourself, the meditation part will happen all on its own.

You'll start to experience a low hum of limitless energy that accompanies all the activities that you engage in.

Eventually, it becomes your whole aura.

And EVERYTHING you do will be… MEDITATIVE.

Painting, writing, making music, eating, and hanging out with friends. All of it.

All great artists have their version of meditation. People have different names for it. But when you find it for yourself, you recognize all of its faces.

Only someone who can become an observer will have free will.

Only someone that isn't living life on automatic… Has the agency to determine their future.

I've been meditating my whole life.

I've been meditating before I realized it was called meditation.

But because my process was so different than what other people were describing, I had no clue I had tapped in.

I believe that everyone can discover THEIR OWN set of rituals. Rituals that will help them restore their vitality.

Let's find yours.

Everything you will read here… They aren't laws. They're clues.

You don't have to invest 20 minutes. It can be more. Or less. As long as you're pushing yourself past your comfort zone, you will get better at it.

It's not about doing it at a particular time of day.

And it doesn't have to be done sitting in the lotus position. You can do it lying down, sitting on a bus, walking, standing against a wall… Anywhere.

And you don't have to breathe a certain way.

So if you're not focusing on your breath, what should you be "doing"?

Practice doing nothing.

Close your eyes and feel the "me, myself and I-ness of it".

Hang out there.

Don't expect anything special to happen.

No "concentration" is needed.

Don't expect it to relax you.

That isn't the point.

The point… is to stop looking for a point. Can you do that for 20 minutes?

It will be anything but relaxing.

It'll get you agitated if anything.

No apps. Using an app on your phone to meditate is like lighting scented candles near a gas station.

When you want to get centered, get to your essence, or engage in flow… Please put your phone and everything that's a distraction as far away as physically possible.

TRUTHLOTION: If you can't give your mind those periodical breaks from the external world, then you're probably not ready to be a dedicated artist yet.

Let the unplanned sounds that surround you be the soundtrack.

Let things be.

Don't condemn your thoughts. Don't judge your thoughts. Don't fight your thoughts.

Just watch your thoughts… Like when you're watching Netflix and you have no expectations of the plotline.

Feel bored.

Feel restless.

Allow crazy thoughts. Allow overthinking.

Your mind will ask you "Why the fuck you are doing this?"

Laugh at it.

And remember that none of this is meditation yet. These are the obstacles on your way to mediation.

Fight through it.

Don't concentrate on your breath.

Don't concentrate on anything.

Don't DO anything.

Babe, you're always DOING something.

This is the 20 minutes when you will DO nothing.

And it'll be hard at first. Like the first day at the gym. When even a 10-pound weight will cause you pain.

Or like your first jog… After 1 minute, you're already out of breath, and you want to stop.

Don't stop.

Stay there for the full 20 minutes (or whatever you decide).

Freaking out a little? Panicking a little? Feeling like your whole existence is in jeopardy or something?

Let yourself sit through whatever goes through your mind.

Let yourself remember that the world will be fine without your contribution.

You're preparing the ground.

You're taking inventory of all the weeds you'll have to remove.

You'll keep coming back to this painful 20 minutes every day until you know all the weeds in your garden by name. Until you can do a daily weed "roll call" in reverse alphabetical order. It's only then that all those distracting thoughts that used to control you start to lose their power. And one by one… they will die.

The point is letting yourself feel whatever you feel right now…

Let yourself freak out.

Let yourself feel boredom.

Watch and feel things without judging.

It's not "good".

It's not "bad".

Until you can do this... "Sitting with yourself and doing nothing at all.." Your mind will give you lifelong problems.

Not being able to STOP the hamster wheel… Will be the #1 cause of distress in your life.

And then, one day, the hamster wheel stops spinning.

You have shifted.

You realize that you are observing things instead of reacting.

And that you are "responding" to things instead of reacting.

Not just when your eyes are closed! But also when they're wide open.

I can't tell you when it will happen for you, but I promise you it will.

You will start to see how ridiculous all those thought patterns you used to invest in are. And when they pop up in the middle of the day? You will recognize them for what they are, and you will be immune to their effects.

The new you feels energy, notices colors, and refuses drama.

You're constantly "receiving" new ideas and hearing new sounds.

You start experiencing something scientists lovingly call "synaptic fire".

And everything you touch feels like "flow".

Flow is nothing more than meditation in action.

Creating your most extraordinary art requires you to perceive things that other people just miss.

And then filter that sensitivity through a unique perspective.

And then you have to be talented enough to express these discoveries in an interesting way.

All of that requires tapping into an energy source that most people have no clue about.

And now you have.

### 7. TRIFECTA II: 10 ‘Sleep Hygiene’ Rituals + The Fast Sleep Military Protocol

High-level creativity comes from deep focus followed by deep rest.

If you've been feeling daytime energy crashes, insomnia, or you always wake up multiple times a night-- you probably have bad sleep hygiene.

When you're serious about sleep, you set TWO alarms. One for when you want to wake up in the morning. And the other (more important) one for when it's time to start your "wind-down" ritual. Without a wind-down ritual, you're ripe for insomnia and interrupted sleep patterns.

Sleep hygiene = healthy habits BEFORE sleep.

If you want to make more art, generate more flow moments, or even party harder without needing drugs… Start getting obsessive about your sleep hygiene.

Like most good things, the results won't be instant. But if you hang in there, your life will change for the incredible within a few weeks.

You should be in lala land by now… You may be sleep anxious (when you don’t sleep because you’re worried about not sleeping), after having battled insomnia for a while. If so, just start again from STEP 4, until your mind gives in.

Will everything be perfect every night? Of course not. "Life" is not a straight line. It will throw you curve balls. Don't let discipline be your failing. That lame. Only real-life events like weddings, birthdays, or consoling a friend should disrupt your routine… And when it does (it always does)... It's all good. Just slip back into your creativity-inducing rituals the following day.

I'm excited for you to figure out your own "wind down ritual" and perfect your own version of the "fast sleep protocol". Let me know if you come up with amazing personal practices that I can share.

### 7. TRIFECTA II: 10 ‘Sleep Hygiene’ Rituals + The Fast Sleep Military Protocol

## Part I: Here are 10 'sleep hygiene rules I live by when I'm entering a new phase of outrageous creative output:

### 1. Go to bed at the same time every night. It worked for Picasso (3 am). It works for Steven King (10 pm).

### 2. Never sleep in. But remember, "sleeping in" is relative. It isn't about what time you wake up. This rule only means don't sleep beyond 8 or 9 hours. If you don't feel rested after 8 hours, take a nap later instead.

### 3. Naps are magical. At the beginning... You may have to pay the price of insomnia with some non-restful nights. Compensate by napping early in the day (only once). Do it sometime between 11am - 2pm. And for 20-30 minutes max. That's how you'll still be able to fall asleep easier that night. Use this until your insomnia goes away and your circadian clock is re-set for your new bedtime.

### 4. Have your last meal as far away from "lights out" as possible. And avoid spicy food.

### 5. Don't drink alcohol to "help you sleep". Yeah, you may doze off faster, but it prohibits DEEP SLEEP. Why should you care? 'Deep sleep' is the sleeping stage for body and brain repair. This is when your immune system gets strengthened. If you want to be one of those people who only gets sick once every couple of years, here's the key.

### 6. Create a "wind-down ritual" for yourself. (THIS IS THE MOST IMPORTANT RULE) What you do one hour before “lights off is EVERYTHING. Best practices? Set an alarm for when it begins so you STOP WORKING. 1. Shut off screens (that means phones, laptops, IPADs, and no TV). 2. Dim the lights (or have less lights on). 3. Burn scented oils, incensed or candles. 4. Make that your time to read a book that has nothing to do with your life and will transport you to another land of thought (biographies are excellent, and so are graphic novels). 5. Night Stretches: Stretching properly starts by creating tension… And then teaching your body to relax during that tension… You do this through controlled, slow “nose to mouth” breathing. (Nose “in”… Mouth “out…) Hold your stretches for 3 to 5 minutes. Anything less isn't enough for your body parts to "learn" what you're teaching it. But the best side effect of night stretches is that all of that relaxing breathing makes you hella sleepy. And it quietens an overthinking mind. Doing this, or any of the other activities above, for your wind-down ritual is your reward for a relentlessly creative work day.

### 7. Sleep in a slightly cooled room. Lower temperatures are a signal for the body to fall asleep. It also helps you STAY asleep as your body temperature lowers at night.

### 8. Only use your bed for sleeping (and f-cking). Don't eat in bed. Don't work in bed. Reading in bed is fine if it's during your wind-down ritual.

### 9. Exercise during the day. Fit bodies sleep way easier.

### 10. (ONLY FOR THE HARDCORE) Go outside in your first 20 minutes of awake time. The morning sun's light energy (even on a cloudy day) resets your melatonin to fire off at the right time later that night to get you "sleepy" for bed.

## Part II: The Fast Sleep Military Protocol (For Creatives)

### 1. Read for 5 to 10 minutes. This moves your mind away from your regular thoughts.

### 2. Lights off.

### 3. Lay on your side to start. (You can switch to your fave position later).

### 4. Breathe deeply. In through nose quickly (filling up stomach). Sneak in a sniffle more, then… Hold for a count of 7. Exhale slowly out through the mouth. Do this 4 times. That’s all you need.

### 5. Relax your eyes. (It could help to gently put your fingers on your eyelids first so you “feel” them. And to make sure they are relaxed.)

### 6. Relax your face. Try to feel if there's any tension on your face. Mouth. Forehead. Ears. And relax those areas completely.

### 7. Visualize yourself doing something you love. I usually visualize creating a synth patch from scratch.

### 8. TRIFECTA III: The Eating Habits Of Prolific Creatives

If you want to have fun in life…

Eat what you want, when you want, and as much as you want.

EAT FOR ENTERTAINMENT.

But if you ever decide to be a creativity machine — Someone who engages in 8-15 hours of daily creative flow

If you're about to start a grueling 3-months of travel, touring as an artist…

Then you might want to change your nutrition habits.

EAT FOR PERFORMANCE.

I only became interested in nutrition as a way to be able to make more art. Especially when I was photographing nightlife every night of the week. I wanted to learn about any behaviors that could give me energy. And also those to avoid that would rob me of energy.

My goal was to live a life of intensity without ever burning out.

Well, I found quite a few tricks through 10 years of trial and error. I still use them to this day.

Besides changing the diet of the entire Weeknd crew while I was on tour with them, this is the first time I'm sharing this information all in one place.

If it worked for them, maybe some of these concepts will work for you too.

DISCLAIMER: I won't repeat the things you should already know, like the importance of water etc...

This module is a compilation of nutritional habits that escape common knowledge.

Let's dive in.

The Healthy Habits Trifecta:

1. Meditation and Exercise

3. Nutrition

So, before you get excited about changing your diet… Understand that nutrition is NOT the first thing you must worry about perfecting.

Sleep and Exercise is.

You can eat all the superfoods you want… Pop vitamin pills all day… Take youth-preserving elixirs… And bombard your body with antioxidants and aphrodisiacs etc…

But if you don't take care of sleep and exercise, all of your considered food choices will go to waste.

If you're depressed, anxious, or unmotivated, the first thing to consider isn't your diet.

It's... "Are you exercising"? Are you sleeping?

Your emotional health begins and improves with exercise and rest. Nutrition only SUSTAINS and GOATIFIES this momentum.

You'll have to make all three of these lifestyle changes to create your sharpest creative mind possible.

Stress kills nutrients. So if you don't exercise and rest, it's like throwing away all the great food choices you made.

Without exercise and sleep, your mind will become a toxin. Your overthinking will burn through those precious nutrients you consumed, leaving very little for the repair and maintenance of a healthy body— and draining you of creative energy,

We creatives don't exercise (only) for a good body or to lose weight… We creatives exercise so that, as Emma Chamberlain puts it, "We can be a better human for the rest of the day."

I can't stress this enough: Master the psychosomatic (mind and body) first. THEN add food to the equation.

If you do it in that order, you'll discover a built-in bonus feature: When you meditate, exercise, and sleep… It makes you want to eat better without any disciplined effort.

So don't believe the hype. Superfoods are bullshit. UNLESS you're doing everything else right. And when you finally are… They're like magic.

This is not an all-encompassing guide. It's only a starting point to get you interested in experimenting with new types of food consumption.

Or… to recalibrate old nutrition habits with new life.

But please…

Don't think you need to follow these 7 "rules" all the time. Get hardcore with them only when you're in full creativity machine mode.

When you're not in that mode... Return to your old ways (if you don't miss feeling awesome).

And also... Don't be a drag.

Go to tapas dinners with friends.

Enjoy ice cream with your family once in a while.

Your body and mind will appreciate the occasional cheat breaks.

"We dig our graves with our teeth." (Old proverb about how our eating habits are the leading cause of our destruction)

It's funny how many health benefits you gain by not eating.

I wish I had discovered intermittent fasting way earlier.

I only started fasting seriously in 2020, but it changed everything. I never lose energy now. My mind is sharp for hours at a time (I still use a timer to stop working every 50 mins to walk, breathe, do sit-ups, whatever is on the interval 'menu' for that day). And when I go to bed, it's not because I'm tired, it's because… "It's time to go to bed". And I fall asleep easily.

It's only when I go back into "norm-core mode" to hang out with friends, or during holidays with family, etc… That I'm reminded of all the shitty symptoms that regular people complain about. Things like feeling sleepy in the afternoon. Lacking energy. Crash and burn. Wandering mind.

Fasting cured those things for me.

It's the best tool I know for concentration and mental sharpness.

But here's the bad part.

The slope to get comfortable with it is steep.

For the first few days, you'll be so hungry that have the opposite effect: You'll be majorly distracted. You'll feel hunger pain. You'll wonder how people do this shit.

But stick with it, and soon enough… Those feelings go away.

Replaced with focus and clarity. A very good trade off for the creative athlete you want to become.

I even do my gym workouts fasted now. This would have been inconceivable to my former self.

The only things I consume during my fast are tea and water. I go back and forth between them (you'll find the list below).

By the way…

If you combine "food fasting" with "social media / phone fasting" at the same time… You will become a new person within a week.

If you don't already know why… Google it.

I love bread, pizza, and spaghetti as much as you do. But if you eat those foods, expect a mid-afternoon slump along with everyone else.

Focus on the ritual of nutritious eating more than you focus on the actual foods themselves.

If you make "eating well" your lifestyle, there's less room to eat bad foods.

It's like my Dr. Pepper story (from the podcast). It's not that discovering green tea filled me with healthy antioxidants… It just gave me no room to engage in my Dr. Pepper addiction.

Fill your day with better foods and let the bad habits will take care of themselves.

Most people don't know this but…

The enzymes that break down protein and the enzymes that break down starches don't work well simultaneously. That's why this combo brings your digestive system to a grinding halt.

That's why eating meat and potatoes make you sleepy.

So when you want to perform at your best… Have meat and vegetables instead. Or potatoes and vegetables.

But never the classic All-American performance suicide combo.

Fruit digests in the lower intestine.

So if you have food in your stomach and THEN you eat fruit, it has to wait around for that food to digest first. You know what that means?

The fruit ferments. And that gives you gas. Now you know.

So, eat fruit first thing in the morning.

Or on an empty stomach. (Excellent to break a fast.)

If you're in "performance mode" and you have any type of digestion problems... avoid spicy food and avoid dairy. Those are usually the first culprit.

I don't want to hate on them. Dairy and spicy makes eating FUN! But if something is still "off" after doing all the above... Look to these known sources of digestive conflict.

WATER — I know I said I wouldn't state the obvious, but since I know you're STILL not drinking enough water, I will put it here anyways. Nothing you will put in your body is more important than this elixir of life. Drink enough water and it helps fix everything. Don't drink enough and your problems will multiply.

FAV TEAS (high in antioxidants, but because they have caffeine, I don't consume them past noon to protect my sleep)

FAV NON-CAFFEINATED TEAS

green rooibos (non-caffeinated)

fresh ginger tea (non-caffeinated drinks)

pu'ur tea for digestion (non-caffeinated, after dinner)

Chamomile Tea (non-caffeinated, nighttime)

(I drink water and tea. That's it. No alcohol. No soft drinks. No juice. -- Until it's time to be social.)

Mate (this was #1 for students)

lemon ginger tea

blue lotus tea

water and salt

water and lemon juice

pineapple ginger lemon water

grapefruit juice

lion's mane mushroom powder in matcha

azafran tea

one beer, no more

Nuts and grains

Almonds (high in magnesium and melatonin — sleep inducers)

Cherries (the melatonin queen)

Skyr (Icelandic yogurt)

Asian sweet potato (it's purple)

Square of dark chocolate (78% and up) — This kills your sweet tooth when you need it to

Steak with vegetables or salad (no starches like potatoes)

Blueberries

Vegan proteins: tofu, tempeh, TVP and seitan

Tahini and apple, walnuts, and almonds

Plain greek yogurt

Corn / Beans / Squash (the 3 sisters)

Tulsi — Holy basil. A plant from India. It's an adaptogen so when you take it long term it calms you down and is great for focus. In yoga and Hindu traditions, it's considered a goddess and there are special rituals just for taking care of the plant)

Shiitake mushrooms

Chaga mushrooms.

Ferments — Like kombucha, kimchi, beer are lactó fermentación. Ferments resets you and gives you focus to create. And kōji which is used to make miso, sake, and soy sauce.

### 9. Too Many Cooks In The Kitchen Of Your Mind

Having too many mentors is just an elaborate method of procrastination.

When you outsource your thinking... Then you don't have to take action. That way you can keep searching for some "ultimate truth" that you're looking for. Convincing yourself that maybe it's that next super-wise person that's gonna give it to you.

Truth is more elusive than that.

You will never believe anything that you don't physically experience yourself.

Instead... Once you get your information from a credible source... Act on it. Right away.

See, you can hear the same thing from 8 different people in 8 different ways in 8 different languages and it will never truly sink in. Not until you go out and experience it yourself. In your bones. Make it your flesh. Right now, if you're struggling with moving forward it may be that there are too many cooks in the kitchen of your mind.

You know when you hear those magic words come out of someone's mouth and you're like wow... that felt like a breakthrough?

Don't go and ponder it.

Go act on it. Immediately.

Get another coating of plasma on your brain to etch that emotion memory into your noggin for good. That's the only way to make it truly sink in.

You're looking for a certain spirit. And once you find that spirit, that feeling, it doesn't need corroberation. This isn't science. If it works once.... If it brings you higher... Then why do you need to hear any one else say it for?

But here you are again. Unable to act. Despite the fact that you have a million mentors. Why? Because you have a million mentors. Having so many inputs buys you time so you can "think" about it. Then, after you think about it, you get a second opinion, right? that's why you read all those books and why you listen to all those podcasts.

And then when somewhere along the way you get a contradictory opinion... Everything stops. Then you're confused. Someone has to be lying. You have this internal debate. Which person is right? Which concept is true? It's literally "over-thinkers anonymous".

When all you have to do in the first place is go out there and test it for yourself.

You don't need to take anyone's word for it.

The people who are further along the journey... All they can do for you, is point to the holes in the ground that THEY came across.

But who knows, maybe those holes already got covered up? Or maybe there are other holes those people didn't see. You gotta go out there and discover things for yourself. Don't get me wrong... Those further along than you... They can help you. By making you pay attention to things you may have otherwise missed. But what they CAN'T do is do the pushups for you.

What you may be suffering from is called Information Junkie Syndrome.

You know what I'm talking about, right? It's when you say:

Let me go watch a YouTube video about meeting strangers. Let me read about how to promote myself. Let me read about making better art. Anything to avoid the thing you should be doing.

That's how you end up standing still.

You can't get your information from a million different sources and then expect it all to be cohesive. That's not how it works.

Successful people indeed have mentors. But ONE at a time.

You need to invest... in one system.

It's possible to take opposite approaches and arrive at the same results.

Like, you can tell someone that they have to meditate and approach things "with love" in order to find their success. And that may be absolutely true for them in that moment.

Or, you can tell someone that they need to tap into their anger and focus by putting pictures of their haters on their fridge to find their success... And, that, may be true also.

It's not the system that gets you there.

It's the fact that you're only following ONE system them that gets you there.

And then once you've moved ahead on the board game. Once you get to a point you're satisfied with. Then... Only then... You can change systems if you gotta.

Go window shopping for new mentors if you need to.

Do whatever you gotta do. But for now only use one at a time so that when you use the framework you've chosen... it's like a silver bullet.

Stop being afraid of missing out on something.

Stop using information as a drug that pacifies you from actually going out there and taking action.

Follow one mentor.

Find that person that doesn't have just the words, but that also captures a certain spirit about them that can lead you into action.

Words are only half of it. Mentors will use them to tire you out, until all you have left to do is ACT...

That's why someone that's doing it, or being it already, is the perfect mentor.

Because when they shut up... They're still speaking the truth.

Pick THAT person to be your Mr. Miyagi for the next little while.

And do whatever they say. Even if you don't understand why you're "waxing on, waxing off".

Once you've found that person or that system... Seriously... ignore everything else.

That is the sort of dedication that gets results.

#messagewave

### 9. Too Many Cooks In The Kitchen Of Your Mind

##### Post a comment

##### 18comments

### 10.How To Process Your Crazy Irrational Feelings

As an artist, surely you know...

There will be ups and downs.

Sometime you feel like you can even set an alarm to it.

Yet somehow, every low always feels so original.

Like it's the first time it's ever happened.

Do you have a strategy for handling those irrational feelings when they arrive?

You should have one for anything that you can count on reoccurring regularly.

It's good for business.

It's good for play.

No matter the emotions, there are two things every creative must learn to do with all those crazy feelings you get.

And you need to do these 2 things AT THE SAME TIME.

AT THE SAME TIME is key.

Here they are...

As a creative, your feelings are part of expressing your job. You'd be crazy not to put them on a pedestal.

You are an emotion machine.

Feel those feelings for all they're worth. Understand where they came from. How unique they are.

New feelings especially. That's a special breed of emotion that has arrived to teach you something major.

These emotions may give you great art one day. If not in the next hour...

You'll be talking about them in interviews and on stage accepting awards some day. To recognize their worth immediately.

Even crazy irrational feelings have a place in your life.

Especially if you're hot-blooded.

You may be the type to switch up feelings because you're bored of the latest ones you've been serving up.

Feel all those fiery emotions and express the full range of who you are.

Because you're also a high-output creative (or aspire to be), there's something else you have to do.

Often within the same hour.

Something that "the normals" will never understand:

I heard Krishnamurti tell this cool little story on YouTube...

"Once, there was a farmer. One of his sons found a horse. His neighbors said he was lucky. The farmer said, "Maybe." The next day, the son was attempting to train the horse, and he fell and broke his leg. The farmer's neighbor said he was unlucky. The farmer said, "Maybe." The next day the country went to war, and the army came by and took his other two sons. They both died in that war. The son with the broken leg healed. His neighbors said he was lucky. The farmer said, "Maybe.""

I don't know if what you're going through today will end up being "the worst" moment of your life or "the best".

But I DO know that if you stay focused on your daily duty as "a creator of beautiful things",... That your self-esteem won't have to suffer. Even if other things are upside-down at the moment.

You can be down AND STILL feel 100% blessed.

You can be hella mad at your mom for constantly triggering your darkest impulses AND STILL wake up at 5 a.m... Before your dentist appointment... To finish a new ground-breaking painting.

Your current government job may make you cry in the parking lot once a month... AND you can STILL be focused enough to make all the baller moves with your crew every weekend. Those green screen videos might get out of this hellhole by next year.

Embrace all these contradictory thoughts.

That's what it means to be a creative.

Feeling a range of things that others don't... Or are afraid to.

You're emotional because you're unsure.

But even when you're unsure, your limbs still work. Use those limbs to make a few moves that put the odds further in your favor today.

Narrow the gap between the vision in your mind and the dire reality you're facing right now.

Do one action that will put a half-smile on your face before you go back to feeling down in the dumps.

Be the walking contradiction most creatives are.

Like, how can you be so productive, making all this art and making all these moves, while you're an emotional wreck?

Ask FKA Twigs.

Ask Nine Ince Nails.

Ask Post Malone.

"Passion" is all about what you're feeling that day. But "obsession" knows it's got a job to do either way.

Let yourself feel what you gotta feel, but give yourself permission to suspend it for the moments you need to make G.O.A.T. moves.

Keep to your self-discipline schedule. "Do the artistic work that needs to be done". It's an amazing way to blunt the negative impact of unruly thoughts.

"IGNORE THE FEELINGS" doesn't mean you don't deal with the emotions later on. They must be dealt with. They must be honored. "IGNORE THE FEELINGS" means you don't let it stop you from doing what must be done today.

Remember... You're an artist with a message for the world... That doesn't suddenly change because you had a fight with boo.

Don't cave into moments you don't understand the full impact of when you can be doing things NOW to influence what those things will mean in the future.

The good feelings are the ones that get the ego thinking you can take a day off. Or that you can start slacking. Noooooooo...

The good feelings will make you feel like the "bad feelings" will never happen again. And that you got things under control.

Don't fall for it.

Nothing could be further from the truth.

Humans were designed to go back and forth between feeling good and feeling bad. Like, for the rest of our lives.

Postpartum depression… The comedown… They are all essential parts of the human experience.

But luckily, we also a certain amount of power to influence HOW LONG we linger in each phase.

There is no reason not to have a grand life with LONG periods of feeling energized, love, and grateful... And SHORT periods of self-doubt and sadness.

Start by practicing this whole "putting your emotions on hold -- feel them later" G.O.A.T strategy.

Human beings have the unique ability to change how they feel in an instant if they choose. Not for an extended time, necessarily. But long enough to get a few things done.

That's how professional artists and performers can do their job no matter what "bad news" they got or what "irrational feelings" have crept up.

They put those feelings on hold when it's game time. You should start practicing this skill now since you're going to be a star one day.

I'd suggest you get intimate with the concept.

The next time you're feeling like shit on a day that was supposed to be productive... Put the feelings on hold. Suspend your knee-jerk reaction to always cave-in to every emotion you feel.

Do what you said you'd do today.

Your actions today are the raw materials for your feelings tomorrow.

Then after you've done your work... If you still feel like it, indulge in overthinking and feeling bad over a big bowl of peanut butter chocolate ice-cream.

And fucking cry, cry, cry...

### 11. Why You Need A 'Weapon List'

I got this email from a student a while ago:

You know what another student did recently?

He wrote down all the things that he had working against him art-wise. Every negative thing he could think of. He didn't hold back.

And then he sent me the list "for accountability".

It was his way of facing the truth. To stay realistic as he continued to forge ahead anyways.

I loved his determination.

But when I got it, it seemed incomplete to me.

So I emailed him back and I asked him to make ANOTHER list.

In this list I wanted him to explain to me... REALISTICALLY... why each of the statements he had made were FALSE.

A few days later he emerged with it:

That's his WEAPON LIST now. He looks at it whenever the "stupid thoughts" creep in. He has ammunition now.

I suggest you do the same.

Let me start you off...

James Murphy STARTED LCD Soundsystem when he was 35. And influenced a whole generation younger than him.

Peaches started making music when she was 32.

2 Chainz made his mark in hip hop when he was 34.

You're 26! Enjoy the cross-section of wisdom and youth (it could last another 40 years if you play your card right).

### 11. Why You Need A 'Weapon List'

#### Dear Father Bronques, even though I just got signed to a record deal, I'm having crazy doubts. I read this amazing biography about Kate Bush recently, and I started feeling like maybe I'm kind of 'late to the party'? I don't know of a lot of 26-year olds that still have yet to release their first project, and still become successful. It seems like it's a young person's game. Rationally, I know these thoughts are stupid and unproductive. And that "I can become anything you imagine". But how can I delete these negative thoughts that persist in my brain when I see people like Billie Eillish out there? My ego keeps pounding me with thoughts like: "give it up, you're too late darling!" Do you have any advice for conquering these toxic thoughts that keep on popping up in my head every now and then?

#### ***Everyone should make a weapon list. That way you have a solid list of REALISTIC responses to your negative thoughts. 'Cause when you're in the moment, feeling low, the good combacks and uplifting responses don't tend to come as quick. It may be hard to remember why you're amazing. Or why you're blessed. Make this your ammunition. Sometimes just having it there is enough to keep the "stupid thoughts" away.

## THE BOOK OF DARES: Run With The Wolves


### 1. The Shadow Self

Right out of the gate I wanna say this:

I roll my eyes at anything and everything that's described as a "personality test".

I hate the idea of people putting me into a box. And I'm guessing you do too?

But if you're looking for answers in your life right now...

Holy shit did I discover a new way of using those silly tests that might blow your mind today.

Let me explain how this landed on my lap.

One night at a group dinner in LA, I met a fun but intense girl obsessed with the Meyers-Briggs personality test. She wanted to share her 'letters' with everyone. And she expected everyone to know theirs. (In California, many 'new culture' corporations force their employees to take this test.)

We got along, and the tequila was good, so later, when we were chillin' she convinced me to take the test online. For shits and giggles. Ok. No harm in that.

One of the letters that came back in the results: 'I'. 'I' stands for introvert.

Oooh, she hated that. For her, it didn't make sense with how we met. My personality was "too fearless, too confident, and too... social".

She couldn't let it go. She was convinced that "I did it wrong." Or that "I was dishonest with my answers". Watching her rationalize the results was painful.

Luckily, I salvaged the night and avoided a continuing debate by switching the conversation back to her... And HER wonderful letters.

But for the next few days, it haunted me. This whole "personality test" thing...

Because TBH it was spot on. I knew it was telling the truth. I AM an introvert.

Even though in many social situations, I project something way different. Somehow that online test got it right.

But ok. So what right?

It's just another system. Like astrology. Like palm reading. Another excuse to philosophize about ourselves. And compare ourselves with others.

It's only months later when I was doing The Drill Down with a friend a week later that its usefulness came to me in a flash.

Everyone's been looking at personality tests all wrong.

It's always the same thing. You do the test. You get your 4 special letters, and then they go read the description that tells you "what kind of person you are".

And then one of two things happen after that:

1. You navel-gaze at how "perfect" the results seem. (I mean, read through most of the comments on the final results page and you'll see what I mean. There are a million "This is so me..." comments down the page.)

2. You call B.S. on these kinds of tests. (Usually me.) You feel that everyone is "both letters", or has been "both letters" at different points. So who cares?

(Hell, I can be both polarities within one day! So I agree.)

But both ways of looking at the results are missing the point.

Let me show you what I mean.

First. Go take the test yourself right now.

What I'm about to show you is only powerful if you can measure it against the results you get for yourself.

I understand your skepticism.

But humor me. It'll be worth it.

This link will open another tab:

MEYERS-BRIGGS PERSONALITY TEST

Okay, so you have your 4 "letters", right?

If you answered everything truthfully, it should be a pretty accurate snapshot of you at this moment in time.

Now do this:

Write out all the opposite letters that you are NOT.

So, if you're an INTJ for example, your new letters would become ESFP.

And then... Write out the full extent of what those opposite letters mean. Here's the full guide:

Now stare at those "opposite" letters on the page... And then come to this understanding:

Let that sink in.

I know you're gonna want to fight me on this one. People always do.

But, you'll come to realize that it's the only way forward.

In psychology lingo, that opposite personality has a name.

It's called 'The Shadow Self'.

And you need to embrace your shadow self if you want to get to your next level.

You know when people say "get out of your comfort zone"? Bungee jumping or "swimming with sharks" is not what they should be engaging in.

FACING YOUR SHADOW SELF shows you the real departure you need to make to escape your comfort zone. It's so blatant and clear, and even an overthinker can't fool themselves out of this one.

So, for example...

If you're an introvert-- Maybe you need to put yourself in more situations where you'll be in the spotlight more.

Or if you're an extrovert, you need to shut the fuck up. You need to listen more... Be quiet more. Move away from being the center of attention for a little while.

Embracing the shadow self will make you feel like you're not "being you".

Your friends and family will ask: who kidnapped the "real you".

Don't panic.

Wait for thesecondary effects.

This is the pathway to your evolution playing out:

You're beginning to master your polarities.

I'm from the school of thought that believes that people can change at any point in their lives. People don't have to be victims of their current limitations.

I mean, when I look around me I see people that have bigger setbacks than I do and they're THRIVING despite any of them.

So my controversial thought for you today is:

Any problems that you're having right now... In any aspect of your life... Maybe it's just because you're not pivoting enough towards one of your other polarities when you ought to be.

Maybe you have a "shadow self" that could use some leaning into.

You don't have to embrace all of your opposites at the same time. It could be one or two of 'the opposite letters' that you need to conquer to achieve your current goals.

Think about a struggle you're going through. A relationship problem, or some "work thing", or another issue that keeps you up at night...

Look at your shadow letters again. If you learned to pivot more towards that extreme, is there one of them that might make your situation better?

Are you in a rocky relationship right now? Maybe you rely too much on feelings (F) when you make decisions about your significant other? Or perhaps you rely too much on logic (L)?

Are you trying to take things to the next level with your photography? Let me guess. You always use intuition and a "no rules" attitude (N) to guide your decisions? Maybe what you need to evolve and get out of your rut is structure (S)?

Or whatever... Imagine the exact opposite. Get it?

People love examples. So here's another one: Is life boring right now? (Damn, really kid?) If you were more EXTROVERTED, could it add some spice? Or maybe if you were more INTROVERTED you might discover exciting details within... Or notice things around you that you've always missed because you were taking up so much room?

Or have you been the 50/50 type for your whole life? Maybe you need to hang out at either one of the extremes to get a few new wins?

These crazy new results is what the world looks like when you learn how to embrace the shadow self.

I remember when I was starting out as a photographer... I knew I couldn't act like an introvert if I was gonna get the kind of pictures that I wanted to get. So I embraced my opposite polarity. I created a character that was outrageously outgoing for those situations.

Remember that Seinfeld episode called 'The Opposite'? Where George Constanza behaves the opposite way of how he usually does to see how much his life would change?

And from that moment on his loser character becomes a winner.

Well, that classic episode was about George embracing his shadow self.

It doesn't mean you can't have your favorite way of being whenever you're chilling with your family. But I'm just saying, when you plateau on your goals... Now you know what to do.Do the opposite for a while.Or even embrace it for a lifetime like I did with my own "situational extroversion".

It's up to you.

What a mindfuck right?

Every goal that you're having trouble reaching right now... Is easily reached by your shadow self.

It's almost annoying.

Until you realized that your shadow self IS LAYING DORMANT INSIDE YOU.

The shadow self is where all your untapped potential lies.

It'll feel scary to go down these new paths.

You will try to grasp for every excuse you can find to stay the same. You might already be doing it right now, reading this.

And to make matters worse...

You'll rationalize that some of the people you hate on the most-- They naturally have the qualities of the shadow self you've for so long rejected.

THAT'S THE POINT!

It kills you, knowing that your best path forward is adopting some of the same characteristics from those you reject to achieve your dreams.

Like... You hate that boring girl that plans everything (S). You're proud that you're seen as a free spirit (N). Well, maybe it's time to be more of "the planning type" to... get your music career going or whatever. Maybe there's something you can learn from them.

Or maybe it's the opposite. Maybe you need to be more of a free spirit to let more magic happen around you. Learn from someone who is by modeling their behavior.

The point is: Let go of all the biases you're holding onto.

Start embracing your nemesis' best qualities. Make those qualities part of YOUR REPERTOIRE

That negative chatter stopping you from embracing your shadow is just your ego talking.

It wants you to resist change.

Even society wants you to suppress your shadow side. It much prefers you to stay predictable and boring.

Fight society's desire for you to conform... You're an artist, remember?

Fight your ego's desire to be consistent. Start joyfully leaning into your polar opposite.

Swing your pendulum to the other side.

Here is a list of polarities beyond Meyers-Briggs. Which opposite polarity could help you out right now?

There is no one true you.

Who you are right now is merely the result of choices you made in the past. Like what your favorite ice cream is. Or, if you even like ice cream in the first place.

But now you know: When what's in the light isn't working, embrace what's in the dark.

Someone (who doesn't have your best interest in mind) convinced you that people can't change. And fooled you into thinking that "being balanced" is good. And that this thinking will somehow lead you to "happiness". It doesn't. It leads to normal. If "normal" makes you happy, then all the power to you. But if you're reaching for "amazing", "next level", or "extraordinary"… The only option left is living in and embracing the extremes.

Start integrating your shadow self into all the aspects of your life that you want to improve. Tap into it's full power.

Start today.

The 21st century belongs to those who master their polarities.

P.S. You want another way of looking at it? When you're struggling with things, you ARE your shadow self. And your opposite traits are the light you need to move into to evolve. Either way you look at it... The process is gonna hurt. But that's how transformations towards legendary always begin.

### 1. The Shadow Self

#### "It's never too late to have a happy childhood." Tom Robbins.

#### Where you get your energy:

#### I - Introverted: quiet, reserved

#### E - Extroverted: loud, outgoing

#### How your day unfolds:

#### N - Intuitive: no rules, you trust your gut, love randomness

#### S - Structure: predictability, love planning, on-time, you love rules

#### How you make decisions:

#### F - Feeling: "in your body", and emotional decision making

#### T - Thinking: logical and rational decision making

#### This is how you approach problems:

#### P - Perceiving: Indecisive, like to keep options open

#### J - Judging: Decisive, things are black and white

## The Meyers-Briggs test isn't about discovering "who you are". No... Instead, it's a way for you to discover the polar opposite character traits that you need to adopt to achieve who you want to become.

### THE PROCESS: You look at your problem. And then you try to see which of your opposite letters (or combination of) will help you solve that problem.

#### Logic | Intuition

#### Tight with money | Loose with money

#### Masculine | Feminine

#### Disciplined | Undisciplined

#### Sensible | Silly

#### Organized | Disorganized

#### Shy | Outgoing

#### Artistic and creative | Logical and precise

#### Nature | Polluted City

#### Playful | Serious

#### Healthy | Unhealthy

#### Early Riser | Night Owl

#### Science | Religion

#### Meditation and Spirituality | Money and Cigars

#### Giving to others | Selfish to myself

#### Think more about the past | Think more about the future

#### Charity | Greed

#### Loud | Quiet

#### Bold and well presented | Understated

### 2. How To Make Your Life A Work Of Art (Chase Atlantic Intro)
