### 3. How To Get Out Of Your Comfort Zone (For Introverts)

If you want to make great art… You have to learn how to get out of your comfort zone.If you want to create something that will move people, inspire them, and make them feel like it's the best time in history to be alive... You have to go to places where other artists have yet to go.To be part of that 1% of successful artists, you have to start doing things that 99% of regular artists are afraid to do.

"But Father, I'm an introvert…"

That's ok. Be an introvert. Be shy.

But be an ambitious introvert. And be shy EXCEPT when it comes to your art.

Besides… I love that you're an introvert. Why? Because getting out of your comfort zone is 1000% more beneficial to the world when it's an introvert doing it.

It's more exciting to watch someone shy do something bold than to watch someone extroverted do the same thing. The stakes are higher. The agony is more relatable.

In this art-expanding module, I will teach you how to practice turning your shadow self "on" whenever you need it. (More about that later...)

None of this is about being courageous… It's about being curious.

It's about asking, "What if?" Just like you should be doing when you're making art.

It's the alchemy of embracing "chance" and learning how to turn it into "serendipity."

Here are a few shy artists who embrace "chance" as a color in their artistic process:

Marina Abramović

Derek DelGaudio

Emma Chamberlain

They're all ambitious introverts.

With 3 things in common.

The irony is that once you finally commit to this "radical" philosophy, you will realize this is actually the least risky artistic path you could take.

For some reason that I have yet to understand— When you choose "the unknown," something extraordinary always happens.

Any time I've ever let go of expectations, embraced life's randomness, and used that energy in my art… It gave me a new career.

When you go that extra mile, far beyond where everyone else is going, eventually… People throw money at you. That's my experience. And that's what I've observed for the successful artists that I've been around.

Let me show you how.

Father says…

"Always choose to dare."

Choosing "dare" reveals the truth of any situation anyways. And it also reveals the truth of who you are.

Choosing "dare" generates more luck around you.

Choosing "dare" sharpens your intuition.

Choosing "dare" is training for the future when it REALLY counts. It will prepare you for the day when a stranger that can help your career comes along (a gatekeeper or a potential collaborator). Approaching them will be easy. You will have practice and confidence under your belt.Choosing "dare" is the most important currency in your arsenal. It's how you achieve meaningful personal transformation.

Choosing "dare" makes you understand the subtle but essential distinction between the "fear of something dangerous" and the "fear of getting out of your comfort zone." The first is the kind of fear you need for survival. The second is the kind of fear that will kill your artistic soul.

If you don't keep putting yourself out there, what kind of art are you hoping to create? What kind of fans are you hoping to attract?

It's renegade season.

It's time to adopt a "Drive-By" Mentality.

Artists love to say how AI art is missing a crucial element: humanity. Yet, those same artists are afraid to talk to their neighbors. How much humanity are YOU bringing to your art if you stay hidden in a corner? Getting out of your comfort zone and interacting with the world is the biggest gift an artist can give themselves in the coming age of AI. It's the only fighting chance you have of surviving the Post-AI renaissance.

Drive-By Mentality is when an opportunity comes along for you to come out of your shell— and contrary to your everyday behavior… You embrace the spirit of the moment.

Your whole life, you were taught never to talk to strangers. And you listened. You were so obedient that it even became your personality. Always averting your eyes. Not realizing how much this fear of confrontation, fear of rejection, and fear of adventure has been stifling your creative potential.

I was lucky. I had a teacher in high school who loved The Beatles. And he would always explain Beatles lyrics. He would use their words as allegories for whatever we were discussing. One day he explained the meaning behind the song "Eleanor Rigby." He explained how it was about missed opportunities. Two lonely people co-existing in the same small town. They could have cured their loneliness at any moment but never did. Until the sad day when their fate was sealed. Death was the only time they made contact. — That's why now, whenever my 'Eleanor Rigby' tendencies creep in on me... Trying to keep me lame and comfortable… I gag those impulses with a spoon and go outside to show the universe I am using my blessings to the fullest.

"Talk to a stranger today."

"Talk to a stranger today" is the most transformative dare I can give you.

Go and make a connection with a human being you don't know.

Go lift the veil of fear that exists within your community

This singular dare has an immense potential to change lives. Yours. A stranger's. And everyone else's that you inspire later when you share the story.

Talking to a stranger makes you realize how small you were playing the game of life before. You'll wonder why you ever waited so long to start doing this.

At first, it's scary. For the same reason it's exciting… Because you never know what a person will say.

But whatever happens… The moment is always life-expanding.

And you always come home with a story.

It can happen on the street. It can be in a cafe. In a library. At a poetry reading. On the train.

"But Father… In my culture, people don't like to be approached."

"I live in a conservative town."

Listen… I've traveled to the most conservative places in the world. China. Turkey. Beirut. Russia. And yes, people are different in different cultures. But you know what? They're also all the same.

I've never been to any city or town anywhere in the world where the people I met weren't moved by art, filled with passion, and didn't have a thirst to connect with other human beings.

"Father, I do dare myself once in a while. I really do."

Sure you do. I see you get out of your comfort zone… When you're on vacation… When you're drunk… And years ago when you had that customer service job...

I'm not talking about that.

I'm talking about "breaking the ice" in environments where everyone else (especially you) usually averts their eyes.

Like, in line at the bank, or in the grocery store, on the plane, in an elevator, at the mall… Places where everyone is "playing it safe."

You will get the true unpredictability factor by doing dares involving other people. 'Cause when human beings are involved, you never have any clue how someone will react.

And with this kind of dare… The possibility of rejection is there.

Ooh… The fear of rejection.

Fear of what other people will think.

Every artist's Achilles heel.

It manifests in so many different ways.

Fear of sharing your art…

Fear of being criticized…

Fear of people "not liking it"…

Talking to strangers is how you practice being immune to all of that.

I swear if you follow this simple prescription… Soon, you won't have to think twice anymore. You'll be so used to coming out of your shell on demand. You'll be able to switch "modes" on a dime.

Yes, even if you're an introvert.

Turn all those micro-moments that pass through your fingers every day... The "down-times" of life… Into artistic potential.

All those times when you would usually avert your eyes—

Avert your apathy instead.

Ask yourself, "What if…?" Then go find out the answer.

Watch what happens when you get back to your art stuff later…

You will have so much more of life to draw from.

Make this your "new me" pledge:

"I will never go a week without daring myself to leave my comfort zone."

And because you're an artist… Document the glorious journey.

Allow it to be messy.

Allow yourself to fail.

Then share the results with your audience.

That's part of the fun. Watching even your losses become incredible stories. And eventually watching those failures become wins.

I got my first photography job after only 3 weeks of taking photos. Even though I pretty much sucked. How? I photographed a random woman on the street and promised to email her the photos later (this is also how I built my first email list too, btw—PRO TIP). She loved the results. Lucky for me, she also happened to be a magazine editor. "If you can make ME look this good, I can't wait to see what you do with models…" She hired me. I did well. I made my first 400$ for photography services. And all because I approached a stranger! I have a million stories like this one. Right up until 10 years later… At the Oscars… I mustered the guts to walk up to Meryl Streep and convince her to go to the wine room so I could get a legendary picture of her with Taylor Swift.

I was still an introvert when I did all of this.

An ambitious introvert.

When you talk to strangers, you start a chain reaction leading to amazing things in your career.

That's why I dare students in The Mystery School to come out of their shells.

The ones who rise to the occasion always come back changed.

"I didn't know I had that in me… Thank you, Father."

Like Tiffany, who just released her new book… I told her… Please don't rely on only your book signings to promote 'Blue Hour.' Use life itself. Whenever you're in a bookstore, approach someone your intuition says could be changed by your words (just like you did instinctively after that first signing). Connect with them deeply (as an empath like you is apt to do), and then share the story on your socials so that your community and coaching clients can see your bravery in action.

Like Alex, who paints and has lost her faith in humanity… DM and meet one of your IG followers for tea. Let that conversation percolate in your subconscious as you finish your next paintings. Strangers have things to teach us if we let them. They have the answers to our problems if we connect with who the energy points us to. It doesn't have to make sense right away. Let it make sense later when you're standing in front of a canvas 5 months from now, and you realize… "Holy Shite… Candice was right!" Then you'll also remember how it started. She was a stranger. Now she's your art show wing-girl.

Like Dominic, who writes bangers and visual treatments for those bangers… Play one of your potential hit songs for a stranger on the subway. Notice their body language as you do it. Notice your own. This one or two-minute exercise will reveal more about how ready your art is for the world than any amount of sitting at home overthinking can ever do. (And yes, of course, film the whole interaction and share the link in your newsletter.)

Like Neena, who's a stylist on the rise… Go to malls and find people who look like they're on a shopping spree and offer to help style them and create a killer outfit. Document everything, and share the results with your followers. Show people what you can do off the cuff with little resources. Don't be surprised if someone hires you from this eventually. Don't forget… Your potential future clients are in your audience too. And they're watching your every move!

Like Karimah, who's been trying to tap into the spiritual current to find the truest and wisest words that her soul can speak and combine it with her paintings… I'm like… Do your improvised spoken word for a stranger every once in a while… When there's that electricity of another human being right in front of you. And film your journey of getting better and better until you're freestyling poetry like @harrymacofficial on Tiktok!

Like Rowan… If I were a comedian like you, I'd approach strangers smoking outside of comedy clubs to see if I could make them laugh at my new jokes. I'd film my weekly exploits with all the anticipation and potential cringe of seeing how those real-world interactions turn out. And I'd continue the exchange and study the comments section.

Like Kate, who is making videos for people to feel less alone… Take your videos further by filming more of those "conversations with strangers in a Dunkin' Donuts." Right now, you're trying to control the output too much. By always filming yourself alone, you're only reinforcing the idea of "aloneness." Defeating your message. Instead, inspire others to break their inner shackles by showing them what it looks like to throw lifelines out there… To not get bites… To feel despondent… But through sheer perseverance… To finally make a life-affirming connection.

Like Sofia, who has a new baby and less time for art… Go to a museum or art gallery once a week with the sole intention of making a new friend among the crowd. Or at the grocery store if time is restricted. Discuss your philosophies about art and life with this kindred spirit. Share those conversations amongst everything else you post on Instagram… Thereby returning your social media to the 4-dimensional representation of your passion that you want it to be.

Like CJ, who's vowed to make his unique illustration style known this year— or die trying… I encourage you to go beyond drawing celebrities. Take photos of strangers to use as source material for your drawings. Then share the picture, the drawing, and a captivating story to document the whole process and inspire your ride or dies.

Like Amanda, who wants to share the art of body movement with the world… You're so talented. From this moment forward… Static posts are no longer allowed. Only dynamic media from now on. What would happen if you asked a stranger to dance with you in the middle of the street? And then you filmed the whole encounter? Do you know how many people are waiting for that invitation? Do you know how many people would be inspired watching it?

Like Daniela and Patricia, two sisters who make herbal magick potions for witches like themselves… I'd borrow some big plastic lab glasses and black lab coats and go out on the street and ask people what your collection's scents smell like. Film everything. Share the edited media online with your spiritual community to give them a "taste" of what you do and your personality. Courageously distance yourself from all the static Shopify stores selling "vanilla" herbal potions to the masses.

I could go on. But you get it.

Steal any of these dares for your liberation.

Don't worry that you might be doing the same dare as someone else. If 10 creative people do the same one, it will come out in 10 different, compelling ways. Every new generation will put its spin on it.

But these are only a few examples.

It's what I'd do if I were in your shoes.

I would seek to operate at the highest possible level by challenging myself daily…

I would make myself undeniable.

I would make my online and offline presence a gift to the world.

I'd use photography, video, and text to create the most inspirational media documenting my crazy journey of comfort-zone-busting exploits so that my audience could ride along vicariously through me.

This is what I invite you to do.

Create media showing yourself reaching for greatness.

When you repeatedly come out of your comfort zone and share it with your community, it will inspire them.

No doubt you've already been doing it, here and there, randomly. But those moments have been too few and far between to have any impact.

"Do it deliberately. Do it consistently."

Repetition makes your fans realize that your courage isn't a one time only thing… It's a way of life.

No one cares about your new album or your new painting (yet). They care about YOU… The art you create is merely a reflection of the life you're living.

So if you want them to hang your canvas on their wall or listen to your music all day... Make your art symbolize the person you've become: Someone who isn't afraid to go all the way.

MAKE SOCIAL MEDIA YOUR LIVING, BREATHING DEPICTION OF HOW YOU'RE LIVING YOUR WHOLE LIFE: LIKE MAGIC. THAT'S THE ONLY ACCEPTABLE USE OF THESE OTHERWISE HARMFUL DISTRACTION-INDUCING PLATFORMS. LEAD BY EXAMPLE. INSPIRE OTHERS TO DO THINGS IN THE REAL WORLD. BUT MOST OF ALL, TAKE HEART IN KNOWING THAT BECAUSE OF YOUR NERVE, YOU AND YOUR GANG OF FELLOW MISFITS WILL BE IMMUNE TO THE "CREATIVE ECONOMY MELTDOWN" THAT'S RIGHT AROUND THE CORNER WITH AI ART HOPING TO DOMINATE.

I know you signed up for The Mystery School to take your art to a new level but guess what?

The best way to start doing that is to take your life to another level as well.

Sure, I want you to feel safe. But that doesn't mean I want you to feel comfortable. There's nothing comfortable about making great art.

Your art can only reflect the person you are and the life you lead.

Once you start putting yourself out there and interacting with strangers more... When you go back to your studio... Somehow, everything will just feel… Different.

It might be a lonely path, but it'll be LESS lonely.

Self-imposed dares are the re-energizers.

Self-imposed dares are the energy boosts that come without a crash.

Master this. Then you're ready for the next level...The Shadow Self.

### 2. have blind faith in the process, and

### 3. surrender to the possibility of nothing coming out of it.

## 1. "TRUTH OR DARE?"

### 4. Your First "Social Experiments"

The reason you get all bent out of shape and moody about your art, music, photography, writing is because you’re taking everything too seriously. You think the challenges you face in your journey are like special snowflakes (they’re not). Your struggles are the same as what every one else out there (and throughout the history of art) has gone through. But the difference between experiencing it as a "healthy artistic struggle" or enduring it as a "dysfunctional artistic struggle" is in how you've decided to perceive your daily challenges. If you're upset all the time... I will prove to you that you’re looking at it wrong. In this module I’m going to show you a different way of looking at EVERYTHING you do so that your highs are higher (and more sustainable) and so that your lows... are always temporary (but still useful as fuck).

Instead of looking at your creative work as "making pretty things", or trying to get famous so you have a career, or clout chasing just to be seen, or trying to gain followers for validation...

What if you decided to look at things in a radical new way?

A way that frees you from the game everyone else is playing.

What if you started using your art-- and those apps on your phone that you use to share that art-- to conduct social experiments?

Social experiments that lead you to the things you're looking for faster.

Don't just use Instagram to post random shit ("post just to post"). Use Instagram to test ideas. Or to push the envelope. Or to see if you can attract a certain type of audience. Use it to see if you can influence "the normals" into paying more attention to the ideas you believe in. Or simply to see what you can get away with. Test the boundaries of society. Where can you move the borders artistically ? How can you mobilize the masses? What can you create that would make governments listen?

But the key is to approach it scientifically.

Write your 'hypothesis down'.

Try it out in the real world

Write the results.

Write down what you're gonna try next.

My buddy Trevor, created the first virtual influencerLil Miquelawith his partner Sara.

It was a social experiment.

Lil Miquela now has 3 million followers. She's been in W and Paper magazine. She's a sought-after model for luxury brands like Off White, Moncler, Prada, and Chanel.

What began as a "digital art experiment" has officially become a viral sensation.

Or how about Amalia Ulman?

Back in 2016, she created the first Instagram art experiment.

Read about it here.

Or how aboutCaroline Calloway and her ongoing social experiment.

Don't just take a "pretty photo".

Don't just release a "nice song".

Combine things that have never been combined.

See how fast you can create a valuable work of art.

Test how subversive you can be. Can you get whole new audiences to adopt your controversial ideas and help you spread them?

"Pretty" and "deep" aren't mutually exclusive. "Pretty" and "testing the boundaries of society" aren't mutually exclusive.

One word. Banksy.

Or at the other end of the spectrum.

WAP is an étude in outrageousness. It is designed to get under your skin. Not just the song. But the video. The cameos. Everything. This song is one of the most successful social experiments of the year.

Madonna's whole career. Every single album she has ever released was an experiment.

The Weeknd's Trilogy was one of the most successful recent experiments in my memory:

"Can we create a rockstar and play Coachella without ever doing one interview or showing the face of an artist in todays selfie media saturated world?"

Beyonce's HUGE surprise album (no promo, no advance listens, totally contrary to the music industry) was a high stakes experiment. No major artist had done that before.

Imagine how, if you started treating your process as experiments... How much it would FREE you?

Oh, but you're more of a "brand" than an "artist"?

So-- Instead of just making consumer products, "test the market".

Push against the norms.

Just like Goop did when they released their"This Smells Like My Vagina" candle.

I mean... Corporations are taking more risks than you? The so-called "artist"?

That's tragic.

Like Warhol did.

He treated all his interviews like they were art. They were so extraordinary they had to be compiled intoa very thick book:(I'll Be Your Mirror: The Selected Andy Warhol Interviews)

Warhol was so convinced that interviews should be treated like art that he started a magazine called 'Interview'.

Treat all your communication with the world as small social experiments.

Just like Jaden and Willow do.

'T Magazine' was their first social experiment to test the boundaries of their fame. Because they saw it that way in their mind, they gave themselves the license to go crazy.

They're still doing it.

What do you think the latest Willow interview about sexuality and blackness is all about?

What would you be capable of if you put yourself under watch?

That's the question Benjamin Franklin (one of U.S.A.'s founding fathers and the guy who, you know... discovered electricity... no biggie) asked himself.

Benjamin Franklin used himself as "the ultimate experiment". And he chronicles it with incredible detail in "The Autobiography Of Benjamin Franklin".

His strategy was to master only one aspect of his personality at a time before he moved on to the next. He had 13 "virtues" that he wanted to achieve. And his progress was logged into a daily journal so he could make sure he was improving.

In his own words:

"My intention being to acquire all these good habits, I thought it would be well not to distract my attention by attempting the whole at once, but to fix it on one of them at a time; and, when I should be master of that, then to proceed to another, and so on, till I should have gone through all thirteen."

Master one thing before progressing to the next.

Everybody tries to change everything all at once. That’s why they fail. They also fail because they don't track their results. They think they're gonna remember. They're lying to themselves.

Oh, and how old was Benjamin Franklin when he came up with all of this stuff?

20 years old.

Don't be like the student who emailed me when I showed him the first draft of this module and said "I've BEEN doing social experiments, bro..." And when I asked him to show me his notes and documentation he said it's all in his head.

Yeah right. How did you feel on Sept. 17? Do you remember that? Nope. If you're not writing it down and 1. tracking your daily hypothesis and 2. tracking your results... Then you're just doing some random Shia Labeouf antics.

Expect those random results too.

No, if you want the benefits of what I’m talking about here get a notebook to do this.Be scientific and disciplined about it.That way you can do cool things like cross reference data ("Oh wow, every Tuesday 'THIS' happens...") That what will make it hella fun. I go as far as using graph paper to keep track of mine. Why graph paper? Purely aesthetic. It's fun. Sometimes I use Google spreadsheets ("What sub-messages get me the most engagement?").

This is where you will putThe Mystery Formulato good use.

Make entering BIG DATA part your daily ritual.

Test things and attach concrete numbers and word to the results.

For one ritualized moment at the end of your day... Turn everything you've observed in your experiment... into unemotional "data".

The best part of this approach?

It will keep forcing you to look at the big picture. And you know why that’s important right? Because "zooming out" is what most artists suck at. They get lost in the details. They get lost in the treesand stop seeing the vibrant forest.

But when you zoom out and do a BIG DAILY DATA DUMP, it helps you take things less seriously.

Divorce yourself from being so emotional about social media, or the "art creation process", or about "other people's opinions".

Now you can look at it all from a healthier lens.

Now everything you do online and offline will exist in service to a bigger reason.

Your little "secret project".

And this will result in less overthinking, less anxiety and less stress.

Other side effects you may experience? Your art starts evolving faster than ever.

Not a bad trade-off, huh?

And the beauty is:

On the surface... You will LOOK like you're doing what everyone else is.

You will SEEM like you're blend in.

And that's why this is the ultimate Ninja move.

You APPEAR to be doing regular things... But onlookers will FEEL that something is different about your approach.

But they'll have no clue why.

"Dude, ever since you joined that Mystery School thing your IG has felt different. I don't get why. But I like it."

The "social experiments" approach is the difference between "sharing your sporadic freak-outs online" (what you were doing before) and "releasing a steady perfume of bottled enthusiasm" (what you'll be doing now).

Suddenly the RIGHT people will be attracted to your energy. And the haters will have violent reactions to it... (just as you predicted).

You will be "trolling for 'the good'".

Now, if that sounds like too much thought and you prefer to release your art just for fun... Cool.

I'm not mad at that. Not at all. This lane is not for everyone.

But if you're career minded and you've been stressed out every time you think about the future...

And you constantly worry about whether or not people will ever notice what you're doing...

I invite you to change your relationship with your art -- and to the tools that you use to share and promote that amazing art.

Start playing a brand new game. A game you control.

Approach your career in a way so that you stay in "flow".

Make your lows as useful as your highs.

Like they say in silicone valley: "Fail fast, fail often".

Let people using "old school" ways fight each other for attention...

Rise above this obsolete kind of thinking-- And get an eagle's eye view of the land.

### 6. Be Your Own Banksy

(aka How To Become A Revolutionary Artist In 3 Easy Steps -- This is a early draft of this module. Email me if you see typos or anything that could make it better for future TMS students.🙏🏾)

Once you've mastered daily practice...

Once you're finally showing up for yourself without fail...

You're ready for the next step.

Making waves.

Getting a reaction.

Seeing how the world feels about what you have to offer.

Don't wait for an official invitation. Don't wait for some gatekeeper to write you back.

Make noise now.

This is how you find other people, like-minded, to start a revolution with.

This is how you get your first die-hard fans.

Musicians... Stop begging people to go to your Spotify page like everyone else is doing. Instead, carry your music around and play your "hit song" for people at parties, in cafes, everywhere… Get feedback. Get people's emails. Get invites. Busk at a flea market with your drum machine. Share your infectious passion with people who will one day say, "I knew her before she was big.... With that energy, I knew she would make it."

Painters… Don't wait for a gallery to hang your works. Display your art in unexpected places. Ask mom-and-pop bookstores if they'll put your canvas up on their wall. Talk to repertory theatre managers. And when you find your perfect spot, put a placard with a description of your artistic vision next to it. With PRICE TAG where all will see it.

What happens when you start moving like this through the world?

Energy starts forming around you. Expectancy. Even people who don't like your art can't help but respect how you're showing up. Because finally…

YOU'RE BEHAVING LIKE YOU ARE YOUR #1 FAN. You are treating your art like it's important.

If you don't have that kind of enthusiasm... How can you expect others to?

That's why "DARE #2" is so crucial.

It's when I dare you to...

Stop waiting for permission.

It's when I dare you to…

"Be Your Own Banksy."

You say you want the world to be less polluted by "content" and blessed with more art.

Cool. But what are you DOING about it?

"Be your own Banksy."

Be among the revolutionary artists of your community.

Make art waves in your city, your town, or your village.

Like this... (@__criatura__)

Create a piece of visual art. Put it up somewhere unsuspecting. Photograph your act of "art vandalism". Double points if you make your artwork political.

If you're a writer… Slip one of your poems to a stranger.

Be your own Banksy.

If you're a photographer… Look at what Tadashi Onishi did in his community.

He shares his street photography by projecting them on city walls at night.

And live stream the results on Twitch.

Be your own Banksy.

If you're a musician… Since you have to create art for your singles, EPS, and albums... And you have to make videos,... Start making a bigger deal of these visual elements. Don't let it be a quick JPG you slap on as an afterthought—or a lazy YouTube visualizer "promotional tool" thingy. Treat your visuals as the bonafide works of art they should be. Giving even more depth to the music. Just like the best musicians have always done with their visuals.

Be your own Banksy.

Or what if you live out in the middle of nature? Are you off the hook? Not at all…

Hang your painting on a tree (in a way not to harm it). And then let it get affected by the elements. You're letting Mother Nature paint on top of it. And every day, take a picture of it to document Mother Nature's new brush strokes. Rain. Bird pecks. Dirt. Wind. Share the progress in your IG story with us every day so we can watch the evolution with you. And after a month, take it down and sell this collaboration with Mother Nature in your Shopify store for $800.

See what I mean?

Be your own Banksy.

When I tell creatives… "Find a way to share your art in the real world…" The same thing happens almost every time.

They complicate it.

They make the idea so convoluted they'll have to delay action forever. It's their way of buying time.

Don't be that person.

Come up with a simple concept and test out a version of it immediately.

You've been sharing work digitally because it requires minimal effort.

What's scarier is... Going out into the real world and getting live feedback.

What's more nerve-wracking is... Seeing the whites of people's eyes.Those things will also have 100 times more impact on your future than an online portfolio ever could.

Creatives study what successful artists have done before them and copy their moves.But unfortunately, by the time it's copyable, it's already lost its impact.

Successful artists sought what no one else had done before and forged their paths.

That's what I'm asking you to do.

To sit with it for longer than 5 minutes before you give up.

What you've been doing is the bare minimum.

You throw things up. You're filled with wishful thinking. Hoping that someone will discover you.

But no one cares about your illustrations on Instagram. #truthlotion

No one cares about your new single on Spotify. #truthlotion

No one cares about the writing you share online. #truthlotion

Static art is quickly becoming the domain of AI.

Where does that leave you?

Becoming a creator of dynamic art.

Modern art lovers are feeling a deep existential need to connect with others. More so now than at any other time in history. They want to be inspired by people who are "tapped in." People who embody the messages in their art.

Be that person for them.

Dynamic art = art that makes a statement.

Dynamic art = art that is living and breathing in the real world.

When I tell you to "Be Your Own Banksy," I'm not saying you should copy Banksy's style or methods. I'm sayingBE INSPIRED BY HIS APPROACH OF NOT WAITING FOR THE ESTABLISHMENT FOR VALIDATION.

If inspiring others through art is high on your priority list…

Then inspire them.

Art is not vandalism.

Art is religion.

And sharing art with the world is how we express our beliefs.

You've been allowing your art to become content.

You've been allowing yourself to settle for creating wallpaper with no message.

It's easy to say, "Make art, not content."

Now, I'm inviting you to DO something about it.

Go beyond Instagram.

Photograph or film the process.

Photograph or film the results.

Put THAT up on IG. Your online audience will start feeling like something real is brewing.

You've been thinking too small. You've been focused only on the World Wide Web. But meanwhile, you forgot about the actual WORLD itself!

Go beyond Instagram.

Everyone shares on social media. That's why this practice, in isolation, keeps you invisible.

Your new MOTTO should be to share your art in the REAL WORLD. Not just online.

Make your social media a museum for your real-world actions.

It's hard to generate momentum for interest in your art when you're not doing things in the real world.

But ironically, the more real-world things you do… The more your social media and overall audience grows.

I invite you to start this loop today.

### 6. Be Your Own Banksy

### "If I didn't start putting my art up in random places, my art would have just sat at home, and no one would have ever seen it. If you wait for people to latch on to what you're doing, you'll be waiting around forever. You might as well cut out the middle man and put it out into the world yourself." -- Banksy

## "Be Your Own Banksy."

### To be part of the 1% of successful artists, you have to start doing things that 99% of regular artists aren't doing.

### 1. ONCE A WEEK, SHARE YOUR ART IN THE REAL WORLD.

### 2. DISPLAY OR SHARE YOUR ART IN A PUBLIC SPACE THAT WASN'T NECESSARILY DESIGNED FOR THAT. DELIGHT PEOPLE.

### 3. DOCUMENT THE MOMENT. DOCUMENT THE INTERACTIONS.

## Doing The Bare Minimum Keeps Your Art In The Shadows

### NO ONE CARES UNTIL… YOU DO REAL-WORLD THINGS TO MAKE THOSE THINGS FEEL SPECIAL.

## Go Beyond Instagram.

### 1. Display, or

### 2. "drop off", or

### 3. have people read or

### 4. have people listen to your art

### where it can have an emotional impact on people— In a way that social media content never could.

### 7. Dealing With The Fear Of Rejection

MINI PODCAST:

You're afraid of rejection.

Let’s analyze the stats for a minute.

Let’s say you get 20 no’s or better yet 100 or 1000 no's... before you get a yes. Would it be worth it?

But wait. Wouldn't it depend on the question that you're asking though?

What if the question you asked a complete stranger was: "Will you leave with me right now on a road trip from New York to California?"

And fourteen people rejected you... but the fifteenth person said yes.

Would you dwell on those fourteen people or would you start packing? And go rent a car?

Funny thing is... Those aren't even the correct odds. They're actually much better. But you would never know that because you haven’t tried. You would never know that because all you do is philosophize and refuse to put your thoughts into action.

You use other people's stats. Instead of getting your own statistic through your own experience.

If you put yourself on the line for a few days you’d see that rejection doesn’t happen as much as you think it does.

You know why?

Because EVERYONE wants to connect.

And if the quality of your crazy idea is good enough, only an idiot or a coward would reject it.

So if you're afraid hearing the word 'no'... just ask a better question.

### 8. The 4th State Of Consciousness

Bronques, I tried to do your dare last week ("get a sexy photo of a complete stranger") and failed. The craziest thing is... I live in LA where everyone supposedly wants their picture taken. Still, everyone I approached said no. I just kept getting rejection after rejection. How come YOU make it look so easy?

When I started doing dares back in the day and I started getting really good "results"... Bruce (part of my artist "dare team") asked me to describe what goes on in my mind when I approach strangers. Is there an opening line that always works? Is there something I say to convince them?

I've never believed in "lines" but still I tried to decode my approach for him as much as I could.

"Holy shit," he said after I explained my ways. "You're using the 4th state of consciousness."

I had never heard ofthatbefore.

Bruce is always reading about all the weirdest philosophies. He broke this new one down for me.

The 1st state of consciousness is simple: "Sleeping". With or without dreams. It's considered the lowest state of consciousness and it's the one furthest from reality.

The 2nd state of consciousness is "waking sleep". Yes, you're technically awake but you're only going through the motions of life. You "exist" and that's all. Just like animals and plants and the rest of nature. You are a slave to instincts. You have no self-awareness.

The 3rd state of consciousness is "reactive sleep". Yes, you're still asleep but now at least you start to see how your actions affect the outside world. You no longer feel helpless. You live with purpose. You use discipline, delayed gratification and power to navigate the world. You seek to have a "positive" influence on your surroundings.

Most people never go beyond the 2nd or 3rd state of consciousness. They don't know a 4th state exists. Lucky ones get glimpses of it in their lifetime like when they have religious experiences... extraordinary drug experiences... transcendental sex... But they are resigned to the fact that it's always temporary. It doesn't have to be.

But what does this have to do with approaching strangers?

Bruce broke it down for me.

Apparently, I had discovered a mystic process without even knowing it. It had a name. It had it's own set of rules. And he explained it like it was simple math.

And once I understood it, I could repeat it "at will". Surprisingly without any diminishing returns. It gave me even more confidence to go further, crazier, with my artistic ideas.

But the most exciting part was... it was teachable.

Anyone that I explained Bruce's 4th state of consciousness explanation to... always did better. You immediately improve. Perfect strangers often become your new best friends.

How I described approaching strangers to Bruce:

"I'm not focused on what they're saying. I'm more concentrated on their energy. I'm listening to how they're receiving my words. I try to understand as quickly as I can what has led them to this very moment when I'm interrupting their day. I try to present this interruption as a way to make the rest of their day better. If I don't believe that I won't approach them. Rejection never enters my mind. It's never about outcomes. I switch into another gear. It's like a video game. I feel like I'm watching myself in a movie and waiting to see what will happen. Sometimes as I'm talking I'm already deciding that this is not the right person and I back myself out of it. I let them think they're letting me down. But when it's the perfect person, I put on the heat. I mirror their body language until I'm communicating with their higher mind. If it's one of my better artistic ideas and they still say no, the only disappointment I feel is for them because I know they're likely to remember this as an opportunity they didn't take... that they may even regret one day. Everyone wants to go home with a story. An artist's role is to give people stories."

How Bruce described the 4th State Of Consciousness to me:

"That's what the 4th state of consciousness is. It's when you see everything around you as energy. You stop preferring certain outcomes because you see everything as flow. The 4th state is self-awareness and complete detachment to situations. You describe looking at yourself like you're standing outside of yourself. They call that "witnessing". And when you get in that state... You're basically egoless which gives you endless energy that others can draw from. That's why people feel comfortable since most people are usually competing for energy. When you're in the 4th state of consciousness you stop listening to the words people say and focus on their body language and vocal inflections. It's exactly how psychics and fortune tellers get their magical insights. You're operating in a primal language. You're approaching people almost like you're coming to give them a gift instead of approaching them like you're bothering them like everyone else does. So of course you'll get better results."

So next time you have to approach a stranger remember these 4 things:

1. See people as spiritual energy not as a physical body. Now you will observe their full potential. Not just the static version in front of you.

2. Watch yourself behave in the situation as if you're watching someone else outside yourself. It should feel like you're watching a movie.

3. Don't approach social situations married to an outcome. Being result-driven will only blind you to what's really going on. You win when you go into it open. The only thing you expect is for the right thing to happen... Whatever it is. You'll even EMBRACE "rejection". An aborted interaction leaves room for the right person to arrive.

4. The right person always arrives.

### 9. "99 Photography Tips" (For Non-Photographers)

No matter what your art form is, you'll need to get better at photography. Photography is key to storytelling online. But if you REALLY want to catch people's eye, start incorporating the random people you meet in the stories you tell also. The results will be exponential,

Here are 99 Photography Tips (for non-photographers) to get you started...

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #1. Take 1,000 pictures a day. With intent. Intent means that you have a goal before you push the shutter. When the results start to match the intent, raise the bar on your intent. Repeat this until you die. At some point along the way someone may ask to publish one of your photos. It may even happen twice.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #2: Photography is showing what hides beyond the surface of what the eye usually sees.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #3: Once you have a connection with your model, your shot-list doesn't matter.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #4: There is no cure for cookie-cutter.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #5: Don't go in with expectations. But if the moment arises, seize it.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #6: Embrace being the third-wheel. It's opportunity in disguise.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #7: No one's in your room at 4 a.m. to do something normal.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #8: Pay attention to coincidences. They are synchronicity in disguise.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #9: Yes, you may be the painter... But always remember that it's the model who brings the palette.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #10: Ignore celebrities. Create new ones.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP# 11: Sometimes photographers are like therapists. And sometimes it’s the model.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #12: Don't "steal" photos. Ask for permission. True, you may miss the moment. But it gives you access to new moments you could never have otherwise.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #13 It’s ok to use the same directions you used “last time”. Every model will give you a different interpretation of the same pose.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #14: Don’t plan your photoshoots. The amazing photographer that’s hiding inside of you only comes out to play when you improvise.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #15: If you can't find someone's wild side. Let their wild side find you.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #16: Everybody has a wild side. It’s up to you to find it.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #17: When you meet sisters. Never shoot one. Always shoot both.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #18: Always try to find out your model's hopes and dreams. Just talking about it will put a glimmer in her eye. And a glimmer is always photogenic.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #19: Bad photoshoots may happen, but they still make for good stories. There's no such thing as a bad photoshoot if it gives you a good story.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #20: When you shoot friends together, they will want to huddle like it's “vacation photos”. Encourage them to be individuals instead.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #21: When you do a group shot, people will tend to stand in a line-up. Use layering instead.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #29: Learn to love dirty tiles just as much as you love marbled floors.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #30: Reinvention should look a lot like invention... or you're doing it wrong.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #31:Make it look like “anybody can do that”.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #35: When you’re a pioneer, half the world thinks you’re a genius, the other half thinks you’re shit. They’re both right until you have a body of work that proves one of them wrong.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #40: The best way to get your model out of their head is to have them participate in creating a moment.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #55: Don't photograph the first person you see. Photograph the second.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #62: Sometimes the person you want to shoot has even better friends.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #63: The only thing more unhealthy than break-up sex is a break-up photo shoot.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #64: If she starts texting her ex... The photo shoot is over.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #65: Sometimes, a hotel room can be more inspiring than a whole city.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #67: The best pictures happen when you try to have your cake and shoot it too.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #68: There is less and less oxygen as you climb to the top.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #69: You're nobody until you're an item on someone's bucket list.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #70: A great outfit can inspire even the smallest minds into submission.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #71: What people call boring nights are really just missed connections.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #72: If you want to make the world look a little more beautiful. There’s only one option: Fall in love with where you are in that moment.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #73: Don't let your relationship deteriorate to the point where a stranger can take a better picture of your significant other than you.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #74: Embrace your awkward side. It'll attract a whole new demographic.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #75: Be shy. Be courageous. Be tender. Be bold. They’re all photographable.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #76: The exciting thing about people isn’t who they are... It’s who they can become. Especially with Photoshop.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #77: Sometimes, connecting with someone starts by simply letting them in.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #78: Highlighter under the eyebrows is magical.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #79:When you go to an art show, always remember that the art isn’t only on the walls.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #84: Once you get good at photography, people will start to say things like, “You only photograph attractive people.” But you will secretly know they’re wrong. A photographer can only photograph what they see. You become a GOOD photographer when you can turn what you see into a picture that matches. Your photos will become a reflection of the excitement you feel for the person or situation in front of you. If you cherish beauty, suddenly everyone will look “beautiful”. Bad photographers are the ones who try to use shortcuts like "shooting models" hoping to compensate for their lack of skills. But all they end up with is a lousy photo of a good-looking person. Why do you think even the hottest people are picky about who shoots them? Because they understand that physical attractiveness won’t ever make a photo great. To get better photographs start dedicating yourself to photographing people’s energy instead.

### 10. Every Artist Is A Renegade

A blocked artist is simply an artist who has to be un-programmed.

The problems start when every time we think about doing something bold, we go and consult whatever past programming we've received to decide whether to do it or not.

But how often is that final decision be based on our authentic selves?

Have you been making art that is merely a collection of borrowed ideas?

Does your artistic vision only reflect the sum total of your upbringing… Your schooling… Your social grooming… Your culture… Your country’s laws… Your religion… Your desire to fit in…

Ask yourself...

How much of your art so far has come from your own authentic voice?

If you’ve been feeling rising anxiety creeping up on you… It’s probably because you’re not living your truth. It’s probably because you’re borrowing someone else’s truth. Every time you play the game, you deny yourself of your full expression.

You go through life putting on masks going along with the crowd for your survival. And before you know it, everything you create is just a mirror of what society or the CULTure wants it to be.

Society relies on people believing that the whole construct isn’t an old white man's fabrication.

But some people decide to untether from groupThink. They shed the masks. They stop being complicit.

It isn’t easy. But they do it for their spiritual survival.

When that second awakening happens to you...

A renegade is born.

There are renegades...

And there are pretenders.

It's easy to spot a renegade.

They’re the people who inspire us.

They used to share the same beliefs as everybody else— But then something happened along the way, and they started going down their own path.

We don't always know what made them change, but we love what they now stand for.

Renegades give us clues about what's possible.

They come up with the concepts/ideas/philosophies that other people share.

Maybe they experienced pain at some point, but now they've found an antidote. An antidote that the masses decry as blasphemy. An antidote that they know is the truth.

Armed with their message, renegades are ready to jump over the rules to get where they gotta go.

They take pleasure in not being a part of the mainstream because the mainstream feels so constricting and lame.

Their clarity about why the conventional way of thinking is wrong, is such, that they'll gladly pay the price of not fitting in.

They wait for the rest of the world to catch up.

The Pretenders are the wannabes. Fake renegades.

You know the type. All talk, no action.

They wear the right clothes. They speak the right soundbites. But because they always disappoint, we end up doubting the real renegades who show up on our path.

They muddy the water.

So here are a few signs to spot them early…

Pretenders are those people who 'steal' the inspiring concepts/ideas/philosophies that renegades come up with and try to pass them off as their own.

Pretenders will use all of their energy to give off a false exterior of strength, but really… They're crumbling inside.

They will say things like "I don't give a fuck," not realizing that if they REALLY didn't give a fuck they wouldn't even be thinking about it. They’d be vibrating at a higher energy.

Another favorite pretender phrase is "maybe it wasn't meant to be”. They love this one because it gives them an easy way out.

(Nothing great was "meant to be". The Mona Lisa wasn't "meant to be". The Taj Mahal wasn't "meant to be". The person you met on the plane that ended up becoming the Godmother to your newborn 2 years later wasn't "meant to be". )

Things happen because renegades make them happen.

Pretenders' "acts of courage" are always tales of nostalgia.

They always "already did that". They always "already went there"

But when you look closely... they're just living off the fumes. They live cozy little lives... and judge the hell out of YOU for doing what they wished they could do.

Pretenders secretly hate renegades for being amazing because it reminds them that they aren't.

Pretenders are the people who will "ghost" you when it’s time for revolutionary action.

Pretenders will justify their failures. They will take the easy way out while making it seem like strength. And they'll sell you "the dream" in the most poetic way.

Pretenders talk so loud they fool you into thinking they're renegades. They muddy the water.

Expose the pretenders. Call them out.

I lied. There’s a third group.

And they're just as inspiring as the renegades are.

They are the “renegades in training”.

The "renegades in training" are those who are trying to improve themselves every day. They haven’t overhauled their whole thinking yet but… They ARE looking for any opportunity they can find to express a new side of themselves.

They are constantly shedding old skin.

For example… They know they're shy. But being shy doesn't stop them from acting like extroverts… In the name of their art.

And they know they're scared. But being scared doesn't stop them from acting courageous when they see injustice.

They’re renegades in training because they’re still looking for their world view.

But as they’re searching, they already know three things for sure…

1. That you're either expanding… Or you're contracting.

2. That if you're "not busy living… Then you're busy dying" (Bob Dylan).

But best of all…

They know that finding how to express their truth is just an iteration away.

Yeah sorry... Totally one last one.

The Retired Renegades

Retired Renegades don't have the energy for the renegade stuff anymore.

Either that or their responsibilities have yanked them out of the game.

But it doesn’t mean they aren’t making a worthy contribution.

They’re the ones who “finance” the active renegades with money, power, connections, and best of all…

Hidden knowledge.

They're the "supportive friends" who rail against the haters.

They are the subversive teachers… Who may look like they’re leading a normal life (to the outside world), but their whole aim is to infuse the next generation with renegade ideology.

They are the receptionist or secretary who secretly "unlocks the office door" so that the renegades can get in and do some renegade shit.

Retired Renegades aren’t doing wild things on the front lines anymore but… they're busy helping renegades infiltrate the system.

Retired Renegades may now be “quietly raising children”. But believe me… They're not raising ordinary children. They're raising mini-renegades. They're indoctrinating their offspring with renegade values.

And we thank them for that.

So tell me…

Are you a renegade?

A renegade in training?

Or a retired renegade?

'Cause I know there are no "pretenders" in here.

But truth be told:

We all have a little pretender inside of us trying to run the show. The only way to suffocate that voice is to dive deep into renegade territory. ’That’s how you give that insidious voice no room to rise.

So, my fellow renegades, I end this by asking you…

What "acts of courage” are next on your horizon?

### 10. Every Artist Is A Renegade

## 1. The Renegades

## 2. The Pretenders

## 3. Renegades in training.

## 4. Retired Renegades

### 11. How I Ended Up Getting Those Epic Ashley Olsen Photos

I love that Warhol quote.

Even US Weekly created that "Just Like Us" column that is "crack" to females waiting for their flights at airports.

But my favorite photos to take? Besides making regular people look like comets in the sky?

Is of famous people doing unusual things.

I mean, why get the same photo that everyone else is getting, right?

That's why most of the time you'll see me flat-out ignore all the celebrities in the room. Most of the time they're too afraid of being "not on brand". At least the B-celebrities are. In the time that it takes to deal with their publicist, I could have taken 10 more awesome pictures. And the funniest part of it all? Being "not on brand" is 10 times better for their career than being "on brand" ever was. But I digress...

So, while every other photographer is trying to get their "money shot" in the V.I.P. section... They leave the whole rest of the room, all to me, to discover an "unknown superstar", being totally ignored

That's why often photographers will say to me the next day "When I see your photos, it's like we photographed two different parties."

And that's exactly the energy I want to bring to parties when I go out.

PHOTOGRAPHY TIP #10: Ignore old celebrities. Create new ones.

But once in a while, a friend will introduce me to someone who happens to be famous.

Like Marvin, the founder of Nylon Magazine did that night.

But you have understand my frame of mind leading up to this encounter...

I only cared about one thing:

Who will be my triptych tonight?

Let me explain.

Back then, every night I would find someone to be my "triptych pinup". For the non-technical: a triptych is when 3 photos are presented as one.

I don't usually care for those "artsy" photographer concepts. But my "triptych pinups" developed out of pure necessity.

You see, back then, I never took vertical photos. I had a very 'IKEA' attitude about my online galleries. Everything had to be in a grid.

But that meant that I couldn't get whole outfits unless I was really far away.

I made the person lie down somewhere.

Which I would do, but that got boring to me.

But, throughthe process of iterations, I developed this new thing... Photograph them in 3 separate sections. Then stitch the photos together!

Just being creative... You know?

So when I met Ashley Olsen... That's what I told her I wanted to do with her.

First words out of my mouth.

Of course as soon as she lay down everyone was freaking out like "What's going on?".

So imagine this. While Ashley Olsen is lying there... The crowd of partiers back away to make room for us... And to get a better view of this unusual scene unfolding... Whispering... Tapping each others shoulders...

Which I didn't mind but one problem... After I took the first test photo, I realized the photo looked "empty".

So I had to tell the whole crowd to COME BACK. Move CLOSER. I needed them to crowd us. Get around the couch so that I could see the feet all around her. I needed people who would see this photo to understand that it was taken at a PARTY.

Reluctantly, people did it. All it took was some of my trusted muses scattered in the room to move first. They never needed "the memo". And Ashley patiently waited smiling.

"Closer... Ok. YOU. Closer..."

And then... When I started by taking photos of Ashley Olsen's feet everyone just wondered "What the hell is going ON?"

Well this is what the hell was going on:

All of this to tell you...

Don't be afraid to get the legendary photo.

Don't be polite just because it's a celebrity.

If anyone understands the power of an image... It's them. At least the A-celebrities do.

So always, always GO FOR IT.

And then later you can ask to take the "boring photo" that the media outlets will demand for "coverage" the next day.

### 12. What Charismatic People Do That Shy People Should Also Be Doing When They Approach Strangers (Without Ever Needing To Come Out Of Their Shell)

People are so focused on knowing the magic words I SAY to strangers that I meet... That they completely miss the (more crucial) invisible step I take BEFORE I even open up my mouth.

I discovered this "technique" way before I started carrying a camera everywhere.

From a semi-controversial source.

Choli (pronounced like Charlie without the ‘r’) always made me do the hardest shyt.

The third day I met him, he said, "Walk up to that girl over there... And get her number."

I was like, "What? As if. I can’t do that. She’ll slap me or something."

I mean... How would someone even go about starting a conversation like that? I got dry mouth just thinking about it.

But today, Choli was going to make me do it. He was already pointing and saying, “That one.

I turned to look.

A cute girl with a big baggy sweater that said “Australia” on it, glided by.

She had headphones on.

CLEARLY she didn’t want to be interrupted

CLEARLY she was on her way to meet her boyfriend. Or worse, her dad.

But Choli insisted. “Go.”

I felt sick to my stomach. And my legs were spaghetti.

But I limped towards the girl anyways. Yep, I walked right into my forecasted failure. Why? Because during that summer in Montreal ages ago, that’s what I signed up for.

But what about you? What did YOU sign up for?

Photographers ask me questions every day like “How do you do THIS... And how do you do THAT”. But without ever ATTEMPTING anything for themselves first.

Instead of imagining every possible scenario hoping to protect yourself from sucking (AKA procrastination 101)... You should instead hurry up and TRY the damn thing first. Invite fresh "bad experiences" and failures that you can draw upon for analysis

You need the "play tapes". Only then can a coach help you

The quality of the answers you get, will come from the quality of the questions you ask... And the best questions come from trial under fire.

That's the way Choli taught me the craziest things that summer. Like this particular afternoon when I fearfully approached the girl wearing an "Australia" sweater.

There were no hours and days spent "speculating" about what might happen...

And because I was willing to put myself through that short term trauma-- Choli was able to share an epic life lesson with me that I'll never forget.

His words would have made NO sense to my stubborn ass without the "play tapes".

What I learned that day is the basis of what I do before I approach EVERY single person I meet on the street. Young or old. Male or female.

It seems so basic at first. Like it shouldn't really make a difference.

But... it does. When you see the person’s whole demeanor change in front of you... In seconds... From following one simple rule... You're like wha--

Super easy.

The hard part? Remembering to do it. Especially if you're nervous. Or if you're in the thick of things.

I even shared this "technique" with the front desk girl at MGM.

We got to talking while I was checking in this week:

She's new to hospitality. And a little shy. I told her about my Choli trick. I thought maybe it could help her "up her game”?

The next day she was like “OMG, thank you! That advice changed my life! No more awkwardness...”

You can never do it "too much". People just love it.

And don't worry. No one will notice what you're up to.

But they will FEEL it.

They might say to their friends... "I can't explain it. But I felt comfortable."

The flip side? If you DON’T do it, they’ll “feel it” too. But in a bad way. They’ll say things like, "I don't know why. It was awkward."

Some people are born charismatic. They do it instinctively.

But the rest of us can learn it. And because you'll have a name for it, you'll consciously know what to do when things are going wrong

Ok, enough talk.

It's as simple as this:

Meet people where they're at.

When someone is walking NEVER EVER get their attention from behind. Always walk next to them or better yet in front of them. Lead THEM.

It sounds like common sense, right? But when I see people approach strangers on the street, it's the first mistake I see them all make. And lagging behind a stranger creeps that person out. It also makes everyone watching uncomfortable too.

If you're "chasing" someone while they're walking, it feels awkward because then they have to keep looking back. Or worse, they never look back. And then you look REALLY bad.

But if you tell someone about your photography (and why you want to take their picture) while you walk ahead of them... Even if that means walking backwards... You will be engaging in the #1 "approaching a complete stranger" power move. And if they hear the right thing, they'll stop.

You've seen it a million times in the movies.

Remember that moment in so many romantic comedies when the couple is walking down the street and they're connecting? And there's "chemistry"... And the guy is talking to her, walking backwards? I think there's even a scene like that in the new 'Joker' movie montage with his "girlfriend".

Yes, always walk in front (or at the very least, beside) the person you're talking to. This will put them at ease.

And you have to do this immediately. At the very beginning. Don't try to get their attention from behind. Only say "hi" when you're clearly ahead of them.

That's the advice I gave my MGM girl

I noticed that she was walking slightly behind me when she was showing me to the elevator which made things unnecessarily awkward. So I suggested she always get ahead of guests and lead the way. That way the moment would feel better for everybody.

I mad her try it again with me, right on the spot. You could feel the shift. The whole dynamic changed.

But that's not the only way to "meet people where they're at".

Remember this too:

If a person is sitting down-- sit down too. Or crouch if theres no seat. But whatever you do... Before you say the first crucial word, always position yourself first. Everyone fucks up because they start talking BEFORE they get into position. And do you know why you do that? It's because you're nervous. But when you're aware, you won't do it anymore.

Don't ask for permission. Just meet them where they're at, so they can be relaxed too.

Books teach people to do it with children... It's even in dog training manuals... But the truth is that you should do this with EVERYBODY. Including your grandma. New people you're introduced to. Even your exes. (ok maybe not your exes)

No one likes to be hovered over. It doesn't feel good. It feels imposing. Hovering over someone doesn't ever feel right.

Meet people where they're at physically.

And like magic, other body language things will naturally flow from this opening gesture. It will make the rest of your interaction more comfortable for everyone involved.

But this is just the beginning.

Imagine what it's like when you "meet them where they're at" PSYCHOLOGICALLY too

But that's another lesson.

### 13. How To Handle A "Third Wheel" Situation

Dear, Renegades,

I always suggest to all photographers that they learn at least some basic stuff about astrology. That magic question from the video: "What sign are you?" is only really effective if you already know some of the basics.

Start with yourself! Know all the good and bad qualities of your sign. 'Cause she's gonna ask you that for sure after she tell you hers. I've actually had some models insist knowing what sign I was before I shot with them just so they could guess my "temperament".

If you want to get a little deeper into it then at least know the signs of the people around you so if she's the same as one of them you can compare.

Don't go any deeper than that though 'cause then you seem like a freak. You're here to photographer her... Not to give her a reading.

Ask further questions in the comments and I'll keep updating this module with more information.

### 14. How To Photograph An Alien

In Hollywood the scientific term for that part of the story where "things get interesting" is: "the call to adventure". It's the moment where you, the hero, has to decide whether to keep having your boring ass life or if you're gonna step outside your comfort zone.

Every day you get 3-4 "calls-to-adventure". But if you never act on them. You'll stop noticing them.

The first thing you gotta know about Drive-By photoshoots is... You can't overthink it. As soon as you get the inspiration to approach someone you have to act on it immediately. Otherwise, you'll talk yourself out of it.

If you're lucky, every once in a while, the person you approach will suggest an idea that's out of your comfort zone. Two seconds ago they were a complete stranger. Now they are a co-conspirator who thinks you should "break into the church across the street and shoot on the roof". Yes, it happens that fast. If you connect, you connect. And if you haven't experienced this yet, it's only because you haven't started doing drive-bys yet. (More on that later.)

That part inside of you that's questioning "can I trust this person that wants me to go on an adventure with them"-- That part is called 'The Liar'. Don't listen to 'The Liar'. People (yes, we all do it) use lack of trust as an excuse for not following up on things. Babe, it's not a trust issue. It's a fear issue. You're just scared.

Remember what the opposite of fear is?

Stop judging things that haven't even happened yet.

It doesn't matter if it turns out great or if it becomes an awkward-fest. What matters is that you have a story to go home with. Never shy away from situations that you can learn from. Embrace every moment that you can add to the highlight reel that will flash before your eyes one day when you're on your death bed.

But for now... I just want to remind you that it's ok to get outside of your comfort zone. It's okay to be uncomfortable. You don't have to course correct everything.

I say this because as you're developing your "guts", you'll find that you always come to point where you have one last chance to change your mind. To jump ship. And 90% of people do. That's why 90% of people don't live up to their full potential. I'm not saying that you need put yourself in danger. But I am saying take calculated risks. Especially if you're a creative soul. Calculated risks are the seeds of your art.

People try so hard to normalize the weirdness they feel when they meet someone for the first time. They're in a rush to get back to safety. And because of that, they never give themselves the time to appreciate the other person as a blank canvas. They ruin the moment with a million questions and small talk in desperation to find common ground. When the best common ground, when you're truly comfortable with yourself and the world around you... Is silence.

The moment you stop overthinking and you just decide (and yes, it IS a choice) to just let go... To enjoy the ride... To let others point the direction forward... That's when you'll start to see all the previously invisible connections that exist between things.

But some people will never let go. They call it "pride"... Like it's a good thing.

I call it what it is:

Remember what the opposite of fear is?

Go out right now and look around for places that would be cool to shoot. Do this for 30 minutes.

After those precious 30 minutes of "location casting", ask 3 complete strangers if you can take a picture of them.

Back to back.

If you connect with one of them (and you never know... It might even be the first one!)... Turn your little "photo-moment" that you guys are experiencing into a "photoshoot" right on the spot.

Take your new muse to the locations you found previously for even more interesting shots.

And now for the clincher that I hope gets you into some good "trouble".

Let them suggest somewhere you should go that they think is interesting.

That's when the adventure begins.

### 15. Rai's Secret

In photography there's a concept called the "what and the "how". The "what" is your subject and it is constantly changing. But the "how" is your style and that doesn't change. It's what makes you, YOU! It's your taste. But once in a while you get a "what" that is so brand new that you have no idea HOW to treat it. And that is when you learn and grow. That is when you expand your style.

This happened to me when I took my first photos of drug usage at parties. After doing it a few times and seeing the results, I realized that because my style was so reverent, I wouldn't be including these kind of photos in my work. That experience shaped my style. It showed me what Ididn't want to do.

It happened to me when I shot my first day-time party. That first experience outside the world of nightlife, made me realize that it wasn't the time of day that defined my work but... the sexy and the rock and roll. That experience showed me what I wanted todo more of.

And it happened when I met Rai. She made me realize that I don't have to change my style just because she has an illness. When we did Part I of the shoot, I treated her with kid gloves. I wouldn't have done that with someone who wasn't sick. Rai deserved the same kind of boundless photoshoot. That's why I called her back the next morning and told he we weren't done yet. Lucky for me I got the second chance. And it gave her the opportunity to express herself in that grandiose waydespiteher illness. All the same lastnightsparty rules applied: celebrate life. Tell her story. She made me realize that the world is ready for an alternative take on serious subjects.

What things are outside your regular "what" that can help shape and strengthen your "how". Seek them out.That friction may help you get closer to discovering the message that you want to share in your art.

Every time you step out of your zone of comfort, you won't know how to handle it at first... but push through so that you can discover the set of rules that make your style your own.

Embrace the moments and the people that make you question the "factory settings" that you were born with.

### 16. I Fell In The Hottub

##### Post a comment

### 17. Renegade Angles: How To Master Looking At Things In Different Ways

Three months after I started my career, I got sick after Christmas.

I don't get sick much, but when I do... (like most males), I act like it's "the end of the world".

But what made the timing of this fever and flu even worse was that I had a big job coming up in 4 days:

The Tribeca Grand Hotel (NYC) had hired me to shoot their New Year's Eve party.

They were counting on me.

And to make matters worse, yes worse... Santa brought me a new camera for Christmas.

I know that SHOULDN'T be a bad thing, but... As any photographer knows... There's a "learning curve" you have to go through before you can master a new piece of gear.

I had to find a way to shortcut this.

I ALSO had to nurse myself back to health.

In the dead of winter.

Alone. (My roommates were gone until mid-January.)

So, the first thing I did (after a mini-panic attack) was something I learned from my computer nerd days...

Read the whole manual before you touch the equipment.

That left-brain trick is a Godsend if you're looking for speed.

Read the manual from top to bottom so you know everything it can do. That way, whenever you run into problems later... Your memory knows where to access a possible solution.

Please understand something, though...

Back then, I didn’t know ANYTHING technical about cameras. I didn't understand f-stops, exposure, shutter speed or any of that techie stuff.

So instead of worrying about all of that, I treated "learning the camera" like I was "learning a video game":

"When you do THIS, the picture comes out like THAT..."

And "If you want THIS effect, then turn THAT knob".

I memorized every setting there was, lying in bed. I compared all the diagrams in the manual to the complicated hunk of plastic and steel in my hand.

(In the end, it only took me 6 hours. Guys, it's so crazy how much you can get accomplished when you finally decide to put a hoodie over your head, ignore the world, and just do it.)

But none of this technical knowledge would mean anything. Unless I turned my attention back to the only thing that mattered:

Photographing people.

But how was I going to practice THAT?

Remember, I was in "self-quarantine".

I couldn't go out.

I had no roommates to practice on.

So this is what I did:

For four nights... December 27th... December 28th... December 29th... and December 30th... From 7pm to midnight... I turned off all the lights in my apartment except for one lamp, and start taking pictures of every single object I could find... And I'd pretend they were people. My goal was to make items around my apartment "look as glamorous as possible".

I used cereal boxes, my broom, pots and pans, books, and whatever else I could find, to substitute for humans.

My theory was that if I could make simple household objects look good in photos... Then I SHOULD be able to make people look like S U P E R S T A R S !

So I started with my lowest hanging fruit: kitchen appliances.

I learned that certain angles made thin things look better. And that other angles were more flattering for thicker objects. Especially at certain distances.

And a box of Fruit Loops taught that shooting from above, and about 5 inches away... Made things look more "majestic".

I also learned about shooting a little bit "off-axis". And setting my aperture to f/8 gave everything a "Gothic quality" when you blasted the flash.

But the best side benefit of this intense self-quarantine session?

I stopped needing to look through the lens to get a good photo.

By the end of "Day 2", I could accurately frame a picture with my arm extended anywhere. I started seeing the geometric angles that made things look good.

Eye. Camera. Object.

It was the same ‘angle theory’ that I had learned by playing pool with my friend Bruce years ago.

Not having to look through a viewfinder was bound to make me a better photographer out there too. I could keep eye contact with my surroundings AND my muse. Which is crucial in a party setting.

And by the fourth day... After lots of chicken soup, tea, and the tasty pepperoni pizza delivered from across the street (Danny's!)... I felt better.

I was ready for New Year's Eve.

And I’ll never forget the beauty that greeted me when I walked into the lobby of the Grand.

Her name was Karen.

She was the girl of my dreams.

She was wearing a glittery dress and "canary yellow" shoes.

She had come upstairs to make a phone call.

She was one of those fun girls that can make friends with anybody.

She offered me a sip of her champagne and grabbed my arm to lead me to the ballroom downstairs.

But wait, I said. I had to take a picture of her first!

I took that photo using my new ‘cereal box quarantine angle' theory.

Yes, ONE photo.

This legendary technique made her look better than she did in real life. And trust me, she didn't need help.

After she saw the photo she kissed me-- And then she was glued to me all night.

So yeah, self-quarantine is good once in a while.

It may hold the key to your ultimate transformation.
