### 18. Why Guys Who Take Sexy Photos Of Girls Are Fucked

When I started taking pictures... Here is what I brought to the table:

I studied pin-up photography in such depth and eventually mastered "how to pose a girl".

Taking party photos made me figure out how to make the "raw and dirty"... Look beautiful.

I could always take a better picture of a girl than she could take of herself.

But fast-forward to today.

None of those things matter anymore.

We live in the age of Instagram.

The age of selfies.

When a girl takes photos of herself they're often just as good (insofar as emotional communication) as the ones she took with a "professional" photographer. She knows her angles better than you.

Her selfies are way more authentic, more raw, more real, and more natural than anything that YOU could ever take. Why? She knows the model better! 😂

Her selfies capture people's attention and imagination faster. They project a mysterious energy that your "planned studio photoshoots" just can't match.

The dinosaur "sexy photos" photographer is now competing against the model's "all access" "sexy photos" of HERSELF!

So the question is..

Why SHOULD she make plans, drive there, suffer introductions, worry about her safety (or you hitting on her non-stop) and then have to wait 3 months to get photos back?

No, seriously. Why?

What are you bringing to the table that she can't do on her own already?

And in the comfort of her home, no less. With her cute new phone and her bestie acting as a human tripod.

You can ignore these questions and become extinct

Or you can re-align your creativity to your true power.

1. Make "human connection" part of your art.

2. Find your message so that it's not just photos but an 'art project'.

3. Make your photos about the stories too. Elevate their context.

Those are just SOME ideas. Do one. Do them all (like lastnightsparty). Or find your own.

Not only will you be hearing the word "yes" more when you ask someone to shoot... But people will come out of the woodwork now, seeking YOU out. That's what happens when you discover and nurture the "thing" you possess that only you can offer.

But if you don't have your answers yet. I got you.

I suggest you listen closely to the girls in this section. These muses are still investing quality time with photographers... Even though they don't have to anymore.

So get into full-on "empathy mode"for these 'FEMINISM FOR BOYS' modules.

And take a listen to what these girls have to say...

## THE BOOK OF PURPOSE: What's Your Message?


### 1. Finding Your Message: Introducing 'The Drill Down Method'

I often ask people, "What's your message?".

It's usually after they show me their new website... Or they tell me about their new business idea... Or they play me their new song.

But, at some point, if I give a shit, I'm always curious... What IS their world view?

Most artists just shrug it off. "I dunno. It's just art."

Or creatives with brands might say... "It's just a cool idea I had to make tons of money".

The stubborn ones... They try a little harder. They try to come up withsomethingto "wipe that smirk off my face". (Even though I have no smirk on my face, I swear).

They say things like... "Peace and love" or... "Helping people" or... "Changing the world".

We usually leave it there.

It's an innocent question, after all.

Let's go deeper.

Have you ever wondered why you choose to buy the things you do when you're shopping? Or why you like certain people? Or why you listen to particular artists? Or re-watch certain movies over and over again?

Seriously. Think about it for a second. What attracts you to all your favorite things?

I imagine it's because those things “mean something" to you? That they're a symbol for something in your life.

For example:

You like your best friend Sarah because... You grew up with her and she shares all those childhood memories with you.

You like cookie dough ice-cream because it... It's sweet and you like sweets. And you can't believe they made ice-cream out of the thing your mom would never let you steal in the kitchen.

And it works the other way too. With the things you can't stand.

You hate Republicans / PC liberals because... They're ruining the world with their divisive politics.

You never got into Game Of Thrones because... You don't like that "fantasy shit". You're more of a comedy person.

Those tastes you have are what makes up your unique "world".

The things you love.

The things you hate.

Everything else?

Tons of vanity projects are released every day. People figure that if so-and-so did it, then THEY can do it too. Maybe even better. Because, after all, we live in a "you can do it too" culture, where it's wrong not to “pursue your dream”.

So we're left with a sea of copycat music, copycat films, copycat books, copycat brands, copycat restaurants, copycat hotels, and copycat nightclubs... And they're all invisible... or at best "tolerated" by the masses... polluting the landscape and making it harder to see true innovation.

And it's all because no one bothered asking themselves "Why?"

Friends are afraid to challenge each other and ask "Why did you make that?" "Why are you doing that?"

No, you're not allowed to question people in that way. Because asking "Why?" sounds like criticism. And criticism is “shitting on someone's dream”.

Well f-ck it. If no-one's else is gonna help you, I'm going to ask you anyway. I'm gonna bring up the elephant in the room:

And guess what? When your partner (yes, you need a friend to do The Drill Down Method with, if you want the best results) ask helps you get to the bottom of it in a bunch of different sneaky ways... They won't be doing it to "shit on your dream".

Not even close.

Actually... They'll be helping turn your dream into reality.

Why should we care about what you do?

What makes you different from everyone else?

Are you helping to create a better world we live in or are you just a parasite feeding off of it?

What's your message?

Sometimes your message is right there in your circumstances. Or people assign it to you because of your talent or radically focused behavior.

But if you can't answer now...

Maybe after these 7 intense days during The Drill Down Method, you will.

I can’t guarantee that you’ll find your message by doing this workshop. Simply because I don’t know that you have a particular artistic vision at this stage of your career. BUT... The good news is that this process will 1. uncover it if you do, or at the very least 2. point out in stark detail what aspects you need to work on to get there.

Understand this: You don't need to formally KNOW your message to succeed.

But it sure helps to have that clarity when things aren't working out. It's a great filter to put things through when you don't know the next steps to take.

So if you're struggling to make your art catch fire...

"Finding your message" is a perfect place to begin.

### 1. Finding Your Message: Introducing 'The Drill Down Method'

### 2. What Makes A Strong "Message"?

A message is a story.

It starts like this:

A better way.

That someone is you.

Your message takes "your people" (the actual heroes of the story) from their old conception of the world to a whole new one.

And YOU are the tour guide taking them to this new world.

The more that you:

1. tailor your story to your audience,

2. and the clearer the path is to how you’re getting them there

--the more powerful your message will be in uniting "your people" behind you.

For an artist, their message is their worldview. (A brand new way of seeing / doing things). It's your way of expressing your artistic vision expressed to your audience.

For a brand, a message describes your values and how your product (and way of doing business) backs up those values.

A strong message always speaks to a specific audience and always shows them a clear path to this new world.

“Fuck fear” is not a message.

“Freedom at all cost” is not a message.

"Be yourself" is not a message

At worst, they're faceless slogans.

At best, they're nice to put on a t-shirt maybe.

But a message... Those are the words that clearly show us your vision of a better world (or new way of thinking) and it tells us EXACTLY HOW YOU'RE GONNA HELP TAKE US THERE.

Compare this:

The Mystery School slogan:

To The Mystery School message behind it:

Do you know YOUR message?

If not, use this MESSAGE FORMULA to help you (replace what's in the brackets).

(humorous but real example: Kim Kardashian (when she was starting out): "I hate how society's beauty standard is all about being skinny and being "put together". I want to embrace my curves-- and have the freedom to be raw & messy just like real life is-- That's what my reality show is gonna be about. Thick, real girls getting ahead by showing the things that other people in Hollywood sweep under the rug. Who's with me?")

If you're having trouble finding your message... This whole section, 'The Book Of Purpose', will help you find it.

### 2. What Makes A Strong "Message"?

## First... What IS a "message"?

### "Once upon a time the world was one way and then someone came along and showed people a new way."

## A message is not a slogan.

### "Make art not content."

### "A culture that worships image over substance is toxic. It’s up to artists and creatives to restore some sanity to the world by outsmarting the content makers and releasing ART drenched in authenticity and depth. I want to make creativity a new religion, by mentoring the next generation of artists who want to find and share their authentic voice. "

## The 3 ingredients of a strong message:

### 1. Invites people to embrace a new ideal that hasn't materialized in the world yet (THE WHY).

### 2. It shows us how you plan on taking your audience there (THE HOW). Without "the how" you're only venting.

### 3. It is contrarian enough to have hardcore fans (your niche audience - YOUR WHO), AND haters.

## THE MESSAGE FORMULA:

#### The way that(situation / circumstance / group of people -- right now)is(variation of: outdated / boring / fucked). I'd like to(the better situation you imagine)by(doing this particular thing - THE HOW).(Your potential 'believers' - YOUR NICHE AUDIENCE),are you with me?

### 3. Finding Your Message | 35 Famous Creatives And Their Message

If you‘re not interested in clout chasing...

Or selling your body on Onlyfans.com...

If instead, you want the focus on the value of your art...

Then the best "shortcut" I know is:

Make the reason why you do what you do very clear to the world. So they can latch on.

And you do that by having an irresistible message.

The process simplified is this...

First. Find your 'what': IE. Party Photographer

Then. Find your 'how' (your unique way of doing your "what"): IE. Take the craziest photos at parties, not just people standing there.

And then... You lead every bit of communication with your "why" (the reason you do "what" you do "how" you do it): IE. Party photos are boring. Let's create a world where regular people look just as glamorous as celebrities -- and create photos so "real" that you can hear the music in the room just by looking at them.

Your "what" and the "how" are about you.

Your "why" is about your audience.

Your "why" is your message.

Your message is a description of the NEW WORLD that you want to take your "family of fans" to.

It's the journey you're taking them on.

World-class artists who have managed to emerge from the shadows have one thing in common:

They have a message.

A great message succinctly describes the vision you have for a new way of seeing the world.

A message is not a slogan.

A message describes your unique vision of the world and implies what you and I have to do and think in order to get there.

A message is not a slogan.

A message shows the gap between where we are now and where we need to be.

For example: "Black Lives Matter" is a slogan (an expression of the new world order).

But a slogan without a message is powerless. It doesn't give people a plan of action or a new world to aspire to.

"It's time to create a world that's rid of systemic racism" is the BLM message.

It's this message that inspires people into action.

The message tells people where you're taking them to.

The slogan... It's just shorthand for the message.

No-one is interested in a vision of the world that already exists.

A great message is not about you. It’s about making better lives for other people.

YOUR MESSAGE IS BIGGER THAN YOU.

You may be the originator of the message, but the purpose of a great message is to free OTHER PEOPLE from their old ways of thinking. It takes us all into a new world. Just like the creative people you love did for you at some point.

We're all trying to make our lives better.

Every one of us.

That's why people who have a message are so crucial to society. They may not have everything figured out, but at least they have a proposed path out of one aspect of the current situation. To make our lives better.

A great message makes people feel less alone. Tell us: "What is the new world you're bringing us to?"

The path may be as ambitious as "healing the environment" or as subtle as "a new way of painting".

A great message is a call to enhance, make something old new again, to birth or to destroy.

It's what artists mean when they say they "wanna bring the culture forward".

That's why most great messages are by nature contrarian. They are about a refusal to go along with the accepted way of doing things.

We love artist who provide a blueprint for a new world. And the more people these artists find that are sympathetic to their vision, the more we watch these artists rise and rise.

Along the way, other artists may align themselves with their movement to help bring this message forward.

Maybe you share a message (a yet unrealized vision of the world) with another artist out there?

The goal is to get people to accept, agree and adopt your new vision of the world.

And once they do.

Everyone else just copies.

If you're working in the area of film, photography, music, art and fashion etc... and you're creating work piggybacking on someone else's breakthrough message without adding your unique voice to it, then you're just an "assembly line creative".

"Assembly line creatives" copy the basic aesthetic of someone's message without trying to further the intention behind it.

Strong breakthrough messages create a cottage industry for assembly line creatives to follow in their footsteps.

You may be jumping on a bandwagon. But you do provide a service.

Lucky you... You can clock-in and clock-out. There are no stakes in your journey. Your life is comfortable.

Which is fine.

But that also makes you more vulnerable because you're interchangeable with all the other assembly line creatives out there. Because what you’re doing isn't special or inspiring (since it doesn't have your unique voice in it and is only copying the surface). It doesn't bring a community or individuals around it. People don't feel passion for this kind of "art". It's just to keep boredom away (until someone comes around with an actual message).

But don't get me wrong. There is tremendous value in keeping boredom away.

But The Mystery School wasn't created for assembly line creatives.

The Mystery School was designed for the kind of artists who want to wake people up.

"But Bronques," you may ask, "What about all those lame-ass "successful" people you see that have no message? Surely Jake Paul doesn't have a message, right? And Kim Kardashian doesn't have a message, right? Why even bother with a message?"

Not so fast, tiger. Most of them do. You just forgot. Or... You weren't really paying attention while they were making their mark-- to notice. (I'll show you their message below.)

If you try to analyze the message of someone that's already risen out of obscurity... It may leave you confused. Their fame seems so random. But believe me, it's not.

Before they were on your radar, there was a reason people were flocking to their side. All you saw was the aftermath of that success. And now that they're famous, they can afford to expand into other avenues. Everything they do now has the context of their current success. They are "post-message".

But if you really want to understand what made these people stick out, you need to go back to their origin story. That is where you will find their breakthrough message.

This is a really useful exercise because YOU are at the beginning of YOUR origin story.

LikeJon Acuff once said “Don't compare your beginning to someone else's middle.”

So I've collected a few examples of the breakthrough messages that led artists out of obscurity in the past. Hopefully their messages will inspire you to get closer to yours.

And remember, while these messages may seem “obvious” now, at the time they were radical!

Remember life before The Weeknd? (I know you don't) The most cutting edge R&B at the time was a movement called "neo- soul". Artist like Maxwell, D'Angelo and Erica Badu had a smooth jazzy mid-tempo sound. Well, guess what? A Canadian artist and his team of producers made that style of R&B obsolete overnight with a radical message (we'll it discuss below) that is the status quo now.

That's what all the best messages do.

They enhance, bring shit back, birth or destroy.

If you've been behaving like a Assembly Line Creative for the last few years, it's time to get out of riding in the same lane as everyone else.

Tell us what you want to "enhance, bring back, birth or destroy".

Sometimes a message negates everything that came before it.

Sometimes it only seeks to carve out a new space in the world that will co-exist with everything else.

Sometimes it takes over the culture, because that's what the culture needed.

But a message is always an agent of change.

Study those who came before you. You'll see. No matter who the new artist is. If they’re connect with masses of people, it's because they have a message.

People only pay attention to what is “special”. There's no other way to make people pay attention to what you're doing. Unless it's your parents or your bestie...

Your message is what will make complete strangers pay attention.

You can fool people with a new haircut, or some clever PR antics, but your message is what will keep people focused on you after all the noise dies down.

But before we dive in, let me mention the exceptions:

If you’re "ridiculously good-looking"...

Or you were born with a 1 in a billion talent or physical attribute...

Or ended up in the right place at the right time (LUCK!)...

Then you don’t need a message (or some might argue that this IS your message).

I hope you have the foresight to cash in your "free pass" and the 15 minutes of fame you were handed... And quickly parlay this or another more profound part of yourself into a message.

You know... Just in case people decide to move on to the next "freak show" or "platter-du-jour" one day.

For these exceptions... Cash in on OnlyFans and YouTube!

Everyone else?

You need a message.

The most universal and powerful message that you can have as an artist is to bring forth a unique art / music / film / fashion style that no one has experienced before. It typically only happens every 10 years, but if you invent a new form of music, or painting, film-making, or photography concept that everyone else copies... That IS enough of a message. You have profoundly affected the world. Congratulations. I love you.

World doesn't have to mean the planet.

It could be the artworld.

It could be the music business.

It could be the publishing industry or The Austin Slam poetry community.

It could be your own little community of surfboard designers.

It should be whatever 'world' you're passionate about.

But I'm not talking about “you're really good at something" kind of excellence. I'm talking about G.O.A.T. levels of excellence. The "absolute best that the planet has ever known" kind of excellence.

The most universal and powerful message that you can spread as a human being is the "be true to yourself / live life to the fullest" message. But you don't get to merely say it. You have to embody it every day you're alive in order for it to become your message. People that are truly themselves without fear of consequence don't need any other message than their mere existance to succeed. Their middle finger to the inner and outer critic is the ultimate message. A message like this is all you need to propel yourself to the top of whatever sector you're working in. While everyone else has their half-inspired "I'm gonna be myself from now on" moments every few months... These creative human forces of nature live it 24/7/365. That's why we love them. They are a rare, rare breed.

The "other" most universal powerful message that you can spread as a human being is to "love without boundaries". It's the Jesus Christ inspired message. But unless you're gonna take it to that Jesus Christ inspired level (like Ghandi did), it isn't a really a message you're living. You're living a slogan. You're just a "weekend warrior" like everyone else living with their ups and downs, and their loves and hates.

People think Jesus's message was "Love everybody." It wasn't. That's not groundbreaking. "Love thy enemy." was his message. That's the new way of thinking he was trying to take the world to. And that's why he was crucified.

Hey, I never said this was gonna be easy.

RESTAURANTS

Noma (#1 restaurant in the world): The highest form of culinary experience is when all the ingredients are in season and harvested from your own backyard. Let's start a restaurant that showcases this concept and inspire others all around the world to apply it in their own way.

Anthony Bourdin: The best way to experience culture and live life to the fullest is through food. Let's inspire people to adopt that attitude when they travel too.

(A film without a message always feels wrong.)

Tarantino: Dialogue is music. I want to make movies where THAT concept is the centerpiece of this visual medium.

Aaron Sorkin: Dialogue is music. I want to write screenplays where THAT concept the centerpiece of this visual medium. (Same message expressed in a completely different way than Tarantino)

Christopher Nolan: A blockbuster can have as many deep, meaningful, intelligent and complex themes as an iNdie film can. (the whole DNA of what he stands for is in his very first film 'Memento')

Jake Paul: Every single day that you're alive is exciting, you just have to find the hidden gems every day. (And then he created a YouTube channel to prove it. His slogan says it all: "It's every day bro.")

Chanel: Let's make elegance accessible to ALL women.

Kardashian women believed in a new kind of feminine empowerment... "Let's start a television show where we show girls that you can be glamorous AND TOTALLY REAL. We will glorify thick eyebrows, thick asses, be show ourselves at our messiest and still be proud (the "women that run with the wolves" message) . They had this message at a time when NONE of those things were even conceivable in the culture. You had to be skinny, have thin eyebrows and it wasn't cool to be in a reality show and show your messy life "warts and all". Now that's everything a legion of girls are aspiring to be.

American Apparel: The "girl next door" wearing "girls next door" clothing... is sexier than porn stars are.

Terry Richardson: Fashion photography should be raw and sexy and shot with a point-and-shoot. If you have an eye, don't let yourself be limited.

So you thinkg good music doesn't exist anymore? OK boomer.

Every generation's "new haircuts" usually come with a brand new sound, and THAT combo will always be an irresistible message to the youth.

If you're fortunate to have invented a whole new sound and style, then that's all the message you need. Unfortunately, these days, many musicians think that using a different snare sample is a "new sound". But sorry bro, it takes more than that. In the end, the fans will be the judge.

The Weeknd: The Weeknd’s first love is film. So when he started making music, he decided to create a new kind of cinematic R&B. Songs with darker lyrics and a darker sound, bringing his audience of loners and party girls into a different world every time.

Skrillex: Dubstep is the new punk/pop (and that's saying a lot since he started his career in a punk/pop band).

Lady Gaga: Let's bring fashion and outrageous "pomp" back into music (just like Queen -- where her name was inspired from)

Billie Eilish: new haircut + new homegrown sound. "You don't have to be sexy be successful. You don't have to be loud either." This feminist message comes back every couple of years when the pendulum is swinging too far the other side for women.

Kanye: a new sound: "high pitch samples" sound. + post-message: Rappers can be preppy instead of gangster. This guy... Love him, or hate him... But he brings forth a new "post-message" and sound every few years! And other assembly line creatives just copy his scraps. He even managed to shake the political world with his "The president doesn't care about black people." message. That's why I use 'The Kanye Test' in The Drill Down Method.

Rupi Kaur: You can use Instagram to share unapologetically personal and sensitive poetry -- words instead of just selfies.

Steven King: "Scary stories" are serious art. Just as much as classic literature is.

Onlyfans: The "girl next door" is sexier than the porn star.

Nike: Physical excellence and activism go hand in hand in the quest for greatness.

Joe Rogan: Interviews shouldn't be limited to 30 minute or 1 hour boxes. + "post-message": Leader of the Anti-woke culture

Carmela Habibi (my friend isn't famous yet, but she's an example of what I think is the future, when a hot body will be so common, it won't be enough, a new breed of Amazonian "women who run with the wolves" will emerge): Intelligent Thots (the name of her podcast is everything she stands for - just look at her Instagram if you want proof)

Father Bronques (Make Art Not Content): A culture that worships image over substance is toxic. It’s up to artists and creatives to restore some sanity to the world by outsmarting the content makers and releasing ART drenched in authenticity and depth. Let's make pure creativity the new religion.

PERSONALITIES

Muhammad Ali: Physical excellence and activism go hand in hand in the quest for greatness. He made that clear when he changed his name from Cassius Clay and protested the Vietnam war. That's when Muhammad Ali was born, NOT when he won his first fight.

Anthony Robbins: Just like athletes need coaches, regular people need personal coaches too to navigate through life.

Oprah: Let’s make the "self help movement" cool by using the talk show format to make these ideas popular. Post-message: Book clubs aren't only for nerds.

Caroline Calloway: "Girls, let's turn oversharing into an asset, a weapon, and a source of income."

@sarahbahbah: Why not memeify our own lives as a source for our art and creative direction and glamorize our overthinking minds in the process? Let's put a spotlight on our truth.

Basquiat: African art deserves a respected place in the history of art.

Warhol: Everything around you is art. Let's make art accessible to everybody.

Dali: The language of dreams reveal the ultimate truths. + "Post-message": Your life is the real work of art.

Bob Ross: The therapeutic power of making art should be available to everybody."So he made a TV show to show people it was possible.

Trump: Fuck “presidential”. Entrepreneur spirit is what gets things done.

Hillary Clinton's message: SHE HAD NO MESSAGE. THAT'S WHY SHE LOST.

Emma Gonzalez: If older people don't have the energy to change things, the youth will . Slogan: "I call B.S."

Martin Luther King: The "I have a dream..." speech is his message. When your message is so powerful, so clear, so good and so controversial... That it gets you killed. One of the strongest messages ever.

P.S.A mystery student sent me their "message" the other day. I noticed a problem it had that's pretty common when people are on the message quest. Read this... And then put yours to the test: Messages are not about YOU. They're about where you want to take your community, your people, or the world. One “message” I hear all the time is “I wanna help people.” Ok sure, that's great... but that’s not a message. But HOW you wanna help people though... THAT might be the beginning to exposing the message lurking below your surface. For example, an artist who says: “I think patients would benefit if there was more art up in hospitals. I’m going to change that by curating artists to donate art... starting with my local hospital.” Now, that first sentence is a message. It shows us a simple new vision of the world you wanna bring us to. And by default-- it helps people. That's a message a community can get behind (or rally against). So let me clarify this again: A message is not about you. It’s about other people. It’s about freeing people from their old ways of thinking (like a new genre of music does). It’s about taking people to a new place (like creating a society where law enforcement respects minorities). You may end up being one of the prime benefactors of your message... But even if you do... Ultimately, it ain’t about you.

### 4. Finding Your Message | Modern Day Geisha (Part 1)

Do you know what Vision Quest is?

Not the video game.

Not the movie.

No, the Native American ritual that young people have to go through in order to become adults.

Basically it goes like this...

The kid is sent out into nature alone... naked... with no food... and they're not allowed to come back to the village for 4 days and 4 nights. During that time they're supposed to pray and cry out to the Gods... Until they finally see their "vision".

That "vision" may be in the form of a dream. Or it can be from symbols that they see in animal crossings or in the elements of nature.

The "vision" they get tells them what their purpose in life is. It outlines their role in their community. It gives them absolute clarity on how they may best serve their people.

And only after they get this vision can come back.

My friend Beki decided to go on a 3 night Vision Quest with me last month.

She's about to turn 25 and decided to figure out what her message was.

I've done this before with entrepreneurs, singers, rappers and brands.

But never with a model.

Before I did it people would ask me "Are models even supposed to have a message?"

Find out in Part 1 of this new controversial video we shot.

### 5. Finding Your Message | Modern Day Geisha (Part 2)

Can I tell you what happened to Beki since we did "The Drill Down Method" together a year ago to find her message?

First, she started doing weekly face to cam videos revealing personally lived, hard truths about the modeling industry.

As she puts it in her Instagram bio (at the time I'm writing this):"Body positivity and mental health without the sugar coating 🖤"("real, real")

And don't think this is easy for her because she's "pretty". She has to battle daily with one of the biggest creativity killers there is:

Perfectionism

But she fought. And she's won often lately.

And this religious weekly effort very quickly led to her getting a national campaign withMISSGUIDED. They picked her out of hundreds of girls specifically because of how outspoken she was online.

And then more opportunities starting opening up. Like acting.

This is just the beginning for her.

The acceleration of her career happened because she put 3 days aside to ask herself the deep questions.

Instead of hiding behind weekend brunches, mainstream nightlife, or binge-watching Netflix .

This kind of soul searching is what you need sometimes to wake up your sleeping giant potential.

Find your message

There are people in the hospital wishing they had the opportunity you have right now.

Don't waste it.

### 6. Read This Before You Do THE DRILL DOWN METHOD

Ok, let me ask you two questions.

The first one is:

If you answered:

1. "I make art for fun."

2. "I make art for arts sake."

Then you might still be in self-discovery mode right now. Why overload that part of the journey by trying to attach a message to it?

Eventually, a burning sense of purpose does start to take over your work. A time when making "pretty things", or "making hot beats" is no longer enough...

Until that passion rises, don't force it.

But if you DO feel that fire in your belly, then you're in the right place.

Now tell me...

If you answered

1. "Everybody."

2."I make art for myself, and if someone else likes it then great."

Again, maybe you should hold off on "finding your message"?

A message only comes in handy when you're ready to communicating an artistic vision to "your people."

If you believe that you're making your art for "everybody"... Then you definitely DON'T want your art to have a message.

When you have a message you run the daily risk of offending one of those "everybody's" in our hypersensitive culture.

And if it's a really POWERFUL message... Damn, you might even "get cancelled".

Mainstream audiences -- the "everybody's" that many people want to appeal to -- they don't like to be challenged by a "unique artistic vision". The masses prefer the cozy comfort zone of what they already know. They prefer the work of craftspeople and technicians. They are late-adopters to artists.

Hold off on this whole "message business" until you're ready to ruffle some feathers, ok?

And if you make art "for yourself"... Then you definitely don't need to worry about communicating anything to anyone. You're in "Me, myself and I" mode. You don't need a message. All good.

If you're still reading then you're one of the rare ones who have come to peace with this:

ART = CREATIVE SELF EXPRESSION IN SERVICE OF UPLIFTING A PARTICULAR COMMUNITY

That's what Lady Gaga does. That's what Frida Khalo does. That's what Rupi Kaur does. That's what ALL legends do.

And this whole "finding your message" journey is about:

Ok. Glad we got that out of the way.

If you think you're gonna do all the exercises in 'The Book Of Purpose' and that at the end of it all, a little ticker tape will spit out your message... And everyone will cheer. Bad news. It's way more lonely than that.

Purpose is like love: It's generated by passion.

More bad news: Nothing here will generate that passion for you.

More good news: The Drill Down Method will bring out everything that's already there, but been hiding.

Searching for your message is a process. A journey. Just like making art is.

And even though I split this experience into 7 days... Understand that it may take longer or shorter for you.

They key is to only attempt this when you can give it your full attention. Don't rush through. Never gloss over anything. I mean, come on... There's a reason it's called The Drill Down Method. You're supposed to go deep.

You're trying to hit a nerve.

If you get stuck somewhere and you find you can't answer a fundamental question. Don't move forward. Stay in the mud.

Everything else in your life is instant gratification. That's the culture these days. But this process requires you to end the habit of staying on the surface of things.

If you want the truth, that is.

Be ok with sitting with an unanswered question for many nights if that's what it takes.

"Keep the window open."

You're trying to reveal your artistic vision.

We're trying to get you to put it into words the reason your art exists-- So your audience can be riveted by it.

Isn't that end result worth the highest level of introspection?

The Drill Down Method will only be as powerful as your partner is willing to go down the rabbit hole with you.

The Drill Down Method will only be as powerful as HOW MUCH YOU'RE WILLING TO "LET GO" AND REVEAL.

The Drill Down Method is like therapy.

If you hold back... Nothing will come out of it.

If your partner is afraid to call you on your bullshit... Same. Nothing will come out.

It's a lot like art.

Or like life.

You get what you give.

I heard from two students this year who thought their Drill Down was a failure.

They were so focused on "I didn't find my message"-- that they totally missed what they HAD found.

Take Isabella, for example.

She didn't "find her message". But she discovered her Polaris Star.

In her words:

Dear Father Bronques,

Before The Drill Down Method, I had pretty much decided on being a painter. But around DAY 2 of Drill Down, I noticed that MUSIC kept popping up over and over again. I quickly realized that if I didn't follow my music passion, I would seriously regret it. So I made a choice to switch paths even though it feels like I'm starting a whole new journey.

Those five days showed me things I was unaware of. It made me realize that I wasn't struggling with WHAT I wanted to say after all... I had to figure out HOW I wanted to say it. I know that I don't have THEE message right yet, but now that I'm following my true passion, I feel like everything I'm doing is leading to it anyways. I see it coming out in what I sing and write about already.

I appreciate all that you do. Thank you for taking the time to read. I'm open to any suggestions if you think there's something I'm not seeing. Have a beautiful rest of your day!

Not at all, Isabelle... You're seeing everything you need to see.

When you get a major epiphany, don't be afraid to stop and go explore it before you continue.

Don't feel guilty about that.

Come back here later when needing to find your message hits you in the face again (if your current epiphany doesn't lead you there all by itself).

The other example I wanted to share with you is Mayra's experience.

Here is our back and forth:

Dear Father Bronques,

I tried to do the Drill Down Method again (2nd time). I still don "t quite feel like I've arrived at my message. Lately, I've been beating up on myself and getting frustrated.

FATHER BRONQUES: Mayra, let's investigate... How far did you get in The Drill Down?

MAYRA: First time we got to Day 3, the second time to Day 5

FATHER BRONQUES: You can't get to Day 5 without revealing SOMETHING. What did you get so far?

MAYRA: "Everyone is (message excluded for privacy). The world requires us to (omitted). Rejecting the boxes and (omitted). I want to make music that is (omitted).

FATHER BRONQUES: Mayra, WTF? "Everyone is (omitted)" is already a sick little contrarian slogan. Everything else you wrote is already a great foundation to create a brand identity around. It's so YOU. I mean... Can it be fine-tuned? Of course. Do you still need to figure out your audience and how to tie it all into the music you're making? Yeah, no doubt. But THIS is more than enough to build an online presence that's cohesive and aligned with purpose.

MAYRA: Damn, you're right. I had a look through my insta feed and you really can't tell that I am about any of these things. And they are all truly me. You're the first person ever to encourage me to bet on myself. It's scary, but I know it has to be done now. I honestly thought these messages weren't "good enough". As I'm saying it out loud, though, I realize how silly that sounds. I'm starting to understand that this is really just a process:

*a few days later, I heard from Mayra again...*

MAYRA: I started recording vocals for the first time yesterday. No words yet, just sounds, harmonies, etc. It's a whole different feeling now. I also started sending out emails to my email list of 56 people too :) Everything already feels more "right". Thank you for your words.

Don't focus on finding a "perfect message".

Focus instead on the epiphanies that you get everyday.

Those epiphanies will tell you where you need to go next.

I don't care what beautiful "message sentence," you write down at the end of the 7 days... If your whole demeanor doesn't reflect a newfound clarity and purpose... If you're not propelled into action, then you've wasted your time.

Don't start Drill Down if you don't think you have the energy to "move different" afterwards.

Dear student,

When you REALLY find your message...

Food tastes different.

You start to question what type of people you've been hanging out with.

You don't want to waste time anymore. Every second is precious.

You have a burning purpose. You dream about it.

When you look at your Instagram feed, you immediately see everything you need to do to make it more YOU.

You make your website a billboard for your artistic vision.

Every newsletter you send to your list reeks of someone burning with forward momentum.

Even your personal emails are fired up. You might even find yourself adding a new "signature" at the bottom to express "the new you".

You're on a mission.

You have more to say than you can possibly share, so you start needing to stagger your online output.

You struggle with NOT making every conversation at dinner about your passion.

But the best part is this:

When people ask you about your art-- the first words out of your mouth is about WHY you make your art not about how good it is. And because of this, even people outside of your community get excited-- before they even have a chance to experience it.

So if you still think you still want to "go there"...

Allow 'The Drill Down Method' to give you a few epiphanies or reinforce the convictions you were on the fence about.

BUT PLEASE--

While you're doing it... Don't go through the motions.

Don't gloss over questions. Don't skip hard to answer ones.

And don't go into it thinking that something is going to "happen to you".

No one's bringing you a fortune cookie at the end with your message printed out for you to follow.

If you DO have an artistic vision... This process will reveal it.

And it will give you the fortitude to pursue it.

But don't wait to apply it.

Don't dare let yourself go back to "business as usual" after this intense process reveals your truth!

Act on it right away.

Before the outside forces convince you that mediocrity and fitting in is the best path again.

Only ACTION can sustain even the strongest epiphany.

### 7. The Drill Down Method: How To Do It With A Partner That Needs To Do It Too

Ooh, you're finally taking the leap!

Get ready for a fun ride...

The key to doing the Drill Down with a partner is to leave a few days in between for some amnesia to settle in. This will keep it fresh for when you come across the same questions again with the other person.

The whole process should feel as intense as therapy. The whole focus should be on going down the rabbit hole of one person's mind that day.

(One person at a time.)

It's intense, yes. But it's also hella fun.

Btw, one good way to warm up is to do The Meyers Briggs Together:

Have one person ask the questions and enter the data online, while the other person concentrates on giving the best answers. Perfect for breaking the ice.

### 7. The Drill Down Method: How To Do It With A Partner That Needs To Do It Too

#### Here are my suggestions:

### The natural break point in the Drill Down Method is between Day 3 and Day 4. That's always where I take a break when I'm doing it with someone if it's getting too intense to go straight through. Having that extra time to think about "what just happened" is good. Ideas will marinate long after the sessions last. The sessions will conjure up memories (angels and demons), if the person asking the questions that day is probing deeply.

#### So here's the best partner schedule I've found:

#### Do Day 1, 2, 3 with one person.

#### Then switch and do Day 1, 2, 3 with the other person.

#### THEN do Day 4 and 5 (super intense days!) with the first person again.

#### SWITCH and do Day 4 and 5.

#### And then Day 6 and 7 same thing...

#### (If either of you finds your message at any point email me to test it out on me!)

#### Meyers-Briggs Website

### 9. FINDING YOUR MESSAGE: The "Drill Down Method" v 4.1

If you are the student "searching for your message" who is reading this right now... Stop!

Find a friend, a sibling, a mentor or a coach to help you.

(IF YOU DON'T HAVE SOMEONE YOU FEEL COMFORTABLE DOING IT WITH... EMAIL ME AND I'LL SEE IF ANOTHER STUDENT IS AVAILABLE TO HELP YOU)

Please don't try to do this on your own. I know you're stubborn like me, and you think you're "the exception" etc... Use that stubbornness to make sure you get the best ouf of this experience-- DO IT WITH A PARTNER.

Hand them this computer (or your phone -- OR give them your Mystery School log-in if you're doing it long distance..)

Then sit back and relax... 🧡

DEAR STUDENT... STOP READING. THIS SECTION IS FOR YOUR PARTNER'S EYES ONLY!

Dear Trainer,

The "Drill Down Method" is a fun 7 day "therapy session" to help artists / brands find their message.

The Method is best done with the help of someone else (that's you reading).

A friend. A trainer. A coach. A mentor. A therapist. Anyone that can faithfully challenge the student.

Preferably someone who has already achieved it for themselves... Preferably someone who knows what it looks and feels like so they'll be able to recognize it when the student gets there. Someone that can play the role of devil's advocate when the artist's "inner antagonist" starts fighting back.

Your friend will need someone that can push them without fear. Someone that can call them out on their bullshyt.

Because of this, I'm going to be writing all of these modules speaking to that person: YOU.

"Iteration procrastination" is very real. And it's resistance is hardcore. Your job as the trainer is to fight back with love and understanding. Look for clues exactly where the resistance is at it's highest level.

Your friend shouldn't be reading this with you. They should be facing you (or waiting for you to read this to yourself while you're on the phone). You need to see and feel all their body language (or listen to their every breath and pause on the phone).

They shouldn't be taking notes. But you definitely can.

They shouldn't be involved in any other activities except thinking and searching their minds. Put phones on silent.

The time you're about to spend together will be magical. It will bring you closer.

Each session should feel like an intermittent "fast". My suggestion? Drink water or decaffeinated tea. Preferably a warm tea high in antioxidants like "green Rooibus". This way the mind is sharper AND more maleable.

But make no mistake that what's about to happen will be fun!

You're about to help your friend figure out THE MESSAGE they want to share with the world.

Each section should be done on individual day. You need the breaks. Let each day bring both of you into a trance-like state that enables you guys to get to the "essence of things".

All throughout The Drill Down Method, remember to use what I call the 1000 whys.

Keep asking why until you reach profound answers.

Let's begin...

### 9. FINDING YOUR MESSAGE: The "Drill Down Method" v 4.1

### The 1000 Whys

##### Post a comment

##### 23comments

### 10. Day 1: Questions That Will Make You Fall In Love Again

The "Drill Down Method" is a 7 day coaching method to help artists / brands find their message.

The Method is best done with the help of someone else (that's you).

A friend. A trainer. A coach. A mentor. A therapist. Anyone that can faithfully challenge the student.

Preferably someone who has already achieved it for themselves... Preferably someone who knows what it looks and feels like so they'll be able to recognize it when the student gets there. Someone that can play the role of devil's advocate when the artist's "inner antagonist" starts fighting back.

Your friend will need someone that can push them without fear. Someone that can call them out on their bullshyt.

Because of this, I'm going to be writing all of these modules speaking to that person: YOU.

"Iteration procrastination" is very real. And it's resistance is hardcore. Your job as the trainer is to fight back with love and understanding. Look for clues exactly where the resistance is at it's highest level.

Your friend shouldn't be reading this with you. They should be facing you (or waiting for you to read this to yourself while you're on the phone). You need to see and feel all their body language (or listen to their every breath and pause on the phone).

They shouldn't be taking notes. But you definitely can.

They shouldn't be involved in any other activities except thinking and searching their minds. Put phones on silent.

The time you're about to spend together will be magical. It will bring you closer.

Each session should feel like an intermittent "fast". My suggestion? Drink water or decaffeinated tea. Preferably a warm tea high in antioxidants like "green Rooibus". This way the mind is sharper AND more maleable.

But make no mistake that what's about to happen will be fun!

You're about to help your friend figure out THE MESSAGE they want to share with the world.

Each section should be done on individual day. You need the breaks. Let each day bring both of you into a trance-like state that enables you guys to get to the "essence of things".

All throughout The Drill Down Method, remember to use what I call the 1000 whys.

Keep asking why until you reach profound answers.

Let's begin...

A psychologist called Arthur Aron did a study to see whether he could accelerate intimacy by simple asking a series of questions.

Do you want the long answer? Well, you can find the results here. https://journals.sagepub.com/doi/pdf/10.1177/014616729723400

Do you want the short answer?

Yes, you can.

The Drill Down Method starts off by asking a curated set of 20 questions derived from that study

Both of you should be sipping tea and "loosening up your minds" in the right direction.

You're about to find things out that maybe your friend's family doesn't even know about.

Maybe your friend has never "gone there" themselves.

You want to connect to your friend's values and desires.

This will create rapport and trust between both of you for what's to come.

20 Intimate Questions.

1. Would you like to be famous? In what way?

2. What would constitute a “perfect” day for you?

3. When did you last sing to yourself? To someone else?

4. Do you have a secret hunch about how you will die?

5. Name three things you and I seem to have in common.

6. For what in your life do you feel most grateful?

7. If you could change anything about the way you were raised, what would it be

8. Tell me your life story up until now in 3 sentences.

9. If you could wake up tomorrow having gained any one quality or ability, what would it be?

10. If a crystal ball could tell you the truth about yourself, your life, the future or anything else, what would you want to know?

11. Is there something that you’ve dreamed of doing for a long time? Why haven’t you done it?

12. What is the greatest accomplishment of your life?

13. What is your most treasured memory?

14. What is your worst memory?

15. If you knew that in one year you would die suddenly, would you change anything about the way you are now living? Why?

16. How close and warm is your family? Do you feel your childhood was happier than most other people’s?

17. How do you feel about your relationship with your mother?

18. When's the last time you cried?

19. What, if anything, is too serious to be joked about?

20. If you were to die this evening with no opportunity to communicate with anyone, what would you most regret not having told someone? Why haven’t you told them yet?

This has been an intense session. You need to take a break now. Maybe even resume the next day...

### 11. Day 2: The Culture Questions

You're going to need to understand your friend's connection with culture. What they love about art and culture will be accented WITHOUT looking at what they dislike.

Your friend spends so much time already, obsessing about what they dislike about culture, without realizing that this obsession robs them of so much of their energy and power.

Any time they move towards what they dislike (which is so much easier to focus on), listen but gently nudge them back to focusing on what they love.

Realign your friend with their positive influences.

Everything they love constitutes the "perfect world" that they'd like to be a part of. Their message is related to this deeply. This is what they want more of in their lives.

By asking these questions they will be thinking about "message". We choose are favorite things because of what they mean to us.

You should write out the answers to the why's. Don't write the artwork down. The art your friend loves is a reflection on something deeper. Focus on that by removing the source of the feeling.

NOTE: Only ask ONE question at a time and make sure you have answers you fully understand.

Don't let them bypass and say they can't think of one. They will.

For the next two questions, write out the message. Not the person who has it.

Repeat out loud every thing you wrote down. Make sure that they agree with everything you wrote.

Ask them "What do all of these things have in common?"

Map it out for fun. You're the one with the pen and paper...

Help your friend make a Venn Diagram of the reasons why you love these things in culture, where do they seem to overlap? What themes come up over and over?

The chances that your friend's message and what they'd like to convey in their art or business is in the realm of all these words on paper... Are really high.

### 13. Day 3 (Part II): The 'Personal Culture' Questions

Please take a break before this next section (PHONE CALL IS DONE, BACK WITH THE STUDENT).

This break is best taken with the students favorite snack. Not a meal, just a snack. Oreo cookies. Ice cream. Chips. Pita and Hummus. Fruit. Whatever. Something small and enjoyable to them that will divert the mind a little bit.

You and the student need to bask in the glow of all this positive cultural analysis. During your break, keep talking about all the culture you love. If the student ever deviates the conversation to aspects of culture they dislike, nudge them back to the things they love.

After the break.

Now you will really challenge the student about their place in the world. We want them to become aware of the gap between their heroes and values and where they are now. Not in a bad way, but in an inspiring way. We want them to remember what actually motivates them.

They will want to stay on the surface.

You may feel like a a-hole... But you have to continue to go deep.

You have to find answers that go to the core.

The first two questions are warm-up, low stakes questions.

Ok. I lied. They're actually not.

These questions sometimes reveals deep dark secrets about what the student is most concerned about. Probe, but without making a big deal about it. But believe me their "inner critic" is going to go into high alert here. They may even be too embarrassed to share all of the results with you. Play it down. As long as THEY are face to face with the answers is all that matters.)

Now move away from the computer. Bring out the list that you created during the 5 culture questions yesterday and place it somewhere nearby, in view.

All these questions will make the student tired. The sugar crash from the snack won't help either. It might even make them frustrated. Allow this to happen, but don't get wrapped up in it like they are. Remind them that you're hear to find the truth. Even if it's hard.

This is also the place where they will be tempted to quit.

That's why you will need to finish off with something fun. The next section is really fun and easy...

### 15. Day 4: The Contrarian Question

Dear Trainer,

After the last 3 days of analysis, your friend will now feel seen and heard. They will know that you're in the best position to help them because you know things about them now that few people really care to know.

Now we can get to the nitty gritty.

No more fooling around because you don't have to.

You have their trust now.

Ask these 3 questions over and over again until you get solid answers.

Tell the student: "You have no message until you stand for something that can create enemies."

You cannot move past these questions. You need to have strong compelling answers to these questions. Even if it takes days to figure out.

If you've probed deeply, the student should have at least the embryo of a message by now.

Have the student write out that message. As a full sentence. It should express their vision of a future world and how they plan on helping the world get there.

*And look, I know this looks like a short paragraph... But if you're doing it right, this can take hours. But it's worth it. You may be responsible for your friend's most important artistic breakthrough today.

Keep going.

Ok. Time to 10X the message now.

You will help your friend figure out how to execute their message so that it touches the deepest nerve with their audience.

This is why you ask "The Contrarian Question" (created by Peter Theil).

“Most people believe in x, but you think that the truth is the opposite of x.”

A contrarian belief is one that is not currently held by the masses to be true, but YOU believe it should be a common truth. You think it’s the wave of the future.

The student will want to give you answers of things that everyone already believes in. Like equal rights, the environment,"love is the answer"... You know... Generic things. Things the majority already agree on. Remind them that you're looking for something that THEY believe in that MOST PEOPLE DON'T BELIEVE. A topic where they stand alone or with a very small group. So much so that they don't bring it up often.

Give the student examples.

Here are a few answers to the contrarian beliefs that are held by a tiny portion of society. Any of these may become reality one day:

“Cryptocurrency will replace common currency in the future.”

“Women replacing men in powerful positions will give us a better world.”

“Naturopathy is the best way to treat all human illnesses, including cancer.”

But contrarian views DO become the norm eventually.

People used to think that singing in Spanish was a death sentence if you wanted to make pop music in America. But a few people believed the opposite... A contrarian view that is slowly winning that war on the pop charts now.

It takes courage to hold a view that goes against the majority.

Ask the student: What view do they hold that goes against "group think"?

If they can't come up with a contrarian statement, they’ll have trouble finding their message.

PUSH THEM A BIT: "So basically you're saying that 1. You agree with the majority of people about everything? Really? 2. You have no original thought about anything? 3. You're ok with the world (and art) just the way it is? Is that really true?"

Give them more examples:

When Kim Kardashian came on the scene, most people believed that being super-skinny and having thin eyebrows was the ideal in sexiness for a women. But her whole family started pushing a new feminine ideal: thick eye-brows and big asses. That was contrarian THEN... It was a statement that women found refreshing and SLOWLY started adopting.

But you can't use that one anymore. It was contrarian THEN... But it isn't anymore.

Ask them again "What ideas do they hold dear that haven't been adopted by the masses yet?"

The Mystery School contrarian ideas:

You're were attracted to The Mystery School because of it's contrarian views. In a world still thriving on content, Father Bronques dared to say:

"Let's start making art instead of making content."

"The artist should treat the creative process like they're an athlete training."

"Quality AND quantity is attainable to everyone."

"The key to mental health (for artists) is to lead an UNBALANCED life. A life of making MORE art."

"A creative without a message is a craftsperson, not an artist."

"We are leaving the "era of image" and entering the "age of message".

"Social media isn't bad. It's just the way you use it that's bad."

"Don't make your art for everybody. Make it for the precious few. That's the only chance you have of everybody loving it."

Ask them again... "What is YOUR contrarian statement? What do you believe to be true, that the majority of people don't believe to be true... At least not yet?"

This will make clear a promised land that your friend is trying to bring people to. But it also exposes to them who their haters will be in the process! It IS contrarian after all, right? The masses will disagree.

Once they find something real... This is the moment when you ask your friend: "Are you ready to stand for this? Are you ready to stand for something that will make you loved by a some AND hated by others? Are you ready for that?"

Stop for the day.

Tomorrow you will be giving the student's message "The Kanye Test". Tell them that.

You need to let the subconscious mind move around a little bit before you go hard again.

### 15. Day 4: The Contrarian Question

### 16. Day 5: The "Kanye Test" (Advanced)

Start today with the following explanation:

"It's time to bring your message to the masses..."

"If YOU were standing on the suspended platform that Kanye designed for his Saint Pablo Tour... And you decided to stop the music... just like he did every night... to go on a rant..."

And then after some discussion and reflection...

Start here:

Answer these questions...

Question 1: What about the world would you like to change with your art?

Question 2. What group of people thinks the same way as you?

Question 3. What does your version of a "better world" look like?

Question 4. HOW do you plan on getting you and "your people" there?

Everyone is weak with the answer to Question 4. Without the answer for HOW, you don't have a message. You only have a desire. You're only "talking".

Kardashian women believed in a new kind of feminine empowerment that didn't exist at the time. This is HOW they brought their message to the world: "Let's start a television show where we show girls that you can be glamorous AND TOTALLY REAL. We will glorify thick eyebrows, thick asses, be show ourselves at our messiest and still be proud (the "women that run with the wolves" message) . Who's with us?"

Noma (#1 restaurant in the world) believed in a new way of cooking: "The highest form of culinary experience is when all the ingredients are in season and harvested from your own backyard." This is HOW they brought their message to the world. "Let's start a restaurant that's fully immersed in this concept and inspire others all around the world to apply it in their own way. Who's with me?"

Don't let yourself use nothing words like "advance culture forward""oversaturated" "diluted" "cultural reset" "real artists" "focused" "unique" or "compelling" etc.That doesn't tell us HOW.Be specific about what your message is so anyone could easily explain it to their friends (otherwise, how do you expect it to spread?). "I want to expand the human spirit." is a bullshit message that has no legs. But if you say"I want to make clothes out of cactus skin and use the proceeds to support the poor kids in east LA." Now we understand what you mean. You're saying something we can understand, and get behind if we connect with it. "Expand the human spirit?" Not so much.

If there was a "Shark Tank" for creator's messages, your HOW has to be powerful enough that people would want to inviest their money into it. Don't try to be poetic. Or to write a pretty slogan. When you describe HOW, be clear and consise that anyone could easily paraphrase it.

Got it? Ok... Good now you're ready to fill this "message sentence" out:

The way that(situation / circumstance / group of people -- right now)is(outdated / boring / fucked). I'd like to bring(name your potential 'believers')to(a better situation you imagine)by(doing this particular thing). Who's with me?

(example: Kim Kardashian: I hate how society is all about skinny and being "put together". I want to embrace curves for 'thick bitches' like me-- and be raw & messy like real life is-- when we do season 2 of our reality show. Who's with me?)

Or this example of the first student to use The Drill Down to zero in on his message:

"God is a black woman." As God-like as they are, black women are under-appreciated and undervalued by the ones that should be loving them the most: black men. I want to create a lifestyle brand by a black man that serves to uplift black women. All photoshoots and merchandise would focus on and honor black women's greatness. - Aaron DowneyAVRNDWNY©

But remember... YOU HAVE TO BE SPECIFIC!

Another student submitted this as her message:

“The way that close-minded people use their circumstances as excuses is lame as fuck! I’d like to bring people who want MORE to a happier, fulfilling life, by showing them that growth is ALWAYS possible. Who’s with me?”

But wait...

Close-minded about what?

What kind of circumstances?

What sort of excuses do they use?

You'd like to bring "people"... What kind of people?

What kind of growth?

Use all the information that you've gathered about yourself in the past few days to give us a detailed view of what you want to do. If it's not specific, how can we get excited? How can YOU get excited.

Now tell your friend:

"Let's find out how your message resonate with ordinary people."

"Let's see if you can change people's minds."

Now both of you will go outside and ask complete strangers what they think of the message.

Or call some friends and put them on speakerphone and test the message out on them. See how they react.

Do they love it? Do they say, "I never thought of it THAT way..." That's a good sign.

Are they indifferent? Then maybe you're using the wrong language or describing it wrong. Keep tweaking.

Keep iterating on how you express the message until it finally resonates with real people.

You are about to embark on the real journey of an artist now.

This is what artists with a message do every day.

### 16. Day 5: The "Kanye Test" (Advanced)

### What would you say?

### What would be your "message"?

### Write out the manifesto for what would be your Kanye rant. THIS IS SUPER IMPORTANT. If you can't write it down, you don't understand it yet.

### All three parts of thatsentence templateare critical. Define your audience. Name your believers. This is super important. Otherwise it will just be "me, me, me". You need to tell THIS AUDIENCE YOU JUST NAMED where you want to take them. What better world are you taking them to? It can't just be "where we will have no fear" (for example). It need to paint a picture of what that looks like: "Where we will march the streets every night until we get the whole city with us." Or "Take over Spotify with songs about mental health and start our own playlists with artists that with the same message." (for example 😂) A message is about what you are gonna DO. It's about action. Call to actions are what makes people get out of bed. Where do you gonna take us? Nothing about this can be vague. Be confrontational. Keeping it vague is just your fear of marking your territory because then you'll become a target. Like John Lennon, like Muhammad Ali, like Lady Gaga, like Stephen King and like Frida Kahlo.

### 17. Day 6: The Alter-Ego You Need To Create

"One of the challenges of living in a society is wanting to fit in. You need to develop an alter-ego that can protect your message from this natural inclination."

"You don't want to be invisible."

"These next questions are designed to remind you that a message is what will make you NOT be invisible."

"Imagine people are talking about you..."

Make your friend complete this sentence about other people talking about them:

"That’s the girl / guy who..."

"She / He changed my mind about..."

Figure this out before moving on.

Explain to your friend:

"Finding your message is 50% inspiration and 50% just a formal decision... the decision to amplify one small part of the person you are... And doing it for the next three years of your life."

"Start to separate yourself from the full dimensional person that you are... And visualize the singular dimensional person (brand / persona / identity) that you need to show to the world as the best vehicle for your message."

"David Goggins has Goggins"

"Gary Veynerchuck has Gary V"

"Like Batman says in 'Batman Begins'... You have to become A symbol to the people."

FINALLY, ASK THEM: "What name would you give this new alter-ego of yours?"

Ask your friend: "Which ones of these magnetic qualities do you possess?"

LIST OF MAGNETIC QUALITIES:

3. What does X stand for?

4. What does X stand against?

### 18. Day 7: Are You About To Take Over The World?

This will hardly be a day of rest. But you and your friend will feel relaxed knowing that you have found the purpose!

EXPLAIN THIS TO YOUR FRIEND:

"In this section we will break down your message in the steps it takes your audience from their their humdrum life to a more fulfilling life through your expression of it in your art.

"Let's separate your message into the steps of the journey towards achieve this transformation with you.

Write down the key point(s) about how the world is now (in relation to your main message) that is not ok. STATUS QUO. List all your enemies here.

Write down everything you see that can be done to change things. Write down concrete ACTIONS that can be taken.

This is basically your message unfiltered. Add all the nuances and variations to color it. DREAM.

EXPLAIN THIS TO YOUR FRIEND: "Every time you communicate with your fans it will always be about one of these 3 sub-messages." In new wave marketing they're called Broadcast Messages."

"These are the ideas that will precede you every time you enter a room."

"It's what people will hear about you from others, sometimes way before they experience your actual art yet. You want that. It's called pre-framing. It's what will make your art more valuable."

GIVE YOUR FRIEND THESE EXAMPLES TO MAKE IT CLEAR:

MAIN MESSAGE: INSTITUTIONALIZE RACISM EXISTS AND IT NEEDS TO END NOW.

SUB-MESSAGE STATUS QUO: The police are killing us.

SUB-MESSAGE ACTION: Defund The Police

SUB-MESSAGE DREAM: We Police our own Neighborhoods.

Every time they communicate anywhere, you hear them focus on one of those 3 sub-messages. (They have several sub-messages for each step along the journey. This is just a simplified version.)

MAIN MESSAGE: YOU HAVE TO HUSTLE AND LOVE LOSING

SUB-MESSAGE STATUS QUO: People are too impatient with trying to achieve success.

SUB-MESSAGE ACTION: Move back home. Let your ego take a hit.

SUB-MESSAGE DREAM: Legacy: Imagine a world where empathy is the main value in entrepreneurship (to reverse the current Steve Jobs "asshole ideal" that exists now)

Every time he communicates anywhere, you can hear him focus on one of these 3 sub-messages. (He too has more sub-messages than these. This is just a simplified version.)

(THESE ARE ALL THE PLACES WHERE YOU WOULD SHARE YOUR BROADCAST MESSAGES)

on Facebook

in a video form

as promotional materials, magazine shoots

on stage / performance

Now go out there and make it real.

### Step #2. The "We're Not Gonna Take It Anymore" sub-message. This is where you communicate what must be DONE to change things for the better.

### Step #3. The "I Have a Dream" sub-message. You communicate how things could be. You paint a picture of the ideal future for your audience.

## THE BOOK OF INFLUENCE: Make Art Not Content


### 1. The Question You Gotta Be Able To Answer In Your Sleep

There are sixty billion "messages" sent out on digital platforms each day.

How do YOU plan to stand out?

People obsessively try to grow their "following" but rarely stop and think about the message they'd like to communicate to this "audience" they're desperately trying to grow.

But think of people you respect and are influenced by. They have a message. They represent something. That's why you love them. That's why you're influenced by them.

Even the president you may or may not hate has a “message”. And that's why you're weirdly triggered by him.

Everyone else? Playing in the middle. Trying not to say anything too bold or alienating.

Well that's totally fine if you're a "worker". But it's NOT fine if you're an artist... or if you're a brand trying to sell something.

If you can't stand on a stage and tell an audience why what you do is important... then you don't have a message. Whether you're a model, a restaurant, a television show or an insurance company... when you have a message -- it shows.

Even in this visual era we're living in... Words are more important than pictures if you want to build a solid foundation for your business.

I can show you 1 amazing picture of an athlete performing an incredible physical feat:

But you'll have no clue what brand it is until I add the words "Just Do It"...

or maybe...

"It Gives You Wings" instead.

Powerful slogans and symbols all derive from the brand's message.

The message is how people know who they're dealing with.

Powerful messages incite people into passionate action.

Action like... buying... or listening... or getting involved.

But without a message, you will continuously have a crisis of faith.

Native Americans have a thing called "vision quest" where they send their young that are coming-of-age into the woods without food and water for like 4 days. They're instructed to use that time to pray to the Gods until they get their vision – the vision that will tell them their purpose in life, their role in the community, and how they should serve the people. If they can't find it... They're not allowed back.

Every business needs to go through their own "vision quest".

Oh, I've done it with people... I've SEEN the difference.

Sometimes it took 2 days. Sometimes it took 5.

Always intense... soul-searching sessions.

But when you find your message... you literally wanna cry. It's life-changing. What you "need for the video" is obvious now. How to handle social media is suddenly crystal clear. Every new idea can now be measured against something meaningful.

When you have a message all your actions are guided by a different logic.

A bad day working on your mission feels better than a good day would in the old world when you didn't know what you stood for.

But sorry, there are really no shortcuts. You can't get away with "surface" messages like "I want to spread love", or "I want to help people".

Clichés aren't messages.

Your message has to show us a new version of the world that had been missing until YOU arrived.

It takes deep work to find your real message. You know... A message derived from your deepest values and principles.

Most marketing agencies aren't prepared or willing to dive into that process with you.

You may have to do it on your own.

But if you're committed to getting help... Here are the three types of agencies you'll have to sort through in the wild:

1. The “check all the boxes” type that will help you generate middle-of-the-road “content” to feed the beast.

2. The "shiny new objects" type with all the latest hacks and tricks to manipulate your potential customers.

3. The "all ideas must serve the message" type who almost feels like they're part of the family because they're so aligned with your values.

I hope you find a #3.

'Cause remember...

A marketing agency’s philosophy is a macrocosm: however they encourage you to treat your customers is ultimately the same way that they will end up treating you.

What's the only way you can get away with not having a message? Achieve mastery of the core principles in LE$$XN 02...
