### 3. Every Brand Should Have A Muse (Introducing Psychographics)

Photographers shoot models. That's what they do.

But SOME photographers are lucky enough to have a muse. This muse is what inspires their best work.

Every business should have a muse too: their loyal customers.

Call them your audience, fans, clients, avatar, guests, patients... Whatever you like.

But for simplicity here, I'll refer to them as your "audience".

You should understand and love your audience. They give you life.

My first year working with The Weeknd was all about the fans. We even started a website for them... about them. We spent 2-3 hours after every show doing meet and greets and autograph signings.

Serve your audience like that.

Don't worry about your "followers".

Your followers are merely people that have "collected you" over time. When it's time for their end-of-year social media clean up, you might be gone like a fad.

But within all your followers is a devoted audience. They're the people who LOOK for your posts every day.

They're the ones who would notice if you were gone.

Focus on THEM.

Do you want to go viral?

Trick question.

You don't actually want to go viral. That's for attracting the masses. Tons of the wrong people.

The last thing you want to do is attract everybody. Especially by trying to appeal toeverybody. Homogenizing yourself for those who only come to “check you out” doesn't help you in the long run. Those are the passer-bys... the window shoppers.Play for your "true fans" and they'll tell your FUTURE "true fans" about you.

And yes, if you do this well, you'll get haters.

Trust me...

Haters are your second-best spokespeople.

My dad always says, “For every person who hates what you do... there's someone who loves it BECAUSE the other person hates it.”

The noise the haters make to criticize you will be the best PR to attract even more of “your people”.

If you want to grow faster than everyone else you have to ignore all the stuff that everyone else is obsessed about. All of that just feeds your ego and you just do it for outside perception. Obsess about your audience instead. Do more of what's foundational. Add value to your customer's lives and you win. Even if you're not on Snapchat or Fakebook or a part of the Instagram mafia.

But let's dig deeper here.

Do you even know who "your people" are?

So many businesses think it's their "customer demographic".

Guys, we're not in the MySpace era.

Today, in order for you to use all these digital marketing tools more effectively... you're going to have to wrap your head around something more powerful:psychographics.

Ok. Before we get all poetic about it, you should answer basic demographic questions. You should know things about your audience like: gender, where they're from, their race, religion etc...

Don't be afraid to EXCLUDE. You want to EXCLUDE. Who's your audience? Men or women? Yeah, yeah, I know it's both. But who is it REALLY (it doesn't mean others won't like it -- I'm asking you who are you making it for?) Narrow it down. Are you making this for older people or younger people? Urban people or country people.

Next, you figure out the psychographics of your audience. In todays world psychographics are MORE important than demographics.

Demographics is data on things you can see.

Psychographics is about knowing how your audience thinks and feels.

To figure out your audience's psychographics, you need to engage in a little method acting. Imagine "your people" and then you imagine what they want. What websites do they go to online? What food do they eat? Are they spiritual? Do they like video games? What kind of causes would they march for? You should know what they dream of and what would make their day.

And then from now on, when you communicate with them... Do it on their level. Talk to them in the way that you KNOW that they'd be most receptive... every single time.

You need to know your audience better than they know themselves.

You need to be like Bill Clinton back in '92 fighting to win the presidency.

"I feel your painnnnnn..."

Find 10 people to create for. Perfect your craft until they ALL wanna scream and tell everybody they know about you!

Those people will lead you to the next 100... and then the next 1000…

I mean...If you can't attract ten die-hards then how are you planning to rule the world?

When communication is tailor-made for "your people" you pretty much never have to hype anything or use manipulation “tactics“ like the others do.

Hearing from you... becomes (gasp) desirable!

You become your own "word of mouth". They trust you THAT much.

If you don’t believe me read the Bezos letters.

Did you know that Jeff Bezos (the owner of Amazon) wrote anend of year email to all his employees detailing his complete vision for the future... every year since the beginning?

Do you realize that everything he wrote came true?

Guess what the core principle of all those emails were?

That everything you do-- you need to do it for your audience. They are the Polaris Star.

Not in that cheesy McDonalds way that "the customer is always right".

But in the progressive way that even if the customer is wrong... How can we help them out? 'Cause it could have been us on the other side.

And I don’t know about you, but from where I sit Amazon looks to be doing alright.

So even if you didn't have a message, just your sheer obsession and dedication to serving your audience with value could make you successful at what you do. But the only problem with that is that it leaves you vulnerable in your niche to someone who is just as dedicated as you... but HAS a message.

The person, brand, company who has a message and makes it resonate with their psychographic is unstoppable.

All the insanely successful brands and artists out there are doing just that... by design... or by luck.

Know your audience. Ignore the rest.

### 4. Fuck "Followers"... Introducing "Audience Mindset"

First you should understand why people always want more followers.

They want attention.

They want validation.

And they see followers as a direct correlation to fulfilling that addiction.

Post some bullshit...

Then check your phone 140 times a day (That's an actual statistic. And it's sad.)

And that addiction leads to psychosis.

A warped view of reality.

You try to get followers on social media because it's easier than real life. It's the difference between NBA 2K20 and playing on a real court.

What would you have to do in the real world to get those same people to pay attention?

That would be a whole new ballgame, right?

That's why you're chicken shit of approaching strangers. The real stuff... (But we'll deal with that one soon, believe me...)

So instead, you try to attract strangers by being clever online. Where your ego is safer.

I know, I know... Some people have succeeded at making this online "game" a full time job. Especially when it was a new thing back in 2015.

We gave them a name.

Influencers.

But that's a lottery.

The Mystery School is not about creating influencers.

The Mystery School is about creating the people who influence the influencers.

Before you try to "grow" on Instagram... Let's do some housecleaning.

From now on there will be less ego-stroking. And more "doing things with purpose".

If you stopped posting today. Who are the people who would notice? Who are the people who would miss you?

The fans who like every post...

The ones leaving thoughtful comments...

The ones that, if you decide to sell something, they buy...

Who are the ones who would come to your "Instagram funeral"?

Those people are called your audience.

They are the only ones that matter.

And when you finally realize that... You've acquired the keys to your kingdom.

Before you try to attract new people to your audience you need to nurture the ones you already have.

You do that by getting to know them.

If you make a new friend, or you start dating someone, the first thing you do is try to get to know their likes and dislikes etc... And you look for that common ground. Right?

The digital world is no different.

These are PEOPLE on the other end. Stop treating them like numbers.

Treat your Day 1s with care.

When you're too "big" to nurture your audience, you can hire fan clubs to do it for you... But for now... Do the "work".

Make it your duty to understand who your followers are.

That's the right energy.

Instagram shows you the least engaged followers you have and lets you silently remove them. It also shows you your "Least Interacted With".

Use those tools.

Unfollow people that don't align with the new you.

Start fresh to make your IG more succinct and representative of who you are becoming.

Oliver (mystery student) went in...

Your audience is not everybody. It isn't the masses.

It's a community that corals around you for a reason.

What is that reason?

Once you know this... You can proudly take the next step.

Oh, and it's such a powerful move:

Create a series of posts that are soooooo perfectly geared towards your core audience that everyone that doesn't fit in to your new IG's world view will quickly unfollow.

The double reaction you want is:

1. some people saying "fuck this. unfollow." and...

2. others will be like "Wow. I needed to see this today."

That's how you know that you're on the right track.

As mystery student @msthighlicious who does this on a regular basis would say...

"Good Riddance"

What if you concentrated all your energy into being so singular and hardcore about what you stand for that people were forced to either unfollow you or praise you for reading their mind?

Stop being afraid of pissing people off.

You're going to piss people off if you're doing anything decent. Accept this NOW.

It's ok to piss people off. It's good actually. It's engagement. Engagement that will lead to more people like the ones you helped already or that love your art... find you.

Haters are the perfect dog-whistle for attracting more of your true fans.

Piss your "followers" off... Gain an audience.

Remember theSecondary Effectsmodule?

If you go-in 100% on your message, maybe some people will leave... But give it time... your fans will find you.

Now that you're in the right "audience" frame of mind... there's one last step.

Prepare your mind for the upcoming work.

If you can't be consistent, you're not ready to grow an audience.

We can't all be @playboicarti .

Only people that are consistent in the outside world don't need to be consistent on IG. But if IG is your main promotional hustle for getting your work known, then you'll need to start dropping bombs.

Dropping bombs doesn't mean only releasing controversial content.

It's just that what you post just needs to feel like "bombs" to your audience. It's whatever you've promised to deliver. It's the reason they came to you. It could be dope music. An insightful piece of writing. A resource that helps them.

But you need to give it to them on a schedule.

Don't try grow an audience that you can't service with that type of consistency.

That's why I'm mentioning it now. Get ready for it.

In 'The Book Of Influence' I'll be showing you how to make your online world a well-oiled machine. And then you can "scale".

But for now, prepare your mind for the relentless work of consistency.

Imagine you're a t-shirt company with 500 followers and an audience of 100 that buys every time you release something? Uh... You have a business!

An audience that cares about you and that shares what you with others will make you grow faster than any clever or thirsty hashtag could ever do.

“You don't need massive influencers to grow — you can truly do it if you have shareable content that people want to send to their friends.” Koreen (@werenotreallystrangers)

### 5. Your Fans Are Everything. So, Start Acting Like it (Part I): Your Art Doesn't "Matter" (Yet)

I don't care if you're "the next Supreme"...

I don't care if you're about to take "the hairdressing community by storm "...

Or if you're a caffein induced stylist that can "pull from Telfar"...

Or if you're a COVID-inspired fashion photographer...

Or if you're the "Trap Bob Dylan"...

Or if you're the only architect who's mastered the timeless principles of Christopher Alexander...

You are nothing.

Without your fans.

You will not advance.

Without your fans.

Put this up on your wall where you can see it every day:

I know, I know.

You think that what you do is "special".

But it's only gonna be "special" when there's a passionate group of people who says it is.

And I don't mean your family or your friends.

I mean the people who become your NEW "family and friends" BECAUSE OF your art.

I don't just mean the people who buy what you do.

I also mean the people who will be on your team one day to help you promote it.

For example:

I meet so many photographers trying to get known.

They put their pics on Instagram.

It's their "portfolio", they say.

Dear photographers, Did you know that 95 million photos get uploaded every day on Instagram?

Why should we care about yours?

Ok, I'll come back to that in a second.

Another statistic to make you weep:

4000 songs get added to Spotify every day.

I meet singers and producers trying to get known. Some even have labels behind them.

Um, tell me: What about YOUR new single makes it something that I have to hear before I die?

You see, THAT'S the problem.

You can't answer that question in one sentence.

You can't answer that question with conviction.

You can't give me an answer that makes me start typing your name into Spotify while you're still talking.

You have no story.

You have no message.

If you had either of those things, you'd be creating better odds for yourself. You'd have your own lane.

Let me show you how--

No seriously. Let's do the math.

We'll use music as an example.

But this applies to anyone out there with a brand.

So... 4,000 songs released a day, right? Of those 4,000 releases, how many of them are "pop artists"?

Maybe 2000.

How many of them are "pop artists who rap"?

How many are "pop artists who rap exclusively about female empowerment"?

How many are "pop artists who rap exclusively about female empowerment, who have blue hair, and have been releasing consistently for the last 3 years, and never disappeared to go on 'normal people vacations' but have gone "all in" to keep relentless communication their fans documenting all the highs and the lows along the way"?

What I'm trying to tell you is that you need a story.

What I'm trying to tell you is that you need to nurture your audience.

Your "people".

You have to be like that Presets song... SING IT:

You have to know in fine detail who you're doing this for.

Otherwise, your lyrics will suck.

Your pictures will suck.

Your art will suck.

Your brand will suck.

Creative work sucks when it isn't made for anyone in particular.

It sucks when... You're trying to appeal to "everybody".

It makes you vanilla.

Instead, what you want is for your fans to say, "I feel like you made this just for me."

That's what I was talking about in this module:

LE$$XN 02: Every Brand Should Have A Muse

But you only read it. You understood it, but you didn't DO anything about it.

It gave you "motivation",... And then you forgot about it when your friend texted you to go to the new Ramen spot.

But reading is not action. That may have been all you needed for the other modules but you can't get away with that in 'The Book Of Money'.

You need to grab a pen and paper so you can figure this shit out once and for all.

That's what a PR person would do if you had the money to hire one.

YOUR FANS ARE EVERYTHING. START ACTING LIKE IT (PART II)

Don't click that on that link until you have a pen and paper.

And when you do... Don't fucking just "read through it"!

This is not about "motivation" anymore.

It's about action.

The type of action that makes you feel like you've moved the needle in your career today.

This is the stuff no-one calls you out on. Good luck finding anything like what's in this 'action sheet' anywhere else on the internet.

Why? 'Cause I made this for MY people.

Got your pen and paper. Let's go:

### 6. Your Fans Are Everything. So, Start Acting Like it (Part II): How To Find Your Psychographic

The "real questions" you need to be asking are laid out here. Don't rush through this. This is your career.

No artist exists in the minds of their fans without a story attached.

Your fans like you FOR A REASON.

Beyond the art, I mean. A reason that has to do with THEM.

They're connecting with something.

What are they connecting with? Be clear about it. Do you think Taylor Swift can answer this question? Do you think The Weeknd knows the answer? They know in explicit detail.

WRITE YOUR ANSWER DOWN.

What do you WANT them to connect with?

WRITE THAT DOWN.

Have you been communicating about those aspects with them lately?

Or only posting selfies?

And only posting #hashtag filled captions with lame one-liners?

Even if you don't have a message yet...

I know you have a story.

What is it? What about your upbringing, your journey, your process, your beliefs etc... that makes you one-of-a-kind.

WRITE IT DOWN.

See how, when you try to write it down, it's a little challenging because you need to figure out what to focus on?

See how you have to find an angle?

That's what PR people get paid to do.

Without an "angle," people won't connect with you.

That's what makes us human.

You connect with that girl you met on the plane because of her story.

And because you have matching scores on 'The Pattern' app.

You connect that guy at work because of his story.

And you like the way he sees the world.

So why aren't you providing this same connection with your fans?

Now, if you have a message...

Then wow, do you have it made.

Your message IS your story.

Look no further.

When you have a message...People will feel like they connect with you even if they don't like your art. Crazy right? They connect with the reason why you make your art: Your message.

All great artists have a message. But you know that already.That's why you did 'The Drill Down Method' with your mom.So I won't focus on that here.

If you haven't found your message yet, all is not lost.

Figure out your story.

Imagine we're going to share your art with the world. And The New York Times wants to do a story about you or your competition, but they can only choose one. They're going to go with the most compelling story.

What's YOUR story?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Alternate version for people who are brand new:

If you don't have a story yet, then write what you want that story to be this time next year.

Let's start with the basics.

Think to yourself... What type of person is going to resonate with your story?

Can you see what this person looks like in your mind?

Knowing your audience puts your art into better focus. It informs you on how you should communicate with them.

You may have a message (or, at the very least, a story)... But to know how to communicate it, you have to know what language your audience is speaking.

Are they feminists? Trump supporters? Athletes? Mothers? Or did they just join the military?

Who are YOUR fans?

Let's start with the basics: Demographics.

Be binary with this exercise.

For example, is your ultimate fan a boy or a girl?

Don't say both. Pick one. Even though yes, I know, I know... Both COULD be your fans.

But where is it leaning?

Male or female?

WRITE IT DOWN.

How old are they?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Where do they live? A particular country? A particular town?

Hip hop ended up taking over the world. But it began as a form of expression exclusive to the black community in New York City.

WRITE DOWN WHERE THEY'RE FROM.

Don't be surprised if when you start describing your audience, that they seem suspiciously a lot like YOU (or you at some point in your life).The only real difference with you and them is 1. your amazing talent, and 2. you were the one who had to guts to pursue your goals. They see their own potential in all your wins.

Now... Think of your ultimate fan.

The type of person who would be the head of your fan club.

What part of your personal story would resonate with them the most?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What do they like most about your art?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Are they introverts or extroverts?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What causes do they believe in?

WRITE IT DOWN.

How do they dress?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What can't they stop talking about all day? Their relationship. Politics? Tiktok? The environment?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What do they spend most of their free time doing?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What kind of music do they like? Classic hip-hop? None?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What kind of art do they support?

WRITE IT DOWN.

What "influencers" and public figures do they love?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Where do they hang out in the real world?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Where do they hang out online?

WRITE IT DOWN.

Pull all this information together to paint a precise picture of your ultimate fan.

WRITE THE SYNOPSIS DOWN.

Is there someone (or a few people) you know in real life close to this picture you've painted?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN.

If you don't know someone-- Make up a name for your Ultimate Fan.

This is what we call an "avatar".

I call them my "muse".

This is the person that you choose to create art for.

From now on...

When you communicate, you will imagine that you're speaking DIRECTLY to them.

The 3 Rules To Communicate Like Someone Who Has A Career, Not A Hobby:

If what you want to post doesn't follow these 3 rules, use a "personal" account to post that other bullshit. It doesn't fit in here.

Communicate this concise way in EMAILS.

Talk to "your people" this way in your CAPTIONS.

Do the same thing in Instagram Stories.

Do the same in tweets.

Do it in interviews.

Communicate this way even when you meet strangers.

That's right:

Until you're a household name... Paint an unmistakable picture of who you are for everyone you meet.

Make it easy for your fans to identify you. Talk their language, and no one else's.

Guess what? Some people won't like it.

That's the point!

THOSE ARE NOT YOUR FANS.

But for your real fans, everything you do will be a dog whistle calling to their soul.

Ok, you can have the rest of the day off. Today was huge!

Tomorrow, you will re-write this into a concise one page document.

Then you will print it out where you can see it at a glance.

Every time you get stuck writing an email, or a caption, or when people are asking you to describe what your do...

Keep coming back to this document to focus you. Do that until it's memorized. And audience-awareness is second nature.

When you start applying what you've learned about yourself and your fans today...

You will see an immediate change in how people relate to your work.

Congratulations on doing the work that most people don't do (and that's why they stand still).

You have elevated yourcreativity / work ethicscore by 2000%.

You find them online, the way you would in the tactile world...

You go where they hang out.

Now is the time to use the answers to the questions above to do some detective work (it shouldn't be that hard if your fans are a lot like you anyways).

Do they hang out on Instagram? Well, maybe it's time to start using Instagram better then. Be more strategic about your posts now. Are you inviting people that leave complimentary comments to your mailing list? Do you have a mailing list? Are you using it?

Use your social media to tell your story. Don't just post your work. Find your unique way to make people discover the artist behind the work.

How many gatekeepers are you talking to every week?

Gatekeepers are the people who have access to thousands of people at a time. Blog writers. Photographers. Videographers. These are all people who can put you on to their scene in seconds if they like what you do.

Have you made a list of 10 gatekeepers that you can reach out to this week to share your story and your work with?

Who are the bloggers that would fall in love with what you do?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN.

Who are the "influencers" who would be down with your shit?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN.

Who are your peers who are steps ahead of you that would love to help you rise?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN.

Who are the business people like managers, agents, publishers, owners that you should be talking to?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN. (OR WRITE DOWN THE NAMES OF PEOPLE WHO CAN CONNECT YOU TO THEM)

Who has a podcast that would love to chat with someone that has your type of story?

WRITE THEIR NAMES DOWN.

### 6. Your Fans Are Everything. So, Start Acting Like it (Part II): How To Find Your Psychographic

## #1. Let's Unearth Your Story

## 2. Who are "your people"? Part I: Demographics.

## 3. Who are "your people"? Part II: Psychographics.

## 4. Your Avatar

## 5. Communicate Your Story Everywhere -- Always Directed To Your Fans. Forget The Masses From Now On.

### 1. Relate everything to your story / message.

### 2. Talk about only things that you have in common with your fans. (You should feel like you know them intimately now.)

### 3. Never communicate in generalities like you're talking to "the masses". The masses don't matter anymore.

## 6. Help! How do I find my fans?

## This master list is gold. Now it's time to make a plan of action to reach X amount of the names on your list every single week for the next 3 months. And follow through with your emails and DMs. Be persistent, but friendly. This is your career. You're world building. Even someone like Drake is doing the same thing. He's just doing it at a higher level. Fuck making more music, or creating another design, or making another video until you've elevated the art you've just made to it's next level. Creating a new piece of art is the bare minimum starting point of having a career. The next step is letting people know you're here... It's time to SHARE the work with as many people as possible. Beyond a few IG story posts on release week. I know your self doubts, and questioning your self worth will be kicking in right about now. Quieten that voice by reaching out to the people on your master list every day. Watch what happens. Your art is worth that effort, no? -- (Your answer will be what you decide to do once you're done reading this.)

### 🔑 7. Email Is The Mothership

LISTEN TO THIS:

They say email is dead?

Here's the truth:

91% of people check their email daily.

66% of people will buy something online because of an email they received. (Email makes more sales than every other source of marketing available.)

While Facebook has 3 billion users... Instagram has 2 billion users... And Tiktok has 1.5 users...

Email has 5 billion users!

Let THAT sink in.

And what makes the social media numbers worse is that Facebook and Instagram only lets 5% of your followers see what you post. Unless, of course you pay them (by "boosting" posts etc.).

But with email... YOU control it.

YOU own it.

Getting email only sucks when it's email you don't want.

And these days, that's most of it.

So your job as an artist or brand is to write emails that "your people" want.

"But Bronques... People don't evenopenmy emails..."

That's because your emails aren't fun. They’re not inspiring.

You have to write epic emails. You need to inspire your audience. Inspire them with your creativity. Inspire them with your knowledge. Inspire them with your cute products. But never be "middle of the road" with anything you do. This is your life's work! Share your vision. Amplify the details. Listen, you can be as shy as you want to be in real life... but email is no place to hold back! They already love you. That's why they signed up. You can't afford to give them less than 100%.

Try this... Check your inbox right now.

I bet 90% of it is just junk that you delete, delete, delete... BUT... There's also a very small percentage of emails that you're happy to get. Some that put a smile on your face or maybe inspire you. You may even have a special folder for those so you can read them again later.

What YOU need to start doing is: stop writing emails that are designed for people's “delete pile”... and creating those that have a place in their “special folder”.

People open emails because of the way you made them feel the last time they opened one from you.

Everything you see me do on instagram, facebook, twitter or snapchat started with an email. No joke.

"But Bronques... no one READS anymore."

Bro, people read. But only if you write about something they care about.

This is not a theory. I tested it.

Back in September 2018 I did a little experiment. I sent out an email to my list every single day. I called it "30 emails in 30 days". I went against everything that people usually say... "People will get mad." "They'll unsubscribe." "You'll burn people out.".

Guess what?

They were right. All of those things DID happen.

I got 400 unsubscribes in 30 days

But I also got 1,100 NEW subscribers in that same time frame when I shared one of those emails on social with an opt-in link (link to join my list).

And you know what also happened?

My open rates went up!

And people started writing me back to comment and share their own stories.

I developed relationships with the people on my list (relationships that continue to this day).

My "email marketing" became a great source for getting feedback and testing ideas.

And throughout that whole period I was posting LESS on Instagram... but guess what? My Instagram engagement, comments and DMs INCREASED. Why? By the time my followers were seeing photos on my social media the truest fans already knew the backstory through email. They all had this shared BTS knowledge. All my social media platforms became more meaningful because of this new two-way communication that I had now established within my email army.

So now I love it when people 'unsubscribe'.

I know that those people are not "my people".

My open rate is 46% now.

Before I started my "emailing every day" experiment, my open rate was 19%.

It went UP after I started bombarding people's inbox every day. Counter-intuitive, right?

The truth is... People never get tired of hearing from you if you're always addressing their needs. Their "needs" is your message. And those "people" are your psychographic. That's what they signed up for.

"But Bronques," you stubbornly wanna protest, "I only have 20 people on my email list!"

I don't care if you have 8 people on your email list and only 3 opens.

Here's the strategy.

Make email your "pillar content".

Those emails you force yourself to write today will become an endless sources of writing for you to draw from later. The sheer volume of words that you can now pull from when you need to write captions, describe your merch, create compelling ads or find the topic for a new viral video... will leave you stress-free when you're in a pinch.

But the best part is...

That "refurbished writing" can also make you lots of money!

This is not a theory. I tested that too.

I turned my most popular emails into ads, and they all had a relevance score of 10. Every single one. Now if you're not a Facebook ads person let me explain: a high “relevance score” means that Facebook notices that the community likes what you're showing them. Your ads end upcosting you lessAND converting more because the algorithm knows exactly who to show them to.

But the most undeniable business reason to nurture and grow your email list is this:Facebook ads re-targetting.(Sorry, I'm gonna get nerdy here...) When you create a "custom audience" with your email list... you can lower the CPA down to a 1/4 of the price. And if you had segmented and purged your list for the last 3 years you could have gotten it even lower! You get to laugh all the way to the bank while all your competition whines about the rising costs of ads.

I see so many great artists leaving "email marketing" money on the table.

They have a message and a spellbound audience, but they don't ever talk to them.

They get email opt-ins daily but they have no automated "welcome sequences"!

I mean... even a badly written automated welcome email is more polite than NO welcome email.

It reminds me of the first scene of the movie 'The Godfather'. The part where Marlon Brando says: "You come to see me and ask me to kill a man but you never once called to say hello?"

That's how most people behave with email. They ignore their fans until they have a new video to promote, or a new song, or some merch to sell you.

Dig your well before you're thirsty.

Like... Maybe you should start connecting with your fans BEFORE you start asking them for money and favors?

The internet has taught us to be rude. You don't have to follow that trend. (#thequietrevolution btw)

When you start to use your values and principles to navigate social media instead of copying the bad behavior that you see everywhere, your whole experience online will change for the better.

I love movies. I love analogies. So, here's one last one.

One of my favorite scenes in Good Will Hunting is when Matt Damon is telling his therapist (Robin Williams) about his awesome date with a girl. When the therapist asks "Are you gonna call her?" He says "No, I don't want to ruin it. She's so perfect right now." The therapist cuts him up with: "Maybe you don't wanna call her because... YOU'RE so perfect right now..."

That's how artists treat their fans. Afraid of offending. Afraid of unsubscribes. So they go on ignoring all their people until they want something. They're so afraid to offend... that they act indifferently.

While everyone else is stressing out over social media, a few of us are sharing exclusive photos and crazy stories with our fans in a way that’s soooo old school it’s become shockingly... new!

All of the power today is in words.

So now that you and I are on the same page...

I'm gonna show you how to set it up for yourself:

They're all the same. It doesn't matter which one you pick.

Mailchimp is popular and is better for "designed" emails. (free until 2k followers)

Kitis artist friendly and better for mostly text emails (like the one's I send). (free until 500 followers)

If you're thinking of turning your words into a business (writers only) then maybe you should look at Substack too.

ActiveCampaign is the one I use now because I'm managing so many artist students, but I've used the other 2 before my business grew.

I'd encourage you to useKit.combecause it keeps you focused on sending a super-basic email that looks like emails you'd send on Gmail to your friends. That's all you need. Leave fancy emails to evil "marketers" who don't even get their emails opened-up anyways.

A "welcome email" is an email that goes out to people AS SOON AS THEY SIGN UP TO YOUR LIST.

This is important.

Don't collect emails. And falsely convince yourself that you will write them soon.

No, rig your system so that as soon as you add someone's name, or they subscribe on your landing page, theyimmediatelyget an email from you telling them what to expect etc... Make it fun.

But, seriously though.

Don't overthink this step please.

Just write this welcome email like you're writing to a friend. 'Cause, um... You are!'

Remember this sentence when you're not sure what to write:

"Tell the truth."

Whenever we struggle with words it's because we're trying to "present a fake self to people". This isn't Instagram. You don't have to do that anymore. This is the platform where it pays to be real.

This is literally all you need to get in the game:

A "landing page" is a one page "website" that tells people what you're about (keep it short - Mailchimp and ConvertKit both have simple easy to design landing pages you can edit).

The difference between a website and a landing page is focused attention.

Websites are outdated online brochures with distracting links to your socials, and your "about page" (gross)...

But with a landing page you help your audience focus on ONE thing. Just like a storyteller. You guide them to the next part of the journey:

Invite the visitor to join your email list. Tell them exactly what to expect from your emails.

Later, you can grow this into a full-fledged old school website if you want. But for now, make gathering emails the centerpiece of your online presence.

(Btw, notice that I put this step AFTER the "write your welcome email" step? That's 'cause you don't wanna have a landing page where people can sign up before they can get an automatic email reply. So many people get this wrong. I REPEAT. It's not about blindly collecting emails! It's about communicating. If you get someone's email they have to hear from you right away or they'll forget they even signed up...)

Now's the time to put your IG to good use.

Use the LINK IN BIO to send people to your "one page website" so they can join your list. Stop using LINKTREE to give people a million choices. Give them only one option: to get on your email list.

Once they're on your list, you can share new art with them, sell merch, tell them stories. Whatever you want. Instead of the way you have it right now where they only go check out your stuff ONCE.

Now, the link for your email list that your email provider gives you may be too ugly, or too long. If you have $$ you can invest in your own custom URL. But the truth is there's an even better option:

Use a service likebitly.comto create a cute new custom URL that people will wanna click.

The advantage is that now you'll be able to QUICKLY see how many people click on your "link in bio" every day. So fucking useful especially after you promote it on IG story so you can see how well your efforts are doing. There are longer ways to do this using "IG insights" and google analytics, but trust me you don't wanna go there.

And if you notice... I have a custom URL and I still use bitly.

Once you've set all that up, give yourself a pat on the back because:

Just like that... Overnight... Your IG full of selfies is more useful than it was yesterday.

You're starting to take your career more seriously.

I applaud you.

Treat yourself to desert. Take a shot of tequila for me (I can't drink right now -- I'm in full God Momentum).

...and then stick to it.

It doesn't matter if you're only writing to 8 people.

Write about things you both care about.

Get them used to hearing from you.

And use some (or all) of the words you write-- as captions on Instagram. That way you're getting even more use out of all this creativity.

"Pillar content" remember?

Wait a few days after they've received the "welcome email", and then make contact with them by sending a personal non-automated email.

It doesn't have to be long. You're just touching base and giving that "human touch". I love technology just as much as everyone else, but I think that the marriage of digital AND non-digital is the future for creative brands and artists.

You won't be able to do this when you're bigger, but do it when you're small. That's how you turn "nothing" into "something"

Besides, there's a "business" benefit to it also:

Sometimes subscription based emails get filtered into junk folders by faulty algorithms. This gives you a chance to show how much you value their interest in what you're doing AND to remind them to add your address to their address book so that you never end up in junk. (This is called 'whitelisting'.)

When you meet people at parties...

Or on the street...

Or at dinner...

Get their email (and permission).

Add them to your growing list of people that hear from you regularly.

I remember doing this when I started taking pictures.

And you know what's crazy?

I got a job offer or an invitation to somethingalmost every timemy "newsletter" went out.

These were email's I had gathered from everyone I would meet (and you know I meet tons of people).

So as soon as someone in the industry got a new email from me, it's like they suddenly remembered me-- and how I might be perfect for the thing that they're working on.

You've heard the expression "Out of sight, out of mind."

Well, email keeps you always in plain sight, and within mind.

### 9. STOP "PREACHING" ON YOUR SOCIAL MEDIA. DO THIS INSTEAD.

A common mistake I see people make with their captions and emails is "preaching".

It's hard not to preach.

It's hard not to copy that "inspirational content" formula that seems to be working for so many.

Hell, even MY Instagram is all quotes, right? (We'll get to that in a minute...)

But the best content will never be when you flat out tell people what to do. There's a better way I want to share with you today.

Imagine you see this quote: "Until women have freedom, no one has freedom."

Good one right?

If I told you that my friend Jane came up with the quote, you'd be like "Who's Jane?" Whatevz. But nice quote.

But if I told you Rihanna said it... You'd feel more militant about it. Why? Because you know her story. It has context.

But no, she didn't come up with it.

Nelson Mandela did.

See how now it gives it an even deeper context? A MAN came up with this feminist quote... And not just any man. A man who was jailed in his country and then became the leader of his country. A man who knows about losing freedom. That quote has depth now.

What I'm saying is... Don't be the Jane of this story.

How about me?

Well, I didn't start my career with quotes. I started my career by creating work with a message that people cared about. The quotes came way later. When people wanted to understand the philosophy behind what I do.

But so many artists are putting up inspirational quotes before they've done anything that has made an impact on others yet.

And I understand why. They want to write something inspirational. They want to share the strength they're feeling that moment, or that day.

But, why should we listen to YOU when you tell us something like "consistency is key"?

I mean... Unless we just watched you be consistent at something for 8 months, you're just sharing the same truisms as everyone else. But you haven't LIVED it. It's fake wisdom.

Unless your actual art is creating inspirational writing, then inspirational quotes will sound hollow. Especially to anyone who has actually accomplished something.

The world only respects preaching from people who have lived.

If you have nothing to show for yourself...

What can you do instead?

Tell YOUR story.

Your quotes are not valuable yet. But your story is.

Until you give people the context of your life, no one will hear anything you say.

We have to get to know YOUR STORY before you can tell us what to do or what to think.

Set a foundation of why YOU should be listened to.

For example:

Instead of telling us "You should go out in nature every day at least once."

Say something like "I've been going out in nature every morning. I've made it a mini-ritual. And lately I've noticed a change in my skin. I don't get pimples anymore! And I feel less anxious at work etc..."

And over time you'll have more of your fans addicted to your story AND TRYING TO FIND ANSWERS FOR THEMSELVES WITHIN YOUR JOURNEY.

Show us where you got the inspiration for the inspirational quote that you knee-jerk want to preach. If it doesn't come from experience, don't use it.

Talk about YOUR experiences. Tell us stories of people you know.

Become the student of your message before you become the teacher.

Your audience will increasingly hit you up in DMs or write you emails asking for advice, or to share kind words.

Once you've created that kind of following that's intimate with your story, then you can safely move to...

You can be more blatant now. Your followers know you.

Now you've earned the right to "tell them how it is". Your audience has given you that right.

If you can preach while STILL sharing your mini-epiphanies, that's even better.

For example: Notice that I always preach "Talk to strangers". But notice that I also go out there and do it every single day. I have been the living embodiment of that philosophy for my whole career. And at a certain point people started asking me for tips on how to do it. That's when I made the transition (after years of doing it) to Step #2.

But even at that, my "preaching" is mostly IF/THEN statements:

IF you want this result, THEN you should do this.

IF you want to nurture a strong following, THEN start an email list.

IF you want to get your art noticed faster, THEN make sure it has a message.

IF you want to see fast artistic progress, THEN iterate your art every single day.

IF you want better results on social media, THEN stop focusing on numbers and focus on connecting with people.

IF/THEN statements all the way. And they're always based on what I see works for myself and all the clients and artists I work with. It's never something that I read in a book.

Even this module is a long-ass IF/THEN statement:

IF you wanna get more out of your "inspirational content", THEN lead it with your story first.

### 10. HOW TO CREATE MEDIA THAT'S A TROJAN HORSE FOR YOUR ARTISTIC VISION

People who use Instagram, TikTok, and YouTube aren't making art.

They're creating content.

But how about ARTISTS who use these same platforms to promote their art?

Aren't THEY creating content also?

It depends.

According to Merriam-Webster dictionary:

Content = material, such as writing, video, or music that appears on a website or other electronic platform

Media = forms of expression used to communicate ideas or feelings to a group of peopleNotice the subtle difference between these two words?

The definition of 'content' emphasizes "material that appears on a website". It lives and dies online.

Whereas the definition of 'media' emphasizes "communication and expression". It's not limited to appearing online.

The person "creating content" FOR Tiktok doesn't have the same intention as an artist "creating media" ON Tiktok.

Changing the words you use to describe what you do, changes the nature of what you create in the process.

People' creating content' are making sludge for the platforms. The platforms keep making money in exchange for providing a place for you to satisfy their "validation and attention" addiction.

Artists' creating media' are using their chosen forms of expression to communicate to a group of people. They're releasing Trojan horses of ideas into the masses.

Content creators' interactions are always transactional.

But artists interactions should always be about connection.

How do you make sure this comes through?

Start by refusing to call what you make "content".

From now on call what you share on social media (video, photographs, and audio)… MEDIA.

MEDIA = trojan horses for your artistic message.

MEDIA is not the art itself. It's a representation of the art that you share online to connect with your people.

MEDIA = a picture you took of your painting. Or a video of you making music. Or a JPG of your poem written out.

MEDIA is how you bridge the gap between what you do (your art) and the audience you cherish.

When MEDIA is well done, this bridge is just as thoughtful and creative as the art itself. It may even become art in it's own right.

When poorly done, it's… content.

How do you make sure you're creating media? (assuming the art itself already has a vision behind it, of course)

Never post to post.

Consider what kind of media (something that contains your message) would be worth people's attention.

Then take the necessary time to make it.

Often it's coming up with the initial idea that takes hours, but the execution only takes 5 minutes. That's ok.

As long as you work on making it undeniable.

Every post you share should be a microdose of your artistic vision. (See World Building modules)

Even if you're doing a "photo dump". Even if you're posting a "thirst trap". Be subversive. Make it a Trojan horse for something way deeper…

Sharing content without context shows your audience that you take their attention for granted.

You're not Kylie Jenner.

Celebrities are so famous that everything they do automatically has context. Their audience knows so much about them that anything they put online has an embedded narrative.

You're not there yet.

You're a new artist hoping to find your fans. You need to take steps so your future ride or dies "see" you.

Don't be lazy. Don't post something they can easily scroll past. Post thiings to make a connection.

No one wants to see random iPhone b-roll video of your "art thing". That's content. If you want to make it MEDIA, tell us a story. Give us context.

Make it easy for people to resonate with what you're communicating.

Artists send me links all the time without explanation… Like I'm supposed to click on it, get blown away, and praise them for being a genius.

This shows a lack of awareness.

You art doesn't "automatically" matter to anyone. Not even your family. Not even your friends.

You have to make it matter by showing you much you care about it FIRST.

You do that by giving us context.

No one can guess that the person in the picture is a stranger you just met. You have to tell us.

No one can guess how you felt while you were there. You have to tell us.

No one can guess that "this moment was when everything changed". You have to tell us.

Give us the back story to transport us into the world you're building.

Do it with the caption, within the video, or however your creativity tells you to do it. But always...

Tell us why it matters.

Make it impossible for us not to see your genius.

Make it impossible for us not to want to share it with others.

Put the art in a frame.

Stop with your un-edited word diarrhea.

Run-on sentences isn't more "raw and in the moment". It's lazy rationalization for being sloppy.

Be respectful of your audience's attention.

Treat the first thing you write as the first draft it is. Edit it to make sure it communicates something powerful. Let your words sit for a few hours. Come back to it later so you can make sure it reads well.

Save the stream of consciousness for your poetry. For captions and explanations— keep it direct and truthful.

How to best communicate:

Being online is taking time away from you making art.

Being online is interfering with your ability to enter flow.

So if you HAVE to be online, it had better be for a good reason.

GOOD REASON = Helping you elevate your artistic career.

GOOD REASON = Interacting with your audience.

Like asking them who you should collaborate with next.

Like polling them to find out where their head is at.

Like sending them to sign up to your newsletter.

People are scrolling past 500 videos and photos a day. Much of it is baseless, toxic, content.

So when you create media for these platforms, make sure you create work that reflects that you understand this.

Artists are competing against the lowest common denominator "content creators" who already know all this stuff.

So you're gonna have to work twice as hard to create compelling media for the ages.

Did you notice something that ALL the above examples have?

All these artists have created their own visual language with their media.

You instantly recognize their posts among all the copycat stuff online. They have a very particular way of expressing themselves online that sets them apart.

So while you may be tempted to use those same Tiktok fonts, and caption styles as everyone else-- It will date everything you do.

Question every choice you make artistically even though this isn't even the art-- It's just to promote the art. But put the same care into it and your promotion itself will become artful.

Does this sound like too much work?

Well, that "work" is the difference between hearing crickets when you post-- or curating a successful career for yourself.

### 11. You Have A Social Disease (The Instagram Rules)

"I have a social disease."

That's the first line of Andy Warhol's 1979 photo book: 'Exposures'.

And in classic Warhol cultural forecasting... He was right again. We all have a social disease.

But social media is not the enemy. The way we use social media... is.

I predict that by 2021 the way we use social media will transform completely.

Remember...

There was a time that people used to smoke in bars, restaurants and even airplanes. And look at how now that's completely frowned upon and the world has amicably adjusted to it.

That's what's gonna happen to social media also.

People are already sick of it.

They just don't know HOW to stop scrolling. 'Cause that's where their friends are, etc...

But the goal is not to stop scrolling. The goal is not to 'disappear off the grid'.

You need to change YOURSELF.

Don't use social media to show your best 'side'. Use it to show your best 'message'. Stop posting at the "mass-user determined optimal times". Post at the frequency that empowers you. Use the algorithm in your favor by being, gasp... social. Post a photo and then spend the next three days commenting on it. Be the person at the party that brings "life" to it. Make no mistake, social media is a party. And marketing agencies are the pushers trying to sell us their trends and hacks for a new high... Don't buy into it. It's open bar. Get a little tipsy and dance the night away. But never be the last to leave.

You're not here to serve an algorithm. You're here to serve your audience. When you give your fans quality revolutionary goods, the algorithm is designed to reward you. Facebook and Instagram are trying to give their audience the best online experience. Why aren't you?

Produce things that are rare and valuable... and everyone wins.

Don’t post just to post.

Don’t post because someone else posted.

Don’t post because you have too many photos on your drive.

Don’t post because you're bored.

Don’t post to make someone jealous.

Don't post in knee-jerk reaction to haters.

Post to glorify your journey.

Stop trying to beat the algorithm. Instead, try to emulate the algorithm. Even better... Create your own algorithm. It’s called "posting what my true fans need to hear", not just what will make the masses double-tap.

When you focus on the algorithm you end up programming yourself to behave like everyone else.

When most people say 'social media' they're talking about Instagram. Some may check Facebook every day, but most people can't function without Instagram.

But people forget that Instagram is a service. Your pictures, videos and captions all reside on rented land. You're at the mercy of Instagram's whims, their algorithms, their politics and their punishments too. All you can do while you play by their rules is to use it to keep furthering your own values and principles. If you have none, then you'll just end up doing what everyone else is doing: wasting time.

And stop saying Instagram is free. Instagram is NOT free. Its cost to your mental health... is staggering.

I predict that the "perfect lives" we see on social will one day be a thing of the past. Imperfection is about to be on trend. Not the fake-ass "I don't look cute (but I actually do)" photos we're seeing, but an avalanche of authenticity that will be like Nirvana descending on the boy bands. You're gonna start seeing more and more of those IG model "breakdowns" and "posting what is real" rebellions.

The modern marketer will tell you that it's not about likes anymore. It's about engagement.

The new wave marketer will tell you that it's not about engagement, it's about retention. It's about surrounding yourself with people that want EVERY LAST DROP!

Make "content" forthosepeople.

If you're not tending to that kind of following it's because you don't have one. And if you don't have one it's because you have nothing to say.You have no message.

Find what makes you unique and double-down on it. Even if it isn't popular. That's called your NICHE.

Figure out your message and add it to your visual content. Just like having meaningful captions gives people value on an individual post... Having a message gives people more value on an individual profile.

I did a test.

I uploaded an 11 panel, text-only Instagram Story instead of the crazy videos that I usually do... It got more engagement yes... but most of all it had an 80% retention rate. The people that got to the end? Those are my people.

And guess where I found the words for that IG Story?

From an email that I had written... See how new wave marketing works?

I told one of my students to get rid of her IG. None of her people were on it. And besides, she hated it. But she kept it for appearances. But after she got rid of it she could proudly say "I'm not on IG either" and attract more of her like-minded following. IRL.

But of course most of us can't get rid of our IG. Not because we're addicted to it of course... (because we're not right? haha...) No, we can't get rid of it becauseOUR AUDIENCE IS ADDICTED TO IT. And if that's where they congregate to manifest their addiction, you'll have to meet them there to satisfy their needs. But give them something of value for when they land on your stuff.Make art not content.

So tell me again... Why are you updating every day?

Oh, your marketing agency told you that you need to update at least once a day so that “more people can see and engage with your content”. And that "you have to keep updating so that you're top-of-mind with your customers?"

That's straight out of the IG playbook that they've bought into.

Most businesses should only be using Instagram as a store front and only be updating twice a week... just to make sure that anyone that lands there is getting the right message.

If you want to stay top-of-mind, then use DMs. Get to know your audience for REAL.

If you have a 1000 followers then only 100 of them will see your post anyways...

Do you really think you moved the needle today by posting a picture and replying in the "comments" with a few heart emojis?

If your relationship with your fans begins and ends on Instagram then you don't have an "Instagram plan"... You have an I.L.O. -- "Instagram Lost Opportunity".

These marketing companies give you the illusion that they're working... by adding content every day. But the sad truth is that you're still not growing and you're still not connecting.

Oh and another thing.

Look at your marketing agency’s Instagram. See how much it sucks? That's who you've entrusted your “precious real-estate” to.

### 12. THREE COMMUNICATION STYLES TO CONNECT WITH YOUR COMMUNITY

If you're already famous... Or if you’ve found your place in the world and you’re satisfied with it... You don't need to read this.

This module is for creatives who are trying to tear a new asshole into the internet and no longer want to be ignored.

But I will tell you an interesting thing I noticed...

The famous people that still use "world domination communication styles" even when they achieve success (like Drake, or The Kardashians) become unstoppable forces of nature and larger than life cultural icons. Just sayin'.

Reality check.

You know when people say: It's "hard work"?

This is what they're talking about.

But don't let that discourage you. It's also fun.

These are the three ways to post content, write emails, answer comments and keep in touch with your people in our emerging digital world.

No one can beat the person or brand that uses this approach.

It's absolutely impossible.

Jake Paul said it best: "It’s every day bro."

Those who can maintain that intensity are the 1% of content creators.

Casey Neistat created beautifully filmed, narrative "movies" EVERY SINGLE DAY for 3 years. And ended up influencing a whole generation of YouTubers.

Jake Paul grew to 10 Million followers in six months by releasing fully produced dramatic 10-20 minute videos EVERY SINGLE DAY. He's at 20 Million followers now.

It's how I built lastnightsparty too. I photographed and shared pictures of parties before 8AM EVERY SINGLE DAY for 2 years straight. No one could touch me.

This communication style is dazzling to your fans and dizzying to your competition. While they're still recovering from "your last one" you give them "your next one".

The content you create has to be as great as what other people take a whole week or a month to do... Except you do it in a day.

You leave everything on the table and nothing in the vaults.

It's not for everybody, that's for sure.

It’s often the path of the foolish youth because you need energy to pull it off.

But not always: Look at Seth Godin who has a DAILY BLOG and sends a DAILY EMAIL to his fans...

The reason why this approach is so powerful... Is that your followers become closer to you than they are to their friends and even their family.

Look at @beeple_crap who releases a killer 3D design modes every day. His bio says it all... "13 years of everydays."

Or Rupi Kaur when she start out and was sharing a poem a day.

You have to be PHYSICALLY and MENTALLY built for this if you want to keep it up. If you don't think you can keep this communication style going for the next two years, then don't even bother starting.

You'll lose your gains just as fast as you built them.

And then you'll fall into depression.

Try the second, more tempered approach that's super powerful too...

This is the marathon approach.

This will put you in the same league as the 10% of successful creators out there.

You show up at the appointed time / times every week without fail, and you fucking deliver.

And in between... You "disappear" in order to be productive.

This is what gurus mean when they say “be consistent”.

That’s how Kris Jenner built an empire. Slowly and consistently putting her family in our faces until they rose to the forefront of culture.

Never, ever, stopping or slowing down.

Your rhythm should be based on your artist DNA. Let your art dictate the release schedule.

It doesn’t have to be "once a week" or anyone else's pattern.

It just has to be a pattern that YOUR fans will recognize. And then you stick to it.

It's like when The Weeknd disappears and erases all his social media... His fans know he’s building a bomb, and that’s he's entering a new “chapter”. He set up that communication pattern early in his career with Trilogy and he's been consistent ever since.

The internet's most successful serial novel, "Worm", was first published with two to three chapters released every week. John McCrae's "strict publication schedule" was: a new chapter every Tuesday and Saturday, and bonus chapters on Thursdays for donations.

How long did he keep it up?

For 2 years.

He was writing at a rate (11 thousand words a day) of what would be a book a month!

Some things take longer to make. And they require you to disappear. But... IF you keep your promise to your fans (whatever it is), it's totally okay. You're setting up proper expectations.

The previous "daily communication approach" turns fans into friends.

But this "by-appointment communication approach" makes your relationship with your fans into a bonafide romance. There is no romance without distance.

You give them space to dream about you.

I'd suggest this communication style to Producers and Creative Directors too. This is the best way to keep in touch with brands and clients while you're being quietly relentless behind the scenes.

I put this communication style third (for explanations sake)... But the Hybrid communication style is actuallythe second most powerful way to communicate on the internet.

You'll be part of the 5% of artist-creators out there.

This is how it works:

If you're a writer... Since you can't put out a book a day... You release a daily quote or excerpt from whatever 5,000 words you produce every day.

For artists who have art that develops in stages over time like painters, musicians, film-makers... You release "behind the scenes" content every day to keep people excited.

It's like Skrillex or Kenny Beats with their live streams on Twitch.

Actors? Share skits with us every day in between the "real" things you're working on. Keep your craft sharpened by testing simple ideas on your audience daily.

Or how about you creatives out there who have clients? Like designers, yoga instructors, or hairstylists? You guys should be micro-communicating every day too! Every day there’s a cute little story you can share about your community. It doesn't have to be anything major. It's BETTER if it's not something major. Keep it relatable.

So you might be thinking... Isn't the hybrid approach the most powerful approach? Because it's the best of both worlds?

Nope. The Hybrid approach can’t even come close to the Every Day approach.

Here's the difference:

With the "every day approach "you’re creating COMPLETE WORKS OF ART EVERY DAY. You're not just showing the "behind the scenes" of a music video every day-- No, you're releasing a fully edited, kick ass video EVERY SINGLE DAY. Or as a musician, you're releasing a fully produced song EVERY SINGLE DAY.

Yep, just like Casey Neistat and Jake built their careers.

That's why the Hybrid Approach might be better for you. You stay in touch, without the burden of a finished product every day. You're still part of the 5% of the internet that is killin it.

So, if you're not using one of the communication styles that build careers, then what's left?

AKA What everyone else does.

This will work wonders for your sense of acceptance, and lower stress levels. You get to communicate with people "whenever".

But if you're trying to build a following that will carry your art into the stratosphere? Good luck with that approach.

Out of sight. Out of mind.

2 steps forward two steps back.

No matter how cool what you do is, you won't be giving people any reason to feel connected to you. And the digital world is about feeling connected.

I have never seen anyone accomplish anything of lasting value with the random approach.

Don't get me wrong. I HAVE seen many artists who have a carefully crafted "image" of communicating randomly... While their PR team, and / or manager is communicating with hardcore consistency behind the scenes.

If you communicate like “everybody else”... You can expect "everybody else" results.

Which communication style should you choose? It depends on your art form and your level of energy.

Find your artist DNA.

Create relationships. Not bootie calls.

Make your fans feel like your family. Make them feel invested in what you do.

Develop a sense of urgency.

And once you find your mission and your message that urgency will turn into... A state of EMERGENCY. Just like it did for Rupi Kaur, Drake, Casey Neistat, Gary V and Kylie. You'll be affecting lives.

Every time you “don’t feel like” communicating... Someone else does. And they're carving out the space that could have been yours.

Make it "not about you" anymore.

It’s about your mission. And your message. And your fans. And changing the world.

"Yeah Bronques, but I get all in my head..."

Overthinking is what happens when you focus on yourself and not your mission.

Overthinking is what happens when you focus on the same old stories instead of creating new ones by engaging in immediate action.

I love this Mooji quote:

Have all your feelings if you like... Feel the highs and lows... Catch feelings... Be in your feelings... but when it's time to work... Work anyways. Work slower if you have to. But keep working.

Don't let outside influences stop your flow.

If you have enough energy to binge on Netflix, then you have enough energy to create art.

If you have enough energy to scroll Instagram... Then you have enough energy to start creating the next work of genius that can change all of our lives.

When will you begin?

Every day you “don’t feel like it” someone else does. And they're carving out a space that should have been yours.

Decide on a communication style today.

And then stick with it.

Not for a few weeks. Or a few months.

But for the next few years.

Thank me later.

### 13. THE ULTIMATE IG

A pretty girl I know, with 35k followers and a phone full of selfies... Asked ME (a guy who "posts quotes" and has 30k fewer followers than her)... This question -- before we all went into quarantine:

"How do I make my Instagram kick ass more?"

As you probably know, if you live in LA... Deep down... what she's really trying to figure out (and ain't gonna get from me) is:

"How do I get Instagram famous?"

I get it. It's hard not to focus on vanity metrics. After all, that's how we judge everyone else, right?

But that's the very mindset that's murdering us.

If you're fortunate to work in a creative field, you do know there's a different way of looking at social media, right?

One that's tailor-made for you?

One that doesn't have negative side-effects like IG has for everyone else?

And, dare I say... A way of growing your brand or community that's playful and fun.

It's based on the timeless concept of "preeminence". (Big word I know, but gorgeous concept...)

Here's the first thing you do (the easy part):

You stop looking at Instagram like it's the place you go to "kill time"...

And you start looking at it in a controversial new way.

Like it's a tool.

That's what it must become if you're on a journey to creative freedom...

Now, hang with me here. I ain't going down the road of: "post more often", "post at specific times", "create value", or "make great content". Don't worry.

I'm hoping for a more scenic journey than that.

If you'll allow me to feed your old ideas to the tigers... I'd like to suggest a less humiliating way of approaching IG.

A way that will make you smile instead when you open the app on your phone.

But let's review something you keep forgetting:

There are "influencers" with 100k+ followers whose social media presence has zero impact on the world.

And there are superstars with 5k followers whose social media presence has a profound effect on their community.

Most creatives I know would "settle" for the second option if they had to pick one.

Now ask yourself... If you stopped posting on Instagram tomorrow... How many people would come to your Instagram funeral?

Well, THAT'S how many followers you really have.

If you never thought about it that way... Let that new reality sink in for a minute.

But then, go even further with the thought.

Ask yourself a few more follow up questions:

What if you decided to build an Instagram strategy based ONLY on those people?

How would your content change?

Would you lose followers?

Or would this new strategy attract even more people like the ones who already love you?

But the most important question of them all... How would your mental health improve?

If you're tired of chasing the dragon, I'd like to pose a challenge.

Create what I call "The Ultimate IG".

Try to design this new kind of Instagram for yourself.

It's based onThe Strategy Of Preeminence(yes, this is an age-old concept).

It's what I've been using with everyone I've worked with over the past 5 years.

What follows is a guide to building the Ultimate IG. This is always my starting point when I'm wroking with new brands or artists.

After you go through the Ultimate IG process, you will know what to do with your IG and why you're doing it.

Too many creatives are using Instagram aimlessly.

I created this module to make that a thing of the past.

Don't worry, this "work" is fun. As you think about and answer the questions, you immediately start to visualize an Instagram for yourself that is way more kick-ass than when you had no plan or focus.

Let's get started...

PLEASE DOWNLOAD AND USE THE ACCOMPANYING WORKSHEET HERE:

Ultimate IG (Worksheet).pdf

1. DEFINE YOUR OVERALL GOAL: Get more email sign-ups? (THIS IS USUALLY THE BEST ONE) Get people to go to your website? Get people to buy something direct?

2. FOLLOWER GOAL: How many followers are we trying to get? In how much time? HOW are we getting them? Is this even important?

3. COMMENT GOAL: How many comments are we trying to get on each post? Is this important? What KPIs will we track for this? What will we do/try to encourage commenting?

4. What KPIs will we use to track these goals? Also track exponential KPIs: SHARES and SAVES.

An avatar is a description of the person you imagine to be your brand's biggest fan.

It can't be "everybody". It needs to be the people who you imagine would be your "day 1s".

You need to define what types of people your "day 1s" are. Because once you do... You'll only be talking to them.

ANSWER THESE QUESTIONS:

1. DEMOGRAPHIC (WHAT IS THEIR AGE, GENDER, NATIONALITY etc...)

2. GEOGRAPHIC (WHERE ARE THEY FROM? WHERE DO THEY HANG OUT?)

3. PSYCHOGRAPHIC (WHAT ARE THEY INTERESTED IN? WHAT DO THEY STAND FOR?)

4. IDENTITY (DO THEY HAVE A WAY OF IDENTIFYING THEMSELVES IE. Punk, Nurse, X'O, Feminist)

What content could you make that your day 1s would want to share with their friends? Don't gloss over this question. Really think about this.

How can you provide this sort of content to them?

Give your avatar a name. It could even be the name of someone you already know who is pretty much your avatar.

It may be up to two people (IE. a boy and a girl)

Find a picture that resembles them.

From this point forward, understand that everything you do on instagram will be for them. Which means that everyone else... just may not get it. And guess what? That's okay. They'll get it later.

LIST 5 CLOSE INSPIRING "COMPETITORS" FOR YOU TO WATCH.

The best people to pick are people that are similar to you, but ahead of you in the journey of "success".

FOLLOW ALL YOUR COMPETITORS AND INSPIRATIONS

UNFOLLOW EVERYONE THAT ISN'T CONNECTED TO WHAT YOU ARE DOING.

Define Your "WHAT?"

Every brand knows WHAT they do and can clearly articulate what they're all about. Can you? Write it down.

Define Your "HOW?"

What makes you different from the rest? How do you SHOW how good you are without having to even open your mouth? Write it down now.

Define Your "WHY?"

Ah... The big one.

What is your worldview? What is the reason you do what you do? The reason anyone should care. Write it down.

From now on every time you communicate on Instagram, you will be leading with your "WHY?"

You will only talk about the other things after you've talked about your WHY?

For example. With lastnightsparty, I'd never talk about the fact that I take pictures. I'd lead with:

"I think everyone can look like a superstar. I think people should get out of their comfort zone and talk to strangers more."

And then I'd let the work speak for itself. I'd never talk about lenses, or how I'm a photographer. I'd talk about "WHY" I do what I do.

Now, your turn. Re-imagine your Instagram as a place where you talk about your why. I don't need to hear about your new album, your new drawings, your new book or whatever...

I wanna know about WHY you created them.

That's what will attract your DAY 1s.

Put your WHY in your bio.

And remember the "HOW" from above? You can put that in there too.

Make it clear who you are.

Sometimes you should consider making the first line in your bio whatever your greatest accomplishment is.

Add your viral #hashtag if you have one.

Add a call-to-action related to your IG Goal (Remember that one from above?)

Let's start defining what you'll be talking about on your IG.

Your IG is a job. And the people that follow you will be following you because you give them something that they can count on every time.

You have to define what your messages on your IG will be.

These are called BROADCAST MESSAGES.

What do Gary V, Kim Kardashian, Nike and National Geographic have in common?

They're consistent about what they talk about when they communicate with you.

They're always on message.

They each have maximum 3 talking points and they just hammer it home all day.

And if you follow them... It's cause you love what they're hammering home.

What are the 3 broadcast messages that YOU will be choosing to "hammer home" on social media every day?

#### Pick 3.

Make them related to your "WHY?" your "HOW?".

Ignore the "WHAT?".

That should be obvious.

Everyone's instagram is talking about their "WHAT" (what they do).

You'll automatically stand out by not doing that too.

Choose hashtags that go with each message.

BONUS: What do you believe in that you wish you could say, but is way too controversial? Hint. That's what you should say.

Pick 2 content types that would be perfect for your broadcast messages. One of them should be 80% of what you do on your Instagram page. Don't try to do all of them. Your page will be a message. People like following accounts that do one thing well.

Your goal here is to create content that people would share or save. Forget "LIKES".

Write them down.

What is the best caption that will give value to your audience and spread your kind of message?

LONG CAPTION?

STORY CAPTION?

QUOTE CAPTION?

MINIMAL CAPTION?

Write it down.

WHAT WILL YOUR POST FREQUENCY BE?

ONCE A WEEK?

THREE TIMES A WEEK?

ONCE A DAY?

MULTIPLE TIMES A DAY?

Write it down.

MAKE AN INSTAGRAM MOCKFEED.

Use one of the millions of tools out there (I use Later.com) so that you can build what your IG will look like aesthetically in advance.

Leave nothing to chance.

*If you can't see it in your head, you won't get there as quickly.*

THINGS YOU MAY BE TRACKING:

Amount of shares

Amount of engagement

How many people joined your email list

How many DMs you got about something related to your business

How many products you sold

The key is to pick ONLY ONE.

Make that your focus.

And switch around your content until you see those KPIs improving.

But stay on message.

It takes a while to establish a new message online.

The worst thing you can do is dilute it with competing messages like a random selfie, or a random rant about whatever.

Your audience wants to find you.

Make it easy for them.

That's the only reason to build your ULTIMATE IG.

### 13. THE ULTIMATE IG
