### 14. Ten Creative Ways To Share Your Process Online (that isn't another lame Tiktok timelapse)

"I want to be mysterious."

"I want people to think my art comes out of me without effort."

"I hate the idea of setting up a camera or remembering to stop to grab some video while I'm in the middle of working. It doesn't feel natural."

"No one wants to see that!"

"I don't want to play the social media game of making reels or TikToks."

"I'm lazy."

"I don't want to promote myself. It feels like I'm playing into the capitalist mindset."

"I want to share this part of myself with my community. It's the best way I've found to shorten the communication gaps with them. I understand that being on social media is about being social."

"I believe the journey of HOW I make my art is integral to appreciating the art itself."

"I never want my art page to look "dead" like some corporate artist portfolio page or something."

"I want to inspire other artists, like artists have inspired me. When I watch my favorite artist interviews—that's what I want to know about the most. So it only makes sense that my fans would want the same."

"I see where technology is going. Sharing my process has become the key difference between me and artificial intelligence."

"I realized that my lack of sharing the journey of creating stuff was what was hurting my growth the most. Online and offline."

"I want to have another way to introduce people to my work besides only the finished piece. I want as many 'at-bats' as possible."

"I've noticed that when people are aware of my process, it makes the art feel more valuable to them. I guess because they can see what went into it… And then I can charge more!"

"I'm a modern artist. I want to use all the tools available, including social media. I know that if my favorite artists from back in the day would've had had this opportunity, they would have JUMPED ON it!"

When most people think of "sharing their process" online, they think of "making a timelapse" like the ones you see on TikTok or on Reels.

TikTok timelapses are the WORST way to share your process. At least if your goal is to be taken seriously as an artist. Why? Timelapses are only about the end result.

Timelapses are for creatives who are "product" oriented. Do you know another word for "product"? "Content." TikTok timelapses are perfect content because they're all about the finished product.

The alternative to being "product-oriented" is becoming "process-oriented.

Would you rather watch a 5-second timelapse of a sunset? Or watch an actual sunset?

Even 30 seconds of uncut real-time sunset will make a person feel the vibe more than a timelapse of the whole thing.

That's why you're better off sharing ONE KEY MOMENT of your process so we can feel it in real-time. It'll be like landing on a Bob Ross video in the middle of it. Instantly mesmerizing.

No one wants to watch Bob Ross sped up.

Let me remind you. You're not a "content creator". Make that clear by giving us a glimpse of your fascinating behind-the-scenes.

So here are 10 ways to do it-- 10 ways that maybe you didn't think of.

Show them where the magic happens. You don't have to show them everything all at once. Show them your art desk today. Show them your storage tomorrow. Show them your book collection next week. Share little bits as the months go by. And as you add and subtract things.

Think of any artist you love. If they invited you into their studio to see how the magic happens, would you accept the invitation with zeal? Or politely decline?

Look at this artist who found a genius way of sharing his process on Instagram reels—by making videos about how much he hates making reels about his process.

Key takeaway? He's still sharing his process.

If you find that turning on a camera while you're in the flow feels awkward… Do this instead.

Turn the camera on BEFORE. Turn the camera on AFTER. And spill your guts.

See how she does it? If you're a fan of this artist, it's like mana from the heavens!

Share your process for old pieces. Even if you're working on new stuff.

Sharing doesn't have to be chronological. Process is still intriguing even if it's 10 years after the fact. Talk about how something you did ages ago is influencing something today.

Or you can show us how your OLD PROCESS stopped working for you, and how that led to the new one.

Audiences that love you have a voyeurism to see how your art is created.

That's why Kurt Cobain's notebooks are still intriguing even after he's gone.

Everybody loves "making of" documentaries.

Sometimes the documentaries are even more intriguing than the art they're based on.

Apocalypse Now is a classic film. But 'Heart Of Darkness' (about the making of Apocalypse Now, shot by Coppola's wife) is a classic documentary.

Or remember Bennett Coast, the musician I told you about in a mid-week Sermon? His behind-the-scenes video had more impact than the actual music video itself.

This is a very cinematic approach. And mysterious. One of my favorites.

In movies, they sometimes want to wait to reveal the grand artwork. So what do they do? They show the painter at work with the camera pointed at the painter! You see glimpses of their hands. Close-ups of their facial expressions. The subject of what they're painting. Anything but the painting.

You should steal that approach.

It ends up giving off a strong VIBE without revealing the actual work.

Add a voice-over and/or captions.

I did this with The Weeknd when we were on tour.

I filmed him recording songs on the tour bus, in hotel rooms, and in studios… BUT because it was unreleased material, I'd replace the audio of these mini-videos with fan recordings I was collecting.

The kids LOST IT when they saw those videos. Even without the audio, they felt like they were GETTING ACCESS.

It's like when painters do sketches of what will become paintings. Often those sketches are JUST AS WORTHY as the paintings.

Or when you share demos of songs. Some demos turn out better than the final recorded song.

Writers... Look at what I do on my @bronques IG account.

Do you think I sit at a desk daily and try to dream up quotes to put on my Instagram? Hell no.

My quotes come from my longer-form writing. They come from when I'm developing a module, a podcast, a sermon, or even while journaling. You may even notice how something I posted changed or improved by the time the long-form came out. All my Instagram posts are earlier drafts of something bigger.A microdose from the full thing. (like I teach you in 'The Book Of Money').That doesn't make it any less valuable to share. It doesn't have to be "perfect". That's why I turned them into their own thing.

People adore the raw version of an idea's infancy. There's a magic there that can't be reproduced. It's an emotional outburst. It's the spark.

If you're a photographer... Why not make posts about picking the clothes? Or doing the make-up? Or making your whole social media account about the exciting quest of hunting for locations? And only once in a while do we get the end result. It would make us more invested in your photos if you brought us along with you.

Show us the materials you use and tell us about them.

What's that special pen you use to write?

What kind of guitar is that?

Why do you prefer 'GOLDEN' paints?

Show us your camera collection. And the film in your fridge.

Film someone else (even your mom) talking about your process from their point of view.

If you're too shy, interview a friend to talk about how you make art. That's just as fun for us. It's another way of show us your world.

Interview your art teachers, your mentors, other artists you collaborate with so we can get a glimpse of how you make art.

Lighting a candle.

Putting on music.

Making tea.

Getting the light just right.

Mixing paints.

Getting your desk ready.

Putting all your tools out.

Turning all the gear on.

And don't be shy about showing any of these over and over again. You are allowed to film yourself lighting a candle 40 times on your Instagram feed. THAT'S how you genuinely make the audience feel the ritual... Through repetition.

You're scared.

I know all of your excuses (re-read them above).

None of them are original.

It only reveals your fear of THE UNKNOWN. You haven't done it before. You don't know where to start. So you compare yourself to others who do it... And chicken out.

You're trying to be too fancy.

Look at Ethel Cain above. She turns on the camera and shares. No edits. It's just her being genuine with her audience. And that's why her fans love her.

You're trying to be too fancy.

Complicating things is the most classic form of resistance. If you make it complex, needing hours to execute, then you'll have an excuse not to do it.

But the #1 reason you don't share your process is... You love sabotaging your growth. You already KNOW that sharing your process will promote your work to more people. And you KNOW it'll make people better understand what you're put on this earth for. But you'd rather make it harder for the audience to love you--so that you can lick your wounds and remain a tortured artist.

You cling to the romance that "you don't need to show your process because artists throughout the ages didn't show their process".

First of all, that's a lie. If you want the truth, it's a Google search away. But even if it was true… The 2020s, is OUR TIME. Online tools have empowered us. If you really want to emulate the artists of lore, then WHY ARE YOU SCROLLING IN THE FIRST PLACE? THEY didn't "scroll".

You have this romantic notion that an artist is supposed to disappear for years, and came back with a revolutionary art that rocks the world. But guess what?

"Coming down from your ivory tower to share your finished masterpiece" is something you can only do when you become a household name.

But to get there, a new artist has to give an audience a story to INVEST in.

If you're on social media, then use it to empower yourself, instead of blowing out your brain cells.

Isn't it funny how the people who say they "don't want to make content on social media" because they're "artists", are also the most voracious CONSUMERS of that content? If you hate content so much, why are you even on there?

If you don't have a very clear reason WHY you're on social media, then you will keep using it in self-destructive ways.

Social media ISN'T your portfolio. It ISN'T your storefront. It ISN'T where you "promote your latest shit". It ISN'T a place to shamelessly peddle your finished art (surrounded by content) in exchange for "exposure".

Social media isn't about you.

You're an artist. When did you revert to only showing your best self, and taking on this facade? That's what the normals do when they're PRETENDING to be an artist. They keep it one-dimensional. They show only end results. "Look at me. Look at what I did."

And they do it using the least amount of effort. They go through the motions online. Don't you realize we can feel your lack of enthusiasm? Do you think that makes us excited about what you're doing? Fix your attitude. Either post with zeal or don't post at all. That doesn't mean things have to be perfect. Not at all. Just do it with love.

Real artists embrace the messiness of it all. They share their artistic journey and make their online presence 3-dimensional. Say what you want about Kanye, but he is one of the few musicians who at least still behaves like an artist. Messy, controversial, polarizing… Like an artist. And despite his ability to exclude the fans if he wanted to, he STILL shares his process. It's that sharing of his process that makes him "un-cancellable" to his fans.

(feedback implemented from fans to improve mixes on streaming platforms. Who does that?)

When you're an artist, social media is the place you go to communicate an ENERGY. An energy that will attract you people. And that little difference in intention will make all the difference in how you come off on these platforms.

Think about it. When YOU love a work of art, and you meet the creator of that art, what's the first thing you want to know? "What inspired them to make it?" And that is a question about "process".

People want to know about how you made the art, just as much as they want to see the art in its finished form. They want to know the story of how it came to be.

Sharing that with your community can be a wonderful bonding moment.

Even if the resulting art is one of your failures, it's still a special moment describing the adventure.

Sometimes, that ill-fated adventure will inspire the next incredible work of art. And they will have been there for the ride with you.

You may still need to figure out what your message is.

You may not know what you're "trying to say" artistically yet.

But until you figure it out…

YOUR PROCESS IS THE CLOSEST THING YOU HAVE TO A MESSAGE.

How you make your art (your process) tells your audience what you believe in.

Do you make art outdoors in nature? Or do you make it indoors in an all-white room? That communicates.

Do you make it at 4 am in a basement studio with a weak tungsten light? Or do you travel the globe collaborating with the "art elite"? That communicates.

The tools you use, the time you put in, and your odd little rituals reveal how you view the world… Just as much as your art does.

Whatever your process is…

It communicates energy.

One last thing…

You're all guilty of it. And it's got to stop.

Stop trying to be aloof and cool. Stop emulating people who already have established online brands.

If you want to grow… Never post anything online without GIVING CONTEXT!

A few words in your caption… A few words at the beginning of the video… HELP THEM UNDERSTAND WHAT THE FUCK THEY'RE LOOKING AT

Here's a genius way of giving context (and look how well it's paid off for him):

@romanlolo on TikTok

By simply adding 3 seconds of context as his intros, it makes his videos addictive. He does it every time. That's how he hooks you in. And makes you totally invested.

If he had just posted the same exact video WITHOUT that 3 seconds of context, you wouldn't have watched it to the end.

That's why no one cares when you post a random clip of your new music video on social media, telling them to "go listen on Spotify".

Who are you, Drake?

My bad. Even HE doesn't do lame roll-outs like that. Even Drake gives everything context, making it part of an intricate puzzle.

He does it with love.

Listen to this example of DRAKE GIVING CONTEXT:

Never forget. You're sharing in a noisy, distracted environment. So, give depth if you want to catch our eye.

But shhhh… You don't need to tell people what you're doing. "Hey guys, I'm sharing my process." Just start sharing your process like it's the most natural thing in the world (it is). And do it again the next time. No fanfare.

The cumulative effect of doing this will make people see your finished art work in a whole new way. People will feel like they are living this journey with you.

Isn't that what you want?

### 15. Quadrupling Your Followers: What's So Special About Kat?

Kat joined The Mystery School in December 2021. She had 800 followers and she wasn’t really selling tons of paintings yet.

By mid-February 2022, she was selling paintings regularly and had 4,542 followers.

By May 2022 she had 16k followers and was thriving in her new studio. (Instagram killed her account after she got hacked, unfortunately...But that hasn't hurt her Tiktok and her email list!)

So, what’s so special about Kat?

She did it by sharing her story.

She started getting new fans the moment she let people in on what she was doing. They wanted to support her, so they bought her paintings.

Every post she shares has long detailed captions that document a part of her journey.

And Kat doesn't shy away from showing people what they want to see:

“The Artist At Work”.

Here is Kat's pivotal caption:

"Big News! I've left my part-time job so I can focus on my art full time. ✨🥳🎨 Change is scary, and to be honest I've spend a lot of time thinking about how being an artist is not a real job, how only a few can "make it"... At that time being an artist just didn't seem like a viable opportunity. 🤷‍♀️😅 It took me years to change. I started to look for examples. For people who choose to make art and it's working, they are succeeding I decided to work on my skills and insecurities and I slowly started to believe - it can be possible. The results of making this tiny effort, to change my belief, have been huge. A big milestone in my personal and artistic development. 👩‍🎨 I understand it may sound cliche, but believing is the single biggest reason for me being here, in my studio, writing this. Thanks you for being part of this journey, I hope it inspires you to be brave, question less and believe more. 💛☀️🙏"

Wouldn't that kind of caption make YOU want to buy a painting or at least click to follow her journey?

Her KPI (key performance indicator) isn't how many followers she has.

Her KPI is how many followers turn into customers.

REAL engagement and active participants is her goal, so she started talking to her tribe in the same way she would talk if she was updating real-life friends on what she’s been up to lately.

Kat only follows people that reinforce her Polaris Star.

She unfollowed everyone else.

Kat realized, looking at others who were less advanced than her (but killing it), that this game isn’t about “how good your art is.” Nope. There are other factors at play.

So she started studying those people.

“I’d see all these artists online that blew up after a few months of effort, and I just believed that I could be one of those artists.”

Kat turns every thought into a potential post.

She understands that this is part her job.

She understands that without all this "sharing with her audience" she wouldn’t be in the advantageous position she is in now.

“In the beginning it’s hard to figure out what to say. But it’s like everything else. It gets easier and easier.”

She found her cat sleeping on one of her paintings? Ok.... POST TO INSTAGRAM.

She's trying a new art technique? Ok... POST TO INSTAGRAM.

She's having trouble finishing painting? Ok... POST TO INSTAGRAM.

You know how when you join The Mystery School, and I send you a module that I think would be perfect for your personal journey?

Well, when I found out what Kat was trying to do I sent her a link to this module:

HOW TO BUILD A CAREER IN 90 DAYS

2 Days later she announced to her followers that she was doing a 90-Day challenge.

She turned her journey into a game:

90 pieces of art in 90 days.

***Take note MS students… Immediate execution with ideas that inspire you. If you don't move right away, you'll lose the momentum and energy of the moment.

NOTE: Kat told me she was starting a newsletter when we spoke live. And the next day she sent me the landing page URL.

Once again... Immediate execution.

This is what she put on her landing page:

"Subscribe to join the art tribe. Sign up to receive the monthly art letter, access to discounts, and stay up-to-date with my creative journey."

"Art of email" checklist... Did she pass?

Just because you told them once, doesn’t mean you can’t keep telling them every few weeks what your goal is. Some people need reminding. Some people never heard it the first time around.

Kat told me she has 20 pieces and she needs to make more so that there’s more variety. I don't think so. She needs to make those pieces more valuable. You do that by creating a story and a message around them. I explained that she needed to keep sharing her story and whatever shreds of message she’s figured out so far to make people buy her pieces REGARDLESS of what's left online. You raise the value of your work, not by creating more of it, but by creating a story around it that’s compelling. If they relate to the energy that you’re putting out into the world, then they will want to buy ANYTHING and EVERYTHING that you create. And you can get that aura around your work BEFORE the New York Times article... and BEFORE the celebrity endorsements.

NOTE: By the time I put this module together, Kat had already made a new post sharing her story and goals again.

What's so special about Kat?

You mean, besides her talent for painting?

And besides her masterful implementation of the color yellow?

SHE EXECUTES HER IDEAS IMMEDIATELY.

### 16. WRITING CAPTIONS (THE DEFINITIVE 10-STEP GUIDE - Even A Baby Can Do It)

So many people struggle with writing captions.

They want to post something but they have no idea what to write so they settle for emoji's...

Or they steal someone else's quote...

Or they copy the "basic bitch" phrases you see all over Instagram.

You too, may have been fooled into thinking that you have to be a writer, or super witty to do write great captions.

No, all you need is a process.

(DAYS BEFORE)

Collect ideas.

When rappers or musicians go into writing sessions, they bring a notebook of ideas. Or a beat, or a riff so they always have a place to start.

You should do the same.

Write down ideas you get as you go through your daily life. . Put them in your NOTES app on your phone These will be great jump-off points for your captions later.

(HOURS BEFORE)

Get off social media.

Read writing that inspires you.

Read passages from books you love (prose not poetry -- poetry isn't as conversational as we'll need you to be here).

Get in the zone of what good writing actually reads like.

(JUST BEFORE)

Close your laptop. Turn off all devices.

Print out those ideas you've been collecting.

Get a pen and paper.

You might wanna fight me one this, but try it. Writing with "pen and paper" makes ideas flow faster than using a laptop or the phone. It's counter-intuitive, but this "old school" way is the fastest way. Especially if you don't "really know what to write".

It's like the pen becomes a magic wand for ideas. I don't know why, but it works. And if speed is key for you like it is for me, there is no other way. And the side benefit is your writing gets this soulfulness that other people's lacks.

My friend India, who makes a living writing captions, writes by hand too. Check out this video. Even when she was building her website... She used pen and paper:

It's just a snippet. But I had to share because I think this step is important.

Ok. Now, get cozy.

Treat caption writing with the same respect that you'd give to any other creative activity.

"Caption writing is an art form, bro."

Don't believe me? Here's aNew York Times articlefor some inspiration.

The words you put down today could become a script or a book one day. You never know. Get in the "caption writing zone". 'Cause trust me, when it starts flowing there's no stopping it.

Make a list, on the left side of the page, of everything you see or notice in the picture. Objects, expressions, oddities, etc...

Make a list, on the right hand side of everything you DON'T see in the picture. Like, where you are... Or the people you know where there but aren't pictured... Or something interesting that you know (or imagine) that's happening out of frame.

Is there an important lesson you can teach here?

Is there something about the moment in this photo that inspires you?

Something you remember that still puts a smaile on your face?

Behind the scenes information?

Basquiat does this a lot in his paintings. He puts boxes around key words. It has a magical affect on your psychology.

Do it with your list of key words

Look at your list and put a box around the things that have the most emotional resonance.

Writing to a particular person is the ultimate framing device.

If you write captions directed to the masses, they'll always be so vanilla. Instead, choose a person to direct your writing to. A real person. Preferably a friend.

And then write at the top of a brand new page...

Dear (your friends name),

Write to your friend about each of the things you've highlighted.

These ideas don't have to relate to each other yet. Write about whatever reason these things have an emotional connection with you. Conversational.

Tell stories about these things. Give your reader interesting facts about them. Share why these things resonate with you. Or why you think they would resonate with the person you're writing to.

And remember. Write casual. Like you're writing a text.

The way our teachers taught us to write in English class is the wrong way to write captions. This is not an essay. It's you talking. To a friend.

Make it transcription of your thoughts.

Make it conversational. You don't need fancy words.

Imagine a guy who's wife just found out she's pregnant. Does it matter how you tell him? You could use broken english to say it or the fanciest words... the effect will be the same: he's gonna be glad you told him.

The content of your words is more important than how you say it.

Don't second guess this stuff.

There is no 'one' caption. Let the Gods guide you one what energy this caption needs to have TODAY.

Every single person who would write about the things you highlighted... Would write something different. Tomorrow YOU would write something different.

What makes a caption good or not is how much of YOU that you put into it. The more of "your truth" that you inject, the more captivating it will be to a reader.

Don’t think that no one will care about this super specific thing you’re writing about. If you’re passionate about the subject you're writing about, someone else out there will care too. That's the beauty of being so connected on the internet.

But you know that already.

Nah, the real thing you're worried about is the clump of people who will judge you. And that’s what freezes you up. But why are you playing to the people in the back when there are people in the front row standing on their seats who paid to see the whites of your eyes?

Connect with YOUR FANS first. Ignore the haters.

Your pure energy will eventually carry through all the way back and influence the world.

NIJA TRICK: RECORD YOURSELF FREESTYLING

If you’re one of those people who considers yourself a talker, but freeze up when you have to write a caption, then do this:

Record yourself "pretend talking" to your friend about what you've highlighted. Then transcribe the best bits of what you said.

Remember those ideas that you've been collecting?

Now's a good time to take a glance at them.

It's crazy how the most unrelated ideas, can become connected in a magical moment.

Or maybe one of those ideas sends your brain down a rabbit hole. You end up somewhere totally unrelated, but totally awesome. All good. Keep the ideas flowing.

There will be many ideas on your paper now. It's time to choose which one's will make it to the caption. If you've done a good job so far, you may find it hard to choose only one...

Kill your darlings: pick one idea and go with it.

All the other "sick caption ideas"? Add them to your "sick caption ideas notebook". When you use this method of writing captions, you always end up with more extra captions that you may be able to use later. So if you wrote a good metaphor that doesn't work here... don't worry, you can use it later for something else

When you're finished, cross out the "Dear XXX," part at the top.

You will now have a caption with real personality because you directed it to a real person.

People will feel like you wrote for them.

This is what it looks like when I'm working on 3 captions at a time.

If you have time... Don't put it up right away. Giving yourself a break to look at it again later can help you turn an already good caption into a real gem.

NINJA TRICK

Use the “magazine article approach”. Write caption first then find (or create) a picture that suits it.

If speed is your goal, this will be the fastest content creation process.

IF you love writing.

IF you have access to a photographer or you're good with getting photos for yourself.

Alright now... Go write some captions!

P.S. Don't expect crazy reactions right away. They may not even see your captions because you haven't "trained" them to look down there yet. Give it time. They'll think the first long caption is a fluke. People need to trust before they invest in your story. Soon, they will come to expect it.

### 16. WRITING CAPTIONS (THE DEFINITIVE 10-STEP GUIDE - Even A Baby Can Do It)

## STEP ONE: PREPARATION

## STEP TWO: WRITE DOWN EVERYTHING YOU SEE

## STEP THREE: WRITE DOWN EVERYTHING YOU DON'T SEE

## STEP FOUR: PUT BOXES AROUND THE IDEAS YOU WROTE THAT STICK OUT TO YOU

## STEP FIVE: DECIDE WHO YOU'RE WRITING TO

## STEP SIX: WRITE ABOUT THE THINGS YOU'VE HIGHLIGHTED

## STEP SEVEN: LOOK AT YOUR RIFFS NOTEBOOK

## STEP EIGHT: KILL YOUR DARLINGS

## STEP NINE: TAKE OUT THE 'DEAR XXX,' PART

## STEP TEN: SIT ON THE CAPTION

##### Post a comment

##### 13comments

### 17. Why The Website You're Building Is Already Obsolete

Does your website have an "about" page?

Does it have social media icons so that people can connect with you throughout the internet?

Do you have a drop down menu or a header with different important page links?

Do you have a sign-up button for your newsletter?

Then your website is nothing more than a brochure. And no-one has time for a brochure without a succinct message these days.

Maybe that worked 10 years ago but it doesn't now.

If you send your valuable fans to the kind of website I just described then you hate money. You might as well open your wallet and empty it into a trash can.

What you need is a landing page.

A landing page is a "website" that only has one goal. And when people land on it... they know exactly what they need to do. They don't have to think about anything beyond a "yes" or "no". Nothing is confusing.

Confusion never leads to getting more fans.

Confusion never leads to sales.

Confusion only leads to "Good-bye, I'm going back to my IG now..."

No, you don't need an about page. The whole internet is your "about page". No one finds out more about you by reading your about page... They don't believe whatever you write there anyways (in the third person no doubt). They know it's all hype.

When people wanna know more "about" you, they Google you. Or they read your captions on IG. Or your posts on Facebook. Or they sign up to your mailing list.

If your goal is to announce your tour. Make your landing page the dates and put a link to buy tickets. Don't distract them with anything else. Now is not the time to tell them about your merch!

If your goal is to get their email... Then only put an email opt-in form on your page. Nothing else. You'll follow up with extra information about your tour and your merch in your "welcome email sequence". You can send them to those specific pages later... As you communicate with them over the weeks.

You should be a storytelling machine. And your landing page should drop them right in the middle of the action. Don’t give them a million options. This isn’t a choose your own adventure... No. You’re Quentin Tarantino and you’re taking them on a journey. They don’t get options.

Just because Squarespace" or "Wix" put it in the template doesn't mean you have to use it! Don't go through the motions. Don't copy what other people do. Study your own behavior. What do YOU do when you navigate the internet? Design the online experience that would drive your psychographic to tears of joy.

The "customer's journey" is all that matters.

And wherever that journey starts... it ultimately lands on your "website".

So make sure that when they get there they know exactly what to do.

Here's a photographer website that forces you to do what they want you to do:

HARIS NUKEM

### 19. WHATSAPP?? Really??

byTomson Darko(TMS Artist)

If you're sick of algorithms, shadow-bans or having less and less of your followers and fans see your work... There's a new game in town.

I'm going to show you how I created a WhatsApp list with 2000 engaged fans... With an average click through rate of 40%!

Nuts, I know. I mean, look at the data:

My Instagram Story clicks... 8%

Facebook... 15%.

My email newsletter... around 2%.

So, what's my WhatsApp formula?

I send one message a week with a link to my latest blog post.

The only problem?

It doesn't scale.

So if you're lazy. You're gonna hate it.

With my system you're gonna have to get your hands dirty. But it's definitely worth it.

Let me show you how.

WAIT. WHO ARE YOU?

My name is Tomson Darko. I’m Dutch. And I have a blog calledPsychokiller.

I publish fictional (short) stories. They're about the darker themes of life like "feeling alone while surrounded by people", "having sex with people you hate" etc.

When people connect to my work, they show their support by buying my self-published books. That's how I make money.

Facebook used to be my #1 traffic source back in 2016. I had 25,000 fans at the time. The organic reach was 10,000 unique views per post. Very quickly over the years it dropped down to 2,000 - 3,000 unique views.

That stung.

It got harder and harder to reach the fanbase that I had built over the years. Now, every time I published a new story I was reaching less people.

My email list had 3,000 subscribers, but it was not my mothership. I had ignored it for such a very long time that the open rate was pathetic.

And then Instagram. 25,000 fans... but I couldn't reach them anymore unless I wanted to pay for ads. Very frustrating.

So I had to do something.

The answer was WhatsApp. It's the number one social app in the Netherlands.

MAKE A PROMISE

I wondered what would happen if I texted my contacts a link to my latest blog post every Sunday? That was my promise to my contacts. That means that even if I’m on fire and I write 5 posts that week, I still only send that ONE WhatsApp message at the end of the week.

You have to be specific about what you’re offering to your fans. And when are you going to publish? Once a month? Every day? Every week?

Pick a frequency and stick to it.

Pick a content type and stick to it.

Don’t say just say something like "Subscribe for more inspiration". Say "Subscribe and I'll text you with an inspirational quote every morning". Or "Subscribe and I will send you exclusive behind-the-scenes photos every first Monday of the month.

And never break your promise. Give them what they opted-in for.

BROADCAST LISTS

And the best way to do it is with WhatsApp's 'broadcast-list'. Using this, you can send a message to 250 of your contacts at a time.

To create a broadcast-list on Android:

Open WhatsApp.

Go to the Chats screen > More options > New broadcast.

Tap + or type in contact names to choose recipients from your contact list.

Tap Create.

To create a broadcast-list on an iPhone:

Open WhatsApp.

Tap the Broadcast Lists button at the top of the Chats screen.

Tap New List at the bottom of the Broadcast Lists screen.

Type your contacts' names or click the (+) button to choose from your contact list.

Tap Create.

GET A NUMBER SYSTEM

A broadcast-list can have a maximum of 250 contacts. So I've created 10 broadcast lists on my phone for my weekly "blasts". So that things don't get confusing, I make sure to numbering my contacts according to what list they're on. So if "Jennie" is opting-in for my list, I'm going to save her as "1. Jennie". That way if she's ever wants to opt-out, I know where to find her: list 1.

I've heard some people complain about the broadcast-list. "Not everyone on the list gets my message", 'I don't think it works'.

If you're experiencing this, the problem is not WhatsApp. It's your phone. You need a fast processor (min. 2.0 ghz). And you need a minimum of 4GB RAM to text the message to hundreds of people in just a few seconds.

When I tried it with my last smartphone that had 2GB RAM, it didn't work very well. The only way to be 100% sure that everyone will get your messages, is with a fast phone.

I'm using a Samsung A7 android, so I can sync my contacts with Gmail. If the phone fails me, I still have my contacts.

Now... your new follower has to add YOUR number into their contacts too. Otherwise WhatsApp won’t send them your messages.

You can make a "pre-filled" WhatsApp message for your followers for the opt-in.

I'm quoting WhatsApp:

"To create your own link with a pre-filled message that will automatically appear in the text field of a chat, usehttps://wa.me/whatsappphonenumber/?text=urlencodedtextwhere whatsappphonenumber is a full phone number in international format and URL-encodedtext is the URL-encoded pre-filled message.

Using CLICK TO CHAT

If someone wants to opt-out you have to delete them from the broadcast-list FIRST. Then, delete them from your phone. If you delete them from your phone first, you won't find them on the list but they will still receive your messages and probably get pissed-off. You don't want that so do it right.

PROMOTING YOUR WHATSAPP LIST

I promote my list at the end of every blogpost.

Did you like this? Do you want to know when the next post is coming up? I will personally send you a Whatsapp message with info about the blogpost every Sunday. Follow the instructions:

1. Add my number 123344566 to your contact list.

2. Send me a message called 'party on' with your first name or use this quick-link.

3. If you don't want to receive my messages anymore. Just send me a message that says ‘its over’.

PLATFORM FARMING

A few times a year I promoting my WhatsApp-list on my Facebook and Instagram stories. I get about 100 or so newbies that way.

One the last two years I've collected 2,000 contacts in my phone.

You may not like how slow it is. But at least you don't get burnt by algorithm changes.

Building trust and expanding is a slow process, but it’s worth it.

When I started selling Psychokiller merchandise my WhatsApp list were the first to buy stuff. Instagram and Facebook? Crickets.

The followers on my WhatsApp list are my number one fans.

They trust me.

They like my art and they give direct and honest feedback.

"I love this new story" or "You had a type-o in your last post". Real engagement. Not just heart emojis.

I get about 10 new contacts every week.

I lose about 4-5 people every month.

IT'S NOT A CHAT ROOM

Oh and you should avoid using your broadcast-list like a chat.

One time I made that mistake. I wrote: "Hi". Then I received a few hundred replies in 10 seconds from people with "hi" back. Rookie mistake.

Instead make one clear message and say goodbye. Like this:

I hope you have a good day. I wrote a post about leaving the house in the morning before your 'booty call' wakes up. This is the link:www.psychokiller.eu

See you next week!

Some people will reply, but the majority will just take this as a message they don’t have to reply to.

BUT ALWAYS REPLY

Always answer your fans. Show them you're human and that you appreciate them when they take the time out to write you. Nurture that relationship.

Some people might even be surprised by your reply. They may think your WhatsApp is controlled by bots.

Show them you're not a bot.

Why does it work so well?

It's a one to one relationship.

And when you show up regularly, you build a real connection. That's what your fans want.

Most people want things to happen overnight, but I've learned that the best methods don't scale.

Maybe, you won't get everybody to trust you with their number. But when you do find those that say "Yes. Here's my number. You can text me!" Those are the ones that may become fans for life.

## THE BOOK OF MONEY: Business Art


### 1. How To Make It Rain (Part I)

"The Creative Economy" has exploded. The number of brands and companies that hire creative individuals to help bring their products and their messages out into the world surpasses any other time in history.

But a few years ago I came across this video that perfectly put into words why so many creatives will continue to get stuck in a downward spiral as soon as they start working with brands.

In case you find it too long, it's too wordy and and don't like "the messenger", I'm gonna dumb-down the concepts within it in this module.

These are essential BUSINESS ART vitamins if you wanna thrive working with "clients".

This is "truthlotion" if there was ever was "truthlotion".

So picture, the creative economy, as a classic, three layer cheese cake.

At the top of the cake is the sour cream topping.

They're the ones with all the money.

And all they want in life is to have more people LOVE them and buy their products. And they're ready to spend to make that happen. 'Cause if they succeed. They'll make way more money.

And at the bottom of the cake is the graham crust.

The worker-bees. Or The technicians.

The technicians are the people that do all the daily things required to make the business move forward. They do the daily tasks that allow the business to operate.

Super important. But let's be honest... pretty much interchangeable.

As a technician you're only as valuable as the particular task that you do is valuable to the company. There are predetermined budgets for whatever it is that you bring to the table.

So... Understand... if you make videos for a brand, or take pictures or you DJ for them, or make logos, or really cool illustrations for their packaging or whatever... There will be a set price that people are willing to pay for that thing that you do. And everyone in the industry knows pretty much what that price is. Or the RANGE you can make. And it's basically a take it or leave it kind of thing. cause if it's not you doing... an hour later, they can find someone else Maybe even hand it off to the intern.

So when things go bad in business, the technicians are the first ones who get their budget slashed... or stop getting hired altogether.

So what does all this mean for you?

It means that if you're a technician... you're a commodity.

If the work you do can be by anyone else, you're a commodity.

A video guy... is a commodity.

The house photographer... is a commodity.

The DJ... a commodity.

Graphic designer... a commodity.

The band playing at the holiday party... a commodity

You may call yourself an artist or whatever.

But most artists are technicians who can be easily replaced by someone cheaper, someone younger, or someone with nicer gear.

It's an assembly line.

The educational systems are cranking out technicians year after year after year.

And self-taught youtube kids will do what you do faster and work for free to move ahead.

So while you may call yourself a creative... In the eyes of a brand or a company or a small business or a marketing agency... you are merely a technician.

And what you do, no matter how pretty it is, no matter how cool it is, no matter how artsy it is... it has a budget range that's been pre-determined by your industry. And you won't be exceeding that number any time soon.

You... Are in the rat race, just like everyone else that's working a 9 to 5 job. Except you just have a more glamorous title. of course. You get to call yourself a 'creative'.

So the million dollar question is?

Is there a way to escape from this drab role of technician?

Is there a way to make money beyond the pre-determined suffocating ranges? And STILL be working as a creative?

Yes, absolutely.

Remember that cheesecake I was talking about?

At the top is the cream, the brand. At the bottom is the crust, the technicians.

Well... you need to get yourself in that coveted middle spot. the creamy cheesecake center.

Say goodbye to graham cracker life.

It's time to start behaving like

A rainmaker.

Yes, that's right.

You need to become a creative who can "make it rain".

You gotta re-program your mind so that you can play the real game that's being played.

From now on, when you start a new working relationship with a brand, your only goal should be to create art that can make it rain.

Just like Richard Avedon did.

Just like Helmut Newton did.

Just like Anton Corbijn.

And Andy Warhol.

When you belong to this elite of creatives, you will have no more caps on your earning potential like technicians do.

You will no longer be a commodity.

Because as a rainmaker, you'll be bringing in more fans to a business, or more customers , or media attention.

And you know what all of those things mean to the brand?

MORE MONEY.

And no matter what they say... that's all they care about. They don't care about your art, unless it's helping them make money.

So If you want to be the artist who get's paid beyond scale, you'll have to shift your focus from making art, to making art that makes it rain.

The middle spot of the cheese cake analogy is the sweet spot where you're gonna want to take your career this year.

That way, in a few months you'll have a manager who will be able to say:

"If you want what we got, this is the price."

So how do you do it?

How do go from being a technician to becoming a rainmaker?

Especially if you're not mega famous, or an influencer or anything obvious like that?

How do you make this shift in your career?

It's all a matter of positioning.

And There Are 5 ways to do it...

How To Make It Rain (Part II)

### 2. How To Make It Rain (Part II)

If you know anything about what I do, you know that nothing that I've ever done has ever been about playing it safe. Yet somehow I've also been able to work with the largest and most conservative corporations in the world. Usually those two things don't work together. It's either you're making artistic things or you're selling out by creating watered down content for brands. But I've never looked at it that way. I grew up thinking that art and commerce were supposed to be intertwined since all of my heroes intertwined the two. I'm talking about Warhol, Prince, Madonna. They all created art that pushed the envelope. But they also did it in this way that was commercially viable too. It was always clear to me that the two could co-exist. So that's just the way I think.

So when I started working with brands, I developed a way of presenting my ideas in a way to get away with the craziest stuff and get payed for it. And it was always win / win. They would always hire me again because I delivered.

And today, with the internet, in an era where we have what's being called the 'creator economy', that balance of power is in the artist's favor more than ever.

But to use that power you need to be able to talk the right language. It doesn't come automatically. You have to think in a new way about your relationships with brands.

Once you start thinking this way, you're able to have very different conversations with people in suits. And then the idea of "selling out" is never even a consideration.

What's the definition of selling out? It's when you do something that your heart isn't into just so you can make money. And typically when you start working with brands, they slowly start asking you to do things that work against what you do to make it work. People who can keep their art pure while working with a brand are living "the dream". And most artists thinking that they'll only achieve this when they're super well known or have tremendous leverage some other way.

Not at all.

You just need a new strategy.

When I've photographed festivals in the past, they would always hire a video guy and a photographer... and then... they'd also hire me.

I was never there as a technician.

I was always there as a rainmaker, 'cause I brought a whole new set of eyes to what they were doing that that the other people that they hired couldn't bring.

And I also another perspective that those people didn't have.

While they were shooting "footage"...

I was shooting stories.

The real FOMO is not in the footage, since all footage looks the same.

The real FOMO is in the stories that people are experiencing.

I was hired as a professional FOMO inducer. This made me a rainmaker for the brands that could afford to hire me.

I remember my first meeting with a Swedish vodka brand called Kanon back in the day. I did the weirdest campaigns and promotions with them. And they always went along with my ideas.

But I never had conversations about art with them. Harry and I approached everything I wanted to do from the angle of how those ideas would help increase their marketshare, or how using certain weirder concepts would help them get the attention of the people they wanted, and how these ideas I was proposing would get people to talk about them more.

As you know, I'm all about art. And I'm all about making bat-crazy shit. But when I talk to brands I only talk about using art as a means to helping them reach their goals.

Most artists? They focus on how "cool" something's gonna be , or how "pretty" it's gonna look.

But guess what happens when you leave the room? The creative department is only on little voice. They have to fight against the sales department and the marketing department vs. the lawyers who hate doing anything that hasn't been test... So you should Talk to the brand in a way that all the departments can see their vested interest in your creative ideas. Otherwise the moment you step out of the boardroom, your art concepts will go through iterations of watering down by time your trip in the company's elevator has hit the ground floor.

Change your thinking from making art solely for making yourself happy. To making art that can move the needle for a brand.

Unless you LIKE knowing that the special low price you're giving someone "just this one time" will be the price bracket that they're gonna see you in..;. forever?

Or... Do you really want to keep working at a hourly rate. Giving them a chinese menu of services you offer... And basically just one step away from asking them if they want fries with that?

Do you wanna keep saying yes to projects that start off great but get more and more watered down until they're unrecognizable. But then you're stuck-- and your name's attached to something that blows?

Often your clients will think they can get their cousin to do what you do for free... They never have a "budget" for your art even though they know you're "worth it". And that will continue as long as you keep focusing on the "content" and not the "context".

The "context" is what the brand is trying to achieve.

You have to learn to create beautiful things based on those goals

They don't care about your "process" or your sensibility or your finesse.

They care about making money.

And once you start caring more abut making money, you'll be better equipped to help them make money too.

You've just been talking to brands all wrong. Today let's fix that once and for all. Today let's talk about how you can keep the weirdness, the artyness, and the edgyness of your work in tact and make brands wanna pay for THAT instead of the watered down version they always end up with.

The most impressive homework you can do if you're going to start working with a brand is to get to know the brand's customers more than the brand does.

Your art will be the main vehicle they use to communicate with that audience. And you should know who you're "talking" to.

Businesses don’t have the headspace to remember to walk in the shoes of their customers all the time.

But you? You’re an artist. That’s ALL you do.

Artists are the queens and kings of empathy. Our words resonate with people. So do our stories. Focus on THAT when you talk to clients... They don't need to know about your artistic "process" and all your touchy-feely rituals.

Don't make your conversations only about art.

Define what you're doing for the brand as "providing a solution to a problem they're having".

That way every conversation you have with the brand keeps highlighting the problem they're having.

And every conversation keeps highlighting you as the problem solver.

You just happen to be using art to solve this problem.

But don't focus on art with the money people.

Just because someone wears a t-shirt, doesn't mean they're not a "suit".

Talk to them as a business owner.

Tell them how what you will do will help their business.

Draw out a diagram where everyone can clearly see how YOUR art is directly responsible for creating growth or transformation for the brand. And keep that straight line in the diagram as your sole focus in all communication with the client.

Don't be a service provider, or a contractor. Become a partner... A co-conspirator. Their rainmaker.

WHEN YOU'RE A RAINMAKER, YOU NO LONGER FOCUS ON YOUR TALENT, YOU FOCUS ON THE OUTCOMES THAT YOUR TALENT PROVIDE.

Become an artist that brings certain kind of ideas to life. And get known for that technique of yours.

So instead of doing the basics of your craft. Specialize. Switch your focus from doing what everyone else in your field can do... to focusing on a magical aspect of your craft that NO ONE can else can do.

Instead of being a photographer. for example, become a food photographer that specializes in set design of wedding receptions.

Your specialized knowledge makes you in-demand and may give the brand extra credibility, which means more sales.

If you become a credible leading voice in a particular scene, when you get hired, you'll also be bringing the cache and credibility of a whole movement behind you that a brand, if they're smart, will be able to piggyback on.

You stop being a mere commodity to brands when you belong to specialized community that aligns to their values. Like a DJ who is a militant feminist, will be the first choice for the gig with a brand who's aligned with the feminist movement.

Your associations make you priceless.

When you've carefully curated your choices, and made it so that all your body work has one clear message. You've positioned yourself so that any brand that hires you is tapping into that message by association. Your whole story and your message gives an added cache to raise the value of the brand. You become a defacto embassador for the brand because they've chosen you for your beliefs, not just your talent.

Try to work with brands who have the same message as you. That way your story becomes part of their story.

Develop a body of work with such a strong message that anyone you work with will immediately get anointed with some of that credibility. Brands will gladly pay for this added value that goes beyond just skills. When you work with brands who share your message, it lends BOTH OF YOU added credibility and value in the eyes of the community you both serve.

And there's no predetermined price for that.

They'll have to negotiate with you.

All brands depend on media platforms for their marketing and promotion. So if you become an expert at creating for a particular platform, you'll become way more valuable to them than if they handed off creative duties to someone that works in their office. If you know how to make art that ignites the algorithms in flames, and is known to taps into the psychology of a certain platform, you will automatically earn your higher pay grade -- And now the weekend intern is no longer your competition.

But the #1 way to become a rainmaker in todays creative economy. Even if you have no followers, no message and no community...

Your real client is not the brand. Your real client is the brand's customers. Get to know them better than you know your friends. Find out what makes them tick. Cause they're the ones who keep everyone's lights on.

Learn how to create videos that show the product "in action. Learn how to photograph a lookbook for a brand that drives traffic to their website.

Use your talent to create multimedia work that will make people more curious about what the brand is up to.

If it doesn't do that, it doesn't matter how pretty it is or how cool the concept is... You've failed.

The most lucrative way to help a brand make money is to help them tell their stories.

Become a professional FOMO inducer.

Nothing attracts people more to a brand than a story they relate to. And the artists that know how to construct stories for themselves and for others are always the most in demand.

That artist can basically name their price.

Learn this skill and you will help brands connect with their audience. And the better you do your job the more devoted the audience will be. If you're a great storyteller, your art will help the brand gain fans for life.

In marketing speak that equates to lengthening the "lifetime value of their customer" (the amount of money they can hope to make from one customer) to much longer timeframes.

And that is the best rainmaking there is.

Rainmaking with yearly dividends.

### 2. How To Make It Rain (Part II)

### “Business art is the step that comes after art. I started as a commercial artist, and I want to finish as a business artist. Being good in business is the most fascinating kind of art. During the hippie era people put down the idea of business. They’d say “money is bad” and “working is bad”. But making money is art, and working is art - and good business is the best art.” Andy Warhol

### "The highest form of art is art that can help people achieve their dreams. Either by inspiring them or moving them into action." Father Bronques

### 3. How To Make It Rain (Part III) - For Photographers & Videographers

A technician tries to negotiate a fee.

Be such a reliable rainmaker that you start working for a percentage of the wealth you'll be creating.

Learn how to make a financial impact on businesses in your town or city with your art.

Figure out can you use video or photography to help your clients succeed.

These are rainmaker videos because they require marketing and storytelling skills that will bring in new customers for a business.

Always know the purpose of why you're creating the video. Have a strategy. Don't let the company "wing it".

Create videos that hook people right away and cut through all the noise that's out there right now.

### 3. How To Make It Rain (Part III) - For Photographers & Videographers

### 1. Master your craft.

### 2. Immerse yourself in the mindset of a rainmaker by re-readingHow To Make It Rain (Part II).

### 3. Figure out where YOUR particular skillset and art fits into the art and science of marketing. How will your art help a brand bringing customers in and make them want to pay for products?

## 3 types of videos every business out there needs in order to grow:

## 1. A Story Video: a 2 minute video that showcases the brand to get people excited about it and keep them relevant.

## 2. A Testimonial video: A video showing people who love the brand. People trust other people like them.

## 3. A Sales video (you sell things that help people): A video that shows how the brands product improves their audience's life. Show the product in action.

##### Post a comment

### 🔑 4. No Polaris Star, No Progress

The Polaris Star is the brightest star in a constellation.

It is the guiding star.

When you're lost, it gives you direction.

You need to have one when you're trying to accomplish anything worthwhile.

Are you good?

Are you thriving?

Or does it sometimes feel like you're on the verge of emotional and creative bankruptcy?

Bankruptcy is when you don't have enough resources to meet your needs.

A sure sign is... You feel overwhelmed.

Another sign is... You don't know what to do because there's too many options.

"You've been cursed with too many talents," you'll say.

"You've been cursed with the inability to choose," I say.

Maybe it's time to focus?

The real epidemic facing creatives today is:not being able to decide what they should focus on.

That's why people have trouble picking their message.

And then when they're out in the real world, they can't pick their Polaris Star either.

If you know your message, then you already know your Polaris Star. RUN WITH IT!

But if you don't know your message, then you need to at least figure out your Polaris Star.

People will sometimes say, "Oh, you mean I need to know my goal?"

No, your Polaris Star is not your "goal".

And it’s that clarity of vision that GIVES BIRTH to what your goals should be.

Decision making becomes easy. You know what to say yes to… And what to refuse.

Knowing your Polaris Star enables you to turn off the noise, ignore the distractions, and ward off the temptation to settle for less. Having your Polaris Star light the way for you is your only chance at developing a resolve that is infinitely sustainable.

People will say “be authentic”. Or “speak your truth”.

But how do you know what that is if you have nothing to measure it against?

When you have a Polaris star you won’t measure "authenticity" and "truth" against your current feelings and moods... You will measure them against the vision of who you truly want to become.

Now, instead of pushing your way through obstacles, you’re pulled forward to your destiny.

Now, instead of being wishy-washy about the future-- it's so clear you can taste it. That's when people will want to attach themselves to your wagon. The world will HELP YOU succeed. But that will only happen when you have a clear vision of where you're headed. If YOU can't see it, neither will we.

I see so many people sawing the very branch that they're sitting on by chasing too many goals at the same time.

Diversification is a strategy that people use when they don’t know what they’re doing. They thin out their resources because they have FOMO.

You’re scared because you don’t know what will work. But you'll never know what works until you focus on one thing.

Yes, even if it fails.

Find out that it's the "wrong thing" faster. And then switch to the winner. In silicon valley they call it "failing fast".

Don't be stuck in the middle for the rest of your life... And then regret.

As a normal human being it’s essential to be well rounded, yes... Complex, yes... Nuanced, yes.

But being the G.O.A.T. is not being a "normal human being".

Being the G.O.A.T means throwing out "well-rounded" for now.

You simplify your existence so that everything revolves around ONE goal.

You refuse to dilute your efforts.

Aaron Z emailed me this week:

"Bronques, I might have 3 messages. Lol. Is that allowed?"

Aaron has been working hard.

But everyone needs someone in their corner.

This was my reply:

Anything is allowed. There are no rules. But success leaves clues:

If you want to be one of the people that has an impact on our culture or society at large... Then you'll need a Polaris Star.

If you're trying to make an impact, narrow down your focus until you've found that ONE thing that you can ride with for the next few years...

I'm not saying this is the only path.

It's just the FASTEST path.

If you want to be the G.O.A.T. ... First be "Michael Jordan the basketball player" before you try your hand at being "Michael Jordan the baseball player". (Yes, that actually happened... But not until he was G.O.A.T -- He gets it.)

Omar Z answered this when I asked him what his career aspiration was:

"Writing poetry, vlogging, and making short films."

Pick a lane, bro.

And don't try to cheat.

A Polaris Star isn't a constellation.

Don't go trying to make what should be ONE GOAL, multi-hyphenated.

Don’t scatter your forces.

No, make it so simple that even a child could understand.

"My goal is to publish a book of poetry by the end of the year."

Take Rupi Kaur for example. She writes poetry just like Omar Z. She also has other talents just like Omar Z. One of those talents is illustration. She's been drawing since she was 5. If you've ever read interviews with her, you'll know that she cherishes illustration. But being a published poet was her Polaris Star. So her drawings became a tool in service to that goal. She picked her one thing and made it #1. And she succeeded at lightning speed.

When will you do the same?

Think about it. Why have you been so afraid of commitment?

Do you feel like you're gonna miss out on something?

Or is it because having only one thing seems too boring?

Or because having laser type focus will mean that you "have no life"?

The reality I'm trying to convey to you before it's too late is:

You miss out on EVERYTHING when you DON'T choose.

When you stay on the surface...

That's what the normals do.

Artists...? They go deep.

Draw your line in the sand.

Put your stake in the ground.

You need to change your diet from your current "emotion-du-jour"...

Into... holding one thought, one goal, one outcome in your mind for the next 9 months.

Once you penetrate, you can deviate.

But until then, be a laser beam.

People may appear supportive when they tell you you can “do it all”. And they may very well be good-intentioned... But those people are doing you the most harm.

The people with your best interest in mind are those who see your strengths, whatever they are and get you to double down on them.

Every time you try to go astray, they remind you to focus.

You only get that kind of advice from people who have been there.

You have to have discipline if you want to achieve your goals.

But the discipline isn’t "doing what must be done".

The discipline is ignoring every other thing trying to get a piece of you.

When Steve Jobs came back to Apple in 1993 (after being kicked out in 1985), the company was on the verge of bankruptcy.

How did he turn things around?

He reduced the number of products they were selling from 350 individual products to a lean 10.

He gave the company their Polaris Star.

Everything that's not the main thing is just a hobby or a distraction.

You can fool yourself --and your uncle at Thanksgiving-- that you can "do it all".

But you can’t fool history.

No one ever became the G.O.A.T. by doing it all. Every example of greatness before us started by doing one thing and excelling at it, and only then expanding.

"But Father Bronques, it's so haaaaard."

I know. Focusing on one thing is not human nature.

Our nature is to go towards the path of least resistance.

Everyone wants to express their "whole self". Whatever that means.

But the passage to that endpoint is the same for all of those who are your heroes.

You must train yourself to become something specific before becoming the full-fledged person you’re destined to flourish into afterward.

The alternative path?

Reject discipline... Be “everything” and do everything... And end up resembling every other dull rock on the edge of the beach.

The choice is yours.

You wanna be a multi-hyphenate?

Jumping between differing art forms?

That won't work. But if you absolutely NEED to split your brain... Then at least be the kind of multi-hyphenate that will help your cause:

Act like an artist and also be your own manager.

Split your time between making your art and opening doors for yourself.

But whatever you do... Make one the servant of the other. You can't serve two masters.

Decide what your walking towards, and you wake up calm every day and follow it.

There won't need to be stress in it.

Because you'll know what you’re doing.

You'll know where you’re going.

You'll stopyearning, and beingover-emotional about results.

You stop feeling pressured by your lack of attainment. Because you'll always see the target in your mind.

Put that one thought in your head at the beginning of the day and hold it there all day at the exclusion of all other thoughts.

The thought you put there becomes your Polaris Star.

It guides your actions.

Your life then becomes the result of those movies you chose to play inside your head.

If you had continued having random thoughts all day, then you'd get a random life.

But now that you have a "bright and loud re-run of your end goal" playing over and over in your head... It eventually becomes true.

(Good… Or bad btw)

No amount of energy spent will get you far if you don’t clearly see where you want to go.

The clearer you see, the faster you arrive.

That's why you should choose your thoughts with as much care as you choose what movies you watch, what clothes you wear, and what you have for dinner.

Before you say, "But, I can't CHOOSE my thoughts. They appear randomly." Let me remind you... Of course they would. Because you’ve never trained your mind to do otherwise. What do you expect?

Minds need to be trained, just like our bodies do.

But it takes practice to focus like a champion.

Why should you have anything less?

P.S. If you need help finding your Polaris Star... Email me right now and ask for the 'Polaris Star Formula Emails'-- and I'll hook you up.

## I keep giving you the solution... And you keep avoiding the truth.

## If you respect your art... Make a commitment to ONE thing for the next few years so that the world can conspire to help you achieve it.

### 5. The Creativity / Work Ethic Hierarchy

When everyone around you wants to be supportive even if it means lying to your face...

Someone has to be truthful.

Someone has to be blunt.

Understand this:

Not everybody should be trying to make art their career.

I analyzed over 80 artists that I’ve worked with over the last 5 years and I came up with a simple Creativity / Work Ethic hierarchy.

1. You’re gifted and super-disciplined.

2. You’re modestly talented but you can outwork everybody.

3. You’re gifted but you're lazy.

4. You’re modestly talented but you have no work ethic.

It's not about IF they'll make it. It's about WHEN.

This is where most creatives could easily fit in. The tragedy is that they think they're a #2, when they're really a #4. They don't know the meaning of real work. They clock it in. They don't sacrifice. Only when they're surrounded by people who are ready to kill for their goals... Starve for their goals... Lose sleep for their goals... End relationships for their goals... Do they realize: "Oh, maybe I need to go harder."

I've known so many talented people that "coulda-woulda-shoulda"... But they didn't. And it was always for the same reason. They never put in the work. A genius that doesn't fulfill their potential? Not cute.

Modestly talented means you're still blending in with the masses. But without work no one will have any incentive to help you.

You have to be honest with yourself starting today.

Do you want this to be a hobby or a career?

There's no amount of talent that will allow you to bypass the tremendous work it takes.

Where do you fit in on the Work Ethic Hierarchy?

If you're not sure... Find someone you trust to tell you the truth.

From now on you should make "seeking the truth about your work" your #1 priority.

Because 'The Book Of Money' is no longer concerned about if people LIKE what you do.

Liking something is easy.

Now it's about... Are they willing to pay for it?

### 6. Identity, Vision, & Message

Laura's (MS student) interpretation of the 3 levels of artistry.@salomea.synthesis

What you're about to read will either

1. confirm what you already know, or…

2. remind you of what you forgot, or...

3. make you finally face the truth, or...

4. piss you off.

Indeed, this module will be the opposite of what "wellness coaches" on social media tell you.

Things like...

"If your art is amazing and you believe in yourself, you'll succeed."

"Perseverance is what all successful artists have in common."

And while it may feel good to hear these "false supportive" messages. They also guarantee a crash when you're faced with reality sooner or later.

First, understand. Not everyone making art is trying to make it as a capital 'A' Artist.

You can be a "mixing engineer", minding your own business, and still put food on the table.

And you can make "nice paintings" for people to decorate their homes— and make a decent living.

Or you can even sing in a cover band. Or tour with a famous singer— And make some decent bread and be happy.

And you can take photos or videos for brands— And get compensated rather well for your visual services.

Yes, yes. You can be great at your craft and get paid good money.

You can be a "creative commodity"… (AKA a "craftsperson")... And still bring home the bacon.

But to become a bonafide ARTIST in the new creative economy, you'll need more than desire and "belief in yourself".

You'll need to put yourself out there in a way that most creatives haven't commited to yet.

You'll need:

Fight me all you want...

And give me all the examples of celebrities getting away with less to prove your point...

But I'm only telling you this straight because I don't want you to treat your career like it's a lottery ticket.

And I'm not saying that having them all guarantees that your art will connect with the masses. Or that you will become a millionaire.

But you need to have these 3 things to have a chance.

Without them? No one will pay you any mind (as an ARTIST anyway). And besides, why should they? Do YOU pay attention to artists without an identity, vision, or message?

Ok, ok... You can get away with not KNOWING your message yet. Sometimes it does take time to discover how to express the invisible.

(But please. Figure it out soon. Because having a clear message is what will give you the power to have the biggest positive impact on people's lives.)

But no artistic vision? No one's gonna go for that.

Your artistic vision is what makes people wanna see what you do next.

And having no artistic identity? No one's gonna go for that.

You need a vibe that you can call your own.

I almost can't believe we're still having this conversation today. But false prophets have gone viral.

Someone has to have the courage to draw a line in the sand.

So here goes...

An artist is not a craftsperson.

An artist is not a commodity.

You can't replace an artist with "the faceless and the nameless".

Once you enter this new creative economy, you have to decide where you stand.

Do you stand among artists?

Or do you stand among the technicians?

Will you be working with people interested in your identity, vision, and message?

Or people who want "someone who can do it fast, and for the least amount of money".

If you want clients, managers, galleries, gatekeepers and other artists to take you seriously as an artist... Set yourself apart immediately.

Have you found a new way to communicate in your art form? Can people tell your art apart from the masses? Do you have a name for your style? Are people starting to copy you?

When you look at your body of work, is it cohesive? Is it saying something? Does it all seem to be a part of the same narrative? Are you building a world?

Is there a specific community that your art speaks to? Are you directly or indirectly helping to create a better world for your people? Are you giving them hope with your art? Are you opening up doors for people who look like you?

Have you been thinking about it?

Have you been acting on it?
