### 7. Master Your Book Ends

Time management is your biggest challenge.

But I don't blame you.

I blame society.

Because society has labeled artists with a certain type of behavior... And artists bought into it.

You're often late... You wait for inspiration to strike... You're moodier than 9 to 5ers... You're an over-thinker... You're a loner...

You do all the things that society thinks constitute "artist behavior".

"Artist behavior" may help you get an emo girlfriend or boyfriend... But it won't help you be creative.

If you want to maximize your potential and achieve "flow", you need to stop seeing yourself how society sees you.

Don't let them brand you an "artist". (Especially when the normals are using "artist" as a dismissal.)

When you're in creation mode, you need to see yourself asan athlete.

Watch any of those Nike ads with sports figures. They could work just as well with a photographer, a writer, a painter, a designer, a hairdresser, or a musician...

Being creative requires just as much discipline as sports does. Expecially when you're on the path to excellence.

It requires FOCUS to become the G.O.A.T at anything.

Every day for us on this journey is "do or die".

But you'll need to master your TIME if you want to achieve this high level of athletic discipline.

And this is only possible when you...

What you do in the morning.

What you do at night.

Always start here.

Especially if you sacrifice large chunks of time to a day job...

Especially if you aren't ready for a full-on God Momentum yet...

Master your book-ends.

Your mornings and your evenings.

That way anything that happens in-between can never bring you down.

First, let's talk about thesecond most (yes, second)crucial part of your day:

Every athlete has A DAILY PRACTICE.

A DAILY PRACTICE is what keeps your subconscious in the zone even when you're doing life's daily chores later... Or even if you have to go to a shitty day job afterward... Or when your out-of-town family takes over your apartment for the weekend.

To develop a morning practice:

Pick ONE thing that you can do every morning WITHOUT FAIL.

Something that will elevate your creative game.

Something where you can see progress.

• Learn a new technique for your craft and practice applying it for 30 minutes.

• Practice an instrument

• Try to recreate photographs you love for an hour

• Write 'morning pages' (continuous writing without editing for 30 minutes straight) then edit what yesterday's morning pages for 10 minutes

You get it.

Wake up an hour earlier if you have to.

But always, always, always do your DAILY PRACTICE in the morning. (When I was on tour, even though I was doing creative work that I loved, I still woke up to improve my skills-- FOR MYSELF)

This will put your brain in creativity mode.

You will "see" things "different" all day.

If you have a day job, this simple daily action will make it impossible for "the man" to steal your soul.

When you go for your lunch break, do something for 15 minutes related to your creative goals. It can be as simple as continuing to read a biography about an artist you love. Or take pictures intensely for a few minutes with a point and shoot or your phone.

This constant injection of creativity moments in your day will prime you for when you DO get the time to be fully creative later that day. Or on the weekend.

Now it won't feel like you're starting from scratch every time you sit to create.

You will ease into the creative process immediately because in essence, you never left.

Compare this to what happens now:

You're exhausted by sun down... You have to try to rev up your energy, your motivation, or your inspiration to do the things you supposedly love!

Don't beat yourself up. It's not your fault... It's because you haven't mastered your book-ends. Starting with your DAILY PRACTICE.

Having A DAILY PRACTICE is what keeps you in the zone.

It keeps you connected to your art, your eye, your success.

Your morning DAILY PRACTICE can be 30 minutes of... making art.

It can be 30 minutes of... editing art.

It can be 30 minutes of... promoting your art.

But whatever you do... Treat it with the same discipline as an athlete.

Which brings us tothe most essential part of your daythat you must learn to worship:

People think that a successful day starts in the morning.

They'll say things like, "I woke up on the wrong side of the bed."

Or they'll tell you how they need "their morning coffee" to be human.

Honestly, the morning means nothing if you don't master this first:

Plan your day-- the night before.

You can predict how successful your week will be by seeing what you planned (or didn't plan) the night before.

If you don't plan what tomorrow will look like... You're only going to reach a fraction of your potential.

And worst of all: other people will move you around like a pawn on a chessboard.

Your "priorities" will float away like leaves in the wind.

You're reading 'The Book Of Money' now. That's no longer acceptable.

"Plan your day-- the night before."

It only takes 10 minutes— AKA 1% of your day— to do it.

You spend more time than that on Instagram, eagerly rotting your brain.

This action is just as easy to do... Except this action will turn your whole life around:

"Plan your day--- the night before."

Choose something you use in your DAILY PRACTICE (paintbrush, instrument, note pad) and place it next to you on the nightstand... Ready for action.

Make it the first thing you see when you wake up.

Make it the first thing you reach for when you wake up. Not your phone.

Put down ON PAPER the steps you will be taking tomorrow to advance your art.

When you make these thoughts your last ones of the day... You're setting yourself up for success.

You are priming yourself.

Your subconscious will start preparing as you sleep.

No one talks about this because it's not 'sexy'.

In most "success circles", people only talk about their daily routine. They fetishize: "What time do you wake up? etc..."

When the sauce is really, "What is your nightly routine?" "How much sleep do you get?"

Your ego will want to get the better of you.

You'll want to walk around and say "I only need 4 hours of sleep," like you're Gary V.

How many athletes do you know that brag about not needing sleep?

And you're a creative athlete, remember? You need sleep.

Stop acting like "an artist" with all those "artists ups and downs". And all that "artist overthinking".

You're a high-output creative professional.

If the new label doesn't feel comfortable yet, it will start to... After you master your book-ends.

That way, everything that happens in-between can only affect you on that one particular day...

But it will never have any impact on your self-esteem.

Reading is nice. I hope you enjoyed that.

But your life won't change without action.

Don't let this be another thing that you read but fail to apply.

Here are the action steps to take for this module:

### 7. Master Your Book Ends

## Master Your BOOK-ENDS.

## MORNINGS.

## EVENINGS.

## SLEEP.

## ACTION TIME

### 1. WRITE DOWN ONE THING YOU CAN DO EVERY SINGLE DAY WITHOUT FAIL. SOMETHING WHERE YOU CAN SEE PROGRESS / IMPROVEMENT OVER TIME. IT CAN BE SOMETHING THAT TAKES AS LITTLE AS 10-30 MINUTES. WHAT MATTERS IS THAT YOU PICK SOMETHING THAT YOU NEVER HAVE TO MISS A DAY WITH. WHAT IS THE ONE THING THAT IF YOU GOT IT DONE WOULD MAKE THE DAY A GREAT DAY? YOUR DAILY PRACTICE CAN BE AN 30 MINUTES OF... MAKING ART. IT CAN BE 30 MINUTES OF... EDITING ART. IT CAN BE 30 MINUTES OF... PROMOTING YOUR ART.

### 2. TONIGHT... SCHEDULE YOUR DAY TOMORROW. PREPARE EVERYTHING RELATED TO YOUR DAILY PRACTICE SO IT'S WAITING FOR YOU WHEN YOU WAKE UP. TAKE OUT YOUR TOOLS. PUT OUT YOUR CLOTHES. GET YOUR WATER READY. RECHARGE BATTERIES. AND FUCK NO: YOU'RE NOT ALLOWED TO TOUCH YOUR PHONE UNTIL AFTER YOU'VE NURTURED YOUR SOUL. PROGRAM YOUR MIND WITH YOUR CREATIVITY AND FURTHERING YOUR GOALS-- NOT WITH WHAT INSTAGRAM'S ALGORITHM DECIDES TO DISTRACT YOU WITH ON THE FEED.

### 3. TONIGHT (CONTINUED)... WRITE DOWN WHAT YOU WILL DO TOMORROWAFTERWORK. PREPARE YOUR ENVIRONMENT SO THAT EVERYTHING RELATED TO YOUR "AFTER WORK ACTIVITIES" ARE WAITING READY FOR YOU WHEN YOU WALK THROUGH THOSE DOORS. ALSO PLAN TO CREATE YOUR WRITTEN PLAN FOR THE FOLLOWING DAY, JUST LIKE YOU'RE DOING NOW. MAKING TOMORROW'S PLAN IS THE MOST IMPORTANT PART OF YOUR DAY.

### 4. BE RELIGIOUS ABOUT YOUR BOOK ENDS AND YOUR LIFE WILL SPIRAL UPWARDS.

### 8. Your Polaris Star, Your Story & Your Message

There are 3 areas of focus that you need to define if making a career out of your art is important. (More in'The Book Of Money')

Understanding these concepts will give you a framework for your career "problem-solving".

This is the most basic focusing mechanism for every aspiring creative.

You can get a lot done with just this one.

Your Polaris Star is your vision of where you see yourself in the future.

And you articulate it in one sentence.

"I'm an artist with my own art gallery."

"I run a 6-figure t-shirt company."

Some call this a "goal". But it's more than that.

A "goal" is just one of the steps to getting to your Polaris Star.

The Polaris Star is your guiding light. It determines EVERY SINGLE MOVE you do.

It's the vision of your future that will give you the motivation for all your immediate goals.

It's the "new you" that you will become.

All the moves you take going forward... Should be in function of your Polaris Star. Until you become that person.

You decide what to eat, who to hang out with, what kind of entertainment to consume, what clothes you wear, how to celebrate your birthday, what time to wake up... based on your Polaris Star.

A Polaris Star is like a "goal" on steroids.

You have a Polaris Star when you're ready to design your whole life around achieving one thing.

And don't share it with anyone (except the few people who are "in it with you"). Keep it to yourself so you don't dissipate it's psychic energy.

When you think of someone like Jeff Bezos who created Amazon, you don't think of someone with a "goal". That's too weak of a description. Jeff Bezos had a Polaris Star, bro. Steve Jobs had a Polaris Star, babe.

Or when Wayne Gretsky's family made all their daily activities, including meals, revolve around Wayne's practice and game schedule when he was a teenager... The Gretsky family had a Polaris Star.

Or Lady Gaga, who had a childhood and adolescence of obsessive music-making until the inevitable happened... She had a Polaris Star.

A Polaris Star will tell you what opportunities are right and which ones are wrong. It'll tell you what to say "yes" to... And what to gracefully ignore.

While everyone is pushing their way through life... Having a Polaris Star will pull you forward even when you're having doubts or depressed.

So, yeah... Your girlfriend in Miami? The one who wants to start an online bikini brand next year... Or your uncle who wants to open a Lebanese restaurant with his high-school buddy who cooks real good...?

They... They have "goals".

If I can go to your IG, and I can't tell what you're "about". You don't have a Polaris Star yet.

If I can have a 1-hour conversation with you and none of the topics we talk about are ever related to your "goals"... Then your life isn't governed by a Polaris Star yet.

Before you release anything out into this noisy, competitive world... Ask yourself:

"Why should anyone give a fuck about what I do or have to say?"

The answer to that question, if you can answer it, is called "your story".

People don't need to know where you were born or what school you went to (unless those things are extraordinary). They want to know what makes you unique or exciting. Like Rupi Kaur fighting and winning against Instagram. Like, a sex tape. Like, being the first of your gender/race to break a glass ceiling. Like, the revolutionary community you're a part of. Like, the heartbreaking / amazing / first-time / unusual event that inspired your work.

What's your ANGLE?

Eventually, your success itself becomes your story. But until then...

Until you get a PR person, to do it all for you...

You have to think like a PR person.

What makes what you're releasing NEWSWORTHY today?

Your friends, family, and current fans already have a story in their mind about you. So when you release something new, they're automatically interested.

They know you.

But if you want to attract NEW people to check your work out... You'll need a powerful story to reel them in.

You know those little placards at museums that describe what an artwork is all about?

You know how... When you read those little descriptions, they give you a whole new perspective on the art?

You know how... When you talk about it later, that's what you tell people?

You need one of those for yourself.

Your story generates curiosity about you. And that it’s that curiosity makes people want to check you out. Think of any time you ever were compelled to check out someone’s art. What did you hear that made you follow through? A story. Always a story.

The difference between a photographer who gets paid 400$ a day and another that gets paid 5000$ a day isn't the photographic quality.

It's that... One of them has a story... And the other does not.

Pre-frame your art (give your audience context) before people experience it by making sure people know your story.

Capture people's attention with a hook.

Your Polaris Star is for you. But your message is for THEM.

Your message is... Your artistic vision articulated to the audience that it's intended for. (Pied Piper style).

Your message is... The emotional component of your work that resonates with your audience long after the individual work is being experienced.

Your message is... The type of communication that places your art in the context of an audience and a culture.

It is all three of these things at the same time.

So maybe...

You started with a loose set of goals.

Then those goals materialized into a powerful Polaris Star. (That's probably around the time you joined The Mystery School. You felt something brewing in your soul.)

But then you have to decide:

WHAT THE FUCK AM I TRYING TO SAY WITH MY ART? WHAT AM I TRYING TO COMMUNICATE WITH THE WORLD. WHERE AM I TRYING TO TAKE MY AUDIENCE TO?

You need to know this.

It's the first question they'll ask you in an interview (or at Thanksgiving dinner).

If the answer is vague, you'll get a lukewarm reaction.

If the answer is fire, they won't be able to get it out of their mind for a week. They'll also wanna help you spread your message even though you never asked.

Knowing your message is so important that I dedicated'The Book Of Purpose', to it. So go there now if you're weak in this area.

But everyone is different.

Some people know their message before they even start making art. But what they don't know is what art form to dedicate their energy to, to communicate it. Those creatives are looking for their Polaris Star.

Others know their Polaris Star and their message. But once they decide to share something to the public, no-one seems to be paying attention long enough to experience the art. They're not connecting. These people need to define their story.

Some people have a great message and a remarkable story. But because they have no Polaris Star, nothing ever happens for them. They're slacking, unmotivated or cursed with talent that has made them lazy

Operate on all 3 gears.

Your Story is your hook. Your Message is for your audience. And Your Polaris Star is for yourself.

If you’re lucky, your story, your message and your Polaris Star will become your greatest work of art.

### 8. Your Polaris Star, Your Story & Your Message

## YOUR POLARIS STAR

## YOUR STORY

### YOUR STORY IS WHAT PEOPLE WILL SAY TO OTHER PEOPLE ABOUT YOU WHEN YOU'RE NOT AROUND.

## YOUR MESSAGE

### 9. Do You Have A Career... Or A Hobby?

Oh. You released your new project this week?

You launched a new product on your Shopify website?

How can you tell the difference between someone who's treating their art like a burgeoning career and... someone who's treating it like a hobby?

Ask them this one question:

When I say new fans, I'm not just talking about the people who will buy it (the consumers).

I'm also talking about the fans who hold powerful positions in the world that can help you get your vision to even more people.

No, "putting it out there" and seeing what sticks is not a "plan".

When you release a new song, a new book, a new product for your Shopify store, a new video, a new show... You need a story to make people care about it.

If you don't have a message... Find a unique angle to make your new project stand out from all the rest.

Unless you have a PR team, a distributor, a thirsty fanbase, and a "product" that is so unique and singular that it opens doors as soon as people experience it...

You'll need a story.

"My art is 'unique'." Or "It's so pretty." Or "I'm awesome." 😂

That's not a story.

Taking an hour or two to figure your story will improve the life expectancy of your project.

In other words... You need to be your own PR person until you can afford one.

When I say what's your story, I mean:

What would you want your publicist to say to introduce you to the world.

What's an unforgettable, catchy, "can't scroll past" story of your career or life.

Where an artist comes from (physically, psychologically, or both) is just as important as the art itself.

That’s the part fans connect to.

What's your origin story?

As stated in'Your Polaris Star, Your Story & Your Message:'"Your story generates curiosity about you. And that it’s that curiosity makes people want to check you out. Think of any time you ever were compelled to check out someone’s art. What did you hear that made you follow through? A story. Always a story."

So ask yourself these hard questions:

WRITE IT DOWN.

WRITE IT DOWN.

WRITE IT DOWN.

Don't release for vanity.

Don't release for validation.

Don't throw your artwork into a black hole of indifference.

'Cause without a story, guess what? That's what you're doing.

Don't make it so your work is fighting on life-support after 'Week One'.

'Cause without a plan, guess what? That's what you're doing.

Week One is always epic.

Your friends and family congratulate you on your new whatever.

Your current fans re-post. You re-post their re-posts.

It's a dream.

You feel good until the truth settles in:

Nothing changed.

You realize that all that 'Week One' love is not enough to sustain a career.

You smoke-screened yourself into thinking something important was going on with a currency of likes and shares.

The real question you should have been asking yourself before you launched your "one-week-long campaign" is:

WRITE IT DOWN.

The other real question is:

WRITE IT DOWN.

The other, other real question is:

WRITE IT ALL DOWN!

That's what you need to figure out NOW... BEFORE you release anything. Figure out your game plan for what you will do 2 weeks later. 1 month later. 3 months later. Create a strategy for each time frame.

Don't blow your whole load in the first week.

Unknown musicians shouldn't promote themselves the same way as established musicians do.

Unknown musicians have to stand out.

LINKTREE was cute until everyone started using it. Now our eyes tune it out. Oh sure, I'll take a quick listen to your song or whatever. But you would have made more of an impact on me if I landed on a page that gave me context into what you're about. A page that would influence how I perceive the music when I finally hear it.

LINKTREE deflates your audience by showing them you're playing the same game as everyone else. "I have new music. Listen to it."

Anything that "everyone" is doing... Should immediately be questioned.

Study what everyone else is doing and find a way to do the opposite.

Musicians that use LINKTREE instead of capturing email (or any other relationship building landing page) reveal something fundamental about themselves:

They're afraid.

They don't have the confidence that they can hold anyone's attention.

They think they need to give people a million options-- So they don't "lose them".

Every step in the journey of someone comes in contact with your art should be obsessed over and scrutinized.

UsingLINKTREEas your first point of contact signals to the world that you don't have a strong vision that can lead us down a journey of your own making.

What I'm suggesting will take more thought, perhaps. It requires as much thought as the music itself. But at least when you're done, you'll know you're not going through the motions.

And later, it might be what OTHER PEOPLE copy.

Stop giving people choices.

Stop making it so easy to discard you in the pile with everyone else.

Be more confrontational. Not in a pushy way. But in a way where it shows that you believe in what you're sharing.

LINKTREE is not an experience. It's a transaction.

Instead... Trade their email address for exclusive access to your new art AND your beautiful mind.

Or design a rabbit hole of a website that takes them through your story and that END with a LINKTREE (after you got their email along the way). When they listen to your music after this rabbit hole, you're POISED to move their soul and emotions.

Stop playing the "Here's my music. Listen to it." game.

It's not like Spotify's 0.00331% royalty rate is gonna pay your bills any time soon anyway.

But when you start honoring REAL relationships with your fans?

Now, THAT might pay the bills one day. (Read this classic 1,000 fans manifesto for the math.) ---LINK OUT!!!!!!!!

Take the reins. Direct how people should experience your art.

Until you have the money to promote and market, your biggest asset is the relationship you nurture your fans.

Control that experience to the finest detail.

And get their fucking email. Jeez.

If someone "signed you" right now, what would it mean without fans? Oh, they're going to help you get fans? You think this is the 90s? This is the era of nurturing fan relationships. Stop waiting for easy street.

### 9. Do You Have A Career... Or A Hobby?

## If you build it, they will NOT come. You need a plan for what to do after you build it.

### "What are you doing to make NEW fans discover your work?"

### What are you doing to make NEW gatekeeper fans discover your work?

### Don't put anything out into the world without a story.

### Why is my new project vital to the world right now?

### What's the cool story behind it that will pique everyone's interest?

### What's the cool story about ME (related to the work) that will pique everyone's interest?

## Getting Past The Dreaded 'Week One Syndrome'

### What can I do that will attract the people this was made for-- That don't know me yet?

### What am I creating that's so riveting that it would make someone hold their pee because they want to know more?

### What am I going to do to keep my project relevant 2 weeks later when the "shiny new object" cycle has evaporated?

## SPECIAL NOTE FOR MUSICIANS:

### Invite people to join you on an adventure instead. That should be the sole purpose of any link you send anyone to. To create an experience for them.

## Until you have a predictable way of attracting new people to your art, you don't have a career... You have a hobby.

### 10. Why You Need To Be "Audience Obsessed" From Now On

I can make a better burger than McDonald's can.

I'm serious. Ask any of my friends.

Maybe you have the same rep among your crew too?

So how come we're not making McDonald's kind of money for OUR burgers?

For the same reason some talented artists will continue to go unrecognized:

Because there is no effort being made to continuously expand our audience.

"Build it, and they will come" is a lie they tell you when you're starting out... To get you motivated.

But if you spend the next three months working on your masterpiece and you never take the steps necessary to nurture your audience...

You will release your art to the sound of crickets.

Your family and your friends might 'repost' or 'retweet' your new project. And you'll see some of the people you've collected, almost by mistake, on social media over the years do the same. But all that 'action' will only satisfy your vanity for a minute until you realize that nothing has changed. You still don't have a career.

Why? You've been focused on making art -- and ignoring the most essential part of your business. Growing your fan base.

And I know why.

Because the answers aren't jumping out at you after 5 minutes of thinking about it... So you say it's not "your thing". You know you need to do it, but don't know HOW to promote yourself. Maybe you've even convinced yourself that self-promotion is sleazy. Or you think it's gross and that you're above it.

But why would you expect this piece of the puzzle to come naturally to you? Self-promotion is just as creative as making art is. It requires practice too. And sometimes, you have to wait a few days before you get that genius idea.

But you'll never get there if audience growth doesn't start to take more real-estate in your brain. And in your heart.

An artist can't sit in their "ivory tower" all day... Only to descend with their masterpiece every few years... And expect the "peasants" to line up for miles in anticipation.

Not even Drake does that.

A new artist needs to be growing their audience WHILE they're working on their masterpiece.

It's your JOB.

You need to be audience obsessed.

The most respectful thing you can do for your art is to create a foundation for it where your audience ANTICIPATES it's arrival.

And you do this by communicating with them with consistency. Fans are your family. You don't get to go away for 6 months and ignore your Instagram.

The 30,000 streams a day...

The viral video on TikTok...

People reposting your last project...

They're all giving you a false sense of security.

None of those things means you have a career.

You only have a career when people are lining up to pay for your work.

Nurturing and growing an audience will give you that career.

You want them to be obsessed with you?

Be obsessed with THEM.

If "being an artist" is where you want your money to come from... Then isn't it time you start focusing on the people who will be giving you that money?

You need to become "audience obsessed".

"Audience Obsessed" is when you switch from making "the best art possible"... To making "the best art possible for your fans".

Your fans are your boss.

That's why you can't only think of them when you're about to drop something.

If anything... That's rude.

They have to be on your mind ALL the time.

Especially when you're in your dungeon creating.

You need to find ways to keep "your people" entertained. That way other people looking in on the fun will want to join in too.

You need to be obsessively growing that fan base.

Not just 3 weeks before you're dropping something!

If you don't do it now, you'll only end up doing it later... When you go work as an assistant for an artist who IS taking their audience growth seriously. <kicking yourself when you see how systematic it all is>

That's why once you decide you want to make this your breadwinner... You can't only be "all about the art".

You need to treat it like 'Business Art'. That's what Warhol used to call it. And Warhol is as 'about the art' as you can get.

And what is Business Art 101?

Supply AND demand.

For all your life you've been 90% focused on creating "supply" (your art). But you've only been 10% focused on creating the demand (nurturing and growing your audience).

Why would you give your art those terrible odds?

Posting about your new release on IG story isn't an artist creating a demand. That's just an artist milking their current audience the same way they see everyone else do it.

Even though in their heart, they know it doesn't feel right.

They haven't EARNED that attention.

Use your creativity to find new strategies to grow that audience.

The keyword in that last sentence is "creativity".

Some strategies may feel like a slog at first, but when they get you momentum, it's funny how fast they become 'fun'.

Some strategies aren't scalable, but they are the basis of what will be your rabid fan base. This foundation will allow for more scalable methods later.

You need to treat marketing, promotion, and sales like they're creative aspects of your business also.

'Cause they are.

And these approaches should be in full bloom all the time. WHILE you're making your art.

And if you play your cards right... All these things you're doing to attract new fans will excite the fans that you already have.

Most artists are on a cycle of:

1. Make stuff for 8 months while they work a day job.

2. Finally, release it and "see if it sticks".

3. A few weeks later, they shrug their shoulders and start thinking about a new project. "This one will be even better!"

That is not a career. That's wishful thinking.

How do artists get known today?

What works better than blogs, press, and even viral content?

Word of mouth.

A friend tells you to check something out and you will. We trust each other 'cause we know everyone else is lying.

And what creates that 'word of mouth'?

- When you collaborate with other artists.

- When you are aligning with other non-artists or brands who have the same message or a similar story as you.

- Influencers that rave about your art creates word of mouth.

- When you do extraordinary unscalable personal things for fans... Or when you stick your neck out to defend your community's opinion... Those create word of mouth.

Your career only grows when people are talking about you.

How do you create that momentum?

Act like THIS every day:

- Make art... Then go promote some merch.

- Make art... Then figure out a cool collaboration you can do with an artist who has a similar audience (it doesn't have to be a bigger artist for this to be mutually beneficial).

- Make art... Then DM your new fans. But wow them by doing it with a voice memo. Also, use some of these casual conversations as market research to find out what attracted them to your community.

- Make art... Then reach out to gatekeepers via email, DM or through 6 degrees of separation. Reach out to any category of human that can get your music in front of fans. Bloggers, publicists, other artists, influencers, dancers...

- Make art... Then make and share a 15-second video or some heartfelt words that tell people a little more of your story and message. Don't overthink it.

- Make art... Then share some behind the scenes of what you're working on with fans to rouse their curiosity.

- Make art... Then test Instagram ads. Use things that have worked organically for ads. Paid advertising is best used for scaling. Once you have a message, story, and art resonating with a small audience, you now have the tools to use paid advertising to scale that resonance intelligently.

- Make art... Then come up with a promo video for stuff you've done in the past (your archives are gold even if you're sick of what you have in there).

- Make art... Then study an artist who's AT YOUR LEVEL that's doing well. Get ideas. Use what you learned THE SAME DAY-- as a test. If it works, add it to this "Make art... THEN" list.

- Make art... then study the ORIGIN STORY of an artist like you who's blown up larger than life. Use what you learned the same day as a test.

- Make art... Then give the audience a micro-dose of your art through social media: twitch, Tiktok, youtube streaming, youtube channel,

- Make art... Then communicate with your fans via email. What will you say? You're doing so many things these days besides just "making art..." that there will be no shortage of things to say. Repeat your message and your story in a new way.

Once you put yourself in motion like this, karmic forces will start working in your favor.

You will start building a vibrant, interactive community.

Before you know it, "people in power" will start to wonder what they're missing out on.

Keep fine-tuning this "Make art... THEN" balance until you make your "project" undeniable.

Make it so that when new people hear about you, they will HAVE to talk about you to their friends.

Your goal is not to get them to like this one piece of art. Or to be there for this "moment" you're having. That doesn't give you a career.

You want true fans.

Fans who don't only care about the art you've made.

But fans who's minds are already in line for the NEXT art you will make in the future.

True fans who are invested in you as an artist

Ok, you're slowly generating word of mouth...

This means that when they hear about you, they'll go check you out.

Either on Instagram (what most people do).

Or your website.

Or they'll Google you.

And when they click... What will they find?

YOU BETTER CONTROL THE NARRATIVE OF WHAT THEY SEE. THIS WILL BE YOUR FIRST IMPRESSION AFTERWORD OF MOUTH HAS PRE-FRAMED YOUR GENIUS. DO NOT LET THEM DOWN!

How do you kill them softly?

Marketing Speak: "Tell your story and spread your message at all your touchpoints."

All your touchpoints should be:

You at your most undeniable.

You at your most irreplaceable.

The moment people land on your media, they're going to make a quick judgment. Followed by a quick decision.

In under a second, they will decide yay or nay. And the only way you can keep them connected is with your story and/or message.

But the best part is... You're not trying to get everyone to love you. So you can be outrageously YOU. The unique creature that will make "your people" will scream YESSSSSSSSSSS to the universe for finding you!

That's why you have to make sure you communicate your story and message immediately. So they know they've found their soulmate artist.

Your story and message is what people will remember.

It's what they'll talk about when they talk about your art to get other people to check you out. The more your story/message resonates, the quicker new people will rush to experience your art for themselves.

Give them something to talk about.

Crafting your story... is part of your art.

Meditate on that fact until it's second nature.

Your art is only ONE aspect of your whole package. Your art isn't only whatever you finished in the studio. YOU are also the work of art.

Beyoncé taught you that.

Basquiat taught you that.

Rihanna continues to teach you that.

You should have a master's degree in crafting your story after watching Drake do it for the past decade.

So tell me... When will you act on these lessons?

Craft your story. Or your brand. Or your persona. Whatever you want to call it.

With everything you release out into the world.

Write the script for the movie that leads people to your work.

You don't need to overthink it.

Listen to how people already talk about you. There may be clues there. All you have to do is amplify it.

Sometimes the story/message is as simple as "She is the new Enya." Or "If Nick Cave was a girl..." And if people keep hearing that about you... that'll be enough for Enya or Nick Cave fans to get curious and find out for themselves if it's true. That's how some people got into Weyes Blood, for example.

You have to reinforce your story and message everywhere your art exists online.

When those fans from the example above go to Weyes Blood's website or Instagram and see ethereal and dark imagery... They will continue exploring. But if they landed on bright colors and a cheesy smiling "LA influencer" looking girl, they'd exit out of there as fast as possible.

Notice how all of this may be happening, and they STILL may not have experienced the art yet. But that's ok. It's setting everything up so that WHEN the art delivers... That persona will be a fan for life.

"Creating demand" is about giving people who discovered you compelling reasons to keep exploring your work more deeply. And then share it with others.

It doesn't stop at words, pr, slogans, and bios either.

Your visuals have to back up your story and message.

Don't just put up random "nice-looking" promo shots of yourself. I mean, unless you're trying to portray yourself as boring and middle of the road.

Instead, create visuals that are like a movie poster for your story and for your message. Visuals that sell the particular story and message that you're sharing. (I don't mean your photos need to look like an actual movie poster-- Just make them tell a story.)

Your message and story is how you get new fans excited. It's how you get the attention of gatekeepers. Often these elements will be their first exposure to you before they get to experience your art.

Yes, through simple words.

If those words are enticing, it will pique their interest to make them want to experience your art.

Giving people exposure to your story and message before they witness the art is called "pre-framing". Make sure the "pre-framing" is doing a good job.

Word of mouth is the ultimate "pre-frame".

And once they arrive at one of your touchpoints...

Get their fucking email.

That way, no matter what platforms you move to, you can always bring your whole community of fans with you.

Know the answers to these four questions like the back of your hand.

Ensure that all your "touchpoints" answer these questions right away so they get your "vibe".

1. What's your name?

You think I'm joking? People fuck this up all the time. Usually, because they're shy. Who are you referred to as? Are you referred as a your GIVEN name, a PSEUDONYM, a BAND name, or a COLLECTIVE? Figure it out, and don't stray from it. It needs to be the same for everyone.

Everything else you share is what will give your chosen name "color". These are the things that will make your name memorable.

2. Why should we care about your art? What's your message? What do you stand for?

Babe, there's so much stuff out there... Seriously, tell them only about the things that make YOU so unique? If you haven't got this figured out yet... Do 'The Drill Down Method' ASAP. Not knowing this stuff is hurting you.

IT'S TIME TO MAKE YOURSELF IMPOSSIBLE TO IGNORE

3. Where do you come from?

As soon as people are interested in your art, they will want to know where you come from. That's just facts.

And like your "name", you need a firm answer that never fluctuates.

Either give them the truthful roots if that fits with your image...

Or give them mythology, if THAT'S your thing...

Again, be definitive about this. Don't give different people different stories.

Give them a powerful answer that reinforces your art, your story, and the message.

Everything that comes out of your mouth should reinforce your art, your story, and your message.

4. Who are my fans?

You're creating a world. And every world needs inhabitants to stay alive.

Your story and message is what bring new inhabitants to the world you have constructed with your art.

But who are those people? Define them.

How are you helping them cope with the world?

Where do members of this community, the ones who need you the most, hang out?

You need to know these things so you can find the rest of them and bring them into your world too.

And once they're in your world. Keep them fed.

Keep them entertained.

### 10. Why You Need To Be "Audience Obsessed" From Now On

## WHAT PSYCHOTIC BEHAVIOR AM I SUGGESTING THAT YOU IMMEDIATELY START ENGAGING IN?

### 11. How To Promote Your Art Without Feeling Gross About It

Here is the audio too:

So here's a simple formula. For every hour that you spend making art, you should put aside another hour to promote it. OR at least an hour trying to find the person who can help promote it for you.

Art is about communication. So when you don't promote your art, you're not finishing what you started. You should be your own number one fan and be relentlessly sharing your new magical concoction.

Like. You have an email list right? But what use is your email list if you're never gonna use it?

And your excuse it... You're afraid that people will get sick of hearing from you? Do you get sick of hearing from your favorite artists?

FRIENDZONED

To me it's just like when you’re afraid to making a move with a girl you like. Even though she's giving you all the signs. You know what's gonna happen right? You're gonna get friend-zoned. You’re gonna get “friend-zoned” with your own art. All because... You didn’t want to push too hard. All Because basically you’re chicken shit. Maybe your fans had a deep ass crush on you at one point but... you never made a move… So now you’ve kinda lost your edge. The other boy came in and stole your spot. Maybe he’s not "good for her", but at least he’s not afraid to tell her what he wants. That boy will tell it like it is. He wants more than “just talking”. He wants love. He wants a relationship. What do you want? You're worried about being nice. Stop being “nice” when your fans give you all the openings. Make a move. Don’t be friend zoned by never bringing up that you do this for a living. You can’t hang out with a girl for 3 months like you're friends and one day just go to kiss her out of the blue. You gotta tell her every day that you love her and what your intentions are. Let people know that you’re selling your art... or your services or whatever. Make it clear every step of the way. Otherwise eventually the world won't "see you that way" anymore. They'll move on. Because now they see you as a "9 to 5er" instead of an artist, a "lifer".

Stop acting like your art is worthless... when it’s actually priceless. Don’t let them hang it on their walls for free. You know what I'm sayin'? Your art is valueable. but you treat it like it belongs in a bargain bin. So then of course... Others do the same.

Posting once on social media about your art isn't called "promotion". That's just called "checking a box". Where's your passion?

Where do you start? This might help.

You have to ask yourself one little question. Your art... What does it cure?

If you don’t feel like your art is the cure for someone’s affliction then of course you'll never be able to sell it. "What affliction is your art a cure for?" Will it make people laugh? Will it make them want to dance? Will it make them less lonely? Will it empower them by expanding their thinking? Will it make them see themselves in a new way Figure that out. Make your art the pill... for someone else's ills.

And once you’ve identified what your art is the cure for... that sentence you came up with will be your “pitch”. Like... I wrote something to help cure loneliness/I think this video I made is pretty funny you should watch it, it might brighten your day/ or "This is my most introspective song ever... can I send it to you?"

YOU HAVE TO PRACTICE MAKING NOISE

Being an artist isn't just about practicing your guitar or learning about cool photographic lighting... You need to practice sharing your work. Like every day of your career.

If you don't practice promoting yourself then when you'll be faced with an opportunity that can change your life you probably won't be ready. When the person that can catapult your career to new heights will walk in the room... That's not the day that you're gonna suddenly be "not shy". You won't know how to do it. You won't know what to say.

The kind of practice I'm telling you to engage in is what will make you certain that when you get presented with an opportunity one day that really matters... YOU DON'T CHOKE.

WHY NO ONE ELSE CAN DO IT FOR YOU

Often people tell me... as their main excuse for not promoting themselves... is that they're just waiting to get a manager for that.

But my question is always. And how exactly are you gonna get a manager if you don't promote yourself?

But you know why you're using this excuse?

People will do anything to not talk to other people. Even hurt themselves. Do you know why artists hate to promote their work? Because it’s the one time that they have to leave the nest. It’s the one time they have to get truly uncomfortable. They will do the least amount necessary just so that they can say they did something today. That’s the moment when we learn as the audience… those of us that are watching closely at least… that the uplifting things that these artists sing about, or that they write about, or that they depict in their photographs... it's just an aesthetic. It's all just for show. They don’t actually live with the courage and conviction they talk about. They’re hobbists. They don’t actually believe that their art holds a cure. They just wanna be famous like that other person from their hometown. ‘Cause when it comes to doing more than the obvious… nah. They’re chicken shit. But let's analyze that for a minute. What exactly are they afraid of? Beating on a few doors? The funniest thing is that when I talk about this... People always feel personally attacked. They literally think I’m talking about them. The truth is... It’s an epidemic. People are making art but they’re ashamed of promoting their work. They accuse the ones out there making noise-- of being too thirsty… But they’re the ones that are thirsty… They're thirsty for approval. That's why they conform. That’s why they don’t go for it. But the best excuse I've heard in my life is also the most tragic. It goes like this: “Do things at your own pace. Build it and they will come.” No babe. The only thing that will come is the realization… uh... when you’re still working a 9-5 a few years later… that those touchy-feely best-self quotes that you double-tap are straight up B.S.. It’s not about 10,000 hours! Gladwell forgot to mention the promotion part. 10 thousand hours will give you mastery. But it won’t make you KNOWN.

MAYBE YOU JUST DON'T BELIEVE

If you believed in your art, you would promote it. Oh... you tell me you believe in it but you’re too shy? Then you don’t believe. It's simple. When you believe… shyness doesn’t play into the equation. Fear doesn’t factor into the script. When you believe, you transcend adversity. Nothing can stop you. You beat doors down. You’re excited. Listen, even if you try to withdraw into your shell right now and convince yourself that I’m wrong and that I don’t understand your unique situation… It still won’t change the fact: You don’t believe. You'll find a counter-mantra to my self-empowerment mantra just to make yourself feel better. Words like "Everyone has their own path..." No. You're dabbling. Your 100% only happens 20% of the time. But when you believe, your 100% happens 100% of the time. If I can think of ways that you can be doing more… then you’re not doing enough. I’m not smarter than you. I’m just more relentless than you. Which is fine but... No one should be more relentless than you about your own shit. If I have to convince you to go harder then you don't deserve to play in this arena. I can always tell the people who don’t believe. They’re the ones that say that they can’t... instead of asking the real question. How.

You need to drop bombs every day. You need to put things out into the world that people can interact with. If you're using social media, be social. Write captions to explain your work and put it into a context. Don't expect for your art to speak for itself. Talk about it like you would to your friends. Share it with the same intimacy you'd want your favorite artist to share their work with you.

Photographers

Photographers... Explain the passion behind your photography in your captions so that people can understand your worldview and what makes you different. Take pictures as if they're editorials. Don't be so disposable. When you go out into the world... Take portraits of the people who can influence your career and then email them the best photo of them that you took to open up a dialogue.

Writers... I know people have short attention spans. They don't read. Just share shorter bits. Don't be so precious. Put up some quotes on your social media instead of sharing other people's work. Flex your muscles in your captions. Text a friend a short paragraph and see what they think. Put a little bit of your writing as a signature at the bottom of your emails with a link to your medium page or your blog. You don't have a medium page or a blog? Well fuck... Get one. You grow when you write every day. But You grow even faster when you SHARE your writing every day.

Musicians... Send your music to Instagram models. Give your music to film directors and to screenwriters. Make the perfect playlist for your local coffee shop and mix in your own songs with the others. Tell people why you wrote that song. Share the process of recording. Not like how other people do it, but in a way that's truly your own. Don't think in product cycles as if you're a record label. Use your freedom to overshare. That's what your friends want. That's what your fans need.

My fellow artists... Promote yourselves guys. Your art deserves it.

### 12. Stop Describing Your Art Like You're Writing A LinkedIN Bio!

When I ask creatives what makes them different from other creatives they send me sentences like these:

"I share life lessons through visual storytelling."

"I create impactful art that's relatable."

"I creating groundbreaking content that consistently resonates with my audience."

"I'm sharing a different perspective on life in my art."

I read words like this and I think the same thing everyone else thinks....

You didn't SAY anything.

You didn't COMMIT to anything.

When I come across bios like these, I know that the person writing them hasn't figured out their place in the world yet. So they're using pretty words, cliches, and platitudes to cover it up.

Until you're focused in your thoughts...

You won't be focused in your words...

And until you're focused in your words...

You won't be focused in your actions.

That may work at Thanksgiving dinner when your uncle asks you what you've been up to.

But it won't work in the real world.

Ask yourself:

What kind of impact do you want to make?

What kind of difference do you want to make?

Ok, good. Now flesh it out by following up with the real question:

HOW (artistically) will you do it?

Like, exactly.

Don't bullshit me by saying "I want to help people..."

Be precise.

"I want to overturn the current beauty standards of social media by sharing unabashed pictures of my acne on every single post on IG until I normalize this condition that so many people I know suffer from."

Stop skimming the surface.

If you think you can get away with it because other people do... You're comparing yourself to the wrong people.

Be clear with your goals.

Laser sharp.

"I'm creating fun memes, and sharing short essays-like stories of my troubled mixed-race upbringing in order to unite 20-30 yr old artists living in Harlem and Queens. Once I've penetrated that niche, I will start to raise funding to create a short film with Tribeca film festival guidelines, based on those same themes."

Can you be that clear with your career aspiration?

It's that sort of clarity that makes it come true.

Here's a shortened version of a head-shaking email I received last week:

"I want to create meaning using my artistic voice and move the receiver to tears, laughter, surprise, curiosity, and epiphany. Having purpose and meaning behind the work. I want to make a difference and disrupt and influence the pulse of culture."

Nice words, bro.

Perfect for LinkedIN.

You described what every creative is trying to do with their art.

The problem?

Nothing original about it.

Avoid truisms.

Avoid empty words.

I already know that you want to do amazing things.

That's why you're here. That's why we're talking.

But what you need to describe is HOW you plan on doing it.

IE. Cardi B: I'm gonna create chart-topping pop / R&B anthems to empower strippers.

I can hang my hat on that.

She doesn't need to tell us she's going to be original. When your approach is original everything that follows it will be original too.

Don't tell people how you're gonna make them feel. Tell them what you're gonna do, and if it's powerful... they'll feel it all on their own.

Make a career statement that's so bold you'll end up rallying people behind you (WHILE potentially (hopefully) alienating others).

That's what makes things exciting.

"Writing relatable stories." won't help you find your community.

"Writing stories about my childhood of abuse to share with other survivors" is making a commitment to something more concrete.

Another message I received that made me realize that these lazy descriptions were a pandemic:

"I wanna create films that make you stop scrolling, that are gritty, and that make you think twice."

Uh, isn't that what we're all trying to do?

Go more hardcore like this instead:

"I'm creating 20-minute documentaries on the underground metal scene in Iceland. These docs will live on YouTube and I'll share the research process that goes into them on Twitch until I grow a world-wide community that buys my merch."

Now, THAT'S putting your stake in the ground!

Describe what you're trying accomplishing with your art by injecting unique aspects of yourself into it.

Commit to timelines.

Define the goal posts.

That's what the world is attracted to.

Describe your career in a way that we can imagine a "Made for Netflix" documentary about it.

Even if you're nowhere near getting there yet.

If your idea is amazing... Believe me...

The world will conspire to help you achieve it.

### 🔑 13. How To Message Gatekeepers, Collaborators & Mentors So They Hit You Back

I know you'd rather write a hit song... Or paint a masterpiece... Or take sexy pictures for your Onlyfans... Or simply just scroll for hours for "inspiration"...

Anything but use your precious time to reach out to people who could help build your career.

"I need a manager," you think to yourself.

Ok, but um... How are you going to get a manager without talking to people?

You know what I've noticed? The biggest difference between successful artists I've worked with and the struggling creatives who gave up... Is this one personality trait:

ANY eyes and ears that can help them get to the next step.

You call it "self-promotion". Oof. It sounds so ugly when you put it that way. No wonder you don't want to do it.

And your more extroverted friends, they'll call it "the hustle". Ok. That sounds a little better. But it still doesn't get you going. "Hustling" doesn't feel like "you". You're more spiritual.

Well, my fellow purist, why not call it what it really is?

"Sharing your passion."

When an artist believes in what they're doing, they look for excuses to show EVERYONE.

They believe that their art holds the cure to someone's ills. And they will stop at nothing to administer that cure.

But if you want to share your art with a larger audience than you already have, you'll have to start reaching out to people who have access to this elusive audience.

Problem is...

These people don't even know you exist.

Here is how you change that.

You know that. That's why you freeze up when it's time to do it. That's why you stare at a blinking cursor. That's why you've been procrastinating this forever.

But it's easier than you think.

You only need 3 sentences.

Here's what Bel (mystery student) was going to send out to an "industry person" but luckily didn't:

I hope this email finds you well.

My name is Bel, and I love (Paula's brand).

I'm writing to you because I believe you work with Val Gadot, am I right? Val was my teacher back in 2015, and I've been following her and your agency for a long time.

I'm a makeup artist who recently arrived from Brazil, you're the first person I'm contacting because if I could pick an agency in the world to work with it would have to be yours.

I work in beauty for advertising, both photo and video. I can rock a no makeup look with perfect "bare" skin and I also love to go beyond the conventional beauty. I had Calvin Klein, C&A, Natura, History Channel, Netflix as some of my clients, I'd love to show you some of my work. I hope I can send you a printed version of my portfolio, can you tell me an address I can send it to?

If you are not the right person for me to talk about this, could you please redirect me to someone you think could help me on this hunt?

I also work in consulting for beauty brands (product, education and communication) and in training for companies, brands and schools. Education is a very dear topic to my heart. I'm also experienced in performing presentations and videos for brands and events.

I hope we can make some art together :)

Dear Artist...

What is your goal when you send an email?

Like, toanyone.

While you can't guarantee #2. You CAN guarantee #1.

Even with industry people

And you do that by starting with...

Your first sentence needs to stop them in their tracks.

Please, no boring introductions like most people write.

When people go to their inbox, all they want to do is delete, delete, delete...

So instead--

Change their FOCUS towards you by asking a question tailored to them.

For example... I could re-write Bel's email intro like this:

Or if you're writing to a potential collaborator, use a "HOLD YOUR BREATH" style intro like this:

"I just went through your Instagram profile and, to be honest, I... (write something compelling)"

There is no human alive that won't read through that opening sentence.

The idea is to make sure your first line gets their attention, so you don't get deleted.

Whoever you're writing to has their own goals and their own ambitions... Just like you do.

If you don't know what those goals are yet... Then you aren't ready to write them anything.

Do your research.

Find out what they're working on.

Find out what they're passionate about.

Introduce yourself as the person who wants to help them accomplish their goals.

Your email should make them feel like... "Who is this?"

Show them how you've ALREADY invested time in them:

You get the idea.

Don't ever send cold emails to anyone in the industry without doing research beforehand.

Otherwise all you'll be writing is a form letter.

People hate those.

A little bit of research will open big doors for you.

Find a person you have in common that you can namedrop (with permission).

It's better to spend time writing 2 researched emails or DMs than sending out 20 "form letters" that everyone will just trash anyway.

Now you can finally write about yourself.

But please! Don't give them your life's story! Artists love to blab. Don't.

Just write about the part about youthat's directly related to how you're going to help them achieve THEIR goals...

And keep it short.

Ask them to take action or to answer whatever question you need to be answered.

Here's Bel's new email:

What do you think will happen next?

Paula will cross-check with Val to see if she knows Bel.

Val will rave about Bel ('cause Bel already told her she was gonna name-drop her).

Bel will get her email replied to.

The "work" was NOT in writing the three paragraphs.

The "work" was in doing the research that made writing those paragraphs easy as pie.

Researched emails and DMs get a reply back.

Invest time in researching the people you want in your life.

Do that, and they will rush to help you in return.

### 🔑 13. How To Message Gatekeepers, Collaborators & Mentors So They Hit You Back

#### Successful artists hunger to get NEW eyes and ears on their work.

## Gate-keepers and potential collaborators need to be approached with tact.

### 1. You want them to READ your email.

### 2. You want them to RESPOND to your email.

## SENTENCE / PARAGRAPH #1: A "Pattern Interrupt".

### Hi Paula,

### I don't know if I should be telling you this, but... Your employee, Val Gadot, has a secret side-hustle.

### She's a teacher.

### And guess what? I'm her star student.

## SENTENCE / PARAGRAPH #2: Keep talking about THEM.

### "I know how passionate you are about Aboriginal rights. I've found a make-up community that I will wake people up... and maybe even put you at the forefront..."

## SENTENCE / PARAGRAPH #3: NOW, talk about you.

### Hi Paula,

### I don't know if I should be telling you this but... Your employee, Val Gadot, has a secret side-hustle.

### She's a teacher.

### And guess what? I'm her star student.

### I know how passionate you are about aboriginal rights. I've found a make-up community that will wake people up to (blah blah)... and put you at the forefront of (blah blah)...

### I haven't shared this with anyone else in the industry yet. I'd like to show it to you first. Where can I send it?

### Bel

### (link to IG)

### 14. Writing The Perfect 90-Day Artist Roadmap

If you want to get there in only 3 months you have to have a clear Polaris Star. You have to know WHO YOU ARE TRYING TO BECOME. And you can't be focused on anything else.

Don't dilute your chances by having multiple goals. I see students do that all the time. And that's why things go slow for them. That's why they lose focus. And then they get discouraged.

Every time things moved slower for me, it was because other goals had crept in. So I immediately cleaned house and everything started going at lightning speed again.

It's hard though.

You have to "pour wine into the ocean" for the old goals. Put them on the back-burner.

It's the only way.

IF you want to go fast that is...

Let me put it in perspective for you.

If you're going after a career that a lot of other people want, but you dilute your focus by having multiple goals... Guess what? Your "laser focused competition" will DESTROY you.

You can't be the G.O.A.T. by having multiple goals.

IF (see how I capitalized "if") you want to be the G.O.A.T. THEN you have to have only ONE goal.

IF you want to get there in record time... THEN you have to have only ONE goal.

How fast can we do it?

If you can't validate the career you want in 90 days (with the process I will show you below), then this is not the career for you. If you can't create momentum with these steps, then this is not the career for you.

I'm the last person to wanna crush your dreams, believe me. But I will never encourage delusion either.

I've used this "career validation" method 3 times.

Once for music when I went all in and got a bidding war between record labels within 90 days.

Next, for photography when I picked up a camera and had my pictures in magazines within 60 days.

And then for "creative direction" (such a bullshit title but they had to call me something) when I taught myself marketing and had paying clients within 30 days.

And some of you will say, "Yeah, but that's because you have talent. Or that's because you had connections." My answer to you is... A lot of people have talent. A lot of people have connections (I had NONE starting out. NONE.) Lucky for me, many of these talented, connected people aren't as focused as me. I them by every day.

You and I have something that will beat talent every day of the week:

The "will".

And the other advantage that you'll have starting today:

Write down all the things that have to happen to reach your Polaris Star.

For example. When I wanted to become a full-time photographer. I wrote down:

Get hired by magazines.

Get hired by promoters at clubs.

Go to school for photography.

Get hired by a company to be an in-house photographer.

Intern at a fashion house.

Intern at an online magazine.

Get an agent.

Write down all the daily actions that you can think of that you'd need to do to accomplish this goal.

(example for my photography again)

Take 500 pictures a day. (I took 800 a day)

Go to 5 parties a week. (I went to 7 a week)

Copy one person's style every week until I could easily mimic it.

Go to Barnes and Nobles and study new photographers.

Send my work to magazines.

Research the emails of photo editors in magazines.

Ask yourself this basic question: How does the person who has "the career I want" act every day? Use anyone you can think of that you respect to get your template from. Break down their behavior into all it's useful morsels.

What time do they wake up?

What do they eat?

What is their business / art ratio?

How many cold calls do they make?

How much do they promote themselves?

Do they have a mailing list?

Pick a successful career and analyze how that person behaves. Model all the attributes that you believe led to their success. (But discard all the bad habits they've collected that may eventually rob them of that success!)

What you're creating here is your "personal culture".

Personal culture is... A set of unified behaviors that leads to ONE common goal.

Your personal culture will surround you with the "aura" needed to make people want to help you accomplish your goal. So take this step seriously.

Writing it down will give you clarity.

And clarity is key if you want this to happen quickly. And if you want to stay focused.

Once you have all of these questions answered, you will have a long list of unorganized daily and weekly tasks that will lead you to your goal. But one thing is missing to make it all make sense.

Figure out every drop of time you can commit to your doing your Polaris Star driven ACTIVITIES. Where can you steal time from your day job?

How much $$ can you invest?

MATERIAL ASSETS THAT CAN HELP

A car, free office space, special equipment

Public speaking, copywriting

Contacts, family, friends that might want to help

The PEOPLE resource is the most important one. PEOPLE can help make your lack of the other 4 resources not even matter. Who has your back?

Now, take out your calendar.

I can't tell you how many times I've pulled out a calendar with students, and suddenly, they come face to face with how unrealistic they've been with their time.

Map out all the ACTIVIES onto your calendar until it looks DO-ABLE. At first it'll feel overwhelming. Just keep moving things around until things look realistic. You'll know you're on the right track the more excited you get about it. What happens is, you'll be able to SEE how all those activities over time directly lead to the results you want. The calendar will make you SEE it concretely and it will keep you pumped.

Strategy will keep you focused. Having everything written down in advance will allow you to execute without thinking.

Prioritize the activities that require the least amount of work but that give you the biggest returns.(The 80/20 Rule)

Re-read that last sentence and let it sink in.

The reason people don't achieve their "dreams" is because they don't do what they "love" like it's an obsession. They find repetition boring. They find the consistency tiring. So, instead they end up doing what they "love" once a month and then wonder why nothing is changing.

The creatives who change the world treat the process like they’re athletes in training.

If you can't charge someone yet for your talent, then do it for free. Get yourself in the habit of "doing the thing". Get in the habit of people seeing you "do the thing". You are validating your career. It is more important that you DO at this stage than WAIT. DO, DO, DO!

Look at your 5 resource types and see how you can use them to make things easier for yourself. Everyone has advantages. Use yours.

When I started my career, I didn't wait for people to pay me. I put myself in every photography situation I could put myself in until I became "the only person for the job".

Once you've mapped out the whole process towards your ONE GOAL... All you have to do is put it into application now.

Even "career validation" is an iterative process. (Review 'The Mystery Formula')

Every week you should tweak your actions to keep them in line with the GOAL you want. Then blindly execute for the coming week.

Think. Act. Optimize (based on results).

There is no way that if you have talent for what you're pursuing that you won't begin your path to making money from it within the next 3 months. It's impossible.

Not if you "go all in".

With that said... No time to waste...

Go execute.

### 14. Writing The Perfect 90-Day Artist Roadmap

## STEP #1: CHOOSE YOUR POLARIS STAR

## STEP #2: LIST OF ACTIVITIES

### ACTIVITIES A: The avenues to success.

### ACTIVITIES B. Daily / weekly actions

### ACTIVITIES C. Personal Culture

## STEP #3: THE STRATEGY

### The 5 Resources available to you:

### Strategy = How you've chosen to use your existing available resources to achieve an outcome.

### USE A CALENDAR AS THE "CANVAS" FOR ALL YOUR GOAL-RELATED ACTIVITIES.

### THE QUALITY OF YOUR ACTIVITIES = THE QUALITY OF YOUR RESULTS

### REMOVE AS MUCH FRICTION FROM THE PROCESS AS POSSIBLE.
