### 🔑 The Artist/Audience Relationship

'The Audience Is Present', Marina Abramović

When I ask artists what their relationship to their audience is, it’s funny how quickly they get tongue-tied. Yet still, somehow, they continue the delusion that their fanbase should be “growing”. Simply for existing.

Pressed further, they might say something like, “People are following my journey to watch me make art.” Um, no. No one cares about your journey or your art. The relationship you’re describing is parasitic at best. And that’s why you struggle. You think it’s about you. You think you’re online to “promote yourself”.

Sure, while you’re in your room making art, it’s ok to follow Rick Rubin’s advice of “ignoring the audience”, if that helps you focus on creating.

But once you decide to share your work with real human beings online or IRL, it ain’t about you anymore.

Once you decide you want an audience to care about you after all, you’ll need to define what you want that artist/audience relationship to look like. You’ll need to DEFINE your role within the online conversation. And you’ll need to ASSUME that role so that people care about what you’re doing.

The great thing is, it’s really easy, because there are only 3 types of “artist/audience relationships” to choose from. Three ways of communicating.

Yes, only 3.

1. Inspirational

2. Aspirational

3. Transformational

Before I go on to describe each of them, let’s get something clear. ‘Cause this is where most people get confused:

What I am describing with these words is NOT your art (or your process). I am describing your “artist/audience relationship”.

I am describing HOW YOU COMMUNICATE WITH YOUR AUDIENCE, not the RESULT of what they get out of it. You see... All 3 communication styles above can “transform”. All 3 communication styles above can “inspire”. All 3 communication styles above can make people want to emulate you.

But the other two results (besides your main communication style) will be BY-PRODUCTS of your efforts based on the strength of your art.

The question to ask yourself is… Which “artist/audience relationships” / communication style should guide how you show up online AT THE BEGINNING OF YOUR JOURNEY?

1. Are you building an ASPIRATIONAL relationship with your fans?

2. Are you building an INSPIRATIONAL relationship with your fans?

3. Are you building a TRANSFORMATIONAL relationship with your fans?

ALL successful artists, without exception, embody ONE of these relationships with their audience. Either instinctively or by design.

The problem you’ve been having online is that you haven’t yet decided how you want to show up yet.

You don’t know whether you want your relationship with your audience to be inspirational, aspirational, or transformational. And so you end up sending people mixed signals. And confusing people. And so, they move on.

There are only three types of relationships you can have with your audience.

Let that sink in.

Inspirational, Aspirational, Or Transformational.

An ASPIRATIONAL artist/audience relationship is focused on YOU.

An INSPIRATIONAL artist/audience relationship is focused on THE ART.

A TRANSFORMATIONAL artist/audience relationship is focused on THEM.

“Aspirational” means that you want to use your platform to lead by example. Like, you want to be so good at what you do that everyone wants to be like you. This is what influencers do. This is what celebrities and athletes do. And it's also what 90% of musicians do nowadays (they create "vibes" more than depth -- and that's NOT bad, it's just different).

“Inspirational” means that you want to use your platform to ignite something that’s been dormant in people. That’s what artists who bleed something true in their art are doing. Painters, film-makers, and writers that rip you apart.

“Transformational” means that you want to use your platform to help people change. Your journey is a surrogate for theirs. This is what mentors do. It’s what teachers and gurus do.

Aspirational means… Who you are as a person moves us first.

Inspirational means… The art you make moves us first

Transformational… What you teach us moves us first.

Aspirational: “People either wanna BE you or they wanna FUCK you!”

Inspirational. “Your art makes people cry (tears of joy OR sadness)!”

Transformational: “You help people unlock new levels!”

Are you getting it?

So far, in how you present yourself online, you’ve been trying to be everything to everyone. And that’s why nothing is quite hitting the mark.

Like, you’ll try to have an aspirational relationship with your audience and post like an influencer, but it’s not long before that fills you with utter shame.

And so on other days, you’ll feel more like a pure artist, and want to be inspirational to your audience… And so you'll share your best art for people to see. But the truth is, your art only ever goes halfway, and more often than not, you play it safe. So no one ends up inspired by that.

Or in other moments, you’ll be so inspired by other artist gurus and mentors online, that you'll try to be transformational to your audience, and share diluted IG-caption wisdom, while it’s clear to everyone who’s been watching you these past 3 months that you hardly follow any of your newfound advice.

Stop this endless cycle of lameness.

Pick ONE “audience relationship” to begin the NEXT PHASE of how you show up in the world (online and IRL). Pick and establish your main role for how you will start a healthy new journey with “your people”.

Do this, and from now on, you will know how you need to show up for them online… And they will understand what to expect from you.

If you want to have an aspirational relationship with your audience, then you have to create a persona and/or a world that makes people salivate.

Your audience will be attracted to you because they want to emulate some aspect of how you ARE and/or how you LIVE. You're not here to teach them how (that's "transformational")... YOU'RE here to make people dream by SHOWING them how!

Like, maybe you have aspirational talent. That means the art you make is so good that other artists try to rip you off. And non-artists are simply in awe of your skills. (People wanna BE you.)

Or maybe you have aspirational beauty (or an instantly recognizable personal style). You're hot. You're strong. (People wanna fuck you) Don't be shy about it. Embrace those gifts.

Perhaps you have an enviable environment. Like, where you live is uh-mazing! Either your house or apartment is the stuff of dreams (or you make it look like it is), or the noisy city or rustic farm you live on makes people wish they lived there, too. (Living all alone in a cabin in the forest is just as enviable as living in NYC or Paris!)

Or you're wealthy.

Or you're poor, but you have a creative way of making your life look rich as hell.

Aspirational could mean you are part of an art scene or community that others want to be a part of as well. Or that you are the poster-child for the times we currently live in (or a past/future era)

Or that you have a sense of purpose that’s so clear that it’s enviable. People love your drive and discipline, as well as the fact that you’re on a mission. They wish they could be that dedicated to something.

The more of these you have, the more aspirational you will be for your audience. The fewer of these you have, the more you have to be 10X exceptional in what’s left.

(DOESN'T NEED TO BE EVERYTHING ON THIS LIST, JUST SOME)

- You show off whatever aspirational aspects you possess on full tilt and as often as possible.

-If people talk about, or are jealous of your "art lifestyle" or your scene in the comments, it's working

- World-building isn’t optional for you, it’s mandatory.

- Embrace of Regionality (you "rep" where you're from).

- You create a scene, or you join a scene.

- You are the work of art as much as the art is.

- All influencers and athletes

- MUSIC: most hip hop and pop, punk, and any other music that is more about the "vibes" than "creating something timeless that touches humanity"

- Thirst traps- Basquiat, Salvador Dalí, Frida Kahlo (if you don't know the artists' stories and about the time they lived, you're missing half the story with the impact of their art). Their lives are a work of art.- Rick Owens

- Movie Stars

- Pharrell, FKA twigs, A$AP Rocky, Dojo Cat, Sabrina Carpenter. Their music would have way less impact without their persona. The purpose of their art is to EXTEND their personal brand.

- Emma Chamberlain, Casey Neistat

- Kim Kardashian

- Tavi Gevinson

- early Bronques (as photographer, ticking ALL the boxes) — instantly recognizable personal style, lives in NYC, photographing the most exclusive parties, weird talent for disarming celebrities, part of the hipster art scene, sharing art every morning at 9am discipline

NOTE: Artists who aren’t that original in their art, often rely on other aspirational aspects of themselves to compensate for it (beauty, wealth, connections). That’s not bad, btw, it’s smart. They’re playing to their strengths.

Your personality isn’t the driving force in this artist/audience relationship. The art is.

You can even never show your face, if you prefer it that way.

But either way, the art has to be GREAT. “Good” isn't good enough. You can’t be making art that’s merely decoration.

I REPEAT: TO HAVE AN "INSPIRATIONAL" RELATIONSHIP WITH YOUR AUDIENCE, YOUR ART HAS TO BE OUTRAGEOUSLY GREAT. IT HAS TO BE UNDENIABLE.

People will gloss over this part. They will cherry pick from all the other qualities, and bypass this point. Like, yeah, yeah. But don't be the artist who ignores this truth to make yourself feel better.Face what your role is for this type of artist/audience relationship to work:

Your art has to move people's spirit. It has to “change their life”.

Like others have done for you.

And how do you do that?

By not holding back anything in your art. You “go there”! Your audience expects you to take risks and uncover truths they've even had trouble expressing to themselves.

If you can't go to those heights with your art, then you should look at the other two relationships... "Aspirational" or "Transformational". With those, you can make up for the lack of groundbreakingness in your art by expanding on other worthwhile aspects of your world.

But if "inspirational" is the artist/audience relationship you want, you won’t rely on your personality or environment, or how much you can teach people—it’s the art, all by itself, that will grab people by the jugular.

You can choose to be as elusive as you want, as long as you’re emotionally raw and focused on communicating realness.

Your audience expects to experience extreme emotions when they experience your art: weeping, laughing out loud, rethinking their lives, and sometimes even giving them a desire to live life more fully.

You make your audience "feel understood". You make them "feel seen".

TO HAVE AN INSPIRATIONAL RELATIONSHIP WITH THE AUDIENCE IS THE RAREST OF ALL RELATIONSHIPS BECAUSE IT DEPENDS ON YOUR ART BEING IN THE TOP ESCHELONS OF YOUR FIELD. YOU HAVE TO BE WAY AHEAD OF THE CURVE, TAKING RISKS NO ONE ELSE IS TAKING, INVENTING A NEW ART STYLE, OR MAKING THEM FEEL LIKE THEY NEVER FELT BEFORE.

If you are a musician or a visual artist, you have to be a unicorn.

If your art is decorative... If your music sounds like everyone else... If other people can do the same thing as you... If you have no message... THEN YOU DO NOT HAVE AN "INSPIRATIONAL" RELATIONSHIP WITH YOUR AUDIENCE. You want to have one, I'm sure... But you don't. Sorry. You need to pick either transformational or aspirational to make what you're doing work on grand scale.

(DOESN'T NEED TO BE EVERYTHING ON THIS LIST, JUST SOME)

- The first thing that strikes the audience when they come across you online is how original your art is. The second thing that strikes them is how your body of work feels like it has a message in it (whether or not they can articulate it).

- Online you share the things that emphasize what makes your art "1of 1". Maybe it's that you’re...

1. Bringing a new way of making art to the forefront (pushing your idiom to new heights). Or...

2. You’re talking about things others aren’t talking about (politically, or raw emotions people are afraid to explore). Or...

3. You’ve created a compelling fictional alternate world/reality for people to lose themselves in (as opposed to the "enhanced world based on your personal reality" that the 'aspirational artist/audience relationship' uses).

You need one of these 3 things to be "inspirational". And whichever one you picked... THAT IS THE FOUNDATION OF YOUR MESSAGE! You needn’t look further. MESSAGE = you’re inviting a particular type of person (your people) to share your vision of the world. Make everything you share online a mirror of that world.

- The art you share has to trigger big, deep emotions. And you foster online conversations around those emotions and the art itself.

- Everything you share online is about creating an emotional experience that resonates. You share art and media that reminds your audience about themselves. You are a mirror.

- You strive to connect all the people who feel deep emotions about your art into a space where they can congregate and communicate about THE WORK together.

- You share the process behind your art and how it connects to the emotions it makes your fans feel.

- You hint at (or overtly show) the behind-the-scenes effort you put in to bleed for your art.

- You create a cause aligned to your art, or you join a cause aligned to your art.

- Aphex Twin, Aurora, Kendrick Lamar, Frank Ocean, ANOHNI, Leith Ross. Music is probably the hardest art form to have an inspirational relationship with your audience. 99% of musicians reading this aren't making music original or distinctive enough to fall under this category. Please don't fool yourself. Pick "aspirational" or "transformational" instead so you can prosper without delusion.

- Early Weeknd (never showed his face, it was all about the music), then once he became popular, he added aspirational elements to his artist/audience relationship.

- Directors like Sofia Coppola, David Lynch, Tarantino, and Donald Glover. With directors, the audience doesn't care about "what you do in your personal life" (aspirational) or what your worldview is (transformational)-- unless these things directly pertain to the movie you’re sharing with us. Your contract with the audience is to make them feel deep emotions. That's it! If you can’t make someone laugh, cry out loud, yell at the screen, or shake them up for days, then you are not holding up your end of the bargain.

- Rupi Kaur

- Comedians (if you can make people laugh, you win). We don’t care what you do offstage (you're not aspirational). But when you’re sharing skits online, or doing standup, you need to make us laugh. That’s the contract you have with your audience.

- Writers. If you're going to be the voice inside someone's head, blow their brains out.

- Petra Collins

- Amy Bravo, Yayoi Kusama... Only Painters and illustrators who make art that is beyond “decoration” can have this artist/audience relationship. In other words,visual artists with a strong message and A BOLD NEW ART STYLE.99% of visual artists reading this right now are not making visual art that is original or distinctive enough to fall under this category. Please don't fool yourself. Pick "aspirational" or "transformational" instead so you can prosper online without delusion.

You are a thought leader, a philosopher, and your ideas and art are about inspiring people to change their ways by changing their thinking. But you don’t just imply it (like you would if you were inspirational), you are actually showing them the steps to getting there.

You see that “People Are Hurting” and you use art to help the world heal.

It’s not really about “teaching”. It’s about “activating” your community with new ideas derived from your artistic process.

Your art doesn’t have to be groundbreaking, but your approach to creating it must be unique. You have a way of making art, a process, a way of thinking about it, that people want to adopt (even if they’re not trying to make art that looks like yours).

You have an WORLDVIEW that inspires, and you show others how to adopt it.

Your audience is in love with your mind. They don’t care what art form you choose. It’s the thought behind whatever you do that makes them see possibilities for themselves.

(DOESN'T NEED TO BE EVERYTHING ON THIS LIST, JUST SOME)

- You teach people how to get to a new place in their lives

-If people are talking about how much you've changed their world view in the comments, it's working

- You embody what you teach in your own actions and art (almost “aspirational” but it’s your way of thinking that’s inspiring people here, not your persona)

- Create a school of thought from scratch... Or align yourself to an established school of thought.

- Even if you haven’t arrived at your ultimate “teacher/mentor” status, you’ve figured out a compelling way to show your journey while you’re still learning yourself. You don’t have to have it all figured out to be transformational to others. You just need to be a few steps ahead of your audience for your online presence to be valuable to them.

- Marina Abramović

- Rick Rubin

- Father Bronques

- bell hooks

- Virgil Abloh

- Questlove

Shantell Martin:https://www.instagram.com/shantell\_martin/

“But, Father Bronques, I want to be inspirational.”

Are you a generational talent? Unless you’re one of the art forms that is "inspirational" by default (writing, filmmaking), the chances you will have this artist / audience relationship is low.

Sorry for the blow to your ego, but it’s not about “what you wanna be”. It’s about WHO YOU ACTUALLY ARE. It’s time to stop hating your true self, and trying to be something you’re not. You’re already special. Stop hiding that specialness. Start focusing on what’s naturally there and amplify it. Don’t try to be everything to everyone. Allow your natural gifts to come through.

All 3 of these “artist/audience relationships” will inspire. Just in different ways. Like, look here:

ASPIRATIONAL = you inspire people by who you are or how you live. They’re buying into YOUR VIBE as much as the art. That’s why the art you create will only be valuable to people if it is a vessel for your aura as a person. Eventually, people will see YOU as the work of art. If that sounds like you… Double down on it. Play your lifestyle up to the hilt when you show up online and IRL.

INSPIRATIONAL = you inspire people purely with your art (who you are individually has no bearing whatsoever on your art’s impact). You can never show your face if you want to, and it wouldn’t matter because the art is so fucking good that people need it in their lives. Your art elicits extreme emotions. You are a truth teller, confrontational, and go where other so-called artists are afraid to. This is the rarest of artist/audience relationships. 'Generational Talent' type of rare. "27 Club" type of rare. And because it's so unicorn-like, it will require you to be ok with being on the fringes of society. If that really sounds like you, ok… Double down on it. Be raw and fearless with every artwork you show up with online and IRL.

TRANSFORMATIONAL = you inspire people to change their being, all with your unique way of looking at the world and approaching art. People don’t want to copy you, like in an aspirational relationship… But they DO want to apply your way of thinking to their own lives. You provoke inner rewiring. If that sounds like you… Double down on it. Lead your people to a better way of being human and making art.

BUT PLEASE UNDERSTAND... EVERYONE MAKES THIS MISTAKE... Aspirational, Inspirational, and Transformational are not words to describe your art.

They are words to describe YOUR RELATIONSHIP TO THE AUDIENCE.

It's how you will FRAME everything you say to your fans online and off.

IE.: "I want to tell you a story about something I did."

Aspirational = “I wanna tell you a story about something that I did that’s really cool and you’ll wanna do it too.

Inspirational = “I wanna tell you a story about what I did that made me connect to the essence of this piece I made.”

Transformational = “I wanna tell you a story about what I did that you can learn from if you’re ever in that situation.”

Aspirational relationships make the audience feel just out of reach of the artist (you inspire your audience to dream).

Inspirational relationships make you feel connected to the artist without ever having met them (you make your audience feel less alone in the world).

Transformational relationships feel down-to-earth (you expand your audience's view of themselves).

In aspirational relationships, the main character is you, your scene, and your city.

In inspirational relationships, the main character is your art and the emotions it brings.

In transformational relationships, the main character is your audience and the epiphanies they receive through your worldview.

Doubling down on your artist/audience relationship means framing everything you share with them through the same lens, so they know what to expect, and you always have clarity on how to show up for them.

If you’re brutally honest with yourself, you’ll see that ONE of these communication styles is more natural to you than the other two. CHOOSE IT. And then, double down on it! Show up for your audience with intention and with your proper communication style.

As soon as you pick what that relationship will be, you’ll notice just how much you’ve been sending your audience mixed signals, leaving your followers confused and disengaged.

Every artist succeeding online has doubled down on their artist/audience relationship. None of them is wishy-washy about it. They are not shy about playing their role to the maximum.

Know how you will show up, so your audience knows what to expect.

### 🔑 Artist Bait: Ongoing Narrative

Chelsea Girls, 1966

Once youfigure out what you want your relationship with your audience to look like, you finally have the secret for sharing with intention.

But still, that doesn’t mean that you will instantly know WHAT to share with your people. It may take a few weeks to settle into your new skin.

Look at what you share with your audience right now. Notice that there's no connective tissue tying everything together? It's all "singular posts" vying for people's attention.

And because of that, when you share something, it's almost like you're starting from scratch every time.

What's worse is that-- if someone, by chance, discovers your work online, there's nothing built-in to propel them to go discover everything else.

Today we're going to change that.

The pre-AI era was easy to tame. Your online presence was all about “your portfolio” and every week you’d add to it.

But today, sharing random posts does very little for an artist. Even if one of them goes viral. So what? Virality without a body of work waiting for new potential fans gets you nowhere.

Today, your content graveyard… Oops, sorry sorry, I meant… Your “portfolio”… As it stands, cannot compete against the current online slop it’s pitted against on your feed.

Artists need “online slop” insurance. Fortunately for us, it isn’t that hard to build.

The OPPORTUNITY right now, ironically, is to actually do exactly what you’ve secretly wanted to do since the social media was invented:

Be more human, more authentic, more raw, and more real to get people’s attention.

Nowadays, everyone thinks this means that they have to be outrageous. They think they need to “rage-bait” for attention. They think they have to create content designed to get "a reaction". But that’s empty calories. Zero depth.

That's not YOU.

Luckily for artists, you can WIN just as big by doing the exact opposite.

By creating ARTIST-BAIT

ARTIST-BAIT is when you…

1. Create media that slows people down and makes them feel seen.

2. Share things that nurture community, and specific values.

3. Decelerate the viewer. Focus on more nuanced emotions instead of trying to be confrontational like others do.

4. Share art that is pushes your art form forward. Creating work that is so undeniable people have to check it out.

5. Create media that makes people feel wiser after they come across you. Or that makes them want to go “touch grass” and reconnect to their essence.

Because the content creators have swung the pendulum is soooo far to the other side... This is your time to shine by doing the exact opposite.

My friend Gabi,@sighswoondoes exactly that. She “traps” you by using the aesthetics of the internet, and before you know it, you’ve gone down her rabbit hole of intellectual and spiritual musings.

Yes, it’s absolutely possible to use reverse-slop psychology for "good".

But to do any of that, you’ll have to stop being “middle of the road” like you have been these last few years.

The artist’s insurance against RAGE BAIT is sitting down to figure out, once and for all, what will be your ONGOING NARRATIVE online.

ONGOING NARRATIVE is the perfect ARTIST BAIT.

Now that you know what your artist/audience relationship is, the next thing to figure out is… What is the ONGOING NARRATIVE that matches it?

AN ONGOING NARRATIVE IS A REPEATABLE FORMULA (aka FORMAT) FOR PRESENTING YOUR WORK THAT MAKES PEOPLE TUNE IN TO SEE WHAT YOU WILL DO NEXT. You should be able to describe this formula in one simple sentence. “Tune in to see…”

Right now, all your online presence is a collection of disconnected things you've shared online. But switching your method to ONGOING NARRATIVE unifies all your work into one cohesive whole. When you do this, your online presence immediately gives off an aura of success.

An ONGOING NARRATIVE creates a habit with your audience.

Having an ONGOING NARRATIVE is the cheat code for never being at a loss about what to post.

Your ONGOING NARRATIVE is the frame you will put your whole body of work online in. It’s how you will “package” everything that you do so it beats the “content slop” you’re surrounded by online.

You love examples. So let use the aforementioned@sighswoon(There’s a reason why she is the only person I’ve ever co-hosted a 'Make art not content' podcast with!

SHE IS PURE TMS✨):

1. @sighswoon’s art is writing.

2. @sighswoon has a “transformational” relationship with her audience.

3. @sighswoon’s ONGOING NARRATIVE takes place on her Patreon.

4. @sighswoon's FORMULA = "Dropping knowledge". It is a weekly appointment to help other female artists make sense of being spiritual in a material world. She’s a young “guru” who has none of the negative patriarchal tendencies the word “guru” implies. She has the confidence to teach even while she is still discovering things herself.

4. This format works for @sighswoon because her audience can't wait to hear what new gems of knowledge she will drop to open their minds. She uses Instagram and Discord for microdosing the audience so that they go down the rabbit hole that leads to her amazing Patreon.

Because she has established an ONGOING NARRATIVE, figuring out what to share is fun and easy.

That’s why you need one of those “ongoing narrative” thing-a-ma-jiggies too!

I know, I know… You love examples. So here’s another. These kids totally get it:

CREEK CRAWLERS _

Talk about living up to “Emma Summer”!

In their first video (pinned) they gave their audience something (aspirational) to latch on to. And it turned out to be so compelling to their fans that they beat their goal of “10k by the end of the summer”— IN A FEW WEEKS!

The ONGOING NARRATIVE you will design this week will be the first of many “eras”.

But how do you come up with this first one?

Well, first, you need to understand who the star of the show is.

Inaspirationalartist/audience relationships, the main character is YOU, YOUR “SCENE”, AND/OR YOUR CITY.

Ininspirationalartist/audience relationships, the main character is YOUR ART and the emotions it brings.

Intransformationalartist/audience relationships, the main character is YOUR AUDIENCE and the epiphanies they will receive through your worldview.

Whatever format you choose should focus on the corresponding main character.

“Follow along as I create art…”, or any variation of that sentence, is not a good enough “ongoing narrative”. EVERYONE thinks they’re an artist these days. So that won't be enough to stand out. No one cares about another random person making art.

You’re gonna have to come up with something with more layers than just “you making art”.

Today, an artist’s ONGOING NARRATIVE needs to have a REPEATABLE and compelling HOOK. A HOOK is that catchy thing about how you present yourself/your art online that gets people excited. Something that makes them want to binge-watch everything you make once they discover you. And pretty soon… Wanna see everything you’ll make in the future.

If you can do a good job drawing them into your ONGOING NARRATIVE, they will get addicted to your art.

They will look forward to being part of whatever artist/audience relationship you’ve established with them.

You will have a new fan… For all the right reasons.

Aspirational artist/audience relationships:“I need to find an online format that makes my art persona bingeable.”

Inspirational artist/audience relationships:“I need to find an online format that makes my art process bingeable.”

Transformational artist/audience relationships:“I need to find an online format that makes my art worldview bingeable.”

But please, people… STOP WITH THE LISTS!!

Every time artists describe something they wanna do, they always use a long list of adjectives. Stop that! Long lists just show me (and the audience) that you’re still not committed. That you’re afraid of choosing. You’re trying to please everyone. You’re trying to be a Chinese menu again.

NO LISTS Y’ALL!

Give your audience ONE thing to latch onto that encapsulates the purpose of your channel.

Figure out an ONGOING NARRATIVE that reflects the nature of the relationship you want to establish with them in this new era of yours.

“I love what that artist is doing so much! Once I watch one of their videos, I wanna watch them all.”

FORMULA: RAGE BAIT & SWITCH (aspirational artist/audience relationship)

DESCRIPTION: “While the world was arguing about “(typical rage bait topic)”, here’s what I was doing instead…” Followed by: an artistic video essay of quiet moments returning to the essence of things.

WHY IT WORKS: Uses rage-bait framing but delivers uplifting ARTIST BAIT instead. Starts with the same opening line to give the audience a sense of familiarity every time.

FORMULA: AN IMPOSSIBLE GOAL (inspirational artist/audience relationship)

DESCRIPTION: Another friend of mine, Cocovan (@iamcocovan) started@theworldlettera few years ago. Her goal is to get people from every nation to write a letter to the world and expose her final performance artwork scroll in a gallery at the end.

WHY IT WORKS: You want to see her progression on this massive undertaking. The goal is clear. It involves strangers. Involving strangers is a cheat code to keeping an ONGOING NARRATIVE exciting.

FORMULA: CATCHPHRASE FRAMED ADVICE (transformational artist/audience relationship)

DESCRIPTION: Find a catchphrase that you can make your very own like: “I don’t know who needs to hear this, but…” followed by your art-inspired wisdom.

WHY IT WORKS: Familiar opening line → unexpected drop of emotional truth It feels like a welcome interruption from everything else. YOU become the artist on their feed that can break the hypnotic spell doomscrolling.

FORMULA: “IT LOOKED DIFFERENT IN MY HEAD” (inspirational artist/audience relationship)

DESCRIPTION: Show them what you were attempting to do, then show them what it actually turned out like.

WHY IT WORKS: Curiosity hook. People want to wait around to see the result.

HINT: Your ONGOING FORMULA doesn't even have to be based on the art. It could also be based around the world you're building that contains the art! Figure out a cute recurring formula that amplifies this “world” you’re building around the art. That way, when the corresponding art drops, it will feel completely natural to your audience and like it's the last piece of the puzzle.

CHEAT CODE: Any formula that includes APPROACHING STRANGERS is immediately bingeable if done well. People love “unscripted”. AI can’t generate this kind of human authenticity. It’s the only online narrative that is IMMUNE TO AI.

NONE OF THIS SECTION MATTERS IF YOU DON'T HAVE A RECURRING FORMAT.

NONE OF THIS IS A SHORTCUT TO FIGURING OUT A RECURRING FORMAT.

Got it? Let's continue...

In this new era, yes, you can show up less (like once a week minimum), but now you have to make your appearances more impactful.

Pick the home base of where you’re going to be sharing your ONGOING NARRATIVE, and then make all of your other appearances online lead to where this main show is taking place.

EMAIL, YOUTUBE, INSTAGRAM, a PODCAST, or whatever.

Give your series a name. Pin the first episode. Make a highlight.

Stick to a voice. Keep the same tone and the same emotional rhythm from piece to piece.

Give this new era a name.

Give your audience a name.

Use Visual anchors so that when people see you while scrolling online, they immediately know it’s you.

Use the same fonts everywhere.

There are millions of ONGOING NARRATIVES that you can choose to frame your art online.

You’re creative. You’ll figure it out.

And the cool thing is, once you do, you never have to worry about “What am I going to post?” anymore. And your whole online presence will now have structure. You’ll know how to show up for your people. Improving with each appearance.

But the temptation right now will be to take a long break to “figure all this out”.

No, no, no! Don’t fall for the “resistance”!

Trust me on this one… Figuring out your ONGOING NARRATIVE will never happen by “thinking about it”. It will only happen by taking action. By testing, making versions, iterating and STAYING ON STAGE IN FRONT OF THE CLASS (your audience).

There's no reason that you can't come up with an ongoing narrative format TODAY.

And… Once you get 75% of that idea… Go shoot version 1 immediately. All you need is a good-enough premise. You won’t know if it's a GREAT premise until you execute that first one. Figuring out the other 25% will only happen after the sweat, effort… When you give yourself and your team/confidantes/advisors something concrete to analyze.

Promise me.

Go do version one THIS WEEK!

Don't overthink yourself out of taking immediate action again.

### 15. WORLD BUILDING (PART I): TURNING YOUR ART INTO A BRAND

You know when someone asks you what you're trying to achieve in the next few months, or years, or with your "career" in general... And your answer is kinda vague?

Let's solve that, please?

This is where you're at right now:

You have ideas.

You have followers.

And perhaps you don't know your message yet.

That's not uncommon.

But stubbornly, you still wonder "How can I grow from here?"

World Building is the most important concept for you to master when you're ready to build your career.

And one day, when you can afford a genius manager... You'll hire them to think about this stuff for you. That fast-talking magical being will work on expanding your BRAND ENERGY outward.

But until then... You'll have to do it yourself.

It's not so bad. It's actually a lot of fun once you realize it's creative.

World Building will focus your energy on what matters.

But if you don't know what your art is(the product), or you haven't figured out youraudience psychographicoryour message... Then you need to go back to the earlier modules in The Mystery School and keep working until you achieve The Holy Trinity: Product, Audience and Message.

Just keep in mind that I'm sharing the fastest route I've seen anybody use, and that I've used myself.

World building is an advanced process for turningThe Holy Trinity(once you have it) into a unique, ever expanding, addictive EXPERIENCE for your fans.

Below is the complete journey for building a brand that makes a cultural impact.

Every artist or brand out there making a decent living year after year is operating at this base level.

Even if it's a weak version of it.

The best ones?

They have strong art... They're focusing on a niche audience... And they know their message in their sleep.

Everything that happens in an artist or brand's career is dependent on the synergy between these elements.

Your MESSAGE is the seed that will propel your art and audience relationship to a new level of sustainability and competition.

While achieving The Holy Trinity is indeed a major accomplishment...

The ultimate goal is: "World Building" (Expanding Brand Energy).

World building is the gradual process of turning a product into an Exclusive Experience... An audience into a Fanbase... And your message into a Cultural Shift.

Here are the stages of each.

The reasons for buying your art have changed now. Fans buy everything you do because they f-ck with your message.

Musicians: your albums, your collaborations (you're not just a hit song on a mixtape anymore, they want to hear everything you have to say)

Writers: they buy all your books

Artist: fans buy prints of your work online, they buy your artwork put on objects

Stylists: You are the final word on the subject. You are their thought leader. How your fans present themselves to the world is because of your influence.

They have bought into your worldview. They feel like they've connected to an important idea.

And to them, the products you sell are symbols of that worldview.

The experience you offer is high quality. But it isn't more expensive. It's available to everyone but only a few "understand".

And when they can't get enough of this first level experience...

That's what leads to the creation of the next level of "experience called:

Your art has so much impact on your fans that it creates an energy around your brand. This energy brings to life all sorts of spin offs.

For musicians: The live show and merch are the real money makers. They want to touch you.

Authors: Your book gets a movie deal... Your reading tours

Artists: Your original canvas in a gallery... Your collected works

Stylists: You have your own product line.

If you've taken the time to find your "artist blue ocean" (the combination of product and message that makes you one of a kind), your brand will fast-track what takes everyone else ages.

This is a version of your experience only available to fans with deep pockets.

Musician: A private performance.

Writers: You're ASKED to write a book on a topic. You teach small groups of other established writers.

Artists: a commissioned work.

Stylists: Getting hired to do make-up/hair/styling for a celebrity exclusively...

Ironically, the more expensive the experience, the less "work" you have to do to deliver. That's because at this stage of your career, your "value" is more symbolic than it is effort based.

that generate more income for LESS work.

This is the part of your audience that puts their money where their mouth is.

Alternative products are no longer an option for them.

You are the best version of your category to them.

This is the segment of your FANS who not only love you, but are vocal about it.

They promote what you do so hard that they attracting more FANS even while you sleep.

This is when leaders of other WORLDS become your Superfans.

You know you've arrived when your peers want to introduce THEIR WORLD to YOUR WORLD. It's when the people who have built their own incredible worlds-- Start to recognize and admire yours.

Another sign you've reached INTER-WORLD FANDOM is when big corporations (AKA fans with deep pockets) are ready to pay you to associate THEIR world with YOURS (or at the very least they'll try to gain temporary access to your world). They want to endorse you. They wanna advertise with you. They're ready to pay for access to the eyes and ears of your audience, your fans, and your superfans. They will pay anything to be near you. They do this hoping your aura will somehow rub off on them

It's at this point that you can zoom out and see the world you have built...

Is part of a whole universe.

Slogans and symbols start to emerge as your fans start to find shorthand to share your message between themselves. You and your fans have your own lingo. When your audience starts repeating the words and catchphrases you use like it's their own, you're getting there.

When others start to share your message without prompting from you AND / OR when they start to gather in your name.

You message gets mass adoption. It's bigger than you now. Many people don't even realize that you were the catalyst. The majority of culture shares your worldview (that years ago was on the fringes, wow).

Maybe you're still at the IDEAS / FOLLOWERS / NO MESSAGE level...

That's ok. It's still good to glance at this module now to understand where you're heading.

But please go back and study 'The Book Of Purpose' and 'The Book Of Influence' so you can move forward on a solid foundation.

Use The Mystery School to help you elevate your "great ideas" into a powerful HOLY TRINITY of:

PRODUCT (YOUR ART) / AUDIENCE (RIDE OR DIES) / MESSAGE (VISION).

And you want to expand your brand energy...

You have to know how to create an experience.

## YOU ARE HERE

## BASE LEVEL: THE HOLY TRINITY

### PRODUCT (the ONE thing you provide): art / career / idiom / art form / Polaris Star

### AUDIENCE (those who are listening): customers / clients / psychographic / pocket of people

### MESSAGE (the aspirational worldview that makes you different): articulated in words / a new niche / a new sound / an artist blue ocean.

## HOW YOUR ART BECOMES AN EXCLUSIVE 'EXPERIENCE'

## EXPERIENCE (BASE LEVEL): When your art takes on symbolic meaning for a special group of people. This is what happens when your product has connected with a group's identity.

### 16. WORLD BUILDING (PART II): HOW TO CREATE YOUR POWERFUL ONLINE EXPERIENCE

*Where can you take your audience to, that they will absolutely love, but that they’ve never been to before?

If you can answer this question successfully, you may have a million dollar brand.

Use this module to ask yourself the questions that will help you create an online experience that enhances people’s lives.

World Building is about making everything that you do online mirror the values and principles of your “real world” art or personal philosophy.

Every decision you make should be measured against: “Are we getting our audience closer to (insert whatever your ultimate experience is here)?”

Your experience should have extremely high exchange value (IE. be worth a lot of money - even if only on paper right now).

Build an experience of interconnected parts. (Every move you do online is connected to the other pieces of the puzzle.)

Make people say:

“What the fuck is (insert your brand name here)?????"

"Who the fuck is (insert personal brand here)???"

"I want to be a part of that world! I want to hang out with those people!”

Make it so powerful that even celebrities will want to get in on the action.

How do you want your product/experience/world to be seen by others? (Positioning Question #1)

How do you want yourself to be seen by others? (Positioning Question #2)

What are the repetitive parts of your world?

What are the "serial" aspects of your world that keeps them coming back?

Who are the reoccurring characters?

What are your "catchy" characteristic traits?

Your goal is to create an eyebrow-raising world until it blows up.

But that won't happen until you know what that world is.

That's why you have to answer these questions right now.

And If you're intentional and clear about it... It will happen. It's law.

It has to become your Polaris Star and the only thing on your mind.

Especially when you feel friction.

Purposely keep doing all the things your haters hate but that your Superfans cherish.

This will raise your exchange value until it's through the roof.

Now, it isn't just fun and games anymore.

It's a business.

And the next step is knowing the difference between YOUR WORLD and YOUR TOOLS.

### 17. WORLD BUILDING (PART III): YOUR WORLD VS. YOUR TOOLS

The first thing you have to decide is where is HOMEBASE for your WORLD.

For some of you it will be the "real world".

For example... A brick and mortar business.

Or a studio.

Or an event.

Or a product.

For some of you it's home will be online.

Like a website you build.

For some of you, your WORLD will live on someone else's platform.

Maybe your WORLD will live on Instagram. (side-note, never forget that Instagram's WORLD is an app that lives on someone else's platform. The IPHONE. No Steve Jobs, no Instagram. So when people complain about #freethenipple it makes me laugh because they forget that Instagram has to play by Apple's non-nudity rules. Their whole business model is built on someone else's platform.)

Or your WORLD may live on YouTube.

But the first thing is understanding where your home experience lives (YOUR WORLD). Because everything that is NOT your WORLD will be a TOOL to take your audience back home.

Don't confuse ATTRACTION TOOLS with YOUR WORLD.

Wherever people go to experience your art AND PAY YOU FOR IT is your WORLD.

Everything else should be treated like an ATTRACTION TOOL.

Understanding the distinction will help you manage your priorities every day.

If you find yourself investing more time on Instagram (for example) than in your WORLD, then you have your priorities wrong.

Or if your TOOLS aren't directly leading people to discover your WORLD (but instead you're using platform only to "post fun things"), then you're not treating it like a business.

(That doesn't mean every post has to promote. No, no. But build a strategy. For example... Build a story of posts that leads up to an invitation into your world. Ever notice that everything Drake posts leads up to an executable action on his fans part? That's how YOU need to behave.)

But understand that what's a WORLD for some, may be a TOOL for others. And vice versa.

Take for example YouTube:

How do you choose with so many options available out there?

By knowing who your audience is. (No, it isn't 'everybody'.)

By figuring out where your audience hangs out.

If they hang out at coffee shops, you need to hang out there too and find a way to bring them into your WORLD.

If they hang out on Instagram, you need to develop a presence on IG that serves to bring them back into your WORLD.

Figure out where your potential fans hang out... And hang out there too.

But never forget... That's not HOME.

You're only using this hangout "place" as a place to meet them.

But how do you identify your true fans among all the masses of people going by?

### 17. WORLD BUILDING (PART III): YOUR WORLD VS. YOUR TOOLS

### Most people use YouTube to promote things. But YouTubers use the platform as their WORLD. (That's what generates income for them.) So they use platforms like Instagram etc... to bring their audience back to YOUTUBE where all the action happens. But eventually a YouTuber may get a talk-show. Like Lilly Singh (former YouTuber with her own NBC television show now) And at that point they may decide to use what was once their WORLD (YouTube) as an ATTRACTION TOOL now.They've successfully expanded their brand energy.

## 1. Know the homebase of the WORLD you're building. (Where you make (or will make) your money.)

## 2. Figure out what ATTRACTION TOOLS you should use to attract people to your WORLD.

### 18. WORLD BUILDING (PART IV): YOUR AUDIENCE... NO, IT ISN'T 'EVERYBODY'

"Dear Bronques, Everyone I meet tells me they love my art. But for some reason my work doesn't seem to be connecting with the masses? What am I missing?"

Most creatives spend all day thinking about art.

The art that influences them.

The competition's art.

That's why they end up creating what's known as "art for art's sake".

But one day they wake up and realize "Nothings really happening". And they're confused. They know their art is "amazing"... I mean, all sorts of people tell them that their art is "amazing"... But for some reason they can't turn it into a career.

That's because "getting paid for your art" requires a different skillset than making "art for art's sake".

To get paid for what you do, you have to respect the holy trinity.

I'm guessing you have your art on point.

And I hope to God you've found your message (the reason you do what you do).

But have you ever asked yourself the million-dollar question:

Who are you making this art for?

I'm talking beyond your friends, your family, your boyfriend and all the lonely people that have been following you on Instagram since high school.

What I'm asking you is: What type of complete strangers... Would fall in love with what you do?

If you're thinking "everybody"... That's not a good sign.

You need to know who your audience REALLY is if you wanna make this your career.

Do you think when The Weeknd launched 'House Of Balloons' that he was making music for "everybody"?

Do you think when Dave Chappelle writes stand-up, that he does it to please "everybody"?

Do you think "SoundCloud rappers" get face tattoos that make them unrecognizable to their mothers to be in "everybody's" good books?

Then why are YOU are trying to appeal to the largest group you can? When the fastest path to your success is the complete opposite?

It's crazy but it's true: You need to make art that appeals to the SMALLEST (viable) group possible.

If you want to make this a career.

A group small enough to be feverishly united but big enough to matter and have a financial impact.

And you do that by creating art that's so unique to you that only that. small. group. could love it (for now).

Art that your biggest fans will tell outsiders that "they wouldn't understand."

Ok... Question.

I've asked this before elsewhere, but I need to ask it again here. How many of your followers would notice if you completely stopped posting on social media? Well... THAT'S how many REAL followers you have.

If you don’t have a pocket of people that would mourn the loss of your art, then you haven't brought value to the world yet. You don't have a business.

That "exchange value" is how you make money in this "creativity business".

You're not looking for casual listeners. Causal viewers. Casual readers.

You need to develop a niche of fans (or clients) who believe that you're the "bees knees" WAY before the masses catch on.

That "pocket of people" is what they call in marketing lingo: "your niche".

Figure out your niche. And go after them putting blinders on to the rest of humanity.

It's kinda like fishing.

You have to be the fisherman with the specialized bait, that's trying to catch cod.

Yes, I know you’ll see many juicy salmon swim by. But it’s ok, because you’ve decided to catch cod. Stay focused.

And now because you know what you're looking for... And because you have the right bait (thin slices of squid on your hook), you're gonna catch more cod than anyone else that's using "general bait" just hoping to catch ANY fish.

And people will think you're "lucky" for catching all that cod.

And soon they will line up to buy your cod. (Even the salmon fishermen.)

And eventually, you’ll need a street team to help you run your cod business.

And people will call you "the cod guy".

And you'll make it on 'Ellen'.

It will take patience... And discipline.

That is the actual "shortcut".

That is the "origin story" of all the great artists we love.

But once you know your AUDIENCE and you know the ATTRACTION TOOLS to get them into your WORLD...

How do you get them there? How do you turn this audience into fans?

You do it by using a completely revolutionary new way of looking at content creation.

### 19. WORLD BUILDING (PART V): MICRO-DOSING YOUR AUDIENCE

What's the least stressful way of using social media for your art?

How do you​ keep your audience entertained without getting burnt out yourself?

You use a concept as old as the streets:

Micro-dosing.

First, you have to figure out two things:

You answered that inWORLD BUILDING (PART II): HOW TO CREATE YOUR POWERFUL ONLINE EXPERIENCE

You answered that inWORLD BUILDING (PART III): YOUR WORLD VS. YOUR TOOLS.

With these answers, everything else can fall into place.

Every platform that is NOT YOUR WORLD is now a potential TOOL to bring people into your experience.

There are no rules.

One woman's tools can be another woman's whole experience:

Lululemon is using Tiktok as a tool. But Charli D'Amelio is using Tiktok as her entire experience.

Halsey is using YouTube as a tool. In contrast, Emma Chamberlain uses YouTube as her full experience.

Podcasts can be a tool, or they can be the whole experience.

Onlyfans can be a tool or the whole experience.

So, once again... Figure out:

Whatever you come up with is what we call your WORLD.

Every other platform that isn't your world = ATTRACTION TOOLS.

But the question that haunts so many creatives is...

HOW do you use these TOOLS to get people into your WORLD?

You do what the best drug dealers in the world do:

You micro-dose them.

I mean... Isn't art a drug? Doesn't the best poetry, music, painting, writing, and dance... INTOXICATE us?

So wouldn't that kind of make you the "pusher"?

I'm kidding. But I'm also not.

When David's Tea or innovative Whole Foods brands want to get people addicted to their product, they give you a SAMPLE.

EVERY MICRO-DOSE SHOULD CONTAIN THE ESSENCE OF YOUR ART.

"But, Father Bronques, what if my experience can't be 'bite-sized'?" (It always can. Be creative. But, still I'll humor you here.)

Give them an emotional microdose. Show other people experiencing your world. Give them that "I'll have what she's having" feeling by using the power of video. "Demonstration" is a powerful way of making people feel like they're ALMOST there. It's more potent than... giving them a coupon or a flyer.

But remember... Whatever you share to draw them in needs to be satisfying all on its own.

That's good business.

If you want to feel frustrated or waste energy... Give people enticing but unrelated micro-doses. Yes, it will attract them to your experience. But they won't stick around. Or they'll only stick around for the micro-doses.

If you were an Italian restaurant, would you give people a discount at the apple store? Or would you reel them in for life by giving them a bite of the main dish?

If you're a singer? Would you give them a thirst trap? Or would you give them a taste of your music?

It's easy to "trick" people into giving you attention-- But how satisfying is that if those people aren't committed to your WORLD?

And yes, sometimes it's expensive to give your customers some of your "stash" for free. But if you look at it in terms of the "lifetime value" of your die-hard fans...

It's more than worth it.

Why do you think Ben and Jerry's and Starbucks have days where they give their main thing away for free?

"Lifetime value" of their die-hard fans.

THE "TASTE" SHOULD CONTAIN THE WHOLE EXPERIENCE.

I know, I know... You always want examples:

People go to Instagram and Tiktok for entertainment. So entertain them. Do they want awesome videos? Give them awesome videos. Do they want a heartfelt connection? Give them genuine connections. Give them a taste of your art in the platform's format that contains your whole experience within it.

But don't limit yourself to only social media. There are millions of attraction tools available to you.

Even art forms can be attractions tools.

Take music, for example.

Movie producers use music as a tool to get people to see their movies all the time. They use music in movie soundtracks and trailers to attract fans into their movie world.

Music is a TOOL even for musicians!

MUSIC is the ultimate micro-dose.

A music career today is not about selling songs. It's about getting people HOOKED to songs, so they want the whole experience of the artist. That's why music artists who haven't built a world outside of their released songs have... nothing.

Give them that "music micro-dose" (hit song), and a year later, they've spent $80 on a concert ticket and $150 on merch, and they watch all your pay-per-views on VEEPS.

That's how you create a career with your art.

Know what business you're in.

Know what "your world" is.

(Your world = your experience + where people go to consume it).

Treat everything else as an attraction tool to get them there.

Attraction Tools like SOCIAL MEDIA: Instagram, Tiktok, Twitch, Twitter, Snapchat, and Facebook.

Or attraction tools like TRADITIONAL MEDIA: Podcasts, Onlyfans, Music, TV, radio, magazines, and blogs.

Treat every appearance you make in traditional media as a micro-dose of your experience. You do that by staying on message in interviews and reinforcing the themes that drew in your biggest fans.

Microdose of the experience.

Music: streaming

Painter: sketches, showing yourself painting on youtube

Dancer: American Ballet performing in the park

For a musician, this might be vinyl, merch etc...

For a painter, this might be buying the actual painting.

For a dancer, this could be dance classes, dancing in someone's music video.

For a musician, this is a live show. Or a private performance for a prince in Dubai.

For a painter, this is a commissioned piece (Warhol made millions doing this)

For a dancer, this would be creating choreography for someone.

Ready to build your "world"?

### 20. WORLD BUILDING (PART VI): LANGUAGING

When people say the word “snacks”, what do you think of?

Probably Cheetos, chips…

But what if they say the word “appetizers”, what do you think of?

Probably wings, crab cakes…

But what if someone says “hors d'oeuvres”?

Probably deviled eggs, burrata… The more expensive stuff.

Isn’t it funny how they’re basically all the same thing? They’re all “snacks”. But yet, each word gives you a different vibe.

And isn’t it ironic how artists, the biggest “vibe creators” there are… Often use the most boring words to describe their art?

Welcome to your new world…

Languaging.

Let’s start at the beginning.

When you finish a work of art, what’s the next step?

Sharing it, right?

You share it with the world using the platforms you own (email list, website), and the platforms you borrow (social media).

COPYWRITING is the strategic use of words to get people interested in what you’re doing. (You went throughTHE COPYRIGHTING MODULEalready, right?)

But LANGUAGING is using words to make your art more immersive.

LANGUAGING is the words you use to communicate with your audience once they’ve already entered your world.

It’s best described by example.

When I was working with the 13lunas sisters (TMS artists), I suggested they stop using generic names for their magic potions… Instead, draw words from occult text. No more “perfumes and oils” like every other tincture queen with a Shopify account… Now it’s “elixirs, anointing oils and spiritual Banos”.

LANGUAGING is also how you choose to name yourself…

I also suggested that the sisters never use the shortened version of their names anywhere online (Patty and Dani). And to only use their full names (Patricia and Daniela)… So they sound more… Regal.

LANGUAGING can also be applied to how you name your artform…

Are you a rapper like everyone else… Or are you an “urban poet”? Or a “verbal architect”? Or as Public Enemy famously said “the CNN of black culture”?

I introduced the concept of LANGUAGING to Theresa (TMS artist), last month. She’s building a marketing consultancy business for musicians. I explained to her that she should probably never use the word “marketing”, “consultancy” or “business” anywhere in her branding. Especially if she’s serious about being an alternative to all those gross generic music consultants you see online.

She desperately needs LANGUAGING. She’s working on it. I’ll share/test the new language with you when she finds it. (Email me if you have ideas for her.)

LANGUAGING creates a new world for you and your community. A world where you have your own lingo.

But LANGUAGING is also choosing the words you will NEVER use…

Did you see the video that Jack Conte (founder of Patreon) released on his social media a few weeks ago? He instructed his team to wipe all mentions of the word “content” from anywhere on their site, and all external communication. From now on, they will never use that word to describe what creators are sharing with their audience anymore. (We are winning, congregation!)

Jack Conte understands languaging.

And remember when Sean Parker (Justin Timberlake) says to Mark Zuckerberg in the ‘The Social Network’, “Drop the ’THE’. Just ‘Facebook’. It’s cleaner that way.”

That’s also LANGUAGING.

It’s time you start building a world around your art using LANGUAGING.

Put the words you use under a microscope. Rethink each of them. Make them your own. Like this:

1. Use words people hardly use.

2. Use old words in new ways.

3. Make up words.Should you be calling your paintings “paintings”? Or calling them “snapshots of your dreams”.

Is the place you make art your “studio”? Or your “lair”?

Are you making videos? Or “cinematic diaries”?

Are you just another “pop-punk” musician… Or are you making “revolution music”.

Every time you change the words, you change the vibe the audience gets. You elevate your work before they’ve even fully experienced the actual art.

The words become A PART OF the experience.

Set yourself apart.

Differentiate yourself.

Look at my own use of languaging over the years. I even created a dictionary for my movement:

🔑 THE MYSTERY SCHOOL LEXICON (A-Z)

### 🔑 21. The Copywriting Module

A student started one of my favorite YouTube channels a few years ago. It was about going back to her roots and reconnecting to her cultural heritage. Video by video. So good! Her channel would inspire others to do the same and discover a new world through her eyes.

But every video got further and further away from the original “mission statement” she had started with.

So that’s when I asked her the million-dollar question…

Which I will get to in a second.

Another student sent me his crowdfunding page for the new movie he’s trying to make. In the email, the project sounded promising, until I got to the crowdfunding website… Then my energy drained.

So I asked HIM the million-dollar question also…

Which I will get to in a second.

Most artists believe that the world works in the following way: You share your art, and either the world likes it or it doesn’t. If people like it, you become successful. If they don’t, it’s time to find a “real job”. This deranged artist myth is why so many creative people are on an emotional roller coaster. One day, you’re confident. The next day, you don’t know if you’ll EVER be good enough.

The artist myth is that people are “caught” by art that moves them. All in one sweeping moment of grand emotion.

Sure, that happens sometimes. But only when someone’s defenses are completely down. Like they’re kissing the love of their life, and your song happens to come on. Or they’re backpacking in Europe, they walk into a gallery cafe, they see your little painting in the window sill, and they buy it.

But those instances are rare. Nowadays, people’s defenses are way up.

Personally, I like how crazy it is.

Because it’s truthful. You know that if you somehow manage to get an audience’s attention, you know it’s real. No one (except maybe your friends and family) has the energy to pat you on the back, or look at what you’re doing unless you “catch them, then move them”.

The audience doesn’t lie. When they are moved they will tell you. Or even better… They’ll be speechless. You will feel it in the air. If you don’t get that kind of positive reaction, then they weren’t moved.

But many artists don’t realize that moving the audience isn’t phase I. It’s Phase II.

You have to “catch them” first. You have to get their attention.

“Artists are no better than porn stars or influencers. You’re all in the same business, which is… ‘Seeking Attention’.” — Bob Lefsetz

That’s what makes art agents and record labels so desirable. Their only job is to make sure your art is seen by people. They can’t make people like it, but they can make sure it gets its time in the sun. Once they’ve done that part, it’s up to the charisma of your art to do the rest.

The problem is, you have to CATCH those gatekeepers, too, before they will work on your behalf.

But maybe you’re thinking, I don’t want to catch anyone, I just want to be creative. You’d be missing the point. ALL OF IT is creative, babe. Imagine saying “I only want to make music. I don’t care about the album art” (the thing that catches some people BEFORE they even hear the music). Every step is creative if you let it be. Your instagram should be creative. Your emails should be creative. Your promo videos should be creative. Your website… If you let them be.

When your attempts don’t work at first, don’t cry. This is only feedback. Just try again, but in another way. That’s the journey. It’s called iteration.

If you’re not getting any likes on Instagram it’s not because you suck. It’s because you haven’t figured out how to make people care enough to stop. You see? That’s a different problem.

If no one is adding your songs to playlists, or using them for sync licenses, it’s because they have no clue you even exist. You see? That’s a different problem.

You’ve been putting so much focus on trying to move people with your art that you never bothered to improve the skills of how to make them NOTICE YOU.

The cart before the horse.

Before you can “move them”, you have to “catch them”.

But what I want to get through to you is this… don’t judge your art yet. Not at this phase of the game. No one has even seen it. You’re still learning how to get through the door, remember? THEY HAVEN’T EVEN SEEN IT. You didn’t “catch them” yet.

Have you ever seen a child get excited about what they’re about to show you BEFORE they unveil it? That’s them trying to “catch you” first. They want your full attention before they show you anything. Children understand how it works.

But how do you do that? How do you catch people’s attention? How do you get an audience… Or gatekeepers… Or even collaborators… To notice you? Especially when you’re brand new?

Have you ever seen a child get excited about what they’re about to show you BEFORE they unveil it? That’s them trying to “catch you” first. They want your full attention before they show you anything. Children understand how it works.

There are only three ways.

You don’t need to become a “photographer”. You only need to become great at using photography in a way that serves your art. Invest in finding ways of photographing your art that a professional photographer wouldn’t even think of.

Become an expert at sharing your art with video. Use your phone—It’s good enough. While using the bare minimum, you may invent things that the typical videographer would never think of. Make videos of your art that make us drool for more of it.

But the #1 skill you must sharpen if you want your art to get attention is…

The million-dollar question that I always end up asking artists who aren’t presenting themselves in the most powerful way they can is this:

"HAVE YOU EVER STUDIED COPYWRITING?"

Copywriting = The skill of communicating to get someone to take action.

But copywriting, my fellow artists… Is an invisible art form. The better you do it, the less anyone will notice it. They’ll be too busy ACTING on the words you wrote.

Most artists who communicate online aren’t copywriting. They’re winging it. They’re writing stream-of-conscious. They’re sharing “morning pages” vomit, hoping somehow people care. Don’t get me wrong. “Morning pages” are amazing. It’s a great tool to clear out your brain. But “stream-of-consciousness” babbling online is NOT the way to write to communicate with your community! Or especially with a jaded audience who has their guard up.

Writing a video script, email, or DM… should never be done “off the cuff”. That won’t make it more “authentic”. It’ll just make it unwatchable, unreadable, or boring.

I don't want you to become a "writer" any more than I want you to become a photographer or a videographer. I want you to be a good communicator that get eyes on your work. Not making rookie mistakes, just because you don't know simple copywriting.

You have to “catch them” before you can “move them”.

Copywriting is the process of writing persuasive words that motivate people to take action.

Where could you benefit from learning copywriting techniques?

- When you have to write an IG caption under your art.

- Emailing a potential collaborator.

- DM’ing someone asking for help.

- Writing a newsletter to your fans.

- Text for your website.

- Your script for your YouTube or Tiktok videos.

- Writing a bio.

- Anytime you are trying to sell your art.

So, stop settling for the first words that come to mind, and then wonder why no one is responding. Instead, treat that initial idea as the FIRST DRAFT. Then…

Apply the basics of copywriting:

Copywriting teaches you all of that.

The problem is, most people who teach copywriting have a “sales-y” and gross approach” to it. After all, it’s salespeople and entrepreneurs who are their biggest customers. They teach you how to manipulate, instead of teaching you how to CONNECT.

When I was studying copywriting, I always had to read between the lines to find the more artist-friendly gold. But most creatives I know have no patience for that. That’s why I’ve been on this mission to find something more digestible…

Well, I have two amazing resources for you.

Packed with information that can help you. And presented in a FUN way.

VERY GOOD COPY: 207 Copywriting Micro-Lessons

I ordered the book myself, and yes, I can recommend it to artists. (92% rating on Amazon!)

Eddie has a newsletter, too. So you can subscribe to it first and see if you like his style before fully committing to the book.

VERY GOOD COPY NEWSLETTER

This newsletter has lots of pretty pictures, and it just having it pop up in your inbox should remind you to pay attention to your writing more.

The Marketing Examples Newsletter

These two resources should start you off in the right direction.

### The Artist's Guide To Storytelling

I watch artist's videos and I read their newsletters. And while on the surface, they seem fine, in reality, they aren’t connecting. Artists think they're telling us a story, but all we hear is "word vomit".

For blame, look no further than the creative writing courses we took in grade school. Those teachers did us dirty.

A better definition of storytelling is urgently needed today.

Case in point? Watch this video from The Black Wonder Twins (TMS artist):

Do you see what's "wrong" with it? Do you see what's missing to really make it connect with an audience?

Ok, now watch this one too from Mighty Eli (TMS artist also):

Both of these videos are raw and fun. They have good ideas. But bad execution.

They're missing the same thing YOU are when you make videos for your art.

Learn that word. Memorize it.

You have no STAKES in your storytelling. But after today, I hope that will change.

The definition of storytelling you were taught in school is to “tell us what happed”. And innocently, you’ve been telling stories that way ever since. Not realizing that you’re boring your audience.

The truth is… That was never what storytelling was about.

And you do that by having STAKES.

STAKES represent what a character has to lose or gain as a result of the story's unfolding.

STAKES are the driving force behind a character's actions and motivations, making the audience care about the outcome of the story.

STAKES can be personal, emotional, or external, but they are always clear, HIGH, and ESCALATING as the story progresses. (High! Escalating!)

Without STAKES the audience has nothing to wonder about, and you have nothing to tease them with.

Might Eli's video above has NO STAKES. And that’s why videos like these always fail to resonate beyond the artist’s immediate circle. You see, your immediate circle ALREADY KNOWS YOUR STAKES. That’s why when they see a video like this they love it. They applaud it. They tell you you’re the best. But to an audience that’s wasn’t there for your every waking moment, it’s just images and words. You have given them no reason to get invested.

Same with The Black Wonder Twins video above... Never did I feel like something was hanging in the balance.

“This surgery could ruin my career.”

Nice opening line. But empty words in the end. Because they never told us HOW it might ruin their career. Actually, they did quite the opposite. They described how they have PLENTY OF TIME (5 months) before the surgery to get all their work done. Okayyyy??? And they even told us how they ALREADY have 130 songs recorded. So why should we care? Twins, you have 5 months to mix and master the songs and create the videos. Why is that hard? Where is the conflict? Where is the challenge?

Where are the STAKES?

STAKES is: “I have 5 months to write and record an album before I have an operation. Usually, I write a song a month. So I’m gonna have to find a new gear if I want to get this done. Every week I’m going to add a new layer of complexity so I can reach my goals.”

STAKES is: “I’m going to release this album, make videos, and play the online game to build my career after my operation. Even if I have to do it on painkillers and limited resources.”

STAKES is… explaining why the months before will be hard. STAKES is… explaining why the months after will be hard. With details that make us FEEL IT.

When you make sure your storytelling has STAKES, you show you have empathy. You're saying that you value people's time and attention. You're signaling you want your time with the audience to be fun, not boring.

But The Black Wonder Twins and Mighty Eli aren't doing that yet in their videos.

And neither are you.

Ask yourself these questions after you write the first draft of your script:

“Am I just telling people ‘what happened’? Or am I making them wonder ‘what happens next’? Do I have high and escalating stakes in my storytelling?”

When you put your videos or newsletters through this microscope, you will see weaknesses immediately. Yes, it might even "bum you out" at first because you'll realize the whole thing is structured all wrong. But if you put in the effort to fix it, more of the right people will flock to your community.

Let me show you the difference STAKES makes. Here is the same video, with and without stakes. (Courtesy of Che, a TMS artist who went through the iteration process in WRKSHOP.)

Here is Che's video without STAKES:

I had to ask Che, “What are the stakes in this video?”

Her reply was: “The stakes are finishing this painting before I leave for my trip to Greece. It’s not about the deadline, but it’s about proving myself that I can hold the discipline and story all day way till the end. If I finish, I board the plane with closures if I don’t, I carry the weight of an unfinished piece.”

Ah, so she understands stakes (like I’m sure you do), but she still isn’t including it INSIDE THE VIDEO.

So I replied: “Stakes are not just saying, "it's important". Stakes is explaining WHY IT'S IMPORTANT TO YOU, so we can feel it like you do. Then we will root for you. You have to make sure you tell us THE CONSEQUENCES OF NOT ACHIEVING YOUR GOALS. Don’t assume we know. We don’t. Che, this video should have been about you explaining the reason finishing this painting is important. "I'm going to Greece and I hope I finish this painting on time" isn't stakes. (especially when the painting looks pretty much finished anyway) You need to make us feel it. Something like… "I have so many unfinished paintings. It's starting to make me feel bad as an artist, never finishing. And now I'm going on this trip to Greece. I'm not even excited about it. Not as excited as I should be anyway. And it's all because I know my self-esteem can't handle having another unfinished painting to add to the lot. It'll ruin my headspace. And my holidays. I'll be miserable the whole time thinking about it. That's why it's stressing me out so much right now. I have exactly 5 days to finish the (list what you have to finish), which would normally take me 2 weeks. Somehow, I have to fit it in every night after work. Let's see how far we can get tonight."

So she redid the video. And this is what she came up with:
