### 22. Are You Ready? Like For Real?

Every now and then, people from various industries hit me up and ask me if I "know anyone that can X?"

Because of this, I've already been able to pass along some work to talented Mystery Students who were on my radar looking for jobs.

And now, more and more of the clients that approach me are willing to working with creatives remotely.

They WANT to give new voices a chance. (Thank you, pandemic.)

So, I'd like to expand my current database to include YOU, if you're ready, so that whenever potential clients or collaborators hit me up-- I can recommend you on the fly.

If you're a professional (or aspiring) creative:

video director

video editor

illustrator

photographer

music producer

hair-stylist

make-up artist

creative director

There are brands out there that need your help.

If you're unsure of yourself, use this as an exercise to see IF you’re ready to strut your stuff.

I can give you an honest opinion, without sugar coating anything.

If your professional description isn’t precise, Imma tell you.

If your work examples or presentation need an update, I’ll be brutally honest (sorry, not sorry).

Let's get your "portfolio" tight so I can pass it along immediately when there's a perfect fit. That way you're not scrambling... And end up losing the opportunity.

(But you know the rules... Anything I see, I may use as an example for other students to learn from!)

So if you're interested...

Send me an email - bronques@lastnightsparty.tv - with these 4 things:

If I can help you land your next big client or collaborator, that would make my day.

Here are a few guidelines for the answers:

The best artists create like René Redzepi (the creator of the #1 restaurant in the world, Noma)... With ingrédients that are in season and locally sourced.

The city where you live should inform your work. Use what's around you. You don't have to live in LA or Paris. Make your city your strength. What colors are around you? What unique people? How does your environment have a subliminal influence on your work?

Slashies beware... The more slashes you use IE: photographer / designer / writer... the more you weaken your "personal brand".

Clients don't want to work with artists who are a Chinese menu.

They want an artist with a voice.

Pick your lane. Your niche. Your specialty. Your "thing".

I admit... You get more "no’s" that way.

But remember, you only need a few yeses to have a career.

And they will feel like you’re their soulmate.

Interns, friends of friends, or the person you met on the plane... They need a short description they can tell their boss (or whoever is releasing the budget) to get them excited about YOU-- to make it impossible for them to choose someone else.

You’re a photographer, yes. But what is special about you? Maybe you “take the most debaucherous party pictures on the planet”?

You’re a hairdresser, yes. But what’s special about you? Maybe you're the trusted go-to stylist for the drag queen community in Austin, TX?

People just want to know that you’re professional enough to organize what you do into a nice presentation they can glance at and show other people.

The way you present your work is one of the first ways you establish trust. You DON'T need volume.

If you want to leave the biggest impression with your "portfolio" leave them with more than merely examples of your work... Leave them with an impression of WHAT YOU STAND FOR.

As you prepare your "portfolio", come back here often, and then hit me up when you’re ready to turn the world on it's head.

Why do I keep putting "portfolio" in quotes? It's to remind you to think out of the box. It may be a website. It may be your IG. It may be a singular video that tells your story.

OR... Maybe it's a NEW form of media presentation that gets people excited about your work even before they've seen the contents.

You're a creative.

Be creative even here.

### 23. Free VS Paid

Erika (Mystery Student) sent me this question the other day:

Creators often struggle with the notion of FREE vs. PAID.

I had to come up with a solution for this problem after a few months of launching lastnightsparty. Later I found out that there was a name for what I was using:

Value Ladders

This is how you can create one for yourself.

You need to write down everything you do as a creator that has value.

Write down everything that you can think of. Even if you're not doing it yet.

Scalable is a business conept to describe anything that you do that can reach more and more people without requiring more effort from you. Like playing a show: whether it's 5 people or 100, it's the same effort. That makes that activity scalable.

On the other hand... Shooting a campaign for a brand is NOT scalable because it requires you to do something unique, for one person.

THE SCALABLE LIST:

Put everything you can think of that you do that can easily be done / shared with 1 or 1M people without any extra effort on your part.

THE NON-SCALABLE LIST

Move all the things on the master list that AREN'T scalable to this list.

Things that require more time for you to do...

Or they require you to be physically there because you can't outsource it to anyone else etc...

Or anything that is a 1 on 1 service...

Or special appearance...

Take a good look at the things you put on the SCALABLE LIST and figure out which things on that list should be free and which things should be paid for.

Start a new list for those things called:

THE FREEMIUM LEVEL

For example: Instagram should be on the FREEMIUM LIST.

This is a popular way for creators of giving their audience a piece of what they do for FREE.

Or in Erika's case (question above) it could be doing a weekly "Zoom workout" class.

What you will be able to achieve with the FREEMIUM LEVEL:

The next level... all the stuff that is scalable, but that you will charge for.

What you will achieve with the KILLER PRODUCTS LEVEL:

This is where musicians can make money on merch.

Producers can make audio packs.

Artists can teach classes.

You'll notice that any of these things could have been on the freemium level too. But the key is to officially separate them in your mind and in your presentation so the people in your audience know all the boundaries. And once you set these boundaries, stick to them. That way you never have to feel bad. And your audience never feels cheated.

But where you draw the line is up to you.

For example, Erika could have decided to put "Zoom workouts" on this level instead.

She can charge people to be part of the class for a very small fee and overdeliver with a great product. But then she also could turn around and make "3 first Zoom workout classes" her FREEMIUM LEVEL.

What you will achieve with the EXCLUSIVE LEVEL:

For musicians that may be playing live.

For photographers that's shooting a campaign for a brand.

For a trainer that's one-on-one coaching.

Don't get me wrong. Before you can charge premium dollar for these things you'll have to do versions of them for very small fees.

But use these moments to fine-tune your product.

And then use the results to create value for the other two levels as BONUS MATERIAL. Never give things from the exclusive level for free.

If there isn't money exchanged, there still has to be some sort of trade to establish your value.

Train yourself to always find the trade.

You're on the rise.

Value yourself.

So that you can set up realistic financial expectations for yourself, start to think of your different levels like this:

With those figures in mind you can calculate how many people you have to reach (at a 5% conversion rate) in order to have a viable business.

Are you ready for the hustle it will require?

Girls that use ONLYFANS.COM have mastered this business model. They use Instagram for free stuff to attract people. And then their next level is the monthly subscription. And then the most dedicated fans pay premium prices for the private stuff.

But don't forget this fun "game-changing" fact...

Sometimes your mid-level KILLER PRODUCTS become the cash cow. The mid-level income source can surpass EXCLUSIVE even though you charge more for EXCLUSIVE.

Well, that's the very nature and reward of a popular scalable product.

That's exactly what happened to Metallica and every other metal band in the world.

They make more on merchandise than they do playing live. People want to own rock t-shirts even when they don't listen to the music. And there's no limit to how many t-shirts you can sell.

But there's a limit to how many shows you can play.

So pay attention to ALL the levels equally because they all play off each other.

That's right. Never disregard the FREEMIUM LEVEL. Give it energy. But the right energy. Know WHY you're doing things for free. Review the 4 reasons for FREEMIUM above.

Sidenote: That's why creating THE ULTIMATE IG is essential. A vanity based IG won't cut if you want this business model to work.

Now that you understand the basics, we're going to tackle the concept of how to create a whole experience for your audience in the next module:

WORLD BUILDING

### 23. Free VS Paid

## FIRST, MAKE A MASTER LIST OF ALL YOUR OFFERINGS AS A CREATIVE

#### Your creations themselves.

#### The creations you do for others (commisions, campaigns, one-on-ones)

#### Teaching your knowledge.

#### Giving a peek inside your world.

## THEN, SPLIT THE MASTER LIST INTO TWO LISTS: SCALABLE AND NON-SCALABLE

## FREEMIUM LEVEL

#### 1. Stay creative because creativity is like breathing to you.

#### 2. Try new things out constantly

#### 3. Give people a TASTE of what you do

#### 4. Attract people to the KILLER PRODUCTS LEVEL (but you should be totally fine for them to stay at this level too. 'Cause sometimes those 'static' fans still attract other fans that "level up").

## KILLER PRODUCTS LEVEL

#### 1. Needs to be inexpensive. This is how you figure out who your buyers are.

#### 2. Needs to be AMAZING. Way more value than whatever you decide to charge. Change people's lives. Overdeliver.

#### 3. Attract people to the next level (but you're totally fine if they stay at this level too).

## EXCLUSIVE LEVEL

#### 1. Give people unparalleled access to you.

#### 2. Share one-time only experiences.

#### 3. Make the most amount of money at a time.

## WELCOME TO YOUR NEW BUSINESS MODEL

#### What you do for the FREEMIUM LEVEL will attract 5% of people to pay for the KILLER PRODUCT LEVEL.

#### And the KILLER PRODUCT LEVEL will attract 5% of people to pay for the EXCLUSIVE LEVEL.

### 24. Don't Quit Your Day Job

Why is it that SOME people can still be creative after working a long day job, and then other people are totally brain dead when they get back home from work?

Is it in the genes?

Is it a gift that you're born with?

Or is it a talent that you can learn?

Take my friend Madi for example...

Madi works at a thrift store. And the owner treats her like absolute dirt.

He's always threatening to fire her for just about anything. Even though her energy is probably the best thing he's got going for his little business right now

But because he's a jerk, she never gets to bask in that sense of job security that's so essential to most of us

But guess what , when she gets home, something magical happens....

Like when I used to work at H&M. That was the last job I had before I became a photographer.

My first day working retail happened to be on Black Friday. The absolute worst day to be on the floor.

But luckily for me, the asian guy I was working with taught me everything I needed to know before we opened the doors, and by the afternoon I was killing it.

So eventually I got the managers to put me everywhere:

Divided Red, Divided Black, Hennes Gold, accessories... Whatever it took to learn the ropes.

But do you know where I ended up learning everything I would later use in photography

The fitting room.

It's only when I started doing shifts in the fitting room that I began to fully understand the effect that clothes could have on a women's psyche.

I got see the same Hennes Gold top on a million different body sizes, and body shapes, and I was like ohhhhh.

I started developing an eye for what would and wouldn't work before you even tried something on.

And one day, this woman came in. Tough as nails. The type of person who locks eyes with you and doesn't let go.

Turns out She was the manager for the Aldo down the street. And she wanted me to go work for her. Selling shoes. It was hilarious. She was trying to poach me from H&M.

But here's what she said that stuck with me:

"I need more people like you. You're an artist. You guys do everything with love."

And I had never thought of it that way. I guess I had been approaching my retail job as an extension of my art. And that's when I decided to expand that idea to everything.

So, when I started taking pictures a few months later. And I was with my muse, and she asked me what she should wear... You can pretty much imagine that I had an opinion.

H&M had inadvertently become my apprentisship.

I knew what clothes to pick to make my model look amazing. And what would boost her confidence. And how to hide the things she was self-conscious about. And how to use clothes to solve problems...

But most of all, the fitting room had taught me the correct way of talking to a woman when she's trying on clothes and asking for your feedback

You want to be honest...

But you don't want her to turn on you in the middle of a shoot because you said the wrong thing that completely ruined the vibe.

So what I realize now is that if I had decided to HATE my way through my all of my days jobs, I would have missed a crazy opportunity.

I think what made those jobs bear fruits for me later on was that I always tried to do them with as much dedication as I could muster.

And stay in the moment.

And that's what I see in my friend Madi. She approaches absolutely everything with love.

That's why she always finds the strength to create beautiful art no matter what went down during the day with her horrible boss.

Other people... The ones that are frustrated or angry... They're just worried that maybe they're destined to be stuck in an awful job for the rest of their lives

But when you KNOW that it's temporary, and that you're an artist, and that no matter where you are or what you're doing, that you have to continue to act like artist at all times... Then, you can turn on a different switch in your head when you're working those shitty jobs. Hell, you might even end up doing it with a smile on your face.

And that way, when you get home later...

You're not drained.

You're not burnt out.

You're still operating on that artist continuum.

You still have fuel, and now you can apply it to the real stuff.

And that, I think, is what earns you the right later on, to create art as a full time job.

So remember.

Wherever you are right now... You're not gonna be there forever.

And while it may not look like this situation will benefit you in the future, it absolutely will.

Every situation you will ever be in will inform your art.

If you allow it to.

And it will do it twice.

The first time will be when it magically shows up in your artistic work. Surprising you with it's wisdom.

And the second time will be when you get a chance to share the story with other people that may need to hear it one day.

Ok, so now that you know the importance of letting your 9 to 5 job inform your art as much as you can...

What do you need to do in the rest of your waking hours so that it doesn't steal your soul?

Master Your Book Ends

## THE BOOK OF APPENDIX: Resources To Help You Rise


### 🔑 1. NINE RECOMMENDED BOOKS FOR BUILDING CREATIVE ENERGY

I've read all these books multiple times. Good books should be studied if you really want to get the gold and the silver out of them. I've recommended these to others who have also had their lives changed by them. So, you can invest in all 9 of them knowing they are "risk-free" energy builders.

Paulo Coelho

My favorite book of all time. There are so many secrets unlocks in this book. I read it every year.

Steven Pressfield

This is the book I've read that most closely resembles The Mystery School philosophy. How to conquer your creative demons.

Christopher Alexander

The Godfather of Architechture explains how PROCESS affects the outcome. And how your PROCESS is the difference between creating something that isradiating full of life... And creating something that isdead on arrival. This book is meditative. And it may even make you cry.

Mihaly Csikszentmihalyi

The absolute bible on how to achieve the state of mind that every artist wishes they could stay in forever.

Duane Tudhal

A full documentation of the recording sessions for 1999 and Purple. Day by Day. A guide on how to become the most prolific artist that you can possibly be.

Edward de Bono

The best description of what happens inside a healthy creative person's mind.

Stephen King

Don't let the title fool you. This is a book for ALL creatives.

Oscar Wilde

You don't need to read the whole book. Just read the preface.

Ralph Waldo Emerson

If this short essay doesn't get you back on track every time, maybe you weren't made for this.

I've read all of these books multiple times also, but they're not automatic recommendations only because it depends on where you are on your journey.

Atomic Habits

James Clear

The bible of how to form new positive habits.

Why We Sleep

Matthew Walker

The modern bible on sleep. And how it affects your creativity.

Zero To One

Blake Masters and Peter Thiel

A scientific look at how to create ideas that have never existed before.

The Alter Ego Effect: The Power Of Secret Identities To Transform Your Life

Todd Herman

How entertainers, artists, and athletes use alter-egos to help them do the things they are too afraid to do normally.

The Master Game: Beyond the Drug Experience

Robert S. de Ropp

My friend Bruce introduced me to this book. It explains The 4th State Of Consciousness. The secret to mastering the shadow self.

Autobiography Of A Yogi

Paramahansa Yogananda

I re-read Chapter 12 over and over again. Unfortunately for it to have it's full effect on you, you have to read everything leading up to it. But if you invest that time... When Chapter 12 arrives it is just pure truth. (This was also known as Steve Jobs's favorite book.)

A book to remind you why being original is more likely to make you successful in a world full of "copies of a copy".

Hermann Hesse

A novel about following your own path while everyone else is following gurus.

The Andy Warhol Diaries

Pat Hackett

One of the most prolific artists who ever lived also made time to document every day.

Rebel without a Crew: Or How a 23-Year-Old Filmmaker With $7,000 Became a Hollywood Player

Robert Rodriguez

Shows you to what extent someone can go to to realize their vision when they seem to have no resources.

The Beautiful Fall

Alicia Drake

Watch the complete opposite creative approach of 2 fashion geniuses.

The Rise of Superman: Decoding the Science of Ultimate Human Performance

Steven Kotler

Recommended by Dave:"I’ve actually been interested in flow for almost a decade now after someone explained it to me. I’ve always “known” what flow was, and it’s always been my ultimate goal to get better and better at just flipping that switch and being in it. My absolute favorite book on flow is “The Rise of Superman” by Steven Kotler because it doesn’t read like a textbook, it reads like an exciting adventure that makes you wonder just how amazing the human body and mind is and if we’re capable of so much more than we allow of ourselves."

Start with Why

Simon Sinek

Recommended by Freddy Kuno:"It's popular among Marketing and Entrepreneur folks, but the message is essentially the same as The Drill Down Nethod: you (and people) need to know fucking WHY you do what you do. WHY should anyone listen to you and not to someone else? Follow you and not anyone else? It will also help any creative working for big brands to think about this."

Amusing Ourselves to Death: Public Discourse in the Age of Show Business

Neil Postman

Recommended by Wesley:"It was written in 1985, but I think it’s extremely relevant to the modern media landscape. In the book he argues that “a brave new world” by Aldous Huxley (and it's SOMA drug) is a much better prediction of the modern world compared to “1984”. I find it interesting and somewhat ironic that 1984 is taught in schools as almost a way of instilling fear of a totalitarian government and thoughts censorship, when our current reality is arguably worse."

Consider This: Moments in My Writing Life After Which Everything Was Different

Chuck Palahniuk

Recommended by Tomson:"Yup. The fight club guy. But wow. It is really The Mystery School! His anecdotes... His obsession with testing his writings with his audience... One of my favorite quotes: "Witness the movies that premiered to damning reviews. The Night of the Living Dead. Harold and Maude. Blade Runner. They found a place in public memory, and time has made them classics. So do not write to be liked. Write to be remembered."

Scary Close

Donald Miller.

Recommended by Haley:"This book will challenge the way you love and the way you receive it. It’s a book about giving up the act and picking up true intimacy in this life."

Elizabeth Gilbert

Recommended by Ines:"She really shows you how the low moments are integral part of the process. And how if you don't act on inspiration the moment when it hits you, it will leave. Full of stories to back her points up too..."

Daily Rituals: How Artists Work

Daily Rituals: Women At Work

Mason Currey

Recommended by Ines:"Mason Currey wrote a book called Daily rituals: How artists work. It talks about known artists in all creative fields and what are/were their routines / disciplines / rituals. While I was deciding if it's anything worth buying, I found out that he came across an issue - he got a lot of feedback on the fact that there's only a few women mentioned in the book. So he put together another one called Daily rituals: Women at work. So instead, I bought that one. And it is a gem. So many inspiring stories of creatives I hadn't even heard of, but that really should be celebrated. It's a treasure trove of inspiring quotes on creatives' lives."

Letters to a Young Poet

Rainer Maria Rilke

Recommended by Jillian:"This book always puts everything back into perspective for me. It emphasizes the importance of being alone to look within yourself, and is such an insightful collection of letters and advice."

The Untethered Soul

The Surrender Experiment

Michael Singer

Recommended by David:"These books go very well with the book of mental health. Being able to not get lost in your emotions is a great tool for an artist imho, and Singer's books have helped me so much in dealing with those "dark nights of the soul"

Zen and the Art of Motorcycle Maintenance

Robert M. Pirsig

Recommended by Rowen:"I've avoided this book for a while but when it popped up in a free bin at a random coffee shop, all torn to shit and written over, I had to pick it up. I always thought this book was just some pop psych pulp phenom, full of bullshit platitudes and half baked ideas. Plot twist, it's not that at all."

### 2. FOUR RECOMMENDED FILMS / TV SHOWS FOR BUILDING CREATIVE ENERGY

I've watched these films and TV shows multiple times. Good films should be studied if you really want to get the gold and the silver out of them. I've recommended these to others who have also had their lives changed by them. So, you can safely invest your time in them knowing they are "risk-free" energy builders.

NOTE TO SELF: Don’t binge-watch TV series, biographies and movies like the normals do. Protect your energy. Consume long-form media in 15-20 minute increments instead. I remember the first time I did that. It was with David Lynch’s Mulholland Drive. I felt like I had discovered a secret. You’ll see. It makes you appreciate films in a meaningful new way. It gives you momentum by keeping you in the 4th state of consciousness. So instead of allowing yourself to be immersed and brain-dead like Hollywood wants you to be, you stay acutely aware of the levels of details in the craft.

Love Death + Robots (Season 1, Final Episode), 10 minutes

This is a 10-minute animation every creative should see before they die. It’s the story of an artist who has found how to get to the essence of their art. Need I say more?

This is practically the movie version of The Mystery School. It's shows you the creative process in real time. It's about battling your demons. It's about how social media can ruin your life if you let it. It's about putting everything into something before you even know what it will be. It's about the power of having and sticking to an artistic vision... Even if you're all alone in your bedroom when no one believes in it yet.

Derek DelGaudio

To describe it is to ruin it. You're gonna have to trust me on this one.

Tsubasa Yamaguchi

It's about Yatora, an aspiring artist. He's dealing with four classic artist problems:

1. How to handle it when other people making art seem "better" than you.

2. How to find your artistic voice.

3. How to cope with parents and friends who don't get your art.

4. How to find the courage to "double down on yourself" when all you feel is doubt.

Expect to experience complex emotions.

American Horror Story (Season 10)

It’s the story of a woman who invents a little black pill for artists. This pill makes you create your best work, leading to fame and fortune. The catch? It only works if you’re TRULY talented. If you’re NOT talented and you take it… You lose all your hair and become a walking zombie who needs human blood to survive for the rest of your life.

Season 10 shows us the battle between1. the people who take the pill and are talented,2. those who take it and aren’t talented, and3. those who optNOTto take it and "stay natural".

It's a dark ride.

Secret Mall Apartment (2024)

"I recently watched this. It resonated with me because it seemed to embody so many aspects of The Mystery School lessons. The main character truly lives his message, and everything he does supports it, even when it goes against the established system." -- Hilwna

### 3. TMS LEXICON (A-Z) -- The Artist's Dictionary

The steps you take to constantly remind yourself that life will bring challenges to make things hard for you. So you plan ahead with your contingency plan, your alterned to-do lists etc.. for when it does. (see also 'Life Happens' Protocol)

Days you EARN that are still productive, but where social media, junk food and brain-numbing entertainment is allowed. Always planned IN ADVANCE, and immediately followed by an outrageously discipline workday to numb the monkey mind into a stupor. (Cheat Days still END with perfect discipline. Bedtime is never ever compromised.)

The clause I put in every client contract to allow me to bring chance elements into a creative project to imbue it with magic.

It's when you take your simple attainable goal and you keep adding new elements to it because you're feel "strong", and manic, and like you can take over the world...!! But the moment something throws you off your game-- You get overwhelmed. What was once a garden... Is now full of weeds. Damn. You started with one simple goal. But then you either got bored. Or worse... Cocky-- And now you have too many paths, too many side-projects, and way too many things on your TODO list. Please, get back to the essence.

The Mystery School extended family.

The flowery language you use to avoid being specific about your goals and message. Daydreaming language tricks you into thinking you're on the right path... But because your goals aren't clearly stated, it doesn't have legs to stand on. "Daydreaming Language" is why you get glazed-over looks from your aunt at Thanksgiving dinner when you tell her what you've been up to. "Daydreaming Language " is also the leading cause of your "pendulum of doubt". The opposite? Realistic language. Realistic language is when you put a plan down on paper. A plan you cross-check with people who have been on the path before. Realistic language will keep you motivated even when you're tired. It's definite and clear language that excites the people rooting for you...And gives gatekeepers FOMO. Realistic language is the only way you'll ever enlist people who will help you realize your vision.

It’s when your obsession reaches the level where even death isn’t a deterrent. Your aura takes on an air of calmness now, as you ride each day into your destiny with clarity.

It's when you decide to start doing the things that are intrinsically YOU even if they are unpopular at the moment. It's when you finally KNOW people will catch your wave over time.

The state of mind where someone is open to meeting and engaging with strangers no matter who they are just to get out of their comfort zone.

(a) Sharing high-quality art or media that contains your message... (b) Sharing high-quality art or media that's so fearless in it's expression that it's impossible to scroll by— even in a sea of content..

What you are offering to the world in return for what you want from the world.

Biology patterns you monitor that go beyond sleep.

When you use misleading words, cliches, or "feel good" memes to rationalize your failings or to delay real action.

A brain that has been fried by social media. Your brain is in a constant loop going between a state of zero attention span to experiencing deep moments of self-loathing whenever you’re forced to be with yourself.

God Momentum is self-generated momentum where you no longer need discipline and motivation to get you going. Your desire to procrastinate and delay "the work" is replaced by a sustainable obsession to create. Action and discipline become so enjoyable that it becomes your new way of life. This flow state can last for days, weeks, and sometimes even months.

When you change the meaning of words or concepts so that you can continue to do things the old way. You get hung up on the words and loose the essence.

The voice in your head that gives you every excuse you can find to never get out of your comfort zone.

An 'art insurance' letter you write to your future self (sealed, and placed in a secret place) describing in full detail what steps to take when a real-life emergency threatens your art making schedule.

The artist's worldview. Your artistic vision. A brand new way of seeing / doing things expressed in words to your audience. The best messages also tell people how you plan to achieve that vision. This is the whole reason why your audience f-cks with you.

When you can be happy even when things aren't going your way because you know you're blessed to be alive.

The simple boring activities (reading, meditating, going for a walk) that increase your energy.

Natural Born Creative

The idea that no act of courage is worthier than someone else's. In reality, anyone's step outside their comfort zone is growth.

The order to follow to choose how to get things done: Prioritize things that have a disproportionate effect on your goals.

Your vision of the artist that you will become in the future.

Pretenders are the talkers. Renegades are the doers.

The period of time where you practice a new intense art-making schedule to make sure it's realistic and sustainable.

The art you labor on while you go on being a "creation machine" with everything else.

A social media post, writing, or podcast, that is truthful, but might be painful to hear.

When you become such a creative machine that it's necessary to start logging your output on a spreadsheet, start labeling multiple hard drives, and start keeping a filing system for everything you create. 'VAULT MENTALITY' is what Prince had. He left behind a vault of hundreds of albums to release into the next century!

The voices you hear in your head when you start God Momentum. They ask you to quit. They tell you to cut corners. They encourage you to take increasingly longer breaks. If you fight them, they will eventually quieten. (But unfortunately, they never disappear.)

Art with no message. Art whose only use is decoration. Non-confrontational, “people pleasing” art.

The 'weapon list' is a list you make of everything you can name that's holding you back from success. And right next to each obstacle, you write down a realistic antidote against it. A tool, a recourse, or an ally that you have at your disposal. These are your weapons. Your goal in the upcoming months is to sharpen those weapons.

### 4. THE MYSTERY SCHOOL ROADMAP: 2019-2024 - (Find 2025 onwards in ++CHRCH)

EMAIL RELEASES (FINISHED)

Create Bootcamp #1, Bootcamp #2 of SUPPLEMENTAL MATERIAL delivered exclusively through email.

FINISH CORE TEACHINGS IN ALL SIX MODULES (FALL 2020)

Add 'The Book Of Mental Health'

Revamp 'The Book Of Influence'

Do this as we send out Bootcamp Emails and do next steps.

Price increase (for new students only).

MAKE EMAIL AUTOMATION RESEMBLE TIKTOK ALGORITHM (Each student sees something different depending on their interests) PROTOTYPE MID-2022

PODCAST (FREEMIUM - SPRING 2020 - CURRENT)

Start and iterate the 'Make art not content' podcast.

Use podcast as supplemental content (that only members can fully understand) and to promote The Mystery School.

Skype & Zoom (SUMMER 2021 - SUMMER 2022)

Get every single student interested up to date with NFTs and the new creator economy

Bring back regularly scheduled "one on ones" with students (ongoing)

Supervise random Drill Down Method partners.

REBRANDING (FALL / WINTER 2021)

Bring The Mystery School, 'Make art not content' podcast & lastnightsparty all under one unified brand.

COMMUNITY (SPRING 2021 - SUMMER 2022)

Create 'The Mystery Student Database'.

Outline what 'Make art not content' movement looks like. Start sending EXHIBIT C emails featuring people who are doing social media the right way.

Start promoting 'Make art not content' email list.

Figure out the best technology to give students the daily push they need.

DROP PODCAST EVERY SUNDAY FOR 10 WEEKS IN A ROW (AFTER LABOR DAY 2021)

Gather data to plan 2022

Share resulting high-productivity insights from FALL EXPERIMENT with students.

Guide students who are starting their 40-day God Momentum challenge.

JANUARY 2022 - APRIL 2022

Add 🔑 16:8 Phone Fasting Module

Start adding videos to YouTube channel

Plan collaborations with artists and brands.

Test "BI-POLAR METHOD' for 6 months / If it gives amazing results, add that module to The Mystery School in The Book Of Transformation

Introduce new podcast format / Season 3

Start 'The Consistency Club' to highlight and promote the most focused students in TMS.

Add new modules on nutrition,exchange value, and 'The G.O.A.T. Whisperer' series.

WINTER 2023 - SPRING 2024 (FOCUS ON VIDEO: MANC/FILMS)

Extensive world-building. Finally, bring video into the mix for this next phase.

Use 'The Mystery Formula' to iterate the MANC YouTube channel and gradually increase video production speed. Test formats until we find a series.Then take it on the road.

Invite students (only those who make videos) to participate in MANC videos. Share the secret guiding philosophies I use that can take us all into 2025.

SPRING 2024 (OR WHENEVER I FIND VIDEO FORMULA)

Find a voice and message for the MANC YouTube channel. -- (First viral video happened here)

WINTER 2024 - SPRING 2025 (FOCUS ON BUILDING COMMUNITY)

Start AUDIO Sunday Sermon.

Iterate The Sunday Sermon (audio version). Find the right platform. Find the right vibe.

Monetize Spotify & Apple Podcast.

Figure out how to create an online space for our growing community so TMS artists can help each other and stay motivated BUT NOT BE ANOTHER PLACE TO WASTE TIME LIKE THEY ALREADY DO ON SOCIAL MEDIA.

Build new platoform called ++CHRCH over Christmas Holidays

WORLD TOUR: Travel to film documentaries about aspiring artists and established artists

Organize TMS Meetups in different cities.
